# Lyrebird 2.0 — Exhaustive Code Audit

Comment-blind, every-line audit of all hand-written source (86 auditors over ~56.9K lines; comments stripped so findings reflect actual code behavior, not comment claims).

**527 findings** — p0: 1, p1: 87, p2: 214, p3: 225.

Severity: p0 = crash/data-loss/security · p1 = real user-facing bug or significant gap · p2 = polish/quality · p3 = nit.

By category: bug 136, consistency 76, gap-stub 58, test-gap 52, error-handling 44, accessibility 38, performance 35, dead-code 29, concurrency 29, validation 11, resource-leak 10, security 7, other 2.

## P0 (1)

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesAdvanced.swift`
- **L348** [bug] "Clear Caches" recursively deletes the ENTIRE user caches directory, which destroys downloaded offline music, contradicting the dialog's explicit promise that the library is not affected.
  - _Why:_ fm.urls(for: .cachesDirectory ...).first returns the container's whole caches root (~/Library/Containers/<bundle>/Data/Library/Caches or ~/Library/Caches/<bundle>). PreferencesDownloads.swift:105 stores offline downloads at caches.appendingPathComponent("Downloads"), and Artwork.swift:62-68 stores the Nuke DataCache there too. removeItem(at: caches) deletes ALL of it recursively. The confirmation dialog at lines 88-90 states "Artwork tiles and other temporary data will be removed. Your music library and settings are not affected" — but downloaded songs (the offline music library) live under that exact directory, so a user who taps Clear Caches loses all offline downloads despite being told they are safe. This is silent data loss on a destructive action whose copy actively misleads.
  - _Fix:_ Do not nuke the whole caches root. Clear only the artwork cache the way PreferencesLibrary.swift:274-275 does (Artwork.pipeline.cache.removeAll()), or delete a specific subdirectory, and explicitly preserve caches/Downloads. If downloads must be cleared too, change the dialog copy to warn that offline downloads will be removed. Also handle the removeItem/createDirectory failures instead of swallowing them.

## P1 (87)

### `core/src/client.rs`
- **L274** [bug] send_with_retry retries non-idempotent POST mutations on transport errors and 5xx/408/429, risking duplicate server-side side effects (e.g. add_to_playlist appends the same items twice).
  - _Why:_ A POST that times out after the server has already processed it (common: server commits, response lost) will be retried up to MAX_ATTEMPTS=3 times. For add_to_playlist this duplicates tracks in the playlist; for any future non-idempotent POST routed through send_with_retry it silently double-applies the mutation. GET/auth are idempotent so safe, but the retry layer makes no idempotency distinction.
  - _Fix:_ Gate transport/5xx retries on method idempotency: only auto-retry GET/HEAD/PUT/DELETE (and idempotent POSTs like AuthenticateByName) automatically; for non-idempotent POSTs either don't retry, or require an Idempotency-Key. Alternatively give add_to_playlist a non-retrying send path.
- **L863** [gap-stub] public_playlists is a stub that simply delegates to user_playlists, so it returns the caller's user-scoped playlists rather than server-public playlists. The name promises behavior the body does not implement.
  - _Why:_ Any UI surface that calls public_playlists expecting a distinct set (e.g. publicly shared playlists vs. the user's own) gets the identical result as user_playlists. This is a silent feature gap: the function exists, compiles, and returns plausible data, masking that the public-playlist path was never wired.
  - _Fix:_ Either implement a real query (Items with IsPublic/Shared filter, or the Jellyfin shared-playlist endpoint) or remove public_playlists and have callers use user_playlists explicitly so the gap is visible.
- **L894** [performance] playlists_containing_artist performs up to 200 sequential per-playlist Items requests (each fetching up to 500 tracks) under the single FFI Inner mutex, with no concurrency and no early server-side filtering.
  - _Why:_ Worst case is 200 round-trips of 500-track payloads done strictly sequentially while holding the core mutex that every other FFI call serializes through (per CLAUDE.md every FFI call takes Inner's mutex). On a large library this can stall the whole app for many seconds and saturate the server. There is also no de-dup against limit being satisfied early other than the len check, but each non-matching playlist still costs a full probe.
  - _Fix:_ Bound work much tighter (scan fewer playlists, smaller probe), run the probes concurrently with a bounded join_all / buffer_unordered, and short-circuit. Better: ask the server to filter playlists by artist (ArtistIds/AlbumArtistIds with ParentId per playlist) so the membership test is a HEAD/count instead of pulling 500 tracks.
- **L2436** [bug] rename_playlist performs a lossy read-modify-write that WIPES playlist metadata (Genres, Overview, Tags, ForcedSortName, OfficialRating, etc.) on every rename. It fetches the existing item with NO Fields (`fetch_item(playlist_id, &[])`), then POSTs that sparse body back to `POST /Items/{id}` with only `Name` changed.
  - _Why:_ fetch_item with an empty Fields slice returns a sparse BaseItemDto. Verified against the live test server: `GET /Items?Ids=<pl>` (no Fields) returns keys [Id,Name,RunTimeTicks,ImageTags,ChildCount,UserData,...] but OMITS Genres/Overview/Tags/SortName/ProviderIds — those appear only when Fields is requested. The Jellyfin backend's `ItemUpdateController.UpdateItem` (jellyfin/Jellyfin.Api/Controllers/ItemUpdateController.cs:250-293) UNCONDITIONALLY assigns `item.Overview = request.Overview; item.Genres = request.Genres; item.Tags = newTags; item.ForcedSortName = request.ForcedSortName;` from the request body. Because those fields are absent from the round-tripped body, they deserialize to null/empty defaults and the server overwrites the real values. The test playlist 9c9b2ff6... actually has Genres=[Rock,Ballad,Dance-Pop,Electronic,Hip Hop,Pop,Synth-Pop,Teen Pop]; renaming it through this code path would blank all of them. This is silent server-side data loss on a routine user action.
  - _Fix:_ Request the full editable field set when fetching, e.g. `fetch_item(playlist_id, &["Genres","Tags","Overview","SortName","ProviderIds","DateCreated","ProductionYear"])`, and map SortName -> ForcedSortName before posting. Better: don't round-trip the whole BaseItemDto at all — POST only the fields you intend to change is unsafe given the backend's blind-assign semantics, so instead start from a fully-populated item (all fields the backend reads in UpdateItem) and mutate only Name. Minimal safe change: include at least Genres, Overview, Tags, SortName, ProductionYear, OfficialRating in the Fields list so the echoed values match the current state.

### `core/src/error.rs`
- **L42** [bug] RateLimit Display string uses Rust debug formatting `{retry_after:?}` for an Option<u64>, which renders user-visible text like "rate limited (retry after Some(30)s)" or "rate limited (retry after None s)". Because the enum is `#[uniffi(flat_error)]`, this exact Display string is the ONLY thing Swift receives (each Swift case is `case RateLimit(message: String)` — the structured `retry_after` field is discarded), and the Swift consumer (macos/Sources/Lyrebird/LyrebirdErrorPresenter.swift) does substring matching on `error.localizedDescription.lowercased()`. So this raw debug-formatted string is what flows toward the UI.
  - _Why:_ Debug-formatting an Option leaks Rust internals (`Some(...)`/`None`) into a string that crosses the FFI boundary and is the basis for user-facing messaging. "retry after None s" / "retry after Some(30)s" is broken English and exposes implementation detail. The structured `retry_after` value (which a real UI would use to show a countdown) is unreachable on the Swift side because flat_error collapses the variant to a single message string.
  - _Fix:_ Format the Option explicitly, e.g. `#[error("rate limited{}", retry_after.map(|s| format!(" (retry after {s}s)")).unwrap_or_default())]`, or drop the seconds from the Display and expose `retry_after` via a dedicated accessor. Given flat_error hides the field from Swift, if the UI needs the value it must be surfaced another way (separate FFI method or non-flat error).
- **L196** [consistency] `LyrebirdError::is_retryable()` classifies retryability differently from the actual retry loop in core/src/client.rs (`is_retriable_status`). client.rs treats HTTP 408 (Request Timeout) as retryable and 501 (Not Implemented) as NOT retryable; error.rs `is_retryable` does the opposite — `from_status` maps 408 to `Server{408}` which is not in the `(500..600)` range so 408 is classified non-retryable, while 501 IS in 500..600 so it is classified retryable.
  - _Why:_ Two divergent sources of truth for the same decision. `is_retryable()` is a public method intended for callers to decide whether to retry; if anyone wires it into a retry path (or the FFI) it will retry 501 (pointless — the server doesn't implement the endpoint) and give up on 408 (a transient timeout worth retrying), exactly inverting the internal loop's correct policy.
  - _Fix:_ Make `is_retryable` delegate to the same predicate as client.rs (treat 408 and 429 and 5xx-except-501 as retryable), or have client.rs's loop call `is_retryable` after converting status->error so there is a single classifier. Add a test asserting 408==true and 501==false to lock the contract.

### `core/src/lib.rs`
- **L953** [concurrency] mark_track_started performs a synchronous SQLite write (record_play) while holding the Inner mutex, on every track start.
  - _Why:_ Per CLAUDE.md gap pattern #2, every FFI call on the @MainActor serializes through the Inner mutex on the main thread. mark_track_started is a UI-driven call (track change) and runs a blocking disk INSERT while holding the lock. Under contention (e.g. a concurrent paged list_albums on the main thread waiting for the same lock) this can stall the UI. The DB write also has nothing to do with the player.set_current call but they are bundled under one synchronous FFI hop.
  - _Fix:_ Either marshal the DB write off-thread (self.runtime.spawn / Task.detached on the Swift side) so it doesn't block the caller, or at minimum take the db Arc out of the lock first (let db = self.inner.lock().db.clone();) and perform record_play without holding the Inner mutex, matching the pattern used in set_scrobble_token (line 1139).

### `core/src/player.rs`
- **L298** [bug] set_current() updates s.current and s.state but never updates s.queue_index, allowing current_track to diverge from queue_position / current_in_queue() / the skip & peek cursor.
  - _Why:_ queue_index is the source of truth for skip_next/skip_previous/peek_next/current_in_queue and the queue_position reported in PlayerStatus. set_current is a public UniFFI method (exposed as core.markTrackStarted -> set_current, called by AudioEngine.swift:497 on every track load). If it is ever invoked for a track that is not at the current queue_index, status().queuePosition and current_in_queue() point at a different track than current_track, and a subsequent skip_next/skip_previous advances from the STALE index — jumping to the wrong track. Today the desync is masked only because every call site happens to call skip_*/set_queue first so the index is already correct; this is a fragile invariant with no enforcement and the function name (set_current) strongly implies it should make the queue cursor agree.
  - _Fix:_ Either (a) make set_current locate the track in the queue and update queue_index when found (e.g. if let Some(i) = s.queue.iter().position(|t| t.id == track.id) { s.queue_index = i; }), or (b) drop set_current and require callers to drive current exclusively through set_queue/skip_*. At minimum document/enforce that current and queue[queue_index] must stay equal.
- **L360** [test-gap] Eight public Player methods have zero test coverage in the entire test module (verified: 0 call sites for any of them in lines 360-817): `mark_position` (line 321, including the `.max(0.0)` negative-clamp branch), `set_volume` (line 325, including the `.clamp(0.0, 1.0)` branch), `mark_state` (line 317), `set_current` (line 298, which also forces state to Playing), `clear` (line 345, which resets state=Stopped, current=None, position=0, play_session_id=None, queue, and index), `current_in_queue` (line 151), `set_play_session_id` (line 307), and `play_session_id` (line 313).
  - _Why:_ These are stateful mutators feeding PlayerStatus consumed by the SwiftUI layer. A regression in clamp logic (e.g. accepting volume > 1.0 or negative position), or in `clear()` failing to null `play_session_id` (a known gap-pattern in CLAUDE.md #5 about session leakage), would ship undetected. `clear()` in particular resets six fields and is completely unverified.
  - _Fix:_ Add tests: set_volume(2.0) -> status.volume == 1.0 and set_volume(-1.0) -> 0.0; mark_position(-5.0) -> 0.0; clear() after a populated queue+session -> state==Stopped, current==None, position==0, play_session_id==None, queue_length==0; set_current(track) -> state==Playing && current==track; set_play_session_id(Some(x)) then play_session_id()==Some(x); current_in_queue() returns queue[index].
- **L416** [test-gap] Test `shuffle_and_repeat_are_preserved_across_queue_changes` only verifies that the `shuffle` boolean survives a `set_queue` call; it never asserts that shuffle actually changes playback order. Because the production `set_shuffle` (line 334-336) merely writes a flag that no navigation method ever reads (skip_next/skip_previous/peek_next at lines 169/226/203 never consult `s.shuffle`; it is only echoed back in `snapshot()` at line 110), this test gives false confidence that the shuffle feature works. The test passes precisely because shuffle is a no-op.
  - _Why:_ The only test touching shuffle semantics asserts a tautology (a stored bool is returned). A reviewer/CI sees 'shuffle is tested and green' while the feature does nothing — skip_next on a shuffled queue still plays a,b,c in original order. A regression that breaks real shuffle (once implemented) or the current dead-flag state both pass.
  - _Fix:_ Add a test that sets shuffle on a multi-track queue and asserts skip_next/peek_next does NOT return strictly-sequential original order (or asserts the documented shuffle contract). If shuffle is intentionally unimplemented in core, the test should assert that explicitly (e.g. order is unchanged) and the implementation gap should be tracked, rather than naming the test '...preserved across queue changes' which implies behavior coverage.

### `core/src/scrobble.rs`
- **L220** [error-handling] Scrobbler::submit ignores HTTP 429 / Retry-After from ListenBrainz, collapsing rate-limit responses into a generic Server error
  - _Why:_ ListenBrainz aggressively rate-limits submit-listens and returns 429 with X-RateLimit-Reset-In / Retry-After headers. The project already has a structured LyrebirdError::RateLimit { retry_after } variant (see core/src/error.rs:from_status which maps 429 -> RateLimit). This hand-rolled status handling only special-cases 401 and buckets 429 into LyrebirdError::Server, so the caller cannot back off intelligently and a burst of scrobbles will keep hammering the API and failing. The Retry-After value is discarded entirely.
  - _Fix:_ After computing `status`, before the generic Server error, branch on 429: read the Retry-After / X-RateLimit-Reset-In header and return LyrebirdError::RateLimit { retry_after: parsed } (reuse error::from_status semantics). Ideally route the whole non-success path through LyrebirdError::from_status(status, snippet, retry_after) so 401/403/404/429 are all mapped consistently with the rest of the client.

### `core/src/storage.rs`
- **L133** [security] clear_user_data() (the logout/account-switch wipe) deletes session keys, play_history and the three caches, but does NOT delete the ListenBrainz scrobble token persisted under settings key 'scrobble_listenbrainz_token'. After user A logs out, the token survives in the settings table; when user B logs in on the same machine, is_scrobble_configured() returns true and the app scrobbles user B's listens to user A's ListenBrainz account.
  - _Why:_ This is a cross-account credential leak on a shared/multi-user Mac: the scrobble token is user-personal (per the set_scrobble_token flow in lib.rs:1135) yet it is treated as machine-global and outlives the session it belonged to. The keyring auth token IS cleared on logout (lib.rs:311-315) but this DB-stored token is not, so the wipe is incomplete.
  - _Fix:_ Add "scrobble_listenbrainz_token" to the session_keys array deleted in clear_user_data (or have the logout path in lib.rs explicitly call db.delete_setting(SCROBBLE_TOKEN_KEY)). If the token is intentionally machine-global, that decision should be made explicit, but logout-clearing the auth token while leaving a scrobble token that causes mis-attributed scrobbles is inconsistent and a privacy bug.

### `core/src/tests.rs`
- **L5670** [test-gap] login_keyring_write_is_not_silenced is vacuous: with the in-memory mock keyring it can never exercise the KeyringWrite error path it claims to guard.
  - _Why:_ install_mock_keyring() (tests.rs:39) backs the keyring with an Arc<Mutex<HashMap>> whose set_secret always returns Ok. So login always takes the Ok(_) arm; the Err(KeyringWrite) arm is unreachable. The test name asserts the keyring-write error is 'not silenced', but the test passes identically whether the production code propagates the error, swallows it with try?, or has no keyring write at all. It provides zero regression protection for the behavior it advertises.
  - _Fix:_ Inject a keyring whose set_secret returns an error (extend install_mock_keyring with a fail-mode flag, or install a separate failing mock), then assert the login result is specifically Err(LyrebirdError::KeyringWrite { .. }) — not merely 'Ok or KeyringWrite'. Otherwise the test cannot detect a regression where login silently swallows keyring failures.
- **L6260** [test-gap] heartbeat_fires_at_expected_cadence and heartbeat_stops_after_abort test a private re-implementation (spawn_heartbeat_for_test), not the production heartbeat (LyrebirdCore::start_heartbeat / stop_heartbeat in lib.rs:1214-1279). The helper duplicates the loop logic but diverges from production, so the tests give false confidence that the shipping scheduler works.
  - _Why:_ Production start_heartbeat reads core.player.status() for the track id and pause state, skips ticks when current_track is None, calls try_client_arc() (skip if no session), and stores the abort in self.heartbeat for stop_heartbeat() to take. None of that is exercised. A regression in any of those production paths would pass these tests. The whole point of #639's scheduler (per CLAUDE.md) is the lifecycle integration, which is exactly what is untested.
  - _Fix:_ Construct a LyrebirdCore (as with_client_releases_inner_lock_before_http does), drive playback state via the player, then call core.start_heartbeat(secs, session) and core.stop_heartbeat(), asserting against the mock server. Delete spawn_heartbeat_for_test or keep it only as a thin wrapper that calls the production function.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/AppDelegate.swift`
- **L236** [gap-stub] Dock-tile progress ring never advances during playback — it is only recomputed on play/pause/stop transitions, so the ring is frozen at the position captured when playback started.
  - _Why:_ The entire throttle/scheduleFlush machinery in DockTileController (minInterval=1.0, scheduleFlush, flush) exists to rate-limit *progress* updates, but progress is never fed in mid-track. status.state only changes on play/pause/stop, never on each second of playback. The user sees a progress ring that jumps only when they pause/resume and otherwise sits still — the feature silently does almost nothing. The 1Hz throttle code in DockTileController is effectively dead for its primary purpose.
  - _Fix:_ Drive refreshDockTile on a periodic cadence while playing (e.g. observe status.positionSeconds, or run a 1Hz timer that calls refreshDockTile only when status.state == .playing, matching the existing 1Hz poll contract in CLAUDE.md), and skip when paused/stopped. Then DockTileController's existing throttle correctly coalesces the per-second updates.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/AppModel.swift`
- **L1965** [bug] refreshQuickPicks uses MinDateLastSaved (a server metadata-save-time filter) to express 'played in the last 30 days', which is the wrong dimension and silently drops the very albums Quick Picks is meant to surface.
  - _Why:_ On Jellyfin, MinDateLastSaved filters by DateLastSaved (when the item's metadata was last written on the server), not by when the user last played it. An album the user plays constantly but whose metadata hasn't been re-saved in 30 days is excluded, while a freshly-imported-but-unplayed album that slipped past the IsPlayed filter is favoured. Quick Picks therefore shows a near-empty or wrong shelf on any stable library. This is the only call site passing a non-nil minDateLastSaved (every other refresher passes nil), confirming the intent was play-recency, not metadata-save-recency.
  - _Fix:_ Drop the MinDateLastSaved constraint for Quick Picks (rely on SortBy=PlayCount,SortName + Filters=IsPlayed and the limit), or switch to a play-time-based constraint if one is needed. There is no MinDatePlayed query param, so the simplest correct behaviour is minDateLastSaved: nil.
- **L3228** [gap-stub] addToPlaylist performs an optimistic update that only bumps the playlist summary trackCount, but never touches the playlistTracks[id] / currentPlaylistTracks track cache. Because loadPlaylistTracks(playlistId:) short-circuits on a cache hit (line 3041), the newly added tracks never become visible in the open playlist.
  - _Why:_ The drag-drop caller in PlaylistDetailView.handleDrop does `model.addToPlaylist(...)` then `await model.loadPlaylistTracks(playlistId:)` (PlaylistDetailView.swift:466-467 / 476-477). loadPlaylistTracks(playlistId:) returns the STALE cached list (line 3041 `if let cached = playlistTracks[playlistId]`) because addToPlaylist never invalidated or appended to that cache. The only cache invalidations for playlistTracks are full resets (lines 1243, 1317) and deletePlaylist (line 4967). Net effect: dragging tracks onto a playlist increments the count badge but the track list body does not show the added tracks until the cache is cleared by other means — a visible, reproducible inconsistency.
  - _Fix:_ In addToPlaylist, also update the track cache optimistically (mirror removeFromPlaylist): if playlistTracks[playlistId] exists, append the resolved Track objects (or at minimum invalidate the entry via playlistTracks.removeValue(forKey: playlistId)) so the subsequent loadPlaylistTracks refetches. On server failure, roll the appended tracks back alongside the trackCount decrement that is already present.
- **L3842** [gap-stub] Full-search Playlists scope is permanently empty: bucketSearchResults hard-codes the playlists bucket to [].
  - _Why:_ SearchView.sectionedResults always includes .playlists in allScopes ([.artists, .albums, .tracks, .playlists] at SearchView.swift:305-306), and it is NOT gated by any capability flag. So when the user picks the 'Playlists' scope (or 'All') on the full search page, the Playlists section renders nothing, even though the server has playlists (78 on the reference server). Playlists DO show in the instant dropdown (which uses search_hints incl. Playlist), making the full-search omission look like a broken page.
  - _Fix:_ Either fetch playlists in core.search (add ItemKind::Playlist to the ItemsQuery and map a playlists bucket), or, until that lands, drop .playlists from allScopes in SearchView so an empty section isn't shown. Surfacing an always-empty user-selectable scope is worse than hiding it.
- **L4363** [error-handling] markAllAsPlayed optimistically flips playedById[album.id] but setPlayed never rolls it back on server failure, leaving the UI showing a wrong played state permanently.
  - _Why:_ If the network call fails (offline/timeout), the album row shows the new (wrong) played/unplayed state until a full refetch, contradicting the server. This is the exact optimistic-UI-without-rollback anti-pattern the repo's CLAUDE.md calls out as a silent-corruption bug and that playlist mutations were already fixed for in rc12. The same gap exists at the per-track path (~5239/5242, just outside this range), so it is systemic.
  - _Fix:_ Capture the prior value before the optimistic write and restore it in setPlayed's catch (pass an onFailure rollback or have markAllAsPlayed do the optimistic+rollback itself), mirroring the rollback pattern used for removeFromPlaylist/addToPlaylist.
- **L4948** [bug] duplicatePlaylist caches the SOURCE playlist's Track objects under the NEW playlist id. Those Tracks carry the source playlist's playlistItemId values, so subsequent reorder/remove on the duplicate operate against the wrong (source) playlist-entry IDs.
  - _Why:_ playlistItemId is per-playlist-entry, not per-track. moveTrackInPlaylist (line 5031/5040) and removeFromPlaylist (line 3082) send these IDs to core.reorderPlaylistTrack/removeFromPlaylist. Because loadPlaylistTracks(playlist:) serves the cache first (line 3004), the bad entries are never refreshed, so editing the duplicate either fails server-side or mutates the source playlist's entries.
  - _Fix:_ Do not seed playlistTracks[newId] with source-derived items. Either leave it unset (forcing a fresh fetch with correct playlistItemIds) or re-fetch the new playlist's tracks via core.playlistTracks(playlistId: newId,...) before caching.
- **L5045** [error-handling] moveTrackInPlaylist applies the reorder to local state (playlistTracks/currentPlaylistTracks) immediately, but on a failed core.reorderPlaylistTrack it only sets errorMessage with no rollback. The user sees the track in the new position while the server keeps the old order — silent divergence.
  - _Why:_ Optimistic reorder with no compensating revert (gap pattern #5). Compare removeFromPlaylist (line 3133) and renamePlaylist (line 3900) which both restore prior state in their catch. After a failed reorder the next reorder/remove computes indices/IDs against a list the server doesn't share.
  - _Fix:_ Capture the pre-move ordering (or the moved track's original index) and restore playlistTracks[playlistId]/currentPlaylistTracks in the catch before showing the error.
- **L5239** [error-handling] toggleMarkPlayed optimistically writes playedById[track.id] = target, but setPlayed (the FFI wrapper) never rolls back playedById on failure. A failed mark-played leaves the UI permanently showing the toggled state, diverging from the server until restart.
  - _Why:_ Matches CLAUDE.md gap pattern #5 (optimistic UI without server echo + no rollback). setPlayed updates playedById only on success (state.played); the catch surfaces an error message but leaves the optimistic value, so the row stays falsely played/unplayed. markAllAsPlayed (line 4363) has the identical defect.
  - _Fix:_ Snapshot prior playedById values before the optimistic write and restore them in setPlayed's catch (or have toggleMarkPlayed/markAllAsPlayed roll back). Mirror the rollback pattern already used in renamePlaylist/deletePlaylist.
- **L5286** [bug] The genre name->id cache (_genreIdsByName / _genresLoaded) is never invalidated on sign-out or server switch. After switching servers/accounts it resolves genre names (e.g. "Rock") to the PREVIOUS server's genre IDs, so browseGenre/startGenreRadio/shuffleGenre navigate to or play the wrong server's genre (or surface a false "not found").
  - _Why:_ Both reset paths clear playlistTracks/artist caches/etc. but omit _genreIdsByName/_genresLoaded. The map is keyed by NAME, which collides across every server (all servers have "Rock"/"Jazz"), so a stale entry resolves to a foreign GUID. Confirmed via rg: the only writes are in resolvedGenreId; no removeAll anywhere.
  - _Fix:_ Add `_genreIdsByName = [:]; _genresLoaded = false` to both the sign-out reset (~line 1244) and forgetToken reset (~line 1318). Same applies to playedById/favoriteById which also leak across accounts (lower severity since keyed by GUID).
- **L5300** [bug] resolvedGenreId builds the name->id map with Dictionary(uniqueKeysWithValues:), which traps (fatalError) on any duplicate genre name. Jellyfin's /Genres response is not guaranteed to have globally-unique display names; a single collision crashes the app the first time any genre action runs.
  - _Why:_ Dictionary(uniqueKeysWithValues:) is documented to trap on duplicate keys. Genre names are user/metadata-derived and can repeat (case/whitespace variants, multi-library merges). A duplicate name turns the first invocation of browseGenre/startGenreRadio/shuffleGenre into a hard crash with no recovery path.
  - _Fix:_ Use the non-trapping initializer: _genreIdsByName = Dictionary(pairs, uniquingKeysWith: { first, _ in first }). Optionally normalize/trim names before keying.
- **L6203** [bug] removeFromUpNext only mutates the local display array and never rebuilds the core queue, so the removed track still plays on skip/auto-advance
  - _Why:_ moveUpNext (line 6196) rebuilds the core queue via core.setQueue(tracks: [current]+userAdded+autoQueue, startIndex: 0) after a reorder, but removeFromUpNext does not. There is no didSet/onChange/observer syncing upNextUserAdded back to core (confirmed: only moveUpNext and play(tracks:) call core.setQueue). The QueueInspector shows the row vanish, but core.skipNext() still returns the removed track because Rust's s.queue is untouched, so the 'removed' track plays anyway.
  - _Fix:_ After removing locally, rebuild the core queue the same way moveUpNext does: var allTracks = [current?] + upNextUserAdded.map(\.track) + upNextAutoQueue.map(\.track); core.setQueue(tracks: allTracks, startIndex: 0) (guarding for empty / current==nil), so the core queue reflects the removal.
- **L6222** [bug] clearQueue() never clears the core queue and pauses the playing track, contradicting both its own confirmation-dialog copy and the working command-palette equivalent
  - _Why:_ The core queue is the live source of truth for playback (skipNext()/handleTrackEnded() call core.skipNext(), and set_queue stores s.queue in Rust). This method only empties the Swift display mirror and calls audio.pause(); it never calls core.clearQueue() (which exists and is non-throwing — the command palette's 'Clear Queue' action at line 944 calls it correctly). Consequences: (1) after the user confirms Clear, the next skip / auto-advance plays tracks from the still-populated core queue, so the queue isn't actually cleared; (2) audio.pause() stops the currently-playing track, directly contradicting the QueueInspector confirmation dialog text 'The currently-playing track keeps playing.' (QueueInspector.swift line ~111).
  - _Fix:_ Call core.clearQueue() and refresh status instead of pausing: replace audio.pause() with core.clearQueue(); self.status = core.status(). Do NOT pause the current track, to honor the dialog's promise. Mirror the command-palette action at line 944.
- **L6286** [bug] Save Queue as Playlist adds every track twice: createPlaylist already seeds the new playlist with `ids`, then addToPlaylist re-posts the same `ids`, so the saved playlist contains each track duplicated.
  - _Why:_ core.create_playlist POSTs `Ids: [...]` in the /Playlists body (verified in core/src/client.rs:2008-2013 and asserted by tests.rs:3338-3343, `id_strs == ["t1","t2","t3"]`), which Jellyfin uses to populate the playlist. The subsequent addToPlaylist POSTs the identical ids to /Playlists/{id}/Items. Jellyfin does not dedupe playlist items, so every queue track ends up in the saved playlist twice. This is the entire purpose of FullQueueView's 'Save Queue as Playlist' button (FullQueueView.swift:60 calls model.saveQueueAsPlaylist), so the feature ships broken.
  - _Fix:_ Drop the redundant addToPlaylist call after a successful createPlaylist (createPlaylist already seeds the items). Only call addToPlaylist if the create path is changed to create an empty playlist. Either pass empty itemIds to createPlaylist and keep addToPlaylist, or keep itemIds and remove lines 6286-6288.
- **L6287** [bug] saveQueueAsPlaylist adds every track twice: createPlaylist already embeds the ids, then addToPlaylist re-adds the same ids
  - _Why:_ core.createPlaylist POSTs to /Playlists with the body field Ids = item_ids (confirmed in client.rs create_playlist and the test create_playlist_posts_pascal_case_body_and_returns_id which asserts body["Ids"] == [t1,t2,t3]). The playlist is therefore created already containing all tracks. The subsequent addToPlaylist(trackIds: ids, ...) POSTs the same ids to /Playlists/{id}/Items, so the saved playlist contains every queue track duplicated.
  - _Fix:_ Pass itemIds: [] (or position-only) to createPlaylist and rely on the follow-up addToPlaylist, OR drop the addToPlaylist call entirely since createPlaylist already populates the playlist. Pick one path so each track is added exactly once.
- **L6306** [bug] shuffleUpNext only shuffles the local display array and never rebuilds the core queue, so playback order is unchanged after shuffle
  - _Why:_ Same desync as removeFromUpNext. The QueueInspector reorders visually (it reads model.upNextUserAdded), but core.skipNext() advances through Rust's unchanged s.queue, so the next tracks play in the original (pre-shuffle) order. moveUpNext is the reference pattern that DOES push to core; shuffleUpNext omits the equivalent core.setQueue call.
  - _Fix:_ After upNextUserAdded.shuffle(), rebuild the core queue identically to moveUpNext: assemble [current?]+upNextUserAdded+upNextAutoQueue and call core.setQueue(tracks:startIndex:0) so the shuffled order takes effect on playback.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/ArtistContextMenu.swift`
- **L36** [gap-stub] Artist context-menu "Play Next" queues at most the artist's top 5 tracks, not the artist's catalog, so it behaves nothing like the album/track "Play Next".
  - _Why:_ "Play Next" on an artist implies inserting that artist's music after the current track (like Play All but queued). Instead it inserts only up to 5 "top" tracks (and if the artist's top-tracks shelf was already viewed, it silently reuses whatever was cached at limit 5). Play All / Shuffle All on the same artist use `loadTracks(forArtist:)` (limit 500), so the menu is internally inconsistent and the user gets a tiny, surprising subset.
  - _Fix:_ Make playNextArtist load the full artist track set via the same `loadTracks(forArtist:)` path used by playAll(artist:)/shuffle(artist:), then `core.playNext(tracks:)`; or explicitly call `loadArtistTopTracks(artistId:, limit: 500)`. Do not reuse the 5-item top-tracks cache for a queue-insert action.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/CommandPalette.swift`
- **L361** [bug] Action search matches by hasPrefix only, so common substring queries return zero actions (e.g. "preferences", "shuffle", "queue", "favorites", "library" all match nothing).
  - _Why:_ Action titles are multi-word ("Open Preferences", "Toggle Shuffle", "Clear Queue", "Add to Queue", "Go to Favorites", "Go to Library"). hasPrefix on the full title means typing the salient word never matches — "shuffle" is not a prefix of "toggle shuffle", "queue" is not a prefix of "clear queue". A command palette's core value is discoverability; this makes most actions unreachable by search and only findable via the empty-query default list. The library-search side (server-side) does substring/relevance matching, so the two halves of the palette behave inconsistently.
  - _Fix:_ Use substring matching (contains) and/or token-prefix matching: split the title on whitespace and match if any token hasPrefix(trimmed), or fall back to title.lowercased().contains(trimmed). Consider fuzzy/subsequence scoring for parity with typical palettes.
- **L546** [gap-stub] commitInNewWindow() does not open a new window — it just calls commitSelection(), making the advertised ⌘↩ "new window" affordance a no-op identical to plain Enter.
  - _Why:_ The hints row (line 272) and the ⌘↩ shortcut promise opening the selected artist/album in a new window, but the body is a verbatim duplicate of commitSelection() — it navigates in the same window and closes the palette. The app does have window-opening infra (openWindow in LyrebirdApp.swift), but there is only a single main WindowGroup("Lyrebird") and no per-artist/album window scene, so the feature is not just unimplemented here, it is unsupported architecturally. Users pressing ⌘↩ get a silently wrong result.
  - _Fix:_ Either remove the ⌘↩ button + the "new window" hint (line 272) until a detached-window scene exists, or implement an actual new-window path (e.g. an @Environment(\.openWindow) value driving a value-typed WindowGroup keyed by the selected route) and route artist/album activation through it.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/EmptyLibraryState.swift`
- **L70** [accessibility] EmptyLibraryState uses .accessibilityElement(children: .combine) while containing the interactive "Open Jellyfin web" Button. The combine modifier collapses the subtree into one static element, so the button loses its action/trait and is not reachable by VoiceOver.
  - _Why:_ When a server URL is present this button is the actionable way to reach the web client from the empty-library screen. children: .combine plus a combined label that only contains headline+subtitle means the button's own label and tap action are dropped from the accessibility tree, making the action unavailable to assistive-tech users.
  - _Fix:_ Switch to .accessibilityElement(children: .contain) so the headline/subtitle text and the button each remain accessible, or attach an .accessibilityAction for opening the URL to the combined element.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/EmptyStateView.swift`
- **L115** [accessibility] EmptyStateView merges its entire subtree with .accessibilityElement(children: .combine) even though the view contains interactive primary/secondary CTA buttons. .combine flattens descendants into a single static accessibility element, stripping the buttons of their own .isButton trait and tap action, so VoiceOver users cannot reach or activate the CTAs.
  - _Why:_ This is the shared empty-state used for first-run-no-library ("Change Library"), empty-playlist ("Add Tracks"), and the custom Refresh/Go-to-Library case. Those CTAs are the only escape hatch on those screens; combining children makes them invisible to assistive technology, so a VoiceOver user hits a dead end. Sibling components that contain interactive children correctly use children: .contain (PlayerBar.swift:66, DecadeBrowseRow.swift:42, Chips.swift:57).
  - _Fix:_ Use .accessibilityElement(children: .contain) (so the buttons remain individually focusable/actionable), or keep .combine only when no CTA is present and switch to .contain when primaryCTA/secondaryCTA is non-nil. Alternatively add explicit .accessibilityAction(...) entries to the combined element for each CTA.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/LibraryFilterPopover.swift`
- **L416** [bug] RangeSlider drag math reads value.location.x relative to the offset 16pt thumb, not the track, so the year slider does not track the cursor and snaps thumbs to (near) the lower bound on any drag.
  - _Why:_ DragGesture() defaults to CoordinateSpace.local, i.e. the bounds of the view it is attached to. It is attached to the thumb (a 16x16 Circle), and .offset is a render-only transform that does not move the gesture's local origin. So value.location.x is the touch point WITHIN the thumb (~0...16), not the position along the track (~0...usable, where usable can be ~248). Dividing a 0...16 value by usable yields a fraction near 0, so dragging either thumb collapses the selected year to roughly the minimum bound. The year filter is effectively unusable via the slider.
  - _Fix:_ Drive the gesture from the container's coordinate space. Put .coordinateSpace(name: "rangeSlider") on the ZStack and use DragGesture(coordinateSpace: .named("rangeSlider")), keeping value.location.x. Alternatively, capture the thumb's start offset and use value.translation.width: low/high = startOffset + value.translation.width, then convert offset->value via (offset/usable)*span + lowerBound and clamp.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/PlaylistExport.swift`
- **L31** [gap-stub] Exported .m3u8 stream URLs omit the api_key and all transcoding query params, so the exported playlist's entries are not playable in an external player.
  - _Why:_ The real core builds the same endpoint with required auth/transcoding params (core/src/client.rs:2527 stream_url appends UserId, DeviceId, MaxStreamingBitrate, Container, AudioCodec, TranscodingContainer/Protocol, and crucially `api_key` = the session token). Jellyfin's /Audio/{id}/universal returns 401 without auth. The whole point of the .m3u8 export (issue #98 'Export as .m3u8') is to hand a working playlist to another player; every line here is a URL that 401s. Note the security tension: embedding the bearer token in a file the user shares leaks a credential, so the fix should be deliberate rather than naively pasting api_key.
  - _Fix:_ Decide the contract explicitly. Either (a) append the api_key + the same params the core uses so the file actually plays (accepting that the file then contains a credential, and document/warn the user), or (b) export the public /web details deep-link form (already implemented in webURL) / a static-download URL form that the receiving player can authenticate against, rather than bare unauthenticated /universal URLs. As-is the export is non-functional.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/PlaylistReorderHandle.swift`
- **L104** [bug] Drag-to-reorder carries only the track's item id, not its position or PlaylistItemId, so reordering one copy of a duplicated track moves the wrong copy.
  - _Why:_ The Track model documents that a playlist can contain the same underlying item multiple times, each with a distinct PlaylistItemId (`public var playlistItemId: String?` in the generated bindings, doc: "duplicate tracks in the same playlist can be operated on independently"). The modifier already receives `index: Int` (passed as `index: idx` from PlaylistView.swift:373) but never puts it in the drag payload. applyPlaylistDrop/moveTrackInPlaylist then always grab the FIRST occurrence of that id. Dragging the 2nd/3rd copy of a duplicated track reorders the first copy instead, producing a wrong (and server-persisted, via reorderPlaylistTrack) order. The keyboard reorder path (PlaylistView.swift:382 moveTrackInPlaylist(from: idx,...)) is index-correct, so behavior diverges between keyboard and drag.
  - _Fix:_ Carry the source index (or playlistItemId) in the drag payload and use it on drop instead of re-deriving from the item id. E.g. provide the index as the dragged string and add an applyPlaylistDrop(playlistId:sourceIndex:destinationIndex:) overload, or encode "<index>|<trackId>" and parse it in performDrop. Resolve the moved track by index so duplicates move independently.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/QueueInspector.swift`
- **L296** [bug] The Shuffle button (and the per-row Remove 'xmark') visibly reorders/removes rows in the inspector but does NOT change the actual playback queue, because the AppModel methods they call mutate only local Swift state and never call core.setQueue — unlike moveUpNext, which does.
  - _Why:_ Drag-reorder persists to the Rust core queue, but Shuffle and Remove do not. The UI updates so the user believes the change took effect, yet the next-track engine (driven by the core queue) still plays the old order / the 'removed' track. This is a silent data/state-desync bug exactly of the optimistic-UI-without-server-echo shape called out in CLAUDE.md gap pattern #5.
  - _Fix:_ Make shuffleUpNext() and removeFromUpNext(id:) rebuild allTracks and call core.setQueue the same way moveUpNext does (surfacing errors rather than `try?`), so the inspector's Shuffle/Remove actually re-sequence the playback queue.
- **L583** [gap-stub] Double-tapping a track in the 'Playing From' section does nothing functional — jumpTo(entry:) only pops a 'Jump to track coming soon' toast and never actually starts that track.
  - _Why:_ The auto-queue rows advertise an interaction (double-tap) that silently no-ops behind a 'coming soon' toast. A real implementation is trivially available: AppModel already exposes play(tracks:startIndex:) (AppModel.swift:3988) which calls core.setQueue + audio.play; jumpTo could compute the index of `entry` within [currentTrack] + upNextUserAdded + upNextAutoQueue and call it. Shipping a dead double-tap gesture is a user-facing gap, not a TODO.
  - _Fix:_ Implement jumpTo by building the full track list (current + upNextUserAdded + upNextAutoQueue), finding entry's index, and calling model.play(tracks:startIndex:). Remove the toast/JumpToTrackToast once wired, or keep it only as an error fallback.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/SearchInstantDropdown.swift`
- **L28** [dead-code] The entire SearchInstantDropdown view (all 577 lines, including TopResultHero, ArtistsRow, AlbumsGrid, TracksList, PlaylistsGrid, GenresRow and every sub-tile) is unreachable dead code. It is never instantiated anywhere in the repository.
  - _Why:_ A 577-line view plus its backing AppModel machinery (runInstantSearch, instantSearchResults, pickTopResult, InstantSearchResults, the searchTask debounce) is shipped but wired to nothing — it never renders. This is a large unreachable feature path: dead maintenance burden, and it gives a false impression that instant search-as-you-type is a live feature when no UI surfaces it. The instant-search code (debounce + core.search dispatch) consumes binary size and review attention for zero runtime effect.
  - _Fix:_ Either wire SearchInstantDropdown into the global search UI (an overlay/popover bound to the search field, the apparent intent given runInstantSearch/onChange plumbing), or delete the dead view + the now-orphaned AppModel.runInstantSearch / instantSearchResults / pickTopResult / InstantSearchResults if instant search was abandoned. Track the decision under an issue.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/ServerUnreachableBanner.swift`
- **L83** [accessibility] `.accessibilityElement(children: .combine)` flattens the whole banner — including the Retry Button — into a single static-text element, making the Retry action unreachable by VoiceOver.
  - _Why:_ Combining children collapses the interactive Button into the parent element and the parent is then marked `.isStaticText`. A VoiceOver user can read the warning but can no longer focus or activate Retry — the only recovery affordance on this banner becomes inaccessible. The per-Button `.accessibilityLabel("Retry server connection")` on line 72 is discarded by the combine.
  - _Fix:_ Drop `children: .combine` (and the `.isStaticText` trait) so the icon (already `accessibilityHidden`), the message Text, and the Retry Button each remain individual accessibility elements; or use `children: .contain` so the button stays actionable. Keep the Button as a separately focusable element with a button trait.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/Sidebar.swift`
- **L147** [bug] Footer status is hard-coded "Connected" and shows the loaded-page album count (`model.albums.count`), not the real total — it stays "Connected" even when the server is unreachable.
  - _Why:_ `model.albums` is the paged cache (one page of results), while the true total lives in `model.albumsTotal` (UInt32, used two rows up in `libRow(... count: model.albumsTotal ...)`). So a 20,060-album library reports e.g. "Connected · 100 albums". Worse, the string is unconditionally "Connected" while `serverReachability` is actively tracking failures elsewhere in AppModel — the footer green dot + label lie during an outage, contradicting the ServerUnreachableBanner this same app shows.
  - _Fix:_ Use `model.albumsTotal` for the count and gate the "Connected" label + green dot on actual reachability (e.g. a `serverReachability`-derived state or `model.session != nil` plus reachability), showing a disconnected state when unreachable. Localize the string while at it.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/StreamErrorToast.swift`
- **L118** [accessibility] accessibilityElement(children: .combine) + .isStaticText collapses the entire toast into a single non-interactive static-text element, making the Retry / Go to Track / Dismiss buttons completely unreachable by VoiceOver.
  - _Why:_ When .combine is applied to a container, child accessibility elements (the three buttons at lines 64/82/93, with their own labels at 80/90/100) are merged into the parent and lose their actions/traits. Adding .isStaticText explicitly marks the merged element as non-interactive. A VoiceOver user hears the error message but has no way to retry, navigate to the failing track, or dismiss the toast — the only recovery actions the component exists to offer. The per-button accessibilityLabels at lines 80/90/100 become dead code.
  - _Fix:_ Remove .accessibilityElement(children: .combine), .accessibilityLabel(message) (line 119), and .accessibilityAddTraits(.isStaticText) (line 120) from the container so the buttons remain individually focusable. If you want the message announced as a group, wrap only the Image+Text in their own combined element and leave the buttons as independent siblings (e.g. apply .combine to an inner HStack/VStack containing just lines 51-60).

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/TextFieldSpaceGuard.swift`
- **L64** [bug] Each guarded view installs its own app-global NSEvent local monitor; multiple text fields using spaceKeyGuardForTextField() simultaneously install multiple monitors that all fire on every keyDown anywhere in the app, and each independently inserts a space and consumes the event.
  - _Why:_ NSEvent.addLocalMonitorForEvents installs a process-wide monitor, not a per-view one. If two or more views apply this modifier (the call-site grep shows CommandPalette, SearchView, and others use space-guarded fields), N monitors are registered. On the relevant space keystroke the first monitor returns nil (consumes the event), but the cost is N closures invoked on EVERY keystroke in the app, and the design is fragile: ordering of monitor invocation is undefined, and a stale monitor whose host was removed without dismantle running (e.g. window torn down abnormally) keeps intercepting space app-wide. This is per-keystroke work scaling with the number of guarded fields plus a leak risk.
  - _Fix:_ Use a single shared/global monitor (install once, ref-counted) rather than one per host, or scope the interception to the specific NSWindow/field via the responder check before doing anything. At minimum ref-count installs so only one monitor exists regardless of how many guarded fields are mounted.
- **L114** [bug] On space in a text field the monitor swallows the native key event and synthesizes the character via responder.insertText(" "), which bypasses normal text-input handling: it breaks IME/marked-text composition, undo coalescing, and field-editor selection-replacement semantics.
  - _Why:_ Replacing a real keyDown with a programmatic insertText changes behavior: (1) during IME composition (CJK/dead keys) inserting a literal space mid-composition corrupts the marked range instead of committing it the way the standard space handling would; (2) NSText/NSTextView normally route space through interpretKeyEvents which handles selection replacement and undo grouping — calling insertText directly produces a separate undo entry per space and may not replace a non-empty selection identically; (3) responder here may be the NSTextField itself (line 99 branch), and NSTextField does respond to insertText but the field editor (NSTextView) is the correct target — inserting on the control vs the field editor can diverge. The guard's stated purpose (let space type a space in a field instead of triggering play/pause) can be achieved without consuming the event when the field is first responder.
  - _Fix:_ When the first responder is a text field, simply return the event unchanged (return event) so AppKit performs the normal insertion, rather than returning nil and re-synthesizing with insertText. The play/pause global shortcut should instead check for text-field first-responder and decline, or be registered as a key-equivalent that AppKit already suppresses while editing. If interception must stay, target the field editor (window.fieldEditor) and route through interpretKeyEvents([event]) instead of insertText.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/TrackRow.swift`
- **L179** [bug] The upArrow/downArrow key handlers unconditionally `return .handled`, swallowing the arrow keys even though moveFocus is a no-op (siblings always empty). This breaks the OS/SwiftUI default focus-ring traversal between rows.
  - _Why:_ `.handled` tells SwiftUI the event was consumed, suppressing the framework's built-in arrow-key focus movement. Because moveFocus does nothing (empty `siblings`, see line 216 finding), a keyboard/VoiceOver user who focuses a track row and presses up/down gets *no* movement at all — focus is trapped on the row. TrackListRow.swift:165-171 has the same shape but there moveFocus actually works; in TrackRow it produces a dead key-trap. Returning `.handled` only when focus actually moved would let SwiftUI fall back otherwise.
  - _Fix:_ Return `.ignored` when moveFocus cannot move (e.g. have moveFocus return a Bool and propagate it: `return moveFocus(by: -1) ? .handled : .ignored`), or remove the handlers until siblings are wired. This restores default focus traversal for keyboard/VoiceOver users.
- **L216** [dead-code] Arrow-key focus navigation in TrackRow is permanently dead: moveFocus depends on `siblings`/`siblingIndex`, which default to `[]`/`0` and are never supplied by ANY call site, so it always early-returns.
  - _Why:_ Tree-wide grep confirms the only references to `siblings:`/`siblingIndex:` are the property declarations themselves. The three real construction sites — AlbumDetailView.swift:384, PlaylistView.swift:357, and SearchView.swift:691 (SearchPageTrackRow) — pass only track/number/onPlay(/playlistScope). With `siblings` always empty, `moveFocus` never moves focus. The sibling component TrackListRow.swift:346 does the same thing correctly by reading `tracks[target]` from the full list passed to every row; TrackRow's design (per-row sibling slice) was never wired through, so the up/down feature is inert wherever TrackRow is used.
  - _Fix:_ Either thread the full track list + this row's index from the three call sites (mirror TrackListRow: `moveFocus` over `tracks`/`index`), or drop the `siblings`/`siblingIndex` params and the upArrow/downArrow handlers entirely. Do not leave handlers that claim to handle the key while doing nothing (see related line 179 finding).

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/LyrebirdApp.swift`
- **L251** [gap-stub] Two View-menu items "Show Sidebar" (⌘⌥S) and "Show Queue" (⌘⌥Q) have completely empty action bodies and are hard-disabled with .disabled(true). They ship as permanently greyed-out, non-functional menu commands.
  - _Why:_ A shipping app exposes two menu commands with reserved keyboard shortcuts (⌘⌥S, ⌘⌥Q) that do nothing and can never be enabled. They look like real features to users (and burn two shortcut slots), but are dead ends. The empty bodies plus disabled(true) are a classic stub that rotted in place. Note ⌘⌥Q duplicates nothing functional while a real queue toggle already exists (⌘U -> toggleFullQueue), so "Show Queue" is also misleading.
  - _Fix:_ Either wire these to the real AppModel toggles (a sidebar visibility binding and model.toggleFullQueue) and remove .disabled(true), or delete both Buttons entirely so the View menu doesn't advertise non-existent capabilities and free the ⌘⌥S/⌘⌥Q shortcuts.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/LyrebirdErrorPresenter.swift`
- **L77** [bug] HTTP 403/404/429 errors never map to error.forbidden / error.not_found / error.rate_limit because those branches are nested inside the `server returned an error:` gate, but the core never produces those statuses as a `Server` variant.
  - _Why:_ The presenter matches `error.localizedDescription` (which for the UniFFI flat error is `String(reflecting:self)`, e.g. `LyrebirdError.Forbidden(message: "forbidden: ...")`). But `core/src/client.rs::check_response` calls `LyrebirdError::from_status`, which maps 403->Forbidden, 404->NotFound, 429->RateLimit — dedicated variants whose reflected/Display string is `"forbidden: ..."` / `"not found: ..."` / `"rate limited (retry after ...)"`. None of those contain the substring `"server returned an error:"`, so they skip this gate entirely and fall through to line 114 (`context.fallbackKey ?? "error.other"`). Only an unclassified status reaches the `Server` variant. Result: a 403 shows a generic "Something went wrong" instead of a permission message, a 404 shows generic instead of not-found, and the three dedicated localized keys (error.forbidden/error.not_found/error.rate_limit) are dead code.
  - _Fix:_ Lift the 403/404/429 (and `forbidden`/`not found`/`rate limit`) checks OUT of the `server returned an error:` block so they match the dedicated Forbidden/NotFound/RateLimit variants directly. E.g. add top-level `if description.contains("forbidden") { return "error.forbidden" }`, `... contains("not found") -> error.not_found`, `... contains("rate limit") -> error.rate_limit` BEFORE/alongside the server-error block (mirroring how `not logged in` / `authentication ...` are matched at top level).

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/AlbumDetailView.swift`
- **L83** [bug] moreByArtist is never cleared when navigating to an album with a nil/empty artistId — the previous album's "More by artist" shelf persists and renders under the new album's header.
  - _Why:_ The @State `moreByArtist` is only reassigned inside the `if let artistId..., !artistId.isEmpty` guard and is never reset at task start (lines 67-92 reset isAboutExpanded/isLinerNotesDrawerPresented but not moreByArtist/tracks/detail/fetchedAlbum). When the user navigates from album A (with an artist) to album B that has no/empty artistId, the guard is skipped, so `moreByArtist` still holds album A's artist's albums. moreByArtistSection (line 733) then renders those stale tiles under the header "MORE BY <albumB.artistName>" (line 736 uses the NEW album's name), showing the wrong artist's albums attributed to the new artist. The `.id` filter at line 87 also still references `albumID` of the new album, leaving A's same-id album visible.
  - _Fix:_ Reset the stale album-scoped state at the start of the `.task(id: albumID)` closure before the awaits, and clear moreByArtist when the new album has no artist: e.g. `tracks = []; detail = AlbumDetail(...); moreByArtist = []; fetchedAlbum = nil` at task start, and add an `else { moreByArtist = [] }` to the artistId guard.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/ArtistDetailView.swift`
- **L398** [gap-stub] The 'Start instant mix' transport button is wired to the exact same action as the 'Start artist radio' button — both call model.startArtistRadio(artist:), which is just playInstantMix(seedId:). Two visually distinct buttons (different SF Symbols, different help/accessibility text 'Start artist radio' vs 'Start instant mix') perform byte-for-byte identical behavior.
  - _Why:_ The UI advertises two separate features (artist radio and instant mix are distinct Jellyfin concepts) but delivers one. A user toggling between them gets identical playback, which is a misleading/dead feature path. One of the two buttons is effectively a non-functional duplicate.
  - _Fix:_ Either wire the instant-mix button to a genuinely distinct core call (e.g. a true instant-mix vs a station/radio seed with different limit/seed semantics), or remove the duplicate button so the UI doesn't promise a capability it doesn't have. If they are intended to be the same, collapse to a single button.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/FullQueueView.swift`
- **L134** [bug] Tapping the 'Now Playing' row in the full queue destroys the entire queue, collapsing it to just the one track.
  - _Why:_ FullQueueTrackRow is a Button whose action is playFromHere. For the Now Playing row `queue` is hard-coded to `[track]`, so playFromHere calls model.play(tracks: [track], startIndex: 0), which calls core.setQueue(tracks: [track], startIndex: 0) (AppModel.swift:3990). setQueue replaces the whole queue, so a single misclick on the currently-playing track wipes the user's entire Up Next / auto-queue. There is no queue-preserving jump primitive, so tapping this row can only ever do harm.
  - _Fix:_ Make the Now Playing row non-tappable (render it without the Button, like an info row) or have its action restart/seek the current track via the existing transport instead of model.play. Alternatively pass the full reconstructed queue (currentTrack + upNextUserAdded + upNextAutoQueue) so a tap keeps the queue intact and just seeks to index 0.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/HomeView.swift`
- **L217** [dead-code] The entire Pinned Stations feature is dead: `quickTilesRow` (lines 217-243) and `pinnedStationsRow` (lines 283-316) are defined as computed views but are NEVER mounted in `body` (lines 24-65). The body enumerates every section explicitly (recentlyPlayedSection, artistsYouLoveSection, ... artistRadioRow) and neither row name appears. A repo-wide grep finds zero call sites for either property anywhere in macos/Sources.
  - _Why:_ GenreDetailView's 'Pin <genre> to Home' button calls `model.pinGenreToHome` (AppModel:5553) which writes the station into PinnedStationsStore, but nothing ever renders that store on the Home screen. The user pins a genre, sees a success-shaped no-op, and the pin is invisible forever. Issue #253 ('Pinned stations row') is CLOSED, so this is a shipped-then-dropped regression, not pending work. The whole quick-tiles grid (HomeQuickTile + placeholders) is likewise unreachable.
  - _Fix:_ Either mount `pinnedStationsRow` in `body` (e.g. after `header`) so pinned genres actually appear, or remove the pin-to-home write path, the `pinnedStationsRow`/`quickTilesRow`/`pinnedStations`/`pinnedStationSubtitle`/`handlePinAction`/`handleStationTap` members, the `@AppStorage` property, and disable GenreDetailView's Pin button. Do not ship a write path with no reader.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/LibraryView.swift`
- **L578** [bug] Infinite-scroll pagination stalls whenever a filter is active because the trigger index (filtered list) is compared against the unfiltered loaded count.
  - _Why:_ When filter.isActive, `items.count == filteredAlbums.count` which is < `model.albums.count`. `idx` only ranges over the filtered subset, so `idx` can never reach `loaded - 20`. The last rendered cell's onAppear never satisfies the guard, so loadMoreAlbums() is never called. The user scrolls to the bottom of a filtered list and pagination dead-ends, even though more matching items exist on later server pages. Same defect in triggerLoadMoreArtistsIfNeeded/Tracks/Playlists (lines 591, 605, 619).
  - _Fix:_ Compute the threshold against the displayed (filtered) collection length, not the raw model count: `let displayedCount = items.count` passed in, or trigger when `idx >= displayedCount - paginationTriggerDistance` while still gating on `model.X.count < total`. Better: when a filter is active and the filtered tail is reached but more raw items remain unloaded, keep paging until either enough matches are found or the dataset is exhausted.
- **L578** [bug] Infinite-scroll pagination stalls whenever a client-side library filter is active. The load-more trigger compares the index of the *filtered/sorted* row against the *loaded* count, but filtering shrinks the rendered list below `loaded`, so the threshold is never reached.
  - _Why:_ `idx` is an index into `sortedAlbums`/`items` (which is `model.albums` after `passesFilter`, line 784), but `threshold = loaded - 20` is computed against the raw loaded count `model.albums.count`. With any active filter, `items.count <= loaded`; if the filter removes more than 20 items, the largest `idx` (`items.count-1`) is < `loaded-20`, so `guard idx >= threshold` is never satisfied and `loadMoreAlbums()` never fires. A user who filters a 20k-album library (e.g. by genre/year) scrolls to the bottom of the filtered list and pagination dies — later server pages that would match the filter are never fetched, so the filtered results look incomplete. The same defect exists identically for artists (591), tracks (605), and playlists (619). It is additionally wrong under any non-server sort order (.nameDescending/.mostPlayed/.random/.year*) because the row at sorted-index `loaded-20` is an arbitrary item, not the 20th-from-last fetched item.
  - _Fix:_ Compute the threshold against the rendered collection length, and prefetch based on proximity to the end of `items`, not `model.albums`. Pass the rendered count in (or capture it): e.g. `let threshold = max(items.count - paginationTriggerDistance, 0); guard idx >= threshold else { return }`. Better: drive load-more off the visible window of the sorted/filtered array, and when a filter is active either page the server with the filter applied or keep fetching pages until either the server is exhausted or enough filtered matches exist. Do the same in triggerLoadMoreArtists/Tracks/PlaylistsIfNeeded.
- **L783** [gap-stub] Filtering is performed purely client-side over already-loaded pages, so filtered results are silently incomplete for libraries larger than the loaded window.
  - _Why:_ On the canonical ~20060-album / large-track library only the first page(s) are loaded, so e.g. 'FLAC only' or 'Genre = Jazz' filters the loaded slice, not the catalog. The user sees a handful of matches and reasonably concludes the library contains only those, when thousands more match on un-loaded pages. Combined with the pagination stall above (which prevents auto-loading more while filtering), the filtered view is misleading rather than merely partial.
  - _Fix:_ Push filter predicates to the Rust core / Jellyfin ItemsQuery (genre, year range, etc.) so the server returns the filtered, paginated set; or, at minimum, eagerly page through the full dataset while a filter is active and surface a 'searching N of M' affordance so the result is not silently truncated.
- **L852** [performance] `sortedAlbums`/`sortedArtists`/`sortedTracks`/`sortedPlaylists` are un-memoized computed properties that run a full filter + locale-aware sort over the entire loaded library on every render, and are evaluated up to 3x per render in the default name-ascending mode. On a ~20k-item library this is heavy MainActor work triggered on every hover.
  - _Why:_ `sortedAlbums` does `model.albums.filter(passesFilter).sorted { localizedCaseInsensitiveCompare }`. `localizedCaseInsensitiveCompare` is an expensive locale-aware comparison; on a library the size described in CLAUDE.md (~20,060 albums) an O(n log n) sort with that comparator is a multi-millisecond MainActor operation. In the default `.nameAscending` mode the albums tab evaluates it three times per render: `showAlphabetRail` (263 -> displayedSortNames -> sortedAlbums), `alphabetPresentBuckets` (268 -> displayedSortNames -> sortedAlbums), and `content` (431 -> items). Every hover over any card mutates `hoverID` @State and re-renders LibraryView, so this triple-sort runs on every mouse move across the grid — a classic beachball under the very interaction (hover) the grid is built around.
  - _Fix:_ Memoize the sorted/filtered result so it is computed once per (sortOrder, filter, source-array) change rather than per render: hold it in @State and recompute in `.onChange` of `sortOrder`, `filter`, and the relevant `model.albums`/`tracks`/... arrays, or move sorting off the MainActor into a Task and publish the result. At minimum, compute `let items = sorted...` once and reuse it for `displayedSortNames`/`displayedItemIds`/`content` instead of re-deriving each. Also avoid re-rendering the whole LibraryView on hover (the hoverID @State invalidates everything that reads the sorted arrays).
- **L871** [bug] `.random` sort is implemented as `.shuffled()` inside a computed property, so it re-shuffles on every view re-render. Because hovering any card mutates `hoverID` @State and re-renders the whole LibraryView, the grid visibly reorders on every hover/selection, and different call sites of `sortedTracks`/`sortedAlbums` in the same render get different orders.
  - _Why:_ A computed property is not memoized — SwiftUI re-evaluates `sortedAlbums`/`sortedTracks` on every body invalidation, and `.shuffled()` returns a new random permutation each time. `hoverID` is plain @State on LibraryView, written by every AlbumCard.onHover via the `libraryHoverID` binding (lines 175, 1274/1276), so simply moving the mouse over the grid re-renders LibraryView and re-shuffles the entire list — the cells animate to new positions on every hover. Within a single render, `sortedTracks` is computed independently for `selectedTracks` (288), `displayedItemIds` (252), and the rendered `items` (497), so in random mode the selection banner lists tracks in a different order than the grid, and any index-based logic keyed off one shuffle is inconsistent with another.
  - _Fix:_ Materialize the random order once and keep it stable until the user re-picks Random or the underlying collection changes. E.g. store a `@State private var shuffleSeed = UUID()` (reset in `onChange(of: sortOrder)` when it becomes `.random` and when the source array identity changes) and sort deterministically by `hash(id, seed)`, or cache the shuffled array in @State and only recompute on explicit triggers. Do not return `.shuffled()` directly from a computed property.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/OnboardingView.swift`
- **L503** [gap-stub] FirstSyncStep never triggers a real library sync; the progress bar is purely cosmetic theater driven by a hard-coded timer, and the 'Continue to Home' gate is satisfied by the fake animation regardless of whether any data actually loaded.
  - _Why:_ The screen presents itself as 'Loading your library' with a phase label ('Loading artists…') and a live counter, but it neither initiates nor waits on the actual sync. The real fetch is whatever login()/refreshLibrary() already kicked off; this view has no dependency on its result. If the server returns nothing or errors mid-sync, the user is still told sync is complete and dropped into an empty Home with no error surfaced. The displayed phase labels are decorative and unrelated to what the network layer is doing.
  - _Fix:_ Either drive isReady purely from real signals (e.g. require librarySyncRatio above a threshold AND model.errorMessage == nil), or have onAppear actually await model.refreshLibrary() and surface errors. At minimum, gate 'Continue to Home' on real data rather than the cosmetic timer so users aren't sent to an empty library.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/PlaylistDetailView.swift`
- **L337** [bug] handleRowClick force-indexes tracks[index] with no bounds check; the index is captured at render time and can be stale, crashing if the track array shrank.
  - _Why:_ `index` (idx) is captured by the ForEach row closure at render time (line 321). `tracks` is `model.currentPlaylistTracks`, which mutates from several async paths: a completed remove (removeFromPlaylist), the drop reload (loadPlaylistTracks), a reorder, or the undo flow — all on the MainActor but interleaving with the run loop that delivers the tap. There is a window where the gesture handler runs against a shorter array than the one that produced `idx`, so `tracks[index]` is out of bounds and traps (EXC_BAD_INSTRUCTION). Contrast line 349 which correctly guards with `tracks.indices.contains(i)`.
  - _Fix:_ Guard the access: `guard tracks.indices.contains(index) else { return }` (or use a safe subscript like `tracks[safe: index]`) at the top of handleRowClick before reading tracks[index].
- **L466** [bug] Drag-and-drop add never updates the visible track list: addToPlaylist does not populate the playlistTracks cache, and the follow-up loadPlaylistTracks returns the stale cache instead of refetching.
  - _Why:_ AppModel.addToPlaylist(playlistId:trackIds:) (AppModel.swift:3228-3282) only bumps `playlists[idx].trackCount`; it never appends to `currentPlaylistTracks` or `playlistTracks[playlistId]`. loadPlaylistTracks(playlistId:) (AppModel.swift:3040-3044) is cache-first: `if let cached = playlistTracks[playlistId] { currentPlaylistTracks = cached; return }`. Since the playlist is already loaded (we are viewing it), the cache is populated, so loadPlaylistTracks returns the OLD list and the dropped tracks never appear. Compounding it, addToPlaylist's server write runs in its own un-awaited Task, so the await on loadPlaylistTracks doesn't even sequence after the write. The user drops tracks, the header count increments, but the list does not change — the feature appears broken and won't reflect until the cache is invalidated (e.g. app relaunch).
  - _Fix:_ Invalidate the cache before reloading (e.g. add an AppModel API to clear playlistTracks[playlistId] then refetch), or have addToPlaylist append the added tracks to currentPlaylistTracks/playlistTracks optimistically. At minimum, force loadPlaylistTracks to bypass the cache after a mutation.
- **L603** [bug] Plain tap uses .simultaneousGesture instead of .gesture, so cmd/shift multi-select fires the selection handler AND the plain play+clear handler concurrently, defeating multiselect.
  - _Why:_ The two modifier-qualified .gesture()s are mutually exclusive with each other, but a .simultaneousGesture runs CONCURRENTLY with them — it does not participate in SwiftUI's gesture exclusivity/priority resolution. So a cmd-click fires onClick(.command) (toggle-add the id) AND onClick([]) at the same time; onClick([]) -> handleRowClick(modifiers: []) clears selectedTrackIds to [] and calls model.play (lines 354-359). The reference implementation in TrackListRow.swift:380 uses a plain .gesture(TapGesture().onEnded { onSelect([]) }) precisely so the modifier-held variants win and the plain tap only fires with no modifiers. This screen is the only file in the app using .simultaneousGesture for this pattern. Net effect: cmd/shift-click to build a selection immediately collapses the selection and starts playback, so the multi-select-then-Remove feature (the headline feature of this screen) cannot be used via the mouse.
  - _Fix:_ Replace .simultaneousGesture(TapGesture().onEnded { onClick([]) }) with .gesture(TapGesture().onEnded { onClick([]) }) to match TrackListRow's working pattern, so the modifier-qualified gestures take precedence when Cmd/Shift is held.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesAdvanced.swift`
- **L42** [consistency] hasCompletedOnboarding @AppStorage default is true here but false in every other declaration, so a fresh/never-written key disagrees across the app.
  - _Why:_ LyrebirdApp.swift:603 and OnboardingView.swift:25 both declare @AppStorage("hasCompletedOnboarding") with a default of false. @AppStorage uses the per-property default ONLY when the underlying UserDefaults key is absent. When the key has never been written (truly first launch, or after a defaults reset / migration), this view evaluates the flag as true while LyrebirdApp evaluates it as false. The help text and reset logic in this view (lines 144-147) then describe a state inconsistent with what the app actually shows, and a future read here could mask the fact that onboarding has not run.
  - _Fix:_ Make the default match the other two declarations (false) so the absent-key state is consistent everywhere: @AppStorage("hasCompletedOnboarding") private var hasCompletedOnboarding: Bool = false.
- **L207** [gap-stub] "Show Internal IDs" toggle is a dead-end: it persists advanced.showInternalIds but nothing reads that key, so the documented behavior (IDs shown in detail views) never happens.
  - _Why:_ rg across the whole macos source shows the only references to showInternalIds / "advanced.showInternalIds" are this file (declare + toggle + help) and DiagnosticBundle.swift:104 (which just enumerates the key for export). No detail view (AlbumDetailView, ArtistDetailView, PlaylistDetailView, GenreDetailView) reads advanced.showInternalIds or renders the Jellyfin item UUID — the only monospaced text in those views is .monospacedDigit() for runtimes/track numbers. So the toggle writes a UserDefaults value that no code consumes; the footnote and the on/off help strings (lines 214-216) promise a feature that does not exist. A user enabling it sees no IDs anywhere, a silent gap.
  - _Fix:_ Either wire the flag into the detail views (read UserDefaults.standard.bool(forKey: "advanced.showInternalIds") / @AppStorage in AlbumDetailView, ArtistDetailView, etc. and conditionally show item.id), or remove the section until the feature is implemented. Do not ship a persisted toggle whose advertised effect is a no-op.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesAppearance.swift`
- **L213** [gap-stub] Theme selection is a pure persistence stub: choosing any of the 5 swatches writes appearance.theme but the value is never consumed to change the live UI accent/colors.
  - _Why:_ The UI presents five tappable, selectable theme swatches with an active-ring affordance. Tapping Ocean/Forest/Sunset/Peanut changes nothing visible — the accent stays purple. That's a functional control that does nothing; users will think the app is broken.
  - _Fix:_ Drive the live Theme from AppearanceKeys.theme (read themeRaw where Theme.accent/primary are resolved, using ThemePreset(appearanceTheme:)), or, until the theme engine ships, present the swatches as visibly disabled/'coming soon' rather than as working selectors.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesAudio.swift`
- **L124** [gap-stub] Streaming Quality and Download Quality pickers are dead controls — the chosen PlaybackQuality is never read by the player or core, so every stream is hard-capped at 320kbps regardless of the setting.
  - _Why:_ A user who selects 'Low' to save bandwidth, or 'Lossless'/'Original' for quality, gets none of it — everything streams at the same hard-coded 320kbps cap. The pane presents these as functional audio controls; they silently do nothing. This is a user-facing correctness gap, not a TODO.
  - _Fix:_ Either wire streamingQuality/downloadQuality into the stream-URL builder (pass a computed MaxStreamingBitrate from the tier down through AudioEngine/core instead of the hard-coded 320000 / nil), or gate the controls behind a Capabilities flag until the plumbing lands so the UI doesn't claim a capability it lacks.
- **L225** [consistency] Two separate preference panes (Audio and Playback) both edit the SAME keys playback.streamingQuality / playback.downloadQuality, but with different tier sets — PreferencesAudio omits .automatic while PreferencesPlayback (QualityPicker) includes it. When the stored value is .automatic, the Audio pane's segmented picker has no matching segment.
  - _Why:_ Duplicated controls for one setting are confusing and drift-prone.
