Concretely: the default streamingQuality is .automatic; the first time a user opens the Audio pane the .segmented Picker is asked to select a value (.automatic) that is not in its tag set, producing an undefined/empty selection in the segmented control. Setting it in one pane silently overrides the other.
  - _Fix:_ Remove the duplicate Streaming/Download Quality controls from one of the two panes (keep a single source of truth), or include .automatic in the Audio pane's tiers so the picker can always represent the stored value. Decide which pane owns audio-quality and delete the other's copy.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesGeneral.swift`
- **L124** [bug] The persistent "Show in menu bar" setting is never restored at app launch — it is only applied when the user opens Settings → General. MenuBarController.setVisible(_:) (the persistent toggle) is called in exactly two places, both inside PreferencesGeneral: the toggle setter (line 52) and this onAppear (line 124). There is no scene/AppModel/App startup call site (confirmed by rg across the whole Swift tree: only PreferencesGeneral.swift calls setVisible). So a user who enabled the menu-bar icon in a prior session sees no icon after relaunching until they navigate to the General preferences pane.
  - _Why:_ The persisted @AppStorage("general.showInMenuBar") value silently fails to take effect on startup. The feature only works for the remainder of a session in which the user happens to open General settings. From the user's perspective the toggle 'forgets' its state across launches.
  - _Fix:_ Apply the persisted persistent-menu-bar visibility once at app startup (e.g. in LyrebirdApp scene setup or AppModel init): read UserDefaults.standard.bool(forKey: "general.showInMenuBar") and call MenuBarController.shared.setVisible(...) before any window appears, independent of whether the user opens Settings.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesLibrary.swift`
- **L297** [performance] cache.totalSize is read on the MainActor, performing synchronous disk I/O. refreshCacheSize() wraps the work in `Task { @MainActor in ... }` and then evaluates `cache.totalSize`. In Nuke, DataCache.totalSize calls contents(keys:[.fileSizeKey]) which does a synchronous FileManager.contentsOfDirectory enumeration plus a per-file resourceValues(forKeys:) stat (DataCache.swift lines 380-391, 429-433). The Nuke API doc on totalSize explicitly says: "Requires disk IO, avoid using from the main thread." The artwork cache limit is 256 MB of small images, so this enumerates potentially thousands of files on the main thread.
  - _Why:_ Runs on every Preferences/Library pane open (.task at line 226) and after every Clear Cache. A full directory scan + per-file stat of a populated 256 MB image cache blocks the main thread, hitching the UI exactly when the user opens settings.
  - _Fix:_ Compute totalSize off the main thread: `let bytes = await Task.detached { (Artwork.pipeline.configuration.dataCache as? DataCache)?.totalSize ?? 0 }.value`, then hop back to @MainActor only to assign cacheSizeLabel. Drop the @MainActor isolation from the size computation itself.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesPlayback.swift`
- **L93** [gap-stub] Streaming/Download Quality and Preferred Codec pickers do not affect playback. playback.streamingQuality, playback.downloadQuality, and playback.preferredCodec are written here but no code applies them to stream URL construction or transcoding requests. grep across macos/Sources and core/src shows the only readers are PreferencesAudio.swift (which re-displays the same keys) and DiagnosticBundle.swift:115/119/121. The Rust client (core/src/client.rs) has no streaming_quality/preferred_codec parameter (grep returns nothing).
  - _Why:_ Choosing 'Low 96 kbps' to save bandwidth, forcing 'Original' direct stream, or picking a codec all do nothing — the server's default is always used. Bandwidth-constrained users cannot actually constrain bandwidth, and the subtitles (lines 269-273, 335-339) make concrete promises the app never keeps.
  - _Fix:_ Thread these three settings into the Jellyfin stream/transcode request (DeviceProfile MaxStreamingBitrate, AudioCodec, container) in the Rust client and pass them from AppModel; until then, mark the controls disabled/coming-soon rather than presenting them as live.
- **L134** [gap-stub] "Gapless playback" toggle is non-functional. playback.gaplessEnabled is written here but no consumer reads it. AudioEngine.preloadNextTrack (AudioEngine.swift:609) is invoked unconditionally from AppModel.armNextTrackPreload (AppModel.swift:5772-5775) — gapless/preload behavior is always on regardless of this switch. grep for gaplessEnabled/gapless across macos/Sources and core/src finds only this write and DiagnosticBundle.swift:116.
  - _Why:_ The control claims to enable/disable gapless joins (footnote line 126, help lines 130-132) but toggling it changes nothing — gapless is permanently on. Users who want a clean gap between tracks cannot get one.
  - _Fix:_ Gate armNextTrackPreload()/the cross-item join logic on the gaplessEnabled UserDefaults value, or disable the toggle until the engine honors it.
- **L148** [gap-stub] Crossfade slider is non-functional. playback.crossfadeSeconds is persisted but never consumed: AudioEngine.swift has no crossfade implementation (grep crossfad across macos/Sources/LyrebirdAudio and core/src returns nothing except DiagnosticBundle.swift:114). The slider, its readout, and footnote (line 126) all present a working crossfade feature that does not exist.
  - _Why:_ Setting a crossfade duration of e.g. 6 seconds has zero audible effect; the AVQueuePlayer-based engine never overlaps tracks. The user is given a precise dB/seconds control over a feature that is entirely unimplemented.
  - _Fix:_ Implement crossfade in AudioEngine reading crossfadeSeconds, or hide/disable the Transitions->Crossfade control behind a capability flag until the engine supports overlapping playback.
- **L186** [gap-stub] "Stop after current track" toggle is completely non-functional. The setting writes playback.stopAfterCurrent to UserDefaults but nothing ever reads it: AppModel.handleTrackEnded() (AppModel.swift:5862) unconditionally calls core.skipNext() and plays the next track with no reference to stopAfterCurrent. The footnote (line 178) even promises behavior — "Stops automatically after the current track finishes. Resets to off the next time you start playback" — that no code implements (grep for stopAfterCurrent across macos/Sources and core/src shows only this view's write plus DiagnosticBundle.swift:120 dumping the key).
  - _Why:_ User flips a switch that the UI presents as live (with a confident footnote describing exact behavior) and playback does not stop. This is a silent dead control — worse than a disabled one, because the persisted 'on' state lies to the user every time they open Preferences.
  - _Fix:_ Either wire it: have handleTrackEnded() read UserDefaults.standard.bool(forKey: "playback.stopAfterCurrent"), and if true, stop playback instead of skipNext() and reset the key to false; or, until the playback engine honors it, disable the toggle behind a Capabilities flag like the Last.fm row in PreferencesScrobbling so it isn't presented as functional.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/SearchView.swift`
- **L326** [gap-stub] The "Playlists" search scope/chip and section are a permanently-empty, non-functional feature path. The core search backend never returns playlists and AppModel.bucketSearchResults hard-codes the playlists bucket to []; SearchView nonetheless exposes a Playlists chip (visibleScopes), includes .playlists in the All view (allScopes), and renders a Playlists section that always shows "No playlists matched this query."
  - _Why:_ Users can select the Playlists filter or scroll to the Playlists section in 'All' and will ALWAYS see an empty 'No playlists matched this query.' regardless of query. It advertises a capability the app cannot deliver, which reads as a broken search. Note: the empty-bucket source is in AppModel/core, but SearchView is what surfaces the dead chip/section to the user.
  - _Fix:_ Until core search returns playlists, drop .playlists from visibleScopes and from allScopes (gate it behind a capability flag the same way .genres is gated by supportsGenreActions). When core gains playlist search, populate the bucket in bucketSearchResults instead of hard-coding [] and re-enable the scope.
- **L370** [bug] Search results past index 30 in any section are permanently unreachable; 'Load more' becomes a dead no-op button. perSectionLocalCap (30) is smaller than the search page size (searchPagePageSize = 100 in AppModel), so when the server has no further pages (serverHasMore == false) the reveal count freezes at 30 even though the bucket holds up to 100 locally-loaded items.
  - _Why:_ A single search page returns up to 100 tracks/albums/artists. canLoadMore returns true (revealed 30 < loaded 100) so the button is shown, but handleLoadMore can never push revealed past perSectionLocalCap=30 once the server has no more pages. Up to 70 of 100 results are invisible and the button does nothing when tapped — a confusing user-facing dead end (verified by simulation: reveal sequence [10,20,30,30,30,...] for bucket=100, serverHasMore=false).
  - _Fix:_ Make the local cap at least the page size (e.g. perSectionLocalCap = max(searchPagePageSize, ...)) or drop the cap entirely and let reveal grow to bucketSize: in the non-server branch use next = min(current + revealStep, bucketSize) instead of clamping to 30. The cap must never be below what one page can deliver.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/DiagnosticBundle.swift`
- **L153** [security] Credential-leak in the diagnostic-bundle host redaction fallback: when URLComponents cannot parse the server URL (e.g. a scheme-less URL the user typed), the fallback splits userinfo on the FIRST '@' instead of the last, leaking part of an embedded password into manifest.json.
  - _Why:_ model.serverURL stores the raw string the user typed at login (AppModel.login: `self.serverURL = url`, no normalization in Swift). If a user enters userinfo without a scheme and the password contains an '@' (e.g. admin:p@ss@host), URLComponents(string:)?.host returns nil and this fallback runs. I verified with real Swift that redactServerHost("admin:p@ss@host.internal/x") returns "ss@host.internal" — part of the password ("ss") leaks into the diagnostic bundle that README.txt explicitly promises NEVER contains the password. The bundle is meant to be attached to public GitHub issues.
  - _Fix:_ Split userinfo on the LAST '@' (rest.lastIndex(of: "@")) so the whole user:pass segment is dropped, matching URLComponents semantics. Better: never hand-roll this — prepend a default scheme ("https://") before URLComponents if the first parse fails, and only fall back to "(not signed in)" if that still yields no host. The identical flaw exists in AboutInfo.connectedServerHost (line 115).

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/FullScreenChromeController.swift`
- **L174** [bug] Coordinator.detach() unconditionally resets the *app-global* NSApp.presentationOptions to [], so dismantling/closing one WindowGroup window clobbers a different window that is currently full-screen.
  - _Why:_ NSApp.presentationOptions is process-wide, but each window owns its own Coordinator. If window A is in full-screen (presentationOptions = [.autoHideToolbar, .autoHideMenuBar]) and window B is closed (SwiftUI calls dismantleNSView -> detach), B's detach forcibly sets presentationOptions = [], un-hiding A's toolbar/menu bar while A is still full-screen. The condition `!= []` does not protect against this — it specifically triggers the clobber whenever any other window left non-empty options set.
  - _Fix:_ Only reset presentationOptions in detach() if the detaching window was the one that set them (track ownership), or scope the reset to when this window is the key/main full-screen window. Safer: in detach() do not touch the global state at all unless `window?.styleMask.contains(.fullScreen)` is true for *this* window; otherwise leave NSApp.presentationOptions for whichever window currently owns full-screen.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/MoveToApplications.swift`
- **L214** [bug] Before copying, an existing app at destURL is unconditionally deleted (removeItem). If a DIFFERENT app/version with the same bundle name already lives in /Applications (e.g. a user-installed release while this is a translocated nightly), it is destroyed and replaced without confirmation. removeItem on a running app at the destination can also leave the destination in a half-deleted state.
  - _Why:_ Destination collision is treated as 'overwrite blindly'. If the existing /Applications/Lyrebird.app is currently running, deleting it mid-run is destructive and the copy may then fail, leaving the user with neither a working installed copy nor a clear error.
  - _Fix:_ Detect a pre-existing different/running app at the destination and either refuse with an explanatory alert or move it to Trash via NSWorkspace.recycle(_:) rather than hard-removeItem. Confirm before overwriting an existing app of a different version.
- **L216** [error-handling] The operation is described/named as a MOVE but is implemented as copy-then-(maybe)-delete. If copyItem succeeds but the subsequent relaunch fails (line 229 early-returns), the source is never deleted and the destination copy is left behind. The user ends up with two full copies of the app and no error surfaced to them — only a log line.
  - _Why:_ On relaunch failure the user silently keeps a stale copy in /Applications plus the original, with no UI feedback. Future launches from the temp location will re-prompt and re-copy, accreting copies. There is no rollback of the copy on relaunch failure.
  - _Fix:_ On relaunch-failure, either roll back by removing destURL, or surface an NSAlert telling the user the app was copied to /Applications and asking them to launch it manually. Do not leave a duplicate with only a log message.
- **L228** [bug] Relaunch uses createsNewApplicationInstance=true while the current (translocated/temp) instance is still running, then on success deletes the source and terminates. There is a window where two instances of the app run simultaneously, both potentially holding the same core mutex / writing the same UserDefaults / MMKV-backed state, which can corrupt persisted state or produce duplicate playback sessions.
  - _Why:_ The old instance is not terminated until after the new one has launched and the completion handler fires. During that overlap two app processes share the same on-disk preferences/state and the same Jellyfin session, risking last-writer-wins corruption of window state, scrobble gate, favorites cache, etc.
  - _Fix:_ Quit the current instance immediately after spawning the relaunch (or use a small helper/login-item to perform copy+relaunch after this process exits), so only one instance is ever live. At minimum, terminate before the new instance finishes its first state write rather than after it has fully launched.

### `macos/Sources/LyrebirdAudio/AudioEngine.swift`
- **L495** [bug] reportStopped() for the PREVIOUS track is called after self.player has already been replaced with the new player, so the previous track's stop is reported at position 0 (the new item's position) instead of where it actually stopped.
  - _Why:_ The Jellyfin /Sessions/Playing/Stopped report (and resume point / scrobble position) for the outgoing track is recorded with the wrong position (0). Resume points and last.fm-style scrobbles for the previous track are corrupted on every track change.
  - _Fix:_ Capture the previous player's position and call reportStopped() (or compute positionTicks from the OLD player) BEFORE reassigning self.player = newPlayer on line 475, or pass an explicit positionTicks captured from the old player into reportStopped().
- **L507** [concurrency] play() makes up to two blocking network round-trips plus a synchronous SQLite write on the @MainActor: reportStopped() (line 495) and reportStarted() (line 507) call core.reportPlaybackStopped/Started which do runtime.block_on(network) in Rust, and markTrackStarted (line 497) does a synchronous db.record_play. All run on the main thread after the await returns.
  - _Why:_ Every track change blocks the UI for the duration of two HTTP round-trips to the server plus a disk write. On a slow/lossy connection this is a multi-second beachball on each skip/next/end-of-track.
  - _Fix:_ Move reportStarted/reportStopped off the main thread via Task.detached (marshal nothing back), matching the resolvePlaybackSource pattern already used at line 263. markTrackStarted's DB write should likewise be detached or made fire-and-forget.
- **L609** [gap-stub] preloadNextTrack does real network work (playbackInfo) and builds/inserts a buffered AVPlayerItem into the queue, but the preloaded item is never actually played: every track transition goes through onTrackEnded -> AppModel.handleTrackEnded -> playCurrent -> audio.play(), and play() always constructs a brand-new AVQueuePlayer (line 470), discarding the queued preload.
  - _Why:_ The preload feature consumes bandwidth, CPU, and a network round-trip per track but delivers no gapless playback and no faster start — the work is thrown away. Worse, on natural end the queue briefly auto-advances and starts the preloaded item before play() replaces the player, risking a momentary double-audio/stutter.
  - _Fix:_ Either implement true gapless by having the end-of-track path advance to the preloaded item (player.advanceToNextItem and rewire reporting) instead of building a new player, or remove preloadNextTrack if gapless isn't intended. As written it is dead/ineffective work.
- **L752** [bug] Stall auto-retry cap (maxAutoRetries = 2) is defeated because every stall recovery resets stallRetryCount to 0, so playback can retry-loop indefinitely instead of surfacing "Couldn't play, tap to retry."
  - _Why:_ replaceCurrentItem swaps the AVPlayerItem, which triggers the \.currentItem KVO with old != new, unconditionally zeroing stallRetryCount after each recovery. So when handleStallTimeout next runs, the counter is always 0->1 and never exceeds maxAutoRetries. On a persistent server/network problem the engine retries forever (and re-fires audioEngineDidStall each time) instead of giving up and showing the tap-to-retry failure, draining battery/bandwidth and never reaching a terminal UI state.
  - _Fix:_ Only reset stallRetryCount when the current item changes due to a genuine track advance, not due to in-place stall recovery. Either set a flag (e.g. isRecoveringFromStall) around replaceCurrentItem and skip the reset in the currentItem observer while it's set, or stop relying on the currentItem observer for the reset and reset stallRetryCount explicitly in play()/onTrackEnded only.
- **L974** [gap-stub] When stall retries are exhausted, handleStallTimeout reports failure to the delegate but leaves the player wedged: it does not pause the player, does not set core state to paused/ended, and does not clear the AVPlayer that is stuck in .waitingToPlayAtSpecifiedRate.
  - _Why:_ The app remains in a phantom 'playing' state forever after a hard stall — Now Playing rate stays 1.0, transport UI shows playing, but no audio advances and no further recovery occurs without manual user intervention. Core state and AVPlayer disagree with reality.
  - _Fix:_ On the give-up branch, call player.pause(), core.markState(state: .paused) (or .ended), cancelStallWatchdog(), and stop the heartbeat so the UI and server reflect the failed state.

### `macos/Sources/LyrebirdAudio/MediaSession.swift`
- **L162** [bug] Stale artwork persists in Now Playing when the new track has no artwork. trackChanged() seeds the new info dict with the *previous* track's artwork as a placeholder, and loadArtwork() returns early without ever clearing it when the new track has no imageTag or no resolvable URL.
  - _Why:_ For a track that legitimately has no cover (imageTag == nil) or whose URL fails to resolve, Control Center / the lock-screen / media widget will keep displaying the *previous* track's album art indefinitely. The carry-over is only ever corrected when artwork successfully loads for the new track; in the no-artwork path it is never corrected, so users see the wrong cover for the currently-playing song.
  - _Fix:_ In the early-return branch of loadArtwork (the else at lines 513-519), if currentTrackID == expectedTrackID, remove the artwork key from the Now Playing info (e.g. publish info with info.removeValue(forKey: MPMediaItemPropertyArtwork)). Alternatively, only carry over the previous art when the new track actually has an imageTag, so a no-art track starts blank.

### `macos/Sources/LyrebirdAudio/ReplayGain.swift`
- **L207** [bug] iTunNorm channel selection picks the QUIETER channel's correction, under-attenuating loud tracks (clipping / inconsistent leveling).
  - _Why:_ iTunNorm fields encode per-channel measured loudness where a LARGER raw value means a LOUDER channel and therefore a MORE NEGATIVE dB correction (leftDb = -10*log10(left/1000)). Conservative normalization must attenuate by the loudest channel = the most negative dB. Selecting `abs(...) <= abs(...)` chooses the value CLOSEST to 0 dB, i.e. the quieter channel. Worked example L=0x1000(4096)/R=0x2000(8192): code returns -6.12 dB but the louder right channel needs -9.13 dB, leaving the track ~3 dB too hot. For tracks whose only loudness tag is iTunNorm (gains.iTunNormDb feeds both .track and .album modes via replayGainDb), playback is louder than intended and can clip after preGainDb is added, defeating the whole purpose of the normalization feature.
  - _Fix:_ Pick the louder channel = the more-negative correction: `let chosen = min(leftDb, rightDb)`. (Both are <= 0 for values >= 1000; min() yields the larger attenuation. Keep the existing isFinite guard and ±maxAbsGainDb clamp.)

## P2 (214)

### `core/src/client.rs`
- **L206** [security] auth_header sanitizes device_name (strips control chars, length-caps) but interpolates device_id raw into the same MediaBrowser Authorization header without sanitization.
  - _Why:_ device_id is interpolated inside quotes with no filtering. Today it is a server-generated UUIDv4 (lib.rs:110) so not attacker-controlled, and HeaderValue::from_str (line 217) rejects control chars/CRLF, so header injection is blocked. But a device_id containing a double-quote would produce a malformed-but-accepted header value (quotes are not control chars), and the asymmetry shows the sanitization invariant the code intends was only half-applied. If device_id ever becomes user-settable this is an injection/spoofing vector.
  - _Fix:_ Run device_id through sanitize_header_field (or a stricter UUID/charset check) just like device_name before interpolation, so both header fields share the same hardening.
- **L311** [bug] backoff_for derives its jitter from SystemTime subsec_nanos, which is not a real RNG; concurrent retries firing in the same sub-millisecond window receive correlated/identical jitter, defeating the purpose of jitter (thundering-herd) and making backoff non-monotonic.
  - _Why:_ subsec_nanos resolution varies by platform and many requests retrying together (after a shared 429/503) will sample near-identical nanos, producing near-identical jitter and synchronized retries — the exact herd the jitter is meant to break up. SystemTime is also non-monotonic (NTP steps) so the seed can jump. Functionally low-impact (MAX_ATTEMPTS=3, capped delays) but the jitter is effectively decorative.
  - _Fix:_ Use a real PRNG (e.g. rand::thread_rng().gen_range(0.85..1.15)) seeded independently per call, or a per-client atomic counter mixed into the seed, so concurrent retries decorrelate.
- **L740** [consistency] latest_albums returns total_count = number of items in the fetched window (capped at offset+limit), not the library's true total record count, diverging from every other paginated method which returns total_record_count.
  - _Why:_ Callers that drive pagination/infinite-scroll off total_count (as they do for albums/artists/tracks which return total_record_count) will get a value that never exceeds offset+limit, so it can never signal 'more pages exist' correctly and will under-report the total. The /Items/Latest endpoint returns a bare array with no total, so this is a design limitation, but the asymmetric contract is a footgun. (Confirmed intended by tests.rs:1845, but still inconsistent.)
  - _Fix:_ Either document/return total_count as Option/None for latest_albums, or have callers special-case the Latest endpoint; do not let UI treat its total_count like the server-authoritative total_record_count used elsewhere.
- **L740** [bug] latest_albums reports a truncated total_count that can never exceed offset+limit, breaking any 'has more pages' pagination logic.
  - _Why:_ The server is asked for at most offset+limit items, then total_count is set to the number actually returned. So total_count is capped at offset+limit and never represents the true number of latest albums available. A caller that paginates with the usual `loaded >= total_count` test will stop early or compute the wrong page count, because total_count grows in lockstep with what was already fetched rather than reflecting the catalog. The /Items/Latest endpoint also returns a bare JSON array with no TotalRecordCount, so there is no correct total available from this endpoint at all.
  - _Fix:_ Either document/return total_count as 'unknown' (e.g. u32::MAX or items.len() only when offset==0 and fewer than limit came back), or have callers of the Latest shelf treat it as a fixed non-paginated set. If real pagination of 'latest' is needed, switch to the /Items endpoint with SortBy=DateCreated which returns TotalRecordCount.
- **L913** [performance] playlists_containing_artist issues up to 200 sequential HTTP round-trips (one probe per playlist), each blocking the FFI runtime and serialized through the core mutex.
  - _Why:_ For a server with many playlists this loops up to 200 times, each iteration performing a full Items request that returns up to 500 tracks (PLAYLIST_TRACK_PROBE_LIMIT). The calls are strictly sequential (await in a for loop), and because every core FFI call serializes through the parking_lot::Mutex guarding Inner, this one call can hold the lock for hundreds of network RTTs, beachballing every other core operation behind it. On the 78-playlist test server that's ~78 round-trips per artist-detail open.
  - _Fix:_ Reduce per-playlist cost (see the Limit=1 artist-filter fix), run the probes concurrently with a bounded join_all / FuturesUnordered, and/or short-circuit using cheaper signals. Cap concurrency to avoid hammering the server, but do not block the lock for the full sequential chain.
- **L949** [bug] playlist_features_artist only inspects the first 500 tracks of a playlist, so 'playlists containing artist' yields false negatives for large playlists where the artist appears only past position 500.
  - _Why:_ The probe fetches a single page of up to 500 tracks starting at index 0 and never pages further. A playlist with more than 500 tracks whose only appearance of the target artist is beyond the 500th track will be incorrectly reported as not containing the artist, so it will be silently omitted from playlists_containing_artist results. There is no server-side artist filter on this query (it lists all audio under the playlist), so correctness depends entirely on the probe window covering the whole playlist.
  - _Fix:_ Add a server-side filter so the membership check does not depend on a probe window: query the playlist's Items with ArtistIds/AlbumArtistIds set to artist_id and Limit=1, and treat a non-empty result as a match. That is O(1) per playlist and exact regardless of playlist length.
- **L1993** [gap-stub] create_playlist accepts a `position: Option<u32>` parameter and serializes it as a `StartIndex` query param on POST /Playlists, but the Jellyfin endpoint ignores it — the parameter is silently dropped on the server, so callers passing a position get no effect.
  - _Why:_ Verified against jellyfin/Jellyfin.Api/Controllers/PlaylistsController.cs:77-82 (CreatePlaylist): its only parameters are name/ids/userId/mediaType (all [FromQuery, ParameterObsolete]) plus a CreatePlaylistDto body. There is no `startIndex` parameter on the create route — `startIndex` only exists on the GET items route (PlaylistsController.cs:513). The `position` argument is therefore a dead parameter: the API signature implies callers can choose insertion position at creation, but the server never honors it, producing a silent behavioral gap (e.g. a 'create playlist starting at track N' UI affordance would appear to work but wouldn't).
  - _Fix:_ Either remove the `position` parameter (and the StartIndex append) since it has no server-side effect, or, if positional insert is actually wanted, create the playlist first then issue a separate POST /Playlists/{id}/Items with the proper insert semantics once the core gains that primitive (cf. the deferred #282 insert_next/append_to_queue work). At minimum, drop the misleading StartIndex append at lines 2004-2007.
- **L2014** [error-handling] create_playlist (a non-idempotent POST) is sent through send_with_retry, which retries up to MAX_ATTEMPTS on transport timeouts/connect errors. If the first POST reaches the server and creates the playlist but the response is lost to a timeout, the retry creates a duplicate playlist.
  - _Why:_ POST /Playlists is not idempotent — there is no client-supplied idempotency key and the server assigns a fresh playlist Id per call. The retry path treats it identically to idempotent GETs and to idempotent state-sets (set_favorite/mark_played, which are safe to repeat). On a flaky network where the request commits server-side but the response times out, the user silently ends up with two identical playlists. Severity is p2 (recoverable data-quality issue, not data loss), but it is a real and reproducible duplicate-creation bug on timeouts.
  - _Fix:_ Do not blanket-retry non-idempotent mutations on transport timeout. Options: (a) send create_playlist via send_with_retry_raw with a build closure that only retries on connect-before-send errors, not post-send timeouts; (b) skip transport-error retries for POSTs that create resources; or (c) generate a client idempotency token and have the core de-dupe. The same hazard applies in lesser degree to report_playback_started (duplicate 'Playing' events), but create_playlist is the one with user-visible duplicate state.

### `core/src/error.rs`
- **L23** [consistency] The flattened Display strings of LyrebirdError are an implicit, undocumented cross-FFI contract that the Swift presenter parses by substring. Because of `#[uniffi(flat_error)]`, LyrebirdErrorPresenter.swift routes errors via `error.localizedDescription.lowercased().contains(...)` against these exact strings. The RateLimit Display ("rate limited (retry after ...)") does NOT contain the substring "server returned an error:", yet the presenter only checks for "rate limit" INSIDE its `if contains("server returned an error:")` block — so a 429 RateLimit error never matches the rate-limit key and falls through to a generic fallback.
  - _Why:_ String-shape coupling between the Rust Display impls and a Swift substring parser is brittle and already broken for RateLimit: the user gets a generic error instead of the rate-limit guidance. Any future edit to these `#[error(...)]` strings can silently break Swift error routing with no compile-time signal.
  - _Fix:_ Stop flattening the error (drop `#[uniffi(flat_error)]`) so Swift can match on typed cases instead of parsing strings; or, if flat_error must stay, document the Display strings as a stable contract and add round-trip tests. Short-term, ensure RateLimit's Display contains a token the presenter matches at top level, or fix the presenter to check "rate limit" outside the "server returned an error:" block.
- **L111** [dead-code] `user_message()` and `is_retryable()` have zero non-test callers in the entire core, and they are not reachable across the FFI boundary: the enum is `#[uniffi(flat_error)]`, so Swift receives only flat `case X(message: String)` values and cannot call these methods. Production retry decisions use client.rs `is_retriable_status` (on the raw StatusCode), and production user messages come from the Swift-side LyrebirdErrorPresenter, not from `user_message`.
  - _Why:_ These two methods look like they govern retry policy and user messaging, but they are inert. That makes the inconsistencies above latent traps (they bite the moment someone assumes user_message/is_retryable are the source of truth and wires them in) and means the careful per-variant logic here is untested in production and silently duplicated/contradicted by the Swift presenter and client.rs.
  - _Fix:_ Either delete user_message/is_retryable (and rely on client.rs + the Swift presenter), or make them the single source of truth: have client.rs's retry loop call is_retryable, and surface user_message across the FFI via a dedicated exported function (since flat_error precludes method access on the Swift enum). Document which layer owns error->message mapping.
- **L118** [bug] `user_message()` lumps `InvalidCredentials` together with session-expiry variants and returns "Your session expired. Please sign in again." But `InvalidCredentials` is raised at LOGIN time (core/src/lib.rs:173 on empty username, lib.rs:233 on empty stored username during restore), not on an expired session. Telling a user who left the username field blank that their "session expired" is incorrect and ignores the dedicated Display message ("invalid credentials: username and password must not be empty").
  - _Why:_ Misleading guidance. A first-time login with an empty field has no session to expire; the correct prompt is "enter a username and password". The enum already carries an accurate Display for this case that user_message throws away.
  - _Fix:_ Give InvalidCredentials its own arm returning e.g. "Please enter your username and password." Keep Auth/AuthExpired/NotAuthenticated/NoSession on the session-expired message.
- **L138** [gap-stub] `SelfSignedCertificate` was split out from `Network` specifically so the UI could offer a "Trust this server" affordance (and carries a structured `host` field), but `user_message()` collapses it to the exact same generic string as `Network` ("Couldn't reach the server. Check your connection and try again."), and the `host` is dropped. Combined with `#[uniffi(flat_error)]` (Swift gets only `SelfSignedCertificate(message: String)`) and the Swift presenter (LyrebirdErrorPresenter.swift) having NO branch matching "certificate"/"self-signed", the cert case is indistinguishable from a generic network failure end-to-end.
  - _Why:_ The whole point of the dedicated variant + host field (to prompt the user to trust a self-signed server) is defeated: the user just sees a generic connectivity error with no path forward, so a self-signed-cert server is effectively unreachable with no actionable message.
  - _Fix:_ Return a cert-specific message that names the host and hints at the trust action, e.g. format!("The server at {host} uses a certificate that couldn't be verified. You may need to trust it."). Also ensure the Swift presenter has a branch keyed on the cert message (or expose the variant non-flat) so the UI can route to a trust prompt.

### `core/src/lib.rs`
- **L953** [error-handling] record_play failure is silently swallowed with `let _ =`.
  - _Why:_ record_play returns Result<()> and can fail (DB locked, disk full, corruption). Swallowing it means local play history silently stops recording with no log line and no surfaced error. This is the exact 'swallowed try? / let _ =' anti-pattern the audit targets; other best-effort failures in this file at least emit tracing::warn! (e.g. lines 295, 312).
  - _Fix:_ At minimum log on failure: `if let Err(e) = self.inner.lock().db.record_play(&track.id, now) { tracing::warn!(error=%e, "record_play failed"); }`.
- **L953** [resource-leak] play_history table grows without bound and its only reader (Database::play_count) has no production caller — record_play appends one row per track start forever.
  - _Why:_ Every track the user ever plays adds a permanent row (no LIMIT, no pruning trigger; migration 001 just creates the table + two indexes). For a heavy listener over months this is unbounded local-DB growth feeding a column that production code never reads, so it is pure write amplification with no payoff. Either it is dead instrumentation that should be removed, or a feature (play-count / frequently-played-local) that was never wired up.
  - _Fix:_ Either (a) remove record_play / play_count and the mark_track_started DB write if local play history is unused (the server already tracks PlayCount via /Sessions/Playing*, per CLAUDE.md 'Resolved'), or (b) if it is meant to be used, add a retention cap (e.g. prune rows older than N days or keep last K per track) and wire play_count into a UI path.
- **L953** [dead-code] mark_track_started writes to the play_history table on every track load, but nothing ever reads that data — it is write-only dead storage that costs a synchronous SQLite INSERT plus an `inner` mutex acquisition on the (main-thread) load path for zero benefit.
  - _Why:_ record_play is the only writer of play_history (storage.rs:156). The only reader, Database::play_count (storage.rs:164), has zero non-test callers anywhere in core/ or macos/ (verified with rg), and frequently_played_tracks (client.rs:1490) is a SERVER call that ignores the local table. So every track load performs an unread DB write + takes the global Inner mutex on the main actor (AudioEngine.load calls this synchronously at AudioEngine.swift:497). Pure overhead with no consumer.
  - _Fix:_ Either delete record_play/play_history entirely (and this line), or actually consume play_count for a local 'frequently played' / recently-played fallback. If kept, move the write off the load path (it currently runs on the MainActor before AVPlayer.play()).
- **L953** [consistency] A 'play' is recorded on every track LOAD, not at a listen threshold, so quick-skipped tracks each get a play_history row. Combined with the fact that mark_track_started fires from AudioEngine.load for every transition, local play counts would be wildly inflated relative to the server's threshold-based PlayCount.
  - _Why:_ Jellyfin only increments PlayCount after the scrobble/played threshold (scrobble.rs:56 scrobble_threshold_reached is 4 min or 50%). Recording a local play the instant a track is loaded means skipping through 30 tracks records 30 plays. If play_history is ever surfaced (see the dead-code finding) it will disagree with server PlayCount and with the user's intuition of what they 'listened to'.
  - _Fix:_ Record the play only once the scrobble threshold is reached (mirror scrobble_threshold_reached), or on a genuine 'played' signal — not on load. Today the cleanest fix is to remove it (see dead-code finding).
- **L1144** [security] ListenBrainz scrobble token is persisted in plaintext SQLite (settings table) instead of the OS keyring used for the Jellyfin access token.
  - _Why:_ The ListenBrainz token is a bearer credential (it authorizes submitting listens / playing-now on the user's behalf). Storing it in the plaintext lyrebird.db under Application Support, while the Jellyfin token deliberately uses the macOS keychain, is an inconsistent and weaker security posture for a secret of comparable sensitivity. Anyone with read access to the DB file (backups, sync, other processes) can exfiltrate it.
  - _Fix:_ Store the scrobble token via CredentialStore (keyring) the same way the Jellyfin token is stored, keeping only a non-secret 'configured' flag in settings if a quick is_scrobble_configured check is desired.
- **L1144** [security] The ListenBrainz scrobble token (a user credential) is persisted in plaintext in the SQLite settings table via db.set_setting, whereas the Jellyfin access token goes to the OS keyring via CredentialStore. The scrobble token sits unencrypted in lyrebird.db on disk.
  - _Why:_ set_setting (storage.rs:70) does a plain INSERT of the value with no encryption. The Jellyfin token is deliberately stored in the keyring (login() at lib.rs:190 via CredentialStore::save_token). The ListenBrainz token grants write access to the user's listen history; storing it plaintext in a world-readable-by-the-user db file (and any backup/Time Machine copy) is inconsistent with the keyring treatment of the other credential and leaks it to anyone with file access.
  - _Fix:_ Store the scrobble token via CredentialStore/keyring like the Jellyfin token, not db.set_setting. is_scrobble_configured / scrobble_token (lib.rs:1153/1351) should read from the same secure store.
- **L1235** [bug] The heartbeat loop reports an ended track as still actively playing. It only `continue`s when current_track is None; when state == Ended/Stopped but current_track is still Some, it keeps POSTing /Sessions/Playing/Progress every 5s with is_paused=false, so the server (and every other Jellyfin client's Now Playing) shows a ghost 'now playing' frozen at the final position indefinitely.
  - _Why:_ On natural queue-end with autoplay off, AppModel.handleTrackEnded (AppModel.swift:5862) does: core.markState(.ended) was already set (AudioEngine.swift:902), skipNext() returns nil, autoplayWhenQueueEnds is false -> it `return`s WITHOUT calling audio.stop()/core.stopHeartbeat() and WITHOUT reportStopped(). current_track is never cleared, so the heartbeat task (still alive from the last load) keeps firing. Because state==Ended != Paused, it reports is_paused=false — i.e. tells the server the track is playing forever. The session never transitions to stopped.
  - _Fix:_ In the heartbeat loop, skip/break when state is Ended or Stopped: `if matches!(status.state, PlaybackState::Ended | PlaybackState::Stopped | PlaybackState::Idle) { continue; }`. Independently, handleTrackEnded should call audio.stop() on the dry-queue/no-autoplay branch so reportStopped() and stop_heartbeat() actually run.

### `core/src/player.rs`
- **L255** [error-handling] insert_next() silently drops the passed tracks when the queue is empty (no current track), returning the unchanged length with no error or signal to the caller.
  - _Why:_ This is reachable from the UI: TrackContextMenu/AlbumContextMenu/PlaylistContextMenu 'Play Next' -> AppModel.playNext -> core.playNext -> Player::insert_next. If a user hits 'Play Next' before anything is queued (empty player), the tracks vanish with no playback and no feedback — a confusing silent-failure. The return value is u32 (unchanged length) which the Swift side cannot distinguish from a successful insert into an already-1-length queue. Test insert_next_on_empty_queue_is_noop (line 561) enshrines the drop as intended behavior, but from a product standpoint 'Play Next' on an empty queue should start playing, not no-op.
  - _Fix:_ When s.queue.is_empty() and tracks is non-empty, treat insert_next like a fresh play: set queue = tracks, queue_index = 0, current = tracks[0] (mirroring set_queue). Or change the contract so the caller (AppModel.playNext) falls back to play() on an empty queue, and return a sentinel/Result so the drop is observable.
- **L272** [bug] append_to_queue() extends the queue but does not set current when the queue was previously empty, leaving current=None while queue is non-empty; skip_next from this state cannot reach the appended tracks.
  - _Why:_ Reachable via 'Add to Queue' (TrackContextMenu.swift:58 etc -> AppModel -> core.addToQueue -> append_to_queue). If invoked on an empty player, the tracks are appended but current stays None and queue_index stays 0; status().currentTrack is nil so the UI shows nothing playing, and the only way to start them is an external set_current/set_queue. The matching test append_to_queue_on_empty_queue_just_extends (line 592) asserts current stays None, codifying that 'Add to Queue' on an empty queue produces an inert, hidden queue with no playable entry point.
  - _Fix:_ When the queue was empty before the extend, set queue_index = 0 and current = first appended track so the queue is actually playable, or have the AppModel layer fall back to play() when status.currentTrack == nil.
- **L387** [test-gap] No test asserts the PlayerStatus fields `duration_seconds`, `position_seconds`, `volume`, `state`, or `play_session_id` (verified: zero `status.<field>` assertions for these across lines 360-817). The `snapshot()` duration computation (line 97-101: maps current track through `Track::duration_seconds`, defaults to 0.0 when no current) and the field plumbing for these five PlayerStatus members are entirely unverified.
  - _Why:_ duration_seconds is the value the now-playing UI uses for the scrubber length; if the ticks->seconds divisor (10_000_000) or the None-default ever breaks, the seekbar shows wrong/zero duration with no test failure. state and play_session_id are core to playback reporting (Sessions/Playing) and likewise unguarded at the snapshot boundary.
  - _Fix:_ Extend an existing set_queue test to assert `status.duration_seconds == 180.0` for the track() helper and `== 0.0` on an empty player; add assertions for status.state after set_current/mark_state/clear, status.volume after set_volume, status.position_seconds after mark_position, and status.play_session_id after set_play_session_id.
- **L762** [test-gap] Test `peek_next_matches_skip_next_across_repeated_calls` never calls `skip_next` at all. Despite its name asserting peek/skip agreement, the body only checks that two consecutive `peek_next()` calls are idempotent and that `queue_position` does not advance. The actual peek-vs-skip consistency contract (peek_next predicts what the next skip_next will yield) is never exercised.
  - _Why:_ peek_next exists to pre-load the track skip_next will advance to. If peek_next and skip_next ever diverge (e.g. an off-by-one in one but not the other, or a RepeatMode::All wrap mismatch), no test catches it — this is the one test whose name promises that coverage but does not deliver it.
  - _Fix:_ In the test, capture `let peeked = player.peek_next().unwrap().id;` then `assert_eq!(peeked, player.skip_next().unwrap().id);` and repeat across the queue including the RepeatMode::All wrap boundary (set_queue at last index + RepeatMode::All) where divergence is most likely.

### `core/src/query.rs`
- **L293** [bug] sort_by and sort_order are emitted as two independent CSV lists with no length pairing/validation; a mismatch yields silently wrong sort direction
  - _Why:_ Jellyfin pairs SortBy[i] with SortOrder[i] positionally and falls back to a default (Ascending) for any unpaired sort field. The builder exposes independent `sort_by(Vec)` and `sort_order(Vec)` setters (lines 101-110) with no zip or length check, so a caller doing `.sort_by(vec![A, B]).sort_order(vec![Descending])` gets B sorted Ascending without any error. The result is a silently incorrect ordering rather than a detectable failure.
  - _Fix:_ Either validate at apply()/execute() time that sort_order.len() is 0, 1, or equal to sort_by.len() (returning LyrebirdError::InvalidInput otherwise), or model sorts as a single Vec<(ItemSortBy, SortOrder)> so the two lists cannot drift out of sync. The `sort(column, order)` convenience (line 114) is already safe; the danger is only the plural setters.

### `core/src/scrobble.rs`
- **L95** [validation] track_metadata submits artist_name and track_name without validating they are non-empty; ListenBrainz rejects listens missing either field
  - _Why:_ Track.name and Track.artist_name are plain `String` (core/src/models.rs:60-61, 45) and can legitimately be empty (e.g. an item with a missing Name, or a track whose AlbumArtist/Artists projection came back blank). ListenBrainz's submit-listens API requires non-empty artist_name and track_name and returns a 4xx for empty values. With no client-side guard, every such submit fails server-side (now reported as a generic Server error per the finding above), wasting a network round-trip and surfacing a confusing error instead of being skipped.
  - _Fix:_ Guard at the payload/submit boundary: if track.name.trim().is_empty() || track.artist_name.trim().is_empty(), return early with LyrebirdError::InvalidInput("track missing name/artist for scrobble") (or silently skip in the caller) instead of POSTing a payload the server will reject.

### `core/src/storage.rs`
- **L46** [error-handling] migrate() reads the current schema version with .unwrap_or(0) on the COALESCE(MAX(version)) query. If that read fails transiently (e.g. DB momentarily locked) on an already-migrated DB, current becomes 0, the code re-enters the 'current < 1' branch and runs INSERT INTO schema_version (version) VALUES (1) — which then fails with a PRIMARY KEY/UNIQUE violation (version is INTEGER PRIMARY KEY) and propagates via '?', aborting migrate() and thus Database::open().
  - _Why:_ A swallowed read error is converted into a hard, non-recoverable open failure on a perfectly valid existing database. Because Database::open is on the startup path (lib.rs:105), this can turn a transient hiccup into 'app won't launch'. The data is migrated correctly behind the duplicate-key error, so failing open is the wrong outcome.
  - _Fix:_ Propagate the version-read error with '?' instead of .unwrap_or(0) (the table was just created in the same tx, so a successful read is expected); or make the version insert idempotent with INSERT OR IGNORE / INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING so a re-run can't crash an already-migrated DB.
- **L82** [error-handling] get_setting() uses .ok() on query_row, which collapses BOTH the legitimate 'no such key' case (QueryReturnedNoRows) AND genuine failures (database locked, I/O error, corruption) into Ok(None). A real DB fault is silently reported to callers as 'setting absent'.
  - _Why:_ Callers treat None as 'not configured / not logged in' (e.g. resume_session reads last_server_id via get_setting and bails to Ok(None) on None; is_scrobble_configured flattens to false). A transient locked-DB error during get_setting therefore silently logs the user out / shows them as unconfigured instead of surfacing a storage error the way every other method here does via '?'.
  - _Fix:_ Match explicitly: match stmt.query_row(...) { Ok(v) => Ok(Some(v)), Err(rusqlite::Error::QueryReturnedNoRows) => Ok(None), Err(e) => Err(e.into()) }. This is the same NoEntry-vs-real-error discrimination already done correctly in CredentialStore::load_token (lines 227-231).

### `core/src/tests.rs`
- **L191** [test-gap] The Track.disc_number mapping (RawItem.parent_index_number -> Track.disc_number) is untested across the entire suite. album_tracks_parses is the only Track-producing test that supplies ParentIndexNumber, and it does not assert disc_number; every other Track that sets disc_number does so as construction input (disc_number: None at lines 7274, 8018), and line 2398's parent_index_number assertion is on the SearchHint model, not Track.
  - _Why:_ Multi-disc album ordering depends entirely on disc_number (per CLAUDE.md: "multi-disc lives on ParentIndexNumber"). A break in this single mapping would mis-order or merge discs in the UI and no test would catch it.
  - _Fix:_ In album_tracks_parses add assert_eq!(t.disc_number, Some(1)); to lock the ParentIndexNumber->disc_number mapping.
- **L207** [test-gap] album_tracks_parses feeds a rich Track payload but asserts only name, artist_name, is_favorite, play_count, and duration; it never verifies the album_id, album_name, index_number, disc_number (from ParentIndexNumber), year (from ProductionYear), or image_tag mappings that this code path is the only one to exercise for album tracks.
  - _Why:_ The RawItem->Track conversion (client.rs:2989 maps album_id: r.album_id, album_name: r.album, index_number: r.index_number, disc_number: r.parent_index_number, year: r.production_year, image_tag from ImageTags["Primary"]) is run but its output is discarded by the test. A regression that swaps or drops any of these (e.g. mapping IndexNumber into disc_number, or dropping the Primary image tag) would pass this test silently.
  - _Fix:_ Add assertions for the parsed fields the mock supplies: assert_eq!(t.album_id.as_deref(), Some("a1")); assert_eq!(t.album_name.as_deref(), Some("The Deep End")); assert_eq!(t.index_number, Some(3)); assert_eq!(t.year, Some(2020)); assert_eq!(t.image_tag.as_deref(), Some("abcd"));
- **L830** [test-gap] instant_mix_builds_query_and_parses provides full UserData/ImageTags/album/artist fields in the fixture but asserts only len() and name, leaving field mapping (is_favorite, play_count, album_id, artists, image_tag) unverified.
  - _Why:_ instant_mix maps via `Track::from` (client.rs:1353). Sibling test frequently_played_tracks asserts `tracks[0].play_count==99` (line 1095), proving this projection is regression-prone and worth pinning; instant_mix leaves it unchecked, so a Track::from mapping break for InstantMix rows would pass.
  - _Fix:_ Assert `tracks[0].album_id`, `tracks[0].artists`, `tracks[0].play_count`, `tracks[0].is_favorite`, and `tracks[0].image_tag` against the fixture values (mirroring the frequently_played_tracks assertions).
- **L884** [test-gap] suggestions_builds_query_and_parses asserts the request omits non-Audio types but never exercises the client-side Audio filter on the response, so a regression removing that filter is not caught.
  - _Why:_ The test goes out of its way to assert `!q.contains("MusicAlbum")` / `!q.contains("MediaType=Audio")` (lines 900-907) precisely because the server can still return non-Audio rows that consume Limit slots. But the response-side defense (the .filter) is never tested: if the mock returned a MusicAlbum row alongside an Audio row, the current single-Audio fixture wouldn't notice the filter being deleted.
  - _Fix:_ Add a MusicAlbum (or MusicArtist) entry to the mock Items array and assert the result still contains only the Audio track (len==1, kind Audio), pinning the client-side filter at client.rs:1386.
- **L913** [test-gap] No unauthenticated-session test exists for similar_artists, similar_albums, similar_items, genres, items_by_genre, tracks_by_genre, or frequently_played_tracks. Only instant_mix, suggestions, and lyrics have a *_requires_authenticated_session test in this range.
  - _Why:_ Every one of those production methods begins with `self.user_id.as_ref().ok_or(LyrebirdError::NotAuthenticated)?` (e.g. client.rs:1396 similar_artists, 1515 genres, 1586 tracks_by_genre). That guard is the only thing preventing a panic/wrong request when called pre-login; it is completely untested for 7 endpoints. A refactor that drops the guard (or swaps it for a default user_id) would compile and pass the whole suite.
  - _Fix:_ Add a `<endpoint>_requires_authenticated_session` test for each of the 7 endpoints, mirroring the existing instant_mix one: build an unauthenticated `mock_client`, call the method, and assert `matches!(err, LyrebirdError::NotAuthenticated)`.
- **L1186** [test-gap] genres_builds_query_and_parses_counts asserts IncludeItemTypes contains Audio and MusicAlbum but never asserts MusicArtist, even though production sends all three; dropping MusicArtist would silently pass.
  - _Why:_ MusicArtist in the genres query is what makes artists countable/visible when browsing by genre. The assertion is built with `.any(...)` membership checks specifically to be value-precise, yet omits the third type, so a regression narrowing genre scope (artists disappearing) is not caught.
  - _Fix:_ Add `assert!(include_types.split(',').any(|t| t == "MusicArtist"), ...)` to pin the full three-type set.
- **L1942** [test-gap] public_playlists_mirrors_user_playlists_until_split_lands pins down stub behavior rather than the intended feature. public_playlists() (client.rs:863) simply delegates to user_playlists() and applies no public-vs-private filtering, yet the mock returns a mix of a per-user playlist (p1 path .../users/u1/playlists/...) and shared playlists (p2/p3), and the test asserts all three are returned. There is no test anywhere that asserts public_playlists ever filters OUT the per-user playlist, so the unimplemented feature has zero forward coverage.
  - _Why:_ The test's own name ('until split lands') and message ('mirrors user_playlists today') document that this is a known gap, but encoding the stub as a passing test means the day someone implements the public/private split they must remember to rewrite this test or it will fail spuriously; meanwhile nothing fails today to flag that public_playlists returns private playlists.
  - _Fix:_ Either add an #[ignore]'d (or separate) test that asserts the intended filtered behavior so it surfaces when the feature lands, or at minimum rename to make clear it asserts delegation, and add a TODO-tracking test referencing the split issue so the gap is visible in test output rather than disguised as green coverage.
- **L2057** [test-gap] playlist_tracks_preserves_order_and_builds_query does not actually exercise order preservation. The mock returns the three tracks already in the exact order the test then asserts (t1 'First', t2 'Second', t3 'Third'), and that order is simultaneously id-ascending (t1<t2<t3) and name-ascending (First<Second<Third). The test would pass identically if playlist_tracks re-sorted the items by id or by name, so it cannot distinguish 'preserves the server's playlist order' from any natural sort.
  - _Why:_ Playlist track order is user-meaningful (a curated playlist is an ordered list). A future refactor of playlist_tracks that accidentally introduced a SortBy=SortName (the Fields list already includes ItemField::SortName, line 2076) would silently reorder every playlist and this 'preserves order' test would stay green, giving false confidence.
  - _Fix:_ Make the mock return items in an order that is NOT sorted by id or name — e.g. return t3 'Charlie', t1 'Alpha', t2 'Bravo' — and assert the response comes back in that same server order (tracks[0].id == "t3", tracks[1].id == "t1", tracks[2].id == "t2"). Only then does the assertion prove order is preserved rather than re-derived.
- **L2596** [test-gap] search_paginates_and_exposes_total_record_count seeds rich item data (ImageTags.Primary, ProductionYear, ChildCount, RunTimeTicks, AlbumId, AlbumArtist) but only asserts name + total_record_count for each of the three result kinds; none of the parsed-into-model fields are checked.
  - _Why:_ The client's search() routes items through Artist::from / Album::from / Track::from (client.rs ~2093-2095). A regression in any of those From impls (dropped image tag, wrong year, lost AlbumId) would leave this test green because only `name` is verified. The test name promises 'paginates and exposes' but the exposure of the parsed fields is unasserted.
  - _Fix:_ Add assertions for the model fields the mock deliberately populates, e.g. assert_eq!(results.albums[0].production_year, Some(2002)); assert that the primary image tag / AlbumId on the track parse through (assert_eq!(results.tracks[0].album_id.as_deref(), Some("album-1"))).
- **L2796** [test-gap] set_favorite_falls_back_to_legacy_route_on_404 (and the 405 sibling at 2846) assert only that BOTH the preferred and legacy paths appear in received_requests, never that the legacy call happened AFTER / because of the preferred 404. Request ordering and the 'tried first' guarantee in the assertion message are not actually enforced.
  - _Why:_ If a future refactor inverted the order (hit legacy first, then preferred) or fired both unconditionally, this test would still pass while the message claims ordering was checked. The play_count==Some(5)/Some(1) assert does confirm the legacy body was the one parsed, so body-selection is covered — but call ordering, which the message asserts, is not.
  - _Fix:_ Index into received_requests by position (filter to the two favorite paths preserving order) and assert the preferred path precedes the legacy path; or use a scoped mock with .expect(1) on each and assert the preferred mock was hit exactly once before the legacy.
- **L3505** [test-gap] Test named playlist_tracks_includes_playlist_item_id_in_fields builds two response items that are byte-for-byte identical EXCEPT for their PlaylistItemId ("pi-1" vs "pi-2"), but the only post-parse assertions are page.items.len()==2 and page.total_count==2. It never asserts that the PlaylistItemId values were actually parsed onto the returned Track models (e.g. page.items[0].playlist_item_id == Some("pi-1")).
  - _Why:_ playlist_tracks (client.rs:1063,1076-1081) requests Fields=PlaylistItemId and maps each RawItem via Track::from, and models.rs:86 has `pub playlist_item_id: Option<String>`. The whole point of using two duplicate items distinguished only by PlaylistItemId is to prove that field round-trips into the model and distinguishes otherwise-identical rows. The test only proves the request-side (Fields contains PlaylistItemId via the closure check) and the count; a regression that dropped PlaylistItemId from Track::from would still pass this test, so the response-side parsing the test name advertises is unverified.
  - _Fix:_ After asserting the count, also assert the parsed field values, e.g. assert_eq!(page.items[0].playlist_item_id.as_deref(), Some("pi-1")); assert_eq!(page.items[1].playlist_item_id.as_deref(), Some("pi-2")); (or assert the set of playlist_item_ids equals {pi-1, pi-2} to be order-independent).
- **L4206** [test-gap] set_session_invalidates_library_cache verifies the cache is re-fetched (get_count == 2) but never asserts the second /UserViews request was issued for the NEW user (userId=u2). The /UserViews mock at line 4217 deliberately omits `.and(query_param("userId", ...))`, so it matches both u1 and u2 indiscriminately.
  - _Why:_ The whole point of the test is that a session switch takes effect. A regression where set_session clears the cache but the subsequent user_views() still sends the OLD userId (e.g. user_id not updated, only token swapped) would pass this test. user_views() builds the URL from self.user_id (client.rs:2316), so this is exactly the field that needs pinning.
  - _Fix:_ Add `.and(query_param("userId", "u2"))` to a dedicated mock (or assert the second received request's `userId` query pair equals "u2") so the test fails if set_session doesn't propagate the new user id to the next user_views call.
- **L5052** [performance] retry_recovers_from_transient_5xx executes real wall-clock backoff sleeps (~600ms) instead of virtual time
  - _Why:_ send_with_retry_raw (core/src/client.rs:389-394) calls tokio::time::sleep(backoff_for(attempt)) with BACKOFF_BASE_MS=[200,400,800] and the #[tokio::test] runtime is NOT paused (no start_paused/flavor). Two retries mean ~200ms + ~400ms = ~600ms of real sleep per run. Across the retry test trio this adds >1s of pure idle time to every test run and makes the suite slower and flakier under CI load.
  - _Fix:_ Use #[tokio::test(start_paused = true)] (or tokio::time::pause()) so the backoff sleeps advance virtual time instantly; the request/response sequencing is unaffected by paused time since wiremock responses are immediate.
- **L5121** [performance] retry_surfaces_last_server_error_when_budget_exhausted also incurs ~600ms of real backoff sleep
  - _Why:_ Same root cause as retry_recovers_from_transient_5xx: the 502 path retries to MAX_ATTEMPTS=3, sleeping backoff_for(1)+backoff_for(2) (~600ms) of real time because the test runtime is not time-paused.
  - _Fix:_ Annotate with #[tokio::test(start_paused = true)] so the two real sleeps collapse to virtual time; assertions on hit count and error variant stay valid.
- **L5359** [resource-leak] shuffle_repeat_round_trips_all_variants creates a DB file via a manual temp path and only deletes it at the end, leaking the file if any earlier assertion panics
  - _Why:_ Unlike every sibling test in this file (which uses tempfile::tempdir() whose Drop deletes the dir even on panic), this test manages the file by hand. The remove_file call at the end is unreachable on any failed assertion inside the loop (save_shuffle_repeat / load_shuffle_repeat .expect or assert_eq panic), so a failing run leaves lyrebird_test_sr_<nanos>.db behind in the system temp dir. Repeated failures accumulate stale DB files.
  - _Fix:_ Build the path inside a tempfile::TempDir (tmpdir.path().join("sr.db")) so RAII cleanup runs unconditionally, matching the rest of the suite, and drop the manual remove_file.
- **L5417** [test-gap] No CI-runnable test covers the positive (true) branch of is_cert_error; the only positive test is #[ignore]d and the named unit test exercises only the negative branch.
  - _Why:_ is_cert_error (error.rs:246) string-matches messages like 'invalid peer certificate' / 'self-signed certificate' through the error source chain and returns true. The only test that drives that true path, cert_error_maps_to_structured_variant (line 5443), carries #[ignore = "requires outbound HTTPS to self-signed.badssl.com"], so it never runs in CI. self_signed_cert_error_detected_from_error_chain — despite its name implying it tests detection — only checks the false branch. A refactor that breaks the substring matching (e.g. a rustls message rename) would not be caught by any default test run.
  - _Fix:_ Add a non-ignored unit test that constructs or wraps an error whose Display/source chain contains one of the matched substrings (e.g. a synthetic std::io::Error chain or a recorded rustls error string) and asserts is_cert_error returns true — covering the positive branch without network access.
- **L5484** [test-gap] non_cert_transport_error_stays_network silently passes (vacuous) if anything is listening on 127.0.0.1:19999.
  - _Why:_ The test depends on a connection to a hard-coded port failing. If the request unexpectedly succeeds (port in use on the CI/dev host, a proxy intercepts it, etc.) the let-else returns early and the test passes without asserting anything — a false green. There is no guard that the connection actually failed for the expected reason.
  - _Fix:_ Bind a TcpListener to an ephemeral port (port 0), capture the assigned port, drop/close the listener to guarantee connection-refused, and target that port. Then treat a missing error as a hard failure (panic!) rather than an early return, so the test cannot pass vacuously.
- **L5940** [test-gap] logout_releases_inner_before_http_round_trip detaches the spawn_blocking JoinHandle and relies solely on the channel, so a panic in the blocking closure (e.g. login/logout .expect failing) is swallowed and surfaces only as a misleading 'deadlocked' timeout message.
  - _Why:_ The JoinHandle from spawn_blocking is dropped (not bound/awaited), so a panic inside the closure does not propagate to the test thread. If login or logout panics for an unrelated reason, tx is never sent, the recv_timeout fails with a RecvError, and the failure is reported as 'logout deadlocked holding Inner across the HTTP round-trip (#861)' — misattributing an arbitrary panic to the #861 deadlock regression and obscuring the true cause. tx.send(...).ok() also discards send errors.
  - _Fix:_ Bind the spawn_blocking handle and .await it (or join it) so closure panics propagate and fail the test with the real message; alternatively distinguish RecvError (closure died) from RecvTimeoutError::Timeout (actual deadlock) before emitting the #861-specific message.
- **L5988** [test-gap] rename_playlist_fetches_then_posts verifies only that Name changed, not that the fetched item's other fields survive the fetch-merge-post round-trip — which is the entire reason the method does a GET first.
  - _Why:_ rename_playlist (client.rs:2430) fetches the existing item, mutates only body["Name"], and posts the whole object back. The mock returns Id/Name/Type for pl-1. The test never asserts the POST body still contains Id == "pl-1" and Type == "Playlist". A regression that posts only {"Name": ...} (dropping the merged fields) would still pass this test, yet would wipe server-side metadata on real Jellyfin. The GET mock's presence implies intent to test the merge, but the assertion doesn't cover it.
  - _Fix:_ Also assert body["Id"] == "pl-1" and body["Type"] == "Playlist" (or otherwise assert the fetched fields are preserved) so the test actually guards the fetch-then-merge contract rather than just the single mutated field.
- **L6281** [test-gap] The heartbeat test helper hard-codes is_paused: false, so the production behavior of forwarding the real pause state (PlaybackProgressInfo.is_paused, lib.rs:1241-1246) is never asserted.
  - _Why:_ Reporting is_paused incorrectly to /Sessions/Playing/Progress causes Jellyfin to show wrong Now-Playing state on other clients. Because the test mirrors the body instead of calling production, a bug where is_paused is always sent false would never be caught.
  - _Fix:_ Have the cadence test inspect the JSON body of the captured /Sessions/Playing/Progress requests and assert is_paused matches the player state, via the production start_heartbeat path.
- **L6337** [test-gap] Heartbeat tests only ever pass interval 5s, so production's interval_secs.clamp(1, 10) (lib.rs:1217) is never exercised. A caller passing 0 (would divide-by-zero a naive interval, or here clamp to 1) or >10 is untested.
  - _Why:_ tokio::time::interval(Duration::from_secs(0)) panics ('interval period must be non-zero'). The clamp is the only guard against that, and it has zero coverage. If the clamp were removed/regressed, a 0 interval would panic the heartbeat task at runtime with no test catching it.
  - _Fix:_ Add a test calling core.start_heartbeat(0, ...) and core.start_heartbeat(999, ...) and assert the observed cadence is clamped (>=1 request and bounded), exercising the production clamp.
- **L6435** [test-gap] heartbeat_stops_after_abort calls abort.abort() on a raw AbortHandle returned by the test helper; it never exercises production stop_heartbeat(), which takes the handle out of the self.heartbeat Mutex (lib.rs:1275-1279). The Mutex take/None-guard logic is untested.
  - _Why:_ A bug where stop_heartbeat() fails to .take() the handle (e.g. leaves a stale handle, or double-stop panics) would not be caught. start_heartbeat replacing an existing handle without aborting the old one (a leak/double-fire) is also untested.
  - _Fix:_ Drive through core.start_heartbeat then core.stop_heartbeat and assert no further requests; add a case that calls start_heartbeat twice and asserts the first task is aborted (no duplicate heartbeats).
- **L7063** [test-gap] structured_error_rate_limit_parses_retry_after sleeps ~10s in real wall-clock time because it does not virtualize tokio time. 429 is classified retriable (client.rs is_retriable_status returns true for TOO_MANY_REQUESTS), so client.albums() runs the full retry loop (MAX_ATTEMPTS=3) and on each of the 2 inter-attempt waits calls tokio::time::sleep(min(Retry-After=42s, RETRY_AFTER_CAP=5s)) = 5s real sleep. Two 5s sleeps = ~10s per test run.
  - _Why:_ A ~10s single unit test bloats the test suite and CI wall-clock for no added coverage. The repo already demonstrates the correct fix elsewhere (heartbeat tests at tests.rs:6341/6356 use tokio::time::pause() + tokio::time::advance() inside a plain #[tokio::test]), so this is an avoidable inconsistency, not a runtime limitation.
  - _Fix:_ Add tokio::time::pause() at the top of the test and drive the retry waits with tokio::time::advance(...) + yield_now() as the heartbeat tests do (tests.rs:6341-6360), or switch the attribute to #[tokio::test(start_paused = true)]. This keeps the Some(42) assertion intact while eliminating the real-time sleep.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/AppDelegate.swift`
- **L113** [concurrency] applicationDockMenu reads @MainActor-isolated AppModel state (status, jumpBackIn) without the method being @MainActor; under Swift 5 language mode this compiles but is an unchecked cross-actor access (latent data race).
  - _Why:_ AppModel is declared `@Observable @MainActor final class` (AppModel.swift:13-15). AppDelegate is a plain `final class` with NO class-level @MainActor — the author selectively annotates bind/refreshDockTile/reconnectIfNeeded as @MainActor (lines 181/227/333) but leaves applicationDockMenu, applicationDidFinishLaunching, applicationWillTerminate, handleSleep, handleWake, and the @objc dock* actions un-isolated. Package.swift pins `swiftLanguageVersions: [.v5]`, so the compiler does NOT flag this cross-actor read; it is only safe because AppKit happens to invoke the dock menu on the main thread. The annotation is load-bearing for correctness and its absence is a soundness gap, not a style issue — if any of these were ever called off-main it would race AppModel's mutable state with zero compiler protection.
  - _Fix:_ Annotate the whole class `@MainActor final class AppDelegate` (NSApplicationDelegate callbacks are documented main-thread), or add `@MainActor` to applicationDockMenu, applicationDidFinishLaunching, applicationWillTerminate, handleSleep, handleWake, and each @objc dock action so the cross-actor access is checked rather than assumed.
- **L205** [concurrency] Dock-badge observer's withCheckedContinuation has no cancellation handler, so cancelling dockBadgeTask does not wake the suspended task until the next status.state change. The task (and the strongly-captured AppModel) lingers across rebind/terminate.
  - _Why:_ Task.isCancelled is only re-checked AFTER the continuation resumes, and the continuation resumes only via onChange (next state transition). dockBadgeTask?.cancel() in bind() (line 184) and applicationWillTerminate() (line 102) therefore does not immediately stop the loop. The closure captures `model` strongly (only `self` is weak), so a cancelled-but-still-suspended observer keeps the whole AppModel alive until playback state happens to change. If bind() is invoked more than once (it runs from a SwiftUI `.task` on RootView, LyrebirdApp.swift:45, which can re-fire across view-identity changes), each stale observer survives until the next state flip — a slow, self-healing leak that also means refreshDockTile keeps firing from an observer that was supposed to be retired.
  - _Fix:_ Use withTaskCancellationHandler around the continuation (or withCheckedContinuation's cancellation-aware variant) so cancellation resumes the continuation immediately; capture `model` weakly, or store the AsyncStream-style observation so cancel() tears it down deterministically. Minimal: wrap in `await withTaskCancellationHandler(operation: { await withCheckedContinuation {...} }, onCancel: { continuation.resume() })` with the continuation hoisted, or replace the manual loop with `for await _ in observationStream`.
- **L335** [bug] reconnectIfNeeded snapshots serverURL/session under the @MainActor guard but then performs success side-effects (noteSuccess, refresh*) inside a later Task without re-validating that the session/serverURL still match — a server switch mid-reconnect applies stale-server results to the new session.
  - _Why:_ Wake events fire this after a debounce (handleWake, line 273-278). probeServer runs against the captured `url`; while it is in flight on a utility thread the user could sign out or switch servers (markAuthExpired clears polling/session per AppModel.swift:1391). On success the code unconditionally calls serverReachability.noteSuccess() and three refresh() calls bound to the *current* self/session, attributing a probe of the old server URL to whatever session is now active. This can mark a freshly-failed/expired session as 'reachable' and trigger refreshes the auth state no longer warrants.
  - _Fix:_ After the probe resolves, re-check `guard session != nil, serverURL == url, !authExpired else { return }` before calling noteSuccess()/refresh*; capture the active session token/id and compare, so results are dropped if the server context changed during the probe.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/AppModel.swift`
- **L944** [bug] Command-palette "Clear Queue" action clears the core queue but leaves the local up-next arrays populated, so the queue UI still shows the old queue after the user clears it. It is also inconsistent with the public clearQueue() method, which does the opposite.
  - _Why:_ upNextUserAdded / upNextAutoQueue are the source of truth for the queue inspector and saveQueueAsPlaylist (see AppModel.swift lines 6193-6194, 6267-6272). The palette action calls core.clearQueue() but never clears those arrays, so after "Clear Queue" the inspector still lists tracks and "save queue as playlist" would still save them. Conversely the public clearQueue() (line 6222) clears upNextUserAdded/upNextAutoQueue and calls audio.pause() but never calls core.clearQueue(), so the QueueInspector "Clear" button (QueueInspector.swift:103 -> model.clearQueue()) leaves the core queue intact. The two clear paths are each half-broken and inconsistent with each other.
  - _Fix:_ Route the palette action through the same code path as the QueueInspector button (call a single clearQueue() that BOTH calls core.clearQueue() and clears upNextUserAdded/upNextAutoQueue, then refreshes status), so the local up-next mirror and the core queue can never diverge.
- **L1227** [consistency] logout() and forgetToken() duplicate ~58 lines of identical state-reset code; the two copies have already drifted (forgetToken omits the imageURLCache.removeAll() and session = nil that logout performs), and any future state added to one will silently leak in the other.
  - _Why:_ This is a known conflict hotspot file (~4000-line @MainActor view model). Two copies of a 55-line reset block guarantee drift: a new cache or pending-state field added to logout's reset but not forgetToken's (or vice-versa) leaks stale data across account switches. The existing imageURLCache divergence means forgetToken() can serve stale artwork URLs after the token is dropped.
  - _Fix:_ Extract the shared reset into a single private func resetSessionState() and have both logout() and forgetToken() call it, with each adding only its unique extra steps (logout: session = nil + imageURLCache.removeAll() + detached core.logout()).
- **L1424** [error-handling] refreshLibrary() never clears errorMessage on a successful load, so a transient failure leaves a permanent error banner even after the user retries successfully.
  - _Why:_ errorMessage is only ever reset to nil at login (line 1172), session restore (line 1210), and in play() (line 3995) — confirmed by `rg 'errorMessage = nil'`. retryServer()/retryNetwork() (lines 1143-1158) both call refreshLibrary(), but refreshLibrary sets errorMessage on any failing block and never clears it on a later success. So a one-off network blip during library load shows an error banner that persists through every subsequent successful refresh until the user logs out and back in.
  - _Fix:_ When the library load succeeds (e.g. inside `if anySucceeded { ... }`, or after the three do/catch blocks if no error occurred), set `self.errorMessage = nil` so a recovered retry clears the stale banner.
- **L1987** [bug] Bulk favorite-cache priming is write-true-only: refreshFavoriteAlbums / loadFavoriteAlbums / loadFavoriteTracks set favoriteById[id]=true for items currently in the favorites list but never set false for items that dropped out, leaving stale 'favorited' heart state after an external un-favorite.
