  - _Why:_ favoriteById is a session-lived sticky cache that isFavorite(*) consults first. If the user favorites album A (cache=true) and A is later un-favorited from another client, a subsequent refreshFavoriteAlbums replaces favoriteAlbumsAll (A correctly gone from the list) but never touches favoriteById[A], so it stays true and isFavorite(album: A) keeps returning true everywhere A appears. The cache only diverges in the false->true-stuck direction; nothing in these refresh paths reconciles removals.
  - _Fix:_ When refreshing the authoritative favorites list, reconcile the cache: clear (or set false) the previously-true entries for that item type that are absent from the new result set before re-priming the present ones, or stop priming favoriteById from list fetches and rely solely on per-item mutation results + parsed userData.
- **L2110** [performance] JSON parsing of Items responses (up to 500 entries) runs on the @MainActor: URLSession.shared.data(for:) resumes on the main actor and the synchronous parse (parseAlbumsFromItems / parseTracksFromItems / parseArtistsFromItems / parseAlbumsWithPlayCounts) then runs there.
  - _Why:_ These helpers live on a @MainActor class, so after the network await the JSONSerialization + compactMap over hundreds of dictionaries (loadFavoriteTracks/fetchFavoriteTracks default limit=500) executes on the main thread, risking a scroll/launch hitch. The codebase's own guidance (CLAUDE.md gap pattern #2) calls out main-thread work as a beachball source and prescribes Task.detached marshalling.
  - _Fix:_ Wrap the data fetch + static parse in Task.detached and marshal only the finished [Album]/[Track]/[Artist] back to the main actor (the parse functions are already `static` and operate on Data, so they are trivially movable off-main).
- **L2115** [consistency] Albums fetched via the Items query (jumpBackIn, quickPicks, rediscover, favoriteAlbums) request Fields=...,UserData but the DTO parser discards it (Album.userData hardcoded nil), so server IsFavorite/PlayCount/last-played projections are thrown away and home-screen heart state is wrong for any album not separately primed into favoriteById.
  - _Why:_ The query pays the bandwidth cost of UserData but the value never reaches the model. For shelves other than the favorites list (which additively primes favoriteById), isFavorite(album:) falls through to album.userData?.isFavorite which is always nil -> false. A server-favorited album shown in Recently Added / Quick Picks / Jump Back In renders as un-favorited, and Quick Picks' own playCounts are computed only via the separate parseAlbumsWithPlayCounts path rather than from the parsed model.
  - _Fix:_ Populate Album.userData (and/or a flat isFavorite/playCount) in albumFromDTO from entry["UserData"], the same way trackFromDTO already reads entry["UserData"]["IsFavorite"]/["PlayCount"]. Then the existing isFavorite(album:) fallback works without depending on the favorites list having been loaded.
- **L2474** [bug] albumFromDTO discards the UserData (IsFavorite/PlayCount) the server returns, passing userData: nil, so albums loaded via the items-query path lose their favorite state.
  - _Why:_ buildItemsQuery explicitly requests `UserData` in the Fields list (line 2336), so the JSON has IsFavorite, but albumFromDTO never reads it and hard-codes userData: nil. Albums produced this way feed the home shelves refreshJumpBackIn / refreshQuickPicks / refreshRediscover / refreshRecentlyAdded. isFavorite(album:) (line 4137) resolves favoriteById[id] -> album.userData?.isFavorite -> false, and these albums are never written into favoriteById (only the explicit favorites paths do that at lines 1988 and 2269). Result: an album that is favorited shows the AlbumContextMenu as 'Favorite Album' instead of 'Unfavorite Album' (Components/AlbumContextMenu.swift reads model.isFavorite(album:)) whenever the user reaches it via a Home shelf.
  - _Fix:_ In albumFromDTO read entry["UserData"] and build a UserItemData (it is a uniffi::Record, constructible in Swift) with at least is_favorite/play_count, then pass it as `userData:` — mirroring what trackFromDTO already does for tracks. Alternatively seed favoriteById in the callers as loadFavoriteAlbums does.
- **L2701** [error-handling] Page-gating resolvers and detail loaders catch errors, call handleAuthError only, and return nil/[] without ever surfacing a message to the user.
  - _Why:_ Unlike loadTracks(forAlbum:) (line 2661) and loadPlaylistTracks (3019) which set errorMessage = LyrebirdErrorPresenter.message(...), these swallow non-auth errors silently. resolveArtist/resolveAlbum/resolvePlaylist gate whether a detail page can open at all; a transient server error returns nil so the page silently fails to populate (or won't open) with no feedback and no retry affordance. The shelf loaders (top tracks / similar / playlists) failing silently is acceptable UX, but the resolvers and artistDetail gate whole screens.
  - _Fix:_ For the resolvers and artistDetail, on a non-auth error that ServerReachability.shouldCount accepts, set errorMessage via LyrebirdErrorPresenter (add the appropriate context cases) so the user sees that the page failed to load, consistent with loadTracks/loadPlaylistTracks.
- **L2728** [performance] breadcrumbAlbumName / breadcrumbArtistName always run an O(n) linear scan over the full album/artist list BEFORE consulting the O(1) resolvedNameCache, on every call.
  - _Why:_ These are invoked from MainShell.breadcrumbSegments (Screens/MainShell.swift:544/554), a SwiftUI computed property re-evaluated on every render of the navigation chrome. The `??` evaluates the left operand first, so `albums.first(where:)` scans up to ~20060 albums (and `artists.first` up to ~3839 artists) on the @MainActor on every render even though resolveAlbum/resolveArtist already populated resolvedNameCache (lines 2680, 2748/2759) with an O(1) answer. On a large library this is a per-render O(n) scan on the main thread.
  - _Fix:_ Check the cache first: `resolvedNameCache[id] ?? albums.first(where: { $0.id == id })?.name`. The resolvers populate resolvedNameCache on navigation, so the common breadcrumb case becomes O(1); the linear scan only runs on a genuine cache miss.
- **L2899** [resource-leak] Per-artist/per-album caches (artistAlbumsCache, artistDetailCache, artistTopTracks, artistSimilarCache, artistPlaylistsCache, albumTracks) grow without any per-entry bound; they are only ever cleared wholesale on logout/full refresh.
  - _Why:_ loadArtistAlbums/artistDetail/loadArtistTopTracks/loadSimilarArtists/loadPlaylistsFeaturingArtist/loadTracks(forAlbum:) all insert into their dictionary and never evict (eviction sites only at the bulk resets, lines 1242-1255/1316-1329, plus playlistTracks on delete at 4967). On a 20060-album / 3839-artist library, browsing through many artists/albums in one session accumulates unbounded entries (album track lists, similar-artist lists, etc.) held on the @MainActor model for the life of the session.
  - _Fix:_ Bound the caches (e.g. an LRU / NSCache, or cap the dictionary size and drop oldest), or evict when navigating away. At minimum document a ceiling; an unbounded String->[Track]/[Album] map over a 100k-track library is a real memory-growth risk.
- **L3134** [concurrency] removeFromPlaylist's failure rollback unconditionally appends removedSnapshot back into currentPlaylistTracks with no dedup guard, unlike undoRemoveFromPlaylist which filters !existingIds.contains. If the user taps Undo before the server-side remove failure arrives, the tracks get re-added twice and trackCount is inflated.
  - _Why:_ Race: (1) removeFromPlaylist removes N tracks, sets pendingPlaylistRemoval, fires Task A (server remove). (2) User taps Undo -> undoRemoveFromPlaylist clears pending, re-appends the N tracks (count +N), fires Task B (server add). (3) Task A then FAILS -> this catch appends removedSnapshot AGAIN (count +N again) with no `!existingIds.contains` filter, producing duplicate rows in currentPlaylistTracks and a trackCount inflated by N. undoRemoveFromPlaylist deliberately dedups (line 3168) but this rollback does not.
  - _Fix:_ Mirror the undo path: compute `let existing = Set(self.currentPlaylistTracks.map(\.id)); let reAdd = removedSnapshot.filter { !existing.contains($0.id) }` and append/adjust trackCount by reAdd.count. Also guard the count restore so it can't exceed the pre-removal value.
- **L3191** [bug] undoRemoveFromPlaylist (and removeFromPlaylist rollback, and addToPlaylist) re-insert tracks with core.addToPlaylist(position: nil), which appends to the end of the playlist. Undoing a removal of mid-playlist tracks moves them to the bottom; the original ordering is lost even though the core API supports a position argument.
  - _Why:_ core add_to_playlist accepts `position: Option<u32>` (core/src/lib.rs:689-693), so the original index is recoverable. By passing nil and appending locally, an 'Undo' of removing track #3 of 50 puts it at #50 on both client and server. Users reasonably expect Undo to restore the prior state exactly, not just re-add the tracks somewhere. Same end-append issue applies to the removeFromPlaylist failure rollback (line 3134).
  - _Fix:_ Capture each removed track's original index in PendingRemoval and pass it as `position` when re-adding (re-insert lowest-index-first so positions stay valid), and splice into currentPlaylistTracks at the same indices rather than appending.
- **L3536** [performance] shuffleLibrary loads tracks for up to 25 sampled albums with a sequential await loop, issuing up to 25 serial network round-trips before any playback starts, with no progress indication.
  - _Why:_ loadTracks(forAlbum:) does a network fetch when uncached (AppModel.swift:2634 `try core.albumTracks(...)`). On a fresh library where none of the 25 sampled albums are cached, this is 25 sequential round-trips on the 'Shuffle Library' action. At even 150ms latency that is ~3.75s of dead time before the first note plays, and the user sees nothing happen.
  - _Fix:_ Fetch the sampled albums' tracks concurrently with a bounded TaskGroup (e.g. 4-6 in flight), accumulating until the 200-track cap is reached, then cancel the rest. This turns ~25 serial RTTs into a few parallel batches.
- **L3805** [concurrency] loadMoreFullSearch does not re-validate that the active query is still the one it fetched before merging, so a stale page from a previous query can be merged into the new query's results.
  - _Why:_ If the user types a new query (or changes scope) while a 'load more' is in flight, the stale page resolves afterward and merges old-query items into the new results, plus overwrites searchPageTotal — producing mixed/incorrect results and a wrong 'has more' termination.
  - _Fix:_ After the await in loadMoreFullSearch, `guard searchPageQuery == query && activeSearchScope == <scope-at-start> else { return }` before merging. Optionally track and cancel the load-more task on a new search.
- **L4265** [error-handling] loadAlbumDetail swallows all non-auth errors silently and returns an empty AlbumDetail, giving the user no signal that label/date/people/overview failed to load.
  - _Why:_ A transient server error makes an album silently render with no label, release date, credits, or overview, indistinguishable from an album that genuinely has none. The detail page can't retry or inform. Other loaders in this file (loadTracks(forArtist:), setFavorite, setPlayed) consistently call serverReachability.noteFailure() and set errorMessage on non-auth errors.
  - _Fix:_ On non-auth error, call serverReachability.noteFailure() (gated by ServerReachability.shouldCount) and surface a non-fatal indicator (or set errorMessage). Consider returning an explicit failed/loaded state so the view can show a retry instead of a blank detail section.
- **L4451** [dead-code] playTopTracks(artist:) has zero callers — it is dead code.
  - _Why:_ Unreachable code rots — it diverges from the actually-used playAll path (top-5 vs up-to-500) and misleads future maintainers into thinking a 'play top tracks' affordance exists.
  - _Fix:_ Remove playTopTracks, or wire it to a real 'Play top tracks' menu item if that affordance is intended.
- **L4471** [consistency] toggleFollow/isFollowing are exact aliases of toggleFavorite/isFavorite for an artist; Follow and Favorite are the same backing flag exposed under two different labels in different UI surfaces.
  - _Why:_ On the same artist, the detail header 'Follow'/'Following' button and the context menu 'Favorite'/'Unfavorite' both toggle the one server favorite flag. Toggling one silently flips the other with no indication they are the same state, which is confusing and looks like a sync bug to users.
  - _Fix:_ Either expose a single label consistently (drop the Follow/Favorite duplication for artists), or, if a distinct 'follow' concept is intended, back it with a separate server field. At minimum make both surfaces reflect the shared state with identical wording.
- **L4485** [consistency] Artist 'Play Next' inserts only the artist's top-5 tracks, inconsistent with album/playlist 'Play Next' (which insert the full set) and not gated by the same capability as 'Play All'.
  - _Why:_ A user choosing 'Play Next' on an artist expects the artist queued next, but only 5 tracks are inserted. And if supportsArtistPlayShuffle were ever false, 'Play Next' would still appear while 'Play All' disappears — incoherent menu. The top-5 choice is silent and surprising.
  - _Fix:_ Use loadTracks(forArtist:) (the full set, as playAll does) for playNextArtist, or relabel the menu item to 'Play Top Tracks Next'. Gate it behind the same supportsArtistPlayShuffle flag as Play All/Shuffle All.
- **L4570** [bug] play(playlist:), shuffle(playlist:), playNext(playlist:), addToQueue(playlist:) all enqueue only the first 500 tracks because loadPlaylistTracks(playlist:) is capped at limit 500. Playing a large playlist silently omits everything past track 500.
  - _Why:_ Users expect 'Play'/'Shuffle' on a playlist to play the whole playlist. The 500 cap (line 3008) truncates the queue with no indication. shuffle() is worst: it shuffles only a fixed 500-track prefix, so later tracks never play.
  - _Fix:_ Route playback enqueue paths through loadAllPlaylistTracks (as duplicatePlaylist does), or page the queue, so the full playlist is queued.
- **L4637** [gap-stub] enqueueDownload(playlist:), toggleDownload(tracks:), and updatePlaylistDescription are live no-op/local-only stubs reachable from the UI: they log via Log.app.notice and either do nothing server-side or only mutate in-memory dictionaries that are wiped on sign-out.
  - _Why:_ Per CLAUDE.md gap pattern #1, Log.app.notice("...not yet wired") bodies are live bugs surfaced as menu actions: the user invokes Download / Edit Description, sees nothing happen (or sees a description that silently vanishes on next sign-out), with no UI feedback. These are reachable feature paths, not TODOs.
  - _Fix:_ Gate these actions behind the Capabilities flags (as the other print-stub features are) so the menu items are hidden/disabled until the FFI lands, or persist updatePlaylistDescription via a real core call. At minimum surface a user-visible 'not available yet' state instead of a silent no-op.
- **L4696** [bug] exportPlaylist / exportPlaylistJSON load tracks via loadPlaylistTracks(playlist:) which caps at limit 500 (core.playlistTracks offset 0 limit 500). Exporting a playlist with more than 500 tracks silently truncates the exported file to the first 500.
  - _Why:_ Export writes a persistent file the user trusts as complete; dropping tracks beyond 500 is data loss with no warning. duplicatePlaylist (line 4926) correctly uses loadAllPlaylistTracks for the same need, so the truncation here is inconsistent and avoidable.
  - _Fix:_ Use loadAllPlaylistTracks(playlistID: playlist.id) for both export functions (and ideally for play/shuffle/playNext/addToQueue(playlist:) which share the same 500 cap).
- **L5027** [bug] moveTrackInPlaylist overwrites currentPlaylistTracks with THIS playlist's tracks whenever currentPlaylistTracks is merely non-empty, with no check that the reordered playlistId is the one currently displayed. Reordering playlist A while viewing playlist B clobbers B's displayed list with A's tracks.
  - _Why:_ currentPlaylistTracks is the single buffer backing the currently-open playlist view. The only guard is .isEmpty, not playlist identity, so a drag/reorder on a non-displayed playlist corrupts the visible track list. This is sloppier than removeFromPlaylist, which at least filters by id.
  - _Fix:_ Guard the assignment on the displayed playlist id, e.g. `if currentPlaylistId == playlistId { currentPlaylistTracks = tracks }` (track which playlist currentPlaylistTracks belongs to).
- **L5206** [concurrency] toggleFavorite(tracks:) spawns one independent unstructured Task per track inside the loop. For a large multiselect this fans out up to N concurrent Tasks, each calling setFavorite -> Task.detached -> core mutex, hammering the server and contending the FFI lock.
  - _Why:_ Library multiselect can be hundreds of tracks. Hundreds of simultaneous network requests + mutex acquisitions risk rate-limiting/beachball. toggleMarkPlayed (line 5240) does the same work sequentially in a single Task — the better, throttled pattern — so this is an inconsistency as well as a load concern.
  - _Fix:_ Coalesce into a single Task that iterates sequentially (or batches), mirroring toggleMarkPlayed; or use a bounded TaskGroup.
- **L5294** [bug] Genre name->id resolver caps the lookup table at 500 genres and never refreshes it for the session, so large libraries can't browse / radio / shuffle genres past the 500th
  - _Why:_ browseGenre/startGenreRadio/shuffleGenre all resolve the real server id through this single-page (limit 500) cache. A library with >500 genres yields a partial table, and once _genresLoaded is true it is never rebuilt, so every genre beyond the first 500 (or any genre added during the session) returns nil and the user gets 'Genre \'X\' not found on server' (lines 5312/5327/5339) for a genre that plainly exists in the UI. Dictionary(uniqueKeysWithValues:) also traps if two genres share an identical name.
  - _Fix:_ Page genres until items.count < limit (accumulate offset += 500) before marking _genresLoaded, or fall back to a targeted core lookup-by-name on cache miss instead of giving up. Use Dictionary(_:uniquingKeysWith:) to tolerate duplicate names. Consider invalidating _genresLoaded when the library is refreshed.
- **L5311** [error-handling] browseGenre and startGenreRadio surface "Genre 'X' not found on server" whenever resolvedGenreId returns nil, but resolvedGenreId returns nil on network failure too (it swallows errors via try?). A transient network error during the genre load is reported to the user as a (false) not-found.
  - _Why:_ resolvedGenreId conflates 'genre absent' with 'genres failed to load'. The not-found wording misleads the user (and any reachability accounting is skipped because the throw is swallowed by try?). shuffleGenre at least does proper do/catch around its own track fetch, but the genre-resolution step has the same conflation.
  - _Fix:_ Make resolvedGenreId distinguish load-failure (propagate/throw) from genuine miss, and have callers show a generic 'couldn't load genres' message + run ServerReachability accounting on the load failure.
- **L5344** [bug] shuffleGenre loads only the first 500 tracks of a genre (limit 500) and shuffles that prefix. For genres with more than 500 tracks the 'shuffle' is a non-representative subset; tracks beyond the sort-order prefix never play.
  - _Why:_ Genres on a 20k-album library routinely exceed 500 tracks. A user expecting a genre-wide shuffle gets only the alphabetically-first 500, biasing playback and hiding most of the genre.
  - _Fix:_ Page the genre tracks up to a sane cap (mirror loadAllPlaylistTracks' paging), or use a server-side instant-mix/random sort rather than a fixed 500 prefix.
- **L5856** [error-handling] scrobbleSubmitListen errors are swallowed with try? — a failed scrobble is silently lost with no retry and no surfacing
  - _Why:_ This is the actual listen submission to the user's scrobble service (Last.fm). The gate fires submitListen exactly once per qualifying play; if the FFI throws (offline, rate-limited, expired Last.fm session key), the try? discards it and the listen is gone forever — there is no retry queue and nothing is recorded to errorMessage. This is the silent-corruption pattern CLAUDE.md gap #5 warns about (swallowed try? on an FFI mutation). scrobbleConnected can read true while every scrobble silently fails (e.g. revoked token), so the user has no signal their history isn't being recorded.
  - _Fix:_ Capture the error from scrobbleSubmitListen; on failure either enqueue for retry or at minimum log via Log.net.error and, on repeated/auth failures, surface a one-time non-intrusive notice (and re-check core.isScrobbleConfigured()). At a minimum stop using try? so the failure is observable.
- **L5943** [error-handling] fetchCurrentTrackDetails leaves the PREVIOUS track's credits on screen when the People fetch fails for a new track
  - _Why:_ currentTrackPeople drives the credits panel in NowPlayingSheet.swift and NowPlayingView.swift (Credit.rows(from: model.currentTrackPeople)). On a track change A->B the polling loop (line 6082) calls this without first clearing currentTrackPeople; if B's fetch throws (network blip, non-auth error), currentTrackPeople still holds A's people and currentTrackPeopleForId still equals A's id, so the user sees track A's performers attributed to track B, and the guard at line 5932 prevents a retry. The sibling function fetchCurrentTrackLyrics (lines 6010-6015) handles this correctly by clearing to [] and stamping the new id on error, proving the intended contract.
  - _Fix:_ In the catch block, after handleAuthError, add a `guard status.currentTrack?.id == id else { return }` followed by `currentTrackPeople = []` and `currentTrackPeopleForId = id` (mirroring fetchCurrentTrackLyrics) so the stale credits are dropped and the new id is recorded.
- **L6045** [performance] Polling timer fires synchronous core.status() FFI on the MainActor at 1Hz unconditionally — no skip-when-not-playing guard, contradicting the documented rc11 optimization
  - _Why:_ Per CLAUDE.md gap-pattern #2, the rc11 contract is that this poll 'runs at 1Hz and skips entirely when status.state != .playing' to cut idle wakes from thousands/hour to zero. The body here has no `guard status.state == .playing else { return }` — the only `state` references are the beforeState capture and the menu-bar-visibility check. So core.status() (a Rust Inner-mutex acquisition on the main thread) plus refreshDockTile/driveScrobble run every second even when paused, stopped, or idle, reintroducing the idle main-thread wakes the optimization removed.
  - _Fix:_ After capturing before-values, early-return when neither the previous nor the new state is .playing (e.g. only run the full body while status.state == .playing, but still allow one final pass on the playing->paused transition for menu-bar/dock updates). Re-measure Activity Monitor Energy Impact as the CLAUDE.md note requires.
- **L6196** [error-handling] moveUpNext swallows the core.setQueue error with try?, leaving local array reordered but core queue unchanged on failure
  - _Why:_ If setQueue fails, the local upNextUserAdded order has already been mutated (move at line 6183) but the core queue is not updated, producing a silent desync between the displayed order and actual playback order, with no error surfaced to the user. Other mutations in this file (saveQueueAsPlaylist, addToPlaylist, mediaSessionToggleFavorite) surface errors via errorMessage and/or roll back; this one does neither.
  - _Fix:_ Wrap in do/catch: on failure, surface errorMessage and consider rolling back the local move so display and core stay consistent.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/AlbumContextMenu.swift`
- **L66** [error-handling] "Mark All as Played" performs an optimistic local flip with no rollback when the server write fails, leaving the cached played-state lying about the album.
  - _Why:_ On a failed/offline write the menu state and any UI keyed on `playedById` show the album as played (or unplayed) even though the server rejected the change — exactly the silent-corruption optimistic-UI pattern called out in CLAUDE.md gap #5 (the playlist mutations were fixed to roll back; this one was not).
  - _Fix:_ In setPlayed's catch (or in markAllAsPlayed), restore the previous `playedById[album.id]` value on failure, mirroring the rollback already done for removeFromPlaylist/addToPlaylist.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/AlphabetScrollIndex.swift`
- **L131** [accessibility] The alphabet scroll rail is unusable with VoiceOver: it exposes a single ignored element with a label/hint that says "Drag to jump", but provides no adjustable/activatable action a VoiceOver user can invoke.
  - _Why:_ VoiceOver cannot perform a free-form drag, and the children are ignored, so a blind user has no way to trigger `onSelect`. The hint actively tells them to do something they cannot do. The index becomes a decorative, non-operable control for assistive-tech users.
  - _Fix:_ Add an `.accessibilityAdjustableAction { direction in ... }` that advances/retreats through `letters` and calls `onSelect`, and/or expose each letter as its own accessible button with `.accessibilityAction`. Update the hint to describe the adjustable gesture.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/Artwork.swift`
- **L75** [consistency] Global ImagePipeline.shared is reassigned as a side effect inside a lazy `static let pipeline` initializer.
  - _Why:_ `ImagePipeline.shared` only becomes the custom (disk-cached, decompression-enabled, coalescing) pipeline the first time `Artwork.pipeline` is touched. Any Nuke code path that reads `ImagePipeline.shared` before the first `Artwork` view is built (e.g. prefetching, other LazyImage/`.pipeline()`-less requests, warmup) silently gets the default in-memory-only pipeline with no disk cache and different rate-limiting. The coupling is order-dependent and invisible, so it can cause subtle cache-miss / double-download behavior that is hard to diagnose.
  - _Fix:_ Configure `ImagePipeline.shared` once at app startup (e.g. in the App init / a dedicated bootstrap) rather than lazily as a side effect of accessing `Artwork.pipeline`. Keep `Artwork.pipeline` as a pure value and assign `ImagePipeline.shared` explicitly and eagerly so the global is deterministic regardless of which view renders first.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/CommandPalette.swift`
- **L427** [error-handling] runLibrarySearch swallows search failures: on a thrown error it sets libraryResults = nil with no user-visible signal, so a transient/auth/network failure is indistinguishable from a genuine "no results".
  - _Why:_ core.search can throw on network loss, server error, or expired token. The catch discards the error entirely; the palette then either shows only the prefix-matched actions or the "No matches" empty state, telling the user their query found nothing when in fact the request failed. There is no retry hint and no error surfaced (the repo's own CLAUDE.md flags swallowed errors / missing surfacing as a recurring bug class).
  - _Fix:_ Capture the error into a @State (e.g. searchError: String?) and render an inline error row distinct from the empty "No matches" state, or at minimum Log.app.error the failure. Optionally keep the previous results visible and badge a non-fatal error rather than clearing to nil.
- **L480** [error-handling] actionTitleString() extracts the action title by reflecting over LocalizedStringKey's private internal layout (Mirror child labeled "key"); if that layout changes it silently returns "", which then makes every filtered-action search match nothing.
  - _Why:_ LocalizedStringKey has no public accessor for its key string; the "key" child label is an undocumented implementation detail. If Apple renames/restructures it (or wraps a non-String key, e.g. an interpolated key), the function returns "" for every action. Combined with the line-361 filter, "".hasPrefix(trimmed) is always false for non-empty queries, so the entire Actions category quietly disappears from search results with no error surfaced — a silent feature regression that would only be caught by manual testing.
  - _Fix:_ Don't reflect over LocalizedStringKey. Drive search off a stable, owned String. Either add a plain `searchTitle: String` (or reuse PaletteRow.actionTitleById) on PaletteAction and match against that, so titles are a single owned source of truth that can't break across OS updates.
- **L627** [consistency] Action display titles/symbols are duplicated as a hardcoded English dictionary in PaletteRow (actionTitleById / actionSymbolById) that is a separate source of truth from AppModel.PaletteAction.title (a LocalizedStringKey) and .symbol — they can drift, localization is bypassed, and unknown ids render the raw id string.
  - _Why:_ AppModel already carries the canonical title (LocalizedStringKey) and SF Symbol for each action, but PaletteRow ignores both and re-derives them from a parallel hardcoded map. (1) Any new action added in AppModel renders its raw id (e.g. "playback.foo") until someone remembers to also edit two dictionaries here. (2) The LocalizedStringKey titles will never be localized in the UI because the displayed text comes from the English dict, defeating the purpose of using LocalizedStringKey at all. (3) The symbol shown can disagree with the action's declared symbol.
  - _Fix:_ Render directly from the PaletteAction model: pass the resolved PaletteAction (or its title/symbol) into PaletteRow instead of an id, so Text(action.title) is localized and Image(systemName: action.symbol) is authoritative. Delete the two static dictionaries.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/FormatBadge.swift`
- **L37** [bug] Bitrate rounding distorts the most common MP3/AAC bitrates, showing wrong numbers in the badge tooltip
  - _Why:_ For any bitrate 10-399 kbps the code rounds to the nearest multiple of 10, so 128 kbps -> (128+5)/10*10 = 130, 192 -> 190, 256 -> 260, 320 -> 320 (lucky). The tooltip therefore reports inaccurate bitrates for the exact values users care about (128/192/256). raw is already an exact integer from the server (Track.bitrate is Int64), so there is no quantization noise to smooth out; the rounding only manufactures error. There is also no symmetric path: values >= 400 are shown exactly, so the badge is inconsistent (FLAC shows 1411 exactly but a 256 kbps AAC shows 260).
  - _Fix:_ Drop the rounding entirely and display the truncated kbps: `private var bitrateKbps: Int? { guard let raw = track.bitrate, raw > 0 else { return nil }; return Int(raw) / 1000 }`. If smoothing of genuinely noisy values is ever desired, round to the nearest 1 kbps (i.e. `Int((Double(raw)/1000).rounded())`), never to the nearest 10.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/HomeAlbumTile.swift`
- **L59** [accessibility] Album tile advertises .isButton but exposes no accessibility action for its primary single-tap (play) / double-tap (open album) behaviors
  - _Why:_ The tile's two real actions are wired only as `.onTapGesture(count: 1)` (play) and `.onTapGesture(count: 2)` (open album). Tap gestures are not surfaced to VoiceOver, and `children: .contain` keeps the container as a non-activating group. So a VoiceOver or keyboard user focusing the tile sees the `.isButton` trait and the hint 'Click to play, double-click to open' but pressing it (VO + Space) does nothing, and there is no way at all to reach the open-album action assistively. The only reachable control is the nested Play button, which covers play but not navigation.
  - _Fix:_ Add explicit accessibility actions on the tile, e.g. `.accessibilityAction { model.play(album: album) }` for the default action plus `.accessibilityAction(named: Text("Open album")) { model.navPath.append(AppModel.Route.album(album.id)) }`, so both behaviors are invokable without a pointer.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/HomeQuickTile.swift`
- **L73** [accessibility] `.accessibilityElement(children: .combine)` on the outer Button collapses the nested Play button (lines 43-55, with its own `accessibilityLabel("Play \(title)")`) into a single combined element whose only activation is the outer `action` (navigate to album). VoiceOver users therefore cannot trigger `onPlay` (play-without-navigating); that affordance is pointer-hover-only.
  - _Why:_ The Play action is invisible (opacity 0) until hover and is then merged away from the accessibility tree, leaving assistive-tech users with no way to invoke it. Note this mirrors the same convention in ArtistCard.swift (lines 71/111-114), so it is a repo-wide gap rather than a one-off.
  - _Fix:_ Expose the play action to assistive tech, e.g. add `.accessibilityAction(named: "Play") { onPlay() }` to the combined element, or use `.accessibilityElement(children: .contain)` so the nested Play button remains separately focusable.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/InlineLyricsSnippet.swift`
- **L79** [performance] Active-line timer wakes the main run loop at 2 Hz for the entire lifetime of the view, even while playback is paused/stopped. The `.playing` guard only skips the *work*, not the *wake*: `Timer.publish(every: 0.5, on: .main, ...).autoconnect()` schedules a main-thread fire every 0.5s and the closure early-returns, so paused playback still incurs ~7,200 idle main-thread wakes/hour. CLAUDE.md gap pattern #2 explicitly mandates the poll "skips entirely when status.state != .playing" and runs at 1 Hz; this is double the cadence and does not skip the wake.
  - _Why:_ The snippet lives in QueueInspector, which can stay open indefinitely. A free-running 2 Hz main-thread timer that never pauses contradicts the repo's documented idle-wake budget (gap pattern #2: idle wakes cut to zero by skipping entirely when not playing) and needlessly raises Energy Impact while music is paused.
  - _Fix:_ Drive the timer from playback state instead of a constant publisher: store the cancellable in @State and start/stop it in `.onChange(of: model.status.state)` so it only ticks while `.playing`. Match the 1 Hz cadence used elsewhere (`every: 1.0`) unless 2 Hz is measured to be needed.
- **L80** [bug] The highlighted line goes stale on seek-while-paused and on track end. `updateActiveLine()` is invoked from three places — `onAppear`, the `currentLyrics` change handler, and the timer — but the timer is the only one that reacts to position changes, and it is gated behind `state == .playing`. If the user scrubs the transport while paused (or the track reaches `.ended`/`.paused` at a new position), `positionSeconds` changes but none of the three triggers fire, so the snippet keeps showing the pre-seek line until playback resumes.
  - _Why:_ Seeking while paused is a normal interaction; the snippet then displays the wrong 'current' line, which is user-visible incorrect state.
  - _Fix:_ Add `.onChange(of: model.status.positionSeconds) { _, _ in updateActiveLine() }` (or react to a seek-specific signal) so a position change updates the active line regardless of play/pause state, while keeping the periodic timer gated to `.playing` for the smooth-advance case.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/InstantMixSheet.swift`
- **L337** [gap-stub] The .playlist seed path (icon + subtitle rendering) is unreachable dead code: the picker can never surface a playlist as an instant-mix seed.
  - _Why:_ Jellyfin's /Items/{id}/InstantMix accepts a playlist id, so seeding a mix from a playlist is a real capability the UI structurally implies (full render branches + generateInstantMix handles `.playlist`). But because the seed search never returns playlists and allCandidates omits them, a user can never choose a playlist seed here. The branches survive only because Swift's exhaustive switch over SearchItem mandates them, masking the gap.
  - _Fix:_ Either (a) include playlists in seed candidates — add a `playlists` source (a dedicated playlist search / filter) into `allCandidates` plus a `.playlists` SeedCategory — or (b) if playlist seeding is intentionally unsupported, remove the dead `.playlist` arms (collapse to a default) and document the exclusion so the render code matches reality.
- **L451** [bug] Switching the category tab does not re-validate the current selection, so a selected seed that is filtered out of the visible list stays selected and stays generatable.
  - _Why:_ Pick a track while the 'All' tab is active, then switch to the 'Genres' tab. The track is no longer in `candidates` (so the row/checkmark disappears), yet the footer still reads 'Selected: <track>' and the Generate button stays enabled. The user generates a mix from an item that is not visible in the current filter — confusing and inconsistent with the displayed list. `apply(results:)` only re-validates the selection against new search results, never against a category change.
  - _Fix:_ When `category` changes, clear `selectedSeed` if it is no longer present in the filtered `candidates` (e.g. add a `didSet` on `category` or an explicit handler in the categoryBar button that runs `if !candidates.contains(where: { $0.id == selectedSeed?.id }) { selectedSeed = nil }`).

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/LibraryFilterPopover.swift`
- **L21** [bug] TrackFormat.alac container tokens include M4A/MP4, which also match lossy AAC files, so selecting ALAC false-positively keeps AAC tracks; there is also no AAC/AAC filter option at all.
  - _Why:_ Jellyfin reports container, not codec. AAC audio is almost always delivered in an M4A/MP4 container, so a track.container of 'M4A' for an AAC file will match the ALAC bucket. A user filtering for ALAC (lossless) will see AAC (lossy) tracks mixed in, and pure-AAC libraries have no correct format filter. The format filter is therefore inaccurate for the most common lossy case.
  - _Fix:_ Filter on codec rather than container if the core exposes it, or split the M4A/MP4 container into ALAC vs AAC using a codec/profile signal. Add an explicit AAC TrackFormat case. If only container is available, document the limitation and avoid claiming codec-level accuracy.
- **L75** [gap-stub] LibraryFilter.onlyDownloaded is a dead filter dimension: it is counted in activeGroupCount/isActive but never consumed by any passesFilter, and its toggle only renders when showDownloaded is true while supportsDownloads is hard-coded false.
  - _Why:_ Today the toggle is unreachable (supportsDownloads returns false), so the field is pure dead weight. The moment supportsDownloads is flipped true, the toggle appears, sets onlyDownloaded, flips isActive on, triggers .filter(passesFilter) — and filters nothing, because no passesFilter checks it. That is a latent silent no-op: a user-facing toggle that pretends to work.
  - _Fix:_ Either remove onlyDownloaded until downloads filtering is wired, or implement it: add `if filter.onlyDownloaded, !model.isDownloaded(...) { return false }` to the relevant passesFilter functions when supportsDownloads becomes true. Don't ship a counted-but-unhandled filter dimension.
- **L154** [consistency] Format and Duration filter groups are always rendered regardless of the active library tab, but only the Tracks tab applies them; selecting a Format/Duration on Albums/Artists/Playlists makes the filter appear active yet changes nothing.
  - _Why:_ LibraryView.passesFilter(_:Album), passesFilter(_:Artist), passesFilter(_:Playlist) never consult filter.formats or filter.durations (only passesFilter(_:Track) does). Because activeGroupCount counts formats/durations, the filter button shows e.g. '1 filter active' and filteredAlbums runs .filter(passesFilter) for no effect — the user sees an 'active' filter that silently does nothing, and the unchanged list looks like a bug.
  - _Fix:_ Pass the current LibraryTab into LibraryFilterPopover and only render formatGroup/durationGroup for the tracks tab (and yearGroup only where year applies), or have the album/artist/playlist passesFilter honor these dimensions. At minimum, hide groups that don't apply to the active tab.
- **L394** [accessibility] RangeSlider thumbs expose accessibilityLabel/accessibilityValue but no adjustable action, so VoiceOver/keyboard users can read the year range but cannot change it.
  - _Why:_ The only way to move a thumb is the (currently broken) DragGesture. There is no .accessibilityAdjustableAction, so assistive-technology users have no path to set the year range at all. Combined with the drag bug above, the year filter is inaccessible by any input for these users.
  - _Fix:_ Add .accessibilityAdjustableAction { direction in adjust low/high by one year for .increment/.decrement, clamped to bounds } to each thumb (or to the slider as a whole), so the control is operable without a pointer drag.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/LoadingSkeleton.swift`
- **L137** [bug] Skeleton shimmer sweep runs at 5 cycles/second (0.2s repeatForever, no autoreverse) — a strobing flicker, not a smooth shimmer.
  - _Why:_ The gradient band travels fully across the view and snaps back 5 times per second. That is a flickering strobe over every skeleton placeholder during library first-paint, not the slow gloss a loading shimmer is meant to be. Every other repeating animation in the app is far slower (VinylDisc uses secondsPerRotation; PinnedStationTile uses 0.9s). A 5Hz full-width strobe across a grid of album/artist tiles is visually jarring and reads as a rendering glitch. reduceMotion gates the band entirely, so the only effect of the wrong duration is on users who do NOT have reduce-motion on — i.e. everyone by default.
  - _Fix:_ Raise the duration to a typical shimmer cadence (~1.2-1.5s), e.g. .linear(duration: 1.3).repeatForever(autoreverses: false). Optionally add a short delay between sweeps so the snap-back isn't visible.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/LyricsView.swift`
- **L109** [bug] LRC metadata/header tags ([ar:], [ti:], [al:], [by:], [offset:], etc.) are rendered as visible lyric text lines instead of being stripped.
  - _Why:_ Standard .lrc files begin with ID-tag lines like [ti:Title], [ar:Artist], [al:Album], [by:Transcriber], [offset:+250]. For each, parseTimestamp returns nil (the field after ':' isn't an integer), so extractTimestamps returns ([], line) and parseLRC files it into the untimed bucket. Those lines are then displayed verbatim in the lyrics pane (e.g. the user sees a 'lyric' reading 'ar:Some Artist' or 'offset:+250'). If a file mixes header tags with timed lyrics, the headers also get appended after the timed lines (lines 86-89). This is a user-facing content-correctness bug.
  - _Fix:_ In parseLRC, detect and drop ID tags: a bracket whose inner text matches ^(ti|ar|al|au|by|offset|re|ve|length|lang):.*$ should be consumed as metadata, not emitted as a lyric line. At minimum filter them out; ideally apply [offset:] to all timestamps.
- **L252** [performance] Scrolling-lyrics active-line poll fires at 5Hz unconditionally and does not skip while playback is paused, contradicting the repo's documented idle-wake / skip-when-paused contract.
  - _Why:_ CLAUDE.md gap pattern #2 explicitly establishes a 1Hz cadence that skips when status.state != .playing, specifically to cut idle wakes. This timer runs at 0.2s (5x that rate) and calls updateActiveLine() — which reads model.status and linearly scans every line — even when the track is paused and nothing can change. While the Now Playing lyrics panel is open and paused, that is 5 wakes/sec doing pointless work and forcing scrollTo re-evaluation. The sibling InlineLyricsSnippet uses 0.5s for the same job. Note this is not a hard timer leak: .onReceive(...autoconnect()) is the standard idiom and SwiftUI cancels the subscription on view disappearance.
  - _Fix:_ Drop to 1Hz (or 0.5s to match InlineLyricsSnippet) and early-return from the closure when model.status.state != .playing, mirroring the core.status() poll contract. The activeId still gets a correct initial value from .onAppear's updateActiveLine().

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/MiniPlayerView.swift`
- **L151** [bug] Idle auto-hide can yank the controls (and their anchors) out from under an open settings Menu or volume popover. rearmIdleHide guards only against scrubbing (!isScrubbing), not against an open Menu/popover.
  - _Why:_ Open the '…' menu (or the volume popover) and hold the cursor still for 2s while still hovering the mini player: the idle timer fires, showControls→false, the anchoring Image/Button is destroyed, and the open menu/popover dismisses mid-interaction. Adjusting volume while the cursor is parked over the slider is exactly the 'still hovering, not moving' state that triggers the hide.
  - _Fix:_ Track whether the menu/volume popover is presented (e.g. an isMenuOpen/@State bound to MiniVolumePopover's isPresented and the Menu) and add it to the idle guard: `guard isHovering, !isScrubbing, !isMenuOpen else { return }`, mirroring the existing isScrubbing carve-out. Re-arm the timer when those popovers close.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/NoSearchResultsState.swift`
- **L9** [dead-code] The entire NoSearchResultsState view is dead code — nothing in the app instantiates it. The live search empty-state is ZeroResultsState in Screens/SearchView.swift.
  - _Why:_ A whole unreferenced View ships in the binary and invites confusion: a future maintainer may edit NoSearchResultsState expecting it to affect search, while the real screen (ZeroResultsState) silently diverges. The two already disagree (NoSearchResultsState says 'use fewer or different terms'; ZeroResultsState says 'narrow your query' and offers an artist-name suggestion), so copy/UX drift is already happening.
  - _Fix:_ Delete NoSearchResultsState.swift, or, if it is meant to be the canonical empty-state, replace the private ZeroResultsState in SearchView with it and delete ZeroResultsState. Do not keep two near-identical zero-results views.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/OfflineBanner.swift`
- **L83** [accessibility] Retry button is flattened into a single static-text accessibility element, making it impossible for VoiceOver users to activate.
  - _Why:_ `.accessibilityElement(children: .combine)` merges every descendant — including the `Button(action: onRetry)` on lines 56-71 — into one element. Adding `.isStaticText` then declares that combined element non-interactive. A VoiceOver user hears "Can't reach <host>. Trying again…" but the only recovery affordance (Retry) is absorbed into static text and cannot be tapped. The button's own `.accessibilityLabel("offline.retry.a11y")` on line 72 becomes dead code — proof the author intended the button to be a reachable, separately-labelled control. This is a repo-wide pattern (StreamErrorToast.swift:118-120, ServerUnreachableBanner.swift:83-85 are identical), so the impairment is systemic.
  - _Fix:_ Don't collapse an interactive container with `children: .combine` + `.isStaticText`. Either (a) keep the container as a plain layout and let the Text + Button expose themselves as separate elements (drop the container-level `.accessibilityElement`/`.accessibilityLabel`/`.accessibilityAddTraits`), or (b) use `.accessibilityElement(children: .contain)` so the combined status text and the actionable Retry button both remain reachable. Same fix applies to StreamErrorToast and ServerUnreachableBanner.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/PlayerBar.swift`
- **L262** [accessibility] Scrubber seek only fires on onEditingChanged(false); VoiceOver adjustable gestures update the binding but never trigger the seek, so VoiceOver users cannot scrub playback position.
  - _Why:_ VoiceOver exposes a Slider as an 'adjustable' element. Incrementing/decrementing it invokes the binding's set (mutating scrubPosition) but does NOT fire onEditingChanged. Because model.seek(...) is only called in the onEditingChanged(false) branch, the position the VoiceOver user dials in is silently discarded — the seek never executes. The control announces a value the app then ignores. (Same pattern exists in MiniPlayerView.swift:402, so it is a codebase-wide scrubber a11y gap.)
  - _Fix:_ Add an explicit .accessibilityAdjustableAction { direction in ... } (or move the seek into the set closure / debounce it) so increment/decrement performs model.seek(...) directly, and set isScrubbing during set so displayPosition reflects the in-flight value for VoiceOver.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/PlaylistCard.swift`
- **L74** [accessibility] accessibilityElement(children: .combine) flattens the inner Play overlay button into the card's merged element, so its 'Play <playlist>' action is unreachable to VoiceOver — assistive-tech users can only Open the playlist, not play it from the card.
  - _Why:_ With .combine, SwiftUI merges all descendants (including the nested Play Button) into one element and concatenates labels, dropping the child's independent activation. HomeAlbumTile.swift uses .accessibilityElement(children: .contain) precisely so its play-overlay button stays a reachable child. PlaylistCard (like ArtistCard.swift:111) uses .combine, losing the primary Play affordance for VoiceOver. (Mitigated only because PlaylistContextMenu offers a reachable 'Play' item.)
  - _Fix:_ Either switch to .accessibilityElement(children: .contain) like HomeAlbumTile, or keep .combine on the card and attach .accessibilityAction(named: "Play") { model.play(playlist: playlist) } to expose the play action.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/QueueInspector.swift`
- **L471** [performance] The Up Next list embeds an inner vertical ScrollView inside the screen's outer ScrollView, producing nested-scroll hijacking on macOS once more than 8 user-queued items exist.
  - _Why:_ Two stacked vertical ScrollViews fight for trackpad scroll events; the wheel/trackpad gesture gets captured by the inner region and the outer page stops scrolling (or vice-versa) depending on cursor position, a well-known SwiftUI/AppKit anti-pattern. The fixed inner height makes this reachable for any reasonably long Up Next.
  - _Fix:_ Drop the inner ScrollView and render the LazyVStack directly in the outer scroll (let the page scroll), or move the whole inspector to a single List/ScrollView and remove the bounded-height clamp.
- **L471** [performance] `upNextList` nests a vertical `ScrollView` with a fixed `boundedListHeight` (max 8 rows / 352pt, line 502) INSIDE the outer page `ScrollView` (line 70). For queues longer than 8 items the inner scroll view captures two-finger scroll gestures, making it hard to scroll the outer page past the Up Next region, and the fixed cap hides items 9+ behind an inner scrollbar that competes with the page scroll.
  - _Why:_ Nested same-axis scroll views are a well-known macOS/SwiftUI gesture-conflict source and degrade the experience for any real-world queue (>8 tracks). The 8-row cap also means a long Up Next list is only partially reachable, and the drag-to-reorder gestures live inside the inner scroller, compounding gesture ambiguity.
  - _Fix:_ Drop the inner ScrollView and the fixed height: render the Up Next `LazyVStack` directly in the outer ScrollView (let the page scroll), or if a bounded region is required, gate it so the inner scroll only engages above a threshold and ensure the full list remains reachable. At minimum let `boundedListHeight` grow to the full item count when small so short queues aren't clipped and long ones aren't trapped.
- **L535** [performance] The 'Playing From' section renders every auto-queue entry eagerly in a plain VStack+ForEach with no LazyVStack and no height bound, so a large source context (full album/playlist) instantiates all rows up front.
  - _Why:_ Unlike upNextList (LazyVStack + height cap), this section is non-lazy and unbounded. When 'Playing From' is an album or large playlist, dozens-to-hundreds of QueueInspectorRow views (each with an Artwork) are built immediately, inflating layout cost on the MainActor every time the inspector opens or the queue changes.
  - _Fix:_ Wrap the ForEach in a LazyVStack and apply a bounded-height frame the same way upNextList does, so off-screen auto-queue rows are not materialized.
- **L583** [gap-stub] `jumpTo(entry:)` is a non-functional stub: it ignores its `entry` argument entirely and only shows a "Jump to track coming soon" toast. The double-tap gesture on every "Playing From" auto-queue row (line 544: `.onTapGesture(count: 2) { jumpTo(entry: entry) }`) is therefore a dead feature path — double-clicking a queued track does NOT jump playback to it.
  - _Why:_ The UI advertises a jump-to-track interaction (double-click) that does nothing useful, contradicting user expectation for a queue list. Per CLAUDE.md gap pattern #1, a body that only surfaces a 'coming soon' message is a live gap, not a TODO. The capability is feasible (the model already has `core.setQueue` + `audio.play(track:)` and computes the full track list in `moveUpNext`), so this is unfinished wiring rather than an impossible feature.
  - _Fix:_ Wire `jumpTo` to actually reposition playback: rebuild the full track array (current + upNextUserAdded + upNextAutoQueue), find the index of `entry.track`, call `core.setQueue(tracks:startIndex:)` with that index and `audio.play(track: entry.track)` (mirroring `AppModel.play`). Until the FFI/semantics land (tracked as #282), at minimum remove the double-tap affordance so the UI doesn't promise an action it can't perform.
- **L685** [accessibility] The Up Next row's Remove control is gated behind mouse hover (`if removable, isHovering`), so keyboard and VoiceOver users have no way to remove a queued track, even though the row falsely advertises a button trait.
  - _Why:_ A VoiceOver user lands on a row announced as a button, activates it, and nothing happens — the remove affordance never renders because there is no hover. Reordering is reachable via Option+Arrow (lines 717-729), but removal is mouse-only, making queue editing partially inaccessible.
  - _Fix:_ Add an `.accessibilityAction(named: "Remove") { onRemove() }` on the row when removable (and/or render the remove button when the row is focused, not just hovered), and drop the misleading .isButton trait if the row has no primary activation.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/SearchInstantDropdown.swift`
- **L63** [consistency] onDisappear reaches into AppModel internals and cancels model.searchTask directly, rather than going through an API. This couples the view to the model's task field and can cancel a search that belongs to a different/newer presenter.
  - _Why:_ Direct cross-object task cancellation is fragile: there is exactly one searchTask slot, so teardown of one consumer can abort an in-flight search owned by another. It also bypasses runInstantSearch's own cancellation bookkeeping (which already cancels the prior task on each call). Combined with the dead-code status this is currently inert, but it is the wrong lifecycle contract to copy if the dropdown is revived.
  - _Fix:_ Expose an explicit AppModel.cancelInstantSearch() that nils the task and resets instantSearchResults = .empty, and call that from onDisappear; or clear query (which already cancels via onChange) instead of poking searchTask directly.
- **L92** [dead-code] Even if the dropdown were rendered, its Playlists and Genres sections can never appear: the core SearchResults type has no playlists/genres and AppModel.runInstantSearch hardcodes them to empty arrays.
  - _Why:_ results.playlists and results.genres are always empty, so the guarded sections render nothing and the PlaylistsGrid / PlaylistMiniTile / GenresRow / GenreTile structs (lines 449-565) are unreachable even within an otherwise-live dropdown. Dead branches that look like working features mislead future maintainers into thinking playlist/genre instant results exist.
  - _Fix:_ Remove the playlists/genres sections and their tile structs until core.search returns those facets, or extend the core SearchResults + runInstantSearch to actually populate playlists/genres before relying on these UI sections.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/ServerUnreachableBanner.swift`
- **L36** [consistency] User-facing banner strings are hard-coded English literals instead of LocalizedStringKey, unlike the rest of the UI (Sidebar uses keys like "sidebar.nav.home").
  - _Why:_ The app is localized (String Catalog work tracked in #560; Sidebar/nav use LocalizedStringKey). These error strings will never translate, so a non-English user sees mixed-language UI exactly at an error moment. `accessibilityLabel("Retry server connection")` is likewise an untranslated literal.
  - _Fix:_ Move the message and the "Retry" label into LocalizedStringKey / String(localized:) entries (e.g. "banner.server_unreachable.named" with an interpolated host argument and "banner.server_unreachable.generic").

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/Sidebar.swift`
- **L425** [consistency] `favoritesRow` never reflects the active/selected state, unlike every other nav row, so selecting Favorites gives no visual highlight and no `.isSelected` accessibility trait.
  - _Why:_ `navItem` computes `active = model.screen == screen && model.navPath.isEmpty` and applies accent color, a selection bar, `Theme.surface2` background, and `.isSelected`. `favoritesRow` hard-codes `Theme.ink2` and only `.isButton`. Since `.favorites` is a real `Screen` case reachable via `selectTab(.favorites)`, the Favorites row is the one top-level destination that never appears selected — visually and for VoiceOver users it looks inactive even when it is the current screen.
  - _Fix:_ Compute `let active = model.screen == .favorites && model.navPath.isEmpty` and apply the same accent foreground, selection background/bar, and `.isSelected` trait used by `navItem` (or route Favorites through `navItem` itself).
- **L567** [bug] Inline rename can commit twice: `onSubmit` fires a commit, and the resulting focus loss then triggers the `onChange(of: isFocused)` blur branch which commits again.
  - _Why:_ Pressing Return runs `onSubmit` -> commit (async). The field then loses focus, firing `onChange` with `focused == false`. There is a guard `model.sidebarEditingPlaylistId != nil`, but the first commit clears that id inside an async Task that may not have run yet (it `await`s), so the guard can still see a non-nil id and schedule a second `commitSidebarPlaylistEdit`. For a brand-new playlist this races two `createPlaylist` calls; for a rename it double-fires `renamePlaylist`. The id is cleared synchronously at the top of `commitSidebarPlaylistEdit` (AppModel.swift:4831) only after the awaited body begins, so ordering is not guaranteed.
  - _Fix:_ Make the blur handler idempotent by clearing `sidebarEditingPlaylistId` synchronously before launching the commit Task, or set a local `committed` flag in `onSubmit` and skip the `onChange` branch when it's set, so only one commit path runs per edit session.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/StreamErrorToast.swift`
- **L45** [consistency] User-facing toast body text is a hard-coded English string built via interpolation, while every Button label in the same view uses String Catalog keys — the error message itself is not localizable.
  - _Why:_ The most prominent text in the component — the actual error sentence the user reads — bypasses localization entirely. Buttons are localized but the message is not, so a non-English build shows a hard-coded English sentence with localized buttons. Inconsistent and ships untranslated copy.
  - _Fix:_ Move the message into the String Catalog with a format argument, e.g. message becomes String(localized: "stream.error.skipping \(trackName)") or a LocalizedStringKey with interpolation, matching the localization approach used for the buttons.
- **L80** [consistency] accessibilityLabel is passed a raw String literal ('stream.error.retry.a11y' and 'common.dismiss.a11y') instead of a localized Text/LocalizedStringKey, so these labels render the verbatim key string rather than the localized value — inconsistent with line 90 which uses Text(...).
  - _Why:_ The String overload of accessibilityLabel(_:) treats its argument as a verbatim, already-final string and does NOT resolve it through the String Catalog. The Text/LocalizedStringKey overload (used on line 90) does. So VoiceOver would announce the literal token 'stream.error.retry.a11y' instead of 'Retry'. This is currently masked because the .combine issue (line 118) makes all three labels dead, but it is a latent bug that surfaces the moment the combine bug is fixed.
  - _Fix:_ Wrap the keys in Text for consistent catalog resolution: .accessibilityLabel(Text("stream.error.retry.a11y")) and .accessibilityLabel(Text("common.dismiss.a11y")). Same pattern already used correctly on line 90.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/TextFieldSpaceGuard.swift`
- **L101** [bug] The text-field detection only recognizes NSTextField and NSTextView whose delegate is an NSTextField; it misses NSSearchField, NSComboBox, secure fields whose field editor delegate isn't a plain NSTextField, and standalone editable NSTextViews — so space is NOT guarded in those controls.
  - _Why:_ NSSearchField is an NSTextField subclass so `responder is NSTextField` catches it only if the search field itself is first responder, but while editing the first responder is the field editor (an NSTextView) whose delegate is the NSSearchField — and `tv.delegate is NSTextField` is true for NSSearchField (subclass) but false for NSComboBox or any custom control acting as field-editor delegate. Standalone editable NSTextView (delegate not an NSTextField) returns false. In those cases isTextField is false and the guard returns the event, so whatever global space shortcut exists fires while the user is typing in that control. Inconsistent guarding across field types.
  - _Fix:_ Broaden detection: treat the responder as a text field if it is any NSText/NSControl that isEditable, e.g. check `responder is NSTextView && (responder as! NSTextView).isEditable`, or check window.firstResponder against window.fieldEditor(false, for:) ownership, or test for NSTextInputClient conformance. Avoid hard-coding the NSTextField delegate class.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/TopTrackRow.swift`
- **L125** [accessibility] Redundant/conflicting accessibility configuration: the row is a SwiftUI Button, then additionally marked .focusable(true), .accessibilityElement(children: .combine), and .accessibilityAddTraits(.isButton) — producing double button semantics and an extra focus stop.
  - _Why:_ A SwiftUI Button is already an accessibility element with the .isButton trait and is already keyboard-focusable. Re-adding .isButton via accessibilityAddTraits and forcing .focusable(true) on top of the Button can create a duplicate trait announcement and, depending on focus engine, two focus stops for one visual row (the Button and the explicitly-focusable wrapper). The .accessibilityElement(children: .combine) on top of an interactive Button can also strip the button's own action element the way it does in StreamErrorToast. Net effect for VoiceOver/keyboard users is inconsistent navigation on these rows.
  - _Fix:_ Drop the redundant .accessibilityAddTraits(.isButton) (the Button supplies it) and the explicit .focusable(true) unless a specific focus behavior is needed; if a combined label is desired, set it directly on the Button with .accessibilityLabel/.accessibilityHint without .accessibilityElement(children: .combine), so the button's action element is preserved.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/TrackInfoSheet.swift`
- **L111** [accessibility] In each metadata row the field-name label is hidden from VoiceOver and the value carries no combined label, so under the sheet's children:.contain element a VoiceOver user hears bare values with no context ("1969", "5:33", "FLAC · 320 kbps") and cannot tell album from year from duration from format.
  - _Why:_ Hiding the descriptive label while exposing only the value strips the only context that tells the user which field they're reading. The values are individually navigable (children:.contain) but contextless.
  - _Fix:_ Give each row a combined label, e.g. on the HStack add `.accessibilityElement(children: .ignore)` + `.accessibilityLabel("\(String(localized: label)): \(value)")` (or set the value Text's `.accessibilityLabel("\(label) \(value)")`), so VoiceOver announces field name plus value.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/TrackListRow.swift`
- **L145** [accessibility] `.accessibilityElement(children: .combine)` plus an overriding `.accessibilityLabel` collapses the row into one element and drops the favorite Button's action; VoiceOver users cannot favorite/unfavorite a track from the list.
  - _Why:_ Combining children and then replacing the label with an explicit string means the child Button's accessibility action is not surfaced on the combined element, so there is no VoiceOver-reachable affordance to toggle favorite. (TrackRow.swift has the same gap via `.ignore` at its l.162.) The only actions exposed are the row's play/now-playing.
  - _Fix:_ Add an explicit `.accessibilityAction(named: isFav ? "Unfavorite" : "Favorite") { model.toggleFavorite(track: track) }` on the combined row so the favorite toggle remains reachable, or use `.accessibilityRepresentation` that preserves the heart as a separate actionable element.
- **L202** [bug] When onSelect == nil the row wraps its label in an inner Button (model.play) while the outer view is ALSO .focusable() with its own .onKeyPress(.return){ model.play }. This creates two competing keyboard-focus targets nested inside each other.
  - _Why:_ On macOS a Button is itself focusable; nesting it inside a .focusable() container makes Tab/arrow focus land non-deterministically on either the inner Button or the outer row. The focus ring overlay is keyed only on the OUTER `$isFocused` (`.stroke(isFocused ? Theme.accent.opacity(0.6) : .clear ...)` l.127), so when focus lands on the inner Button the row shows NO focus indicator, and the arrow-key navigation that depends on `isFocused -> model.focusedTrackId` (l.152-156) silently stops working. The sibling TrackRow.swift avoids this by NOT wrapping in a Button (it uses `.onTapGesture(count:1){ onPlay?() }`). This no-onSelect path is live (e.g. GenreDetailView calls `TrackListRow(track:tracks:index:)` with no onSelect).
  - _Fix:_ Mirror TrackRow.swift: drop the inner Button entirely and attach a tap gesture (e.g. `.onTapGesture { model.play(tracks: tracks, startIndex: index) }`) to the single focusable outer view, so there is exactly one focus target and the focus ring + arrow navigation stay consistent.
- **L282** [bug] The favorite heart is wired to fire toggleFavorite from TWO sources: the Button's own action AND a FavoriteTapShield highPriorityGesture, both calling model.toggleFavorite(track:). Single-toggle correctness relies entirely on undocumented gesture-priority winning over the Button's built-in tap.
  - _Why:_ If the highPriorityGesture does not fully suppress the plain Button's internal tap (SwiftUI gesture-priority across a Button boundary is not contractually guaranteed and has regressed across OS releases), the heart toggles twice and cancels itself out -> tapping favorite appears to do nothing. Because toggleFavorite reads isFavorite from the optimistic cache each call, two fires produce a net no-op rather than a visible error.
  - _Fix:_ Pick one mechanism. Either keep the Button action and drop FavoriteTapShield, or make the favorite a non-Button view (Image) whose only tap handler is the shield gesture. Don't drive the same mutation from both a Button action and an overlapping high-priority gesture.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/TrackRow.swift`
- **L191** [bug] `.onKeyPress(.space)` unconditionally returns `.handled` and toggles GLOBAL transport play/pause from a focused row, with no guard that this row is the active track.
  - _Why:_ A row is `.focusable()` and gains focus on click/tab. Pressing Space while merely browsing a focused (non-playing) row toggles the whole player's transport — surprising for a list cell, and it consumes Space so it can never reach any spacebar-activatable control or scroll behavior. Unlike Return (which plays *this* row via onPlay), Space acts on unrelated global state regardless of which row is focused. TrackListRow.swift:177 shares the pattern, so this is a consistency-wide choice, but it remains a questionable affordance.
  - _Fix:_ Either scope Space to act only when `isActive` (this row is the current track), or move global play/pause to a single screen-level/menu key binding instead of every row, and return `.ignored` so the event isn't trapped when the row isn't the player target.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/TrackSelectionBanner.swift`
- **L52** [bug] The 'Queue' button calls `model.addToQueue(tracks:)`, which (per AppModel.swift:5111) falls through to `play(tracks:startIndex:0)` and CLOBBERS the current queue when nothing is playing, and otherwise appends — so 'Queue' silently means 'replace & start playing' in the common empty-player case.
  - _Why:_ A user multi-selecting tracks and clicking 'Queue' with no active playback expects them queued, not for playback to start immediately and the existing (empty) queue to be replaced. This is the known #282 queue-semantics gap, but the banner's label 'Queue' actively misrepresents the behavior. The banner is in scope; it should at least not promise 'append' when the underlying call replaces+plays.
  - _Fix:_ Once core `append_to_queue` lands (#282), point this at true append semantics. Until then, disable/relabel the Queue action when `status.currentTrack == nil`, or label it to reflect that it begins playback when idle.
- **L76** [error-handling] The destructive 'Remove' action fires `onRemove()` immediately with no confirmation, while the comparable Play/Queue/Favorite actions are non-destructive. A multi-track removal is one stray click away.
  - _Why:_ `onRemove` is the playlist-removal path (LibraryView passes it nil; the destructive button only appears in playlist scope). Removing N selected tracks from a playlist is a server mutation with user-visible consequences; a single click in this dense banner triggers it with no 'Are you sure' and no undo affordance surfaced here. The banner can't know whether the caller's onRemove is undoable.
  - _Fix:_ Gate the destructive remove behind a confirmationDialog (e.g. \"Remove \(count) tracks from this playlist?\") or ensure every onRemove caller provides an undo path; at minimum require a confirm for count > 1.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/LyrebirdApp.swift`
- **L31** [error-handling] AppModel construction failure crashes the app with fatalError instead of presenting a recoverable error UI.
  - _Why:_ If the Rust core fails to initialize (e.g. corrupt on-disk state, keychain/permission failure, disk full), the user gets an immediate hard crash with no diagnostics path and no way to recover or reset state. For a shipping consumer app, a fatalError at launch on a non-programmer-error condition (a thrown runtime error, not a precondition violation) is a poor failure mode.
  - _Fix:_ Catch the error, store it, and render a dedicated failure scene (with a "reset local data" / "export diagnostics" affordance and the error text) instead of fatalError, so a recoverable core-init failure doesn't brick the app.
- **L45** [concurrency] appDelegate.bind(appModel:) is invoked from a SwiftUI .task on RootView, and bind() cancels and recreates the dock-badge observer task each time; if the WindowGroup content's task re-runs (view identity churn / multiple windows), the observer is torn down and rebuilt redundantly.
  - _Why:_ AppDelegate.bind does dockBadgeTask?.cancel(); dockBadgeTask = startDockBadgeObserver(model:). A .task on the WindowGroup root runs per view-identity lifetime. Opening additional WindowGroup windows or any identity change re-invokes bind, churning the long-lived dock-badge observation Task. It is not a leak (each bind cancels the prior), but it's fragile lifecycle wiring: the canonical place to bind the app delegate to the model is applicationDidFinishLaunching or a one-shot, not a view .task that can fire more than once.
  - _Fix:_ Bind the model to the AppDelegate once (e.g. guard inside bind() that appModel === appModel already set, or bind in applicationDidFinishLaunching), so re-running the view task does not restart the dock-badge observer.
- **L365** [bug] The mini-player Toggle's setter ignores the value SwiftUI passes and unconditionally calls model.toggleMiniPlayer(), so the toggle action is decoupled from the requested state.
  - _Why:_ toggleMiniPlayer() does isMiniPlayerVisible.toggle(). If the menu Toggle and the model state ever momentarily disagree about the current value (e.g. the window was closed via the OS, which sets isMiniPlayerVisible=false through the willCloseNotification handler, before the menu re-reads get), invoking set flips from the model's value rather than driving to the value SwiftUI intended. A binding setter should honor its newValue (set: { model.isMiniPlayerVisible = $0 }) so get/set stay consistent and idempotent. As written, two rapid activations or a state change racing the menu can leave the toggle out of sync with the actual window.
  - _Fix:_ set: { model.isMiniPlayerVisible = $0 } (drive to the requested value) instead of discarding it and toggling. The onChange(of: model.isMiniPlayerVisible) handler in RootView already opens/closes the window from the state, so setting the bool is sufficient.
- **L383** [bug] Play/Pause is bound to the bare Space key (modifiers: []) as a global app command, which SwiftUI does not auto-suppress while a text field has focus.
  - _Why:_ Unlike AppKit's responder chain, a SwiftUI .keyboardShortcut(.space, modifiers: []) menu command competes with first-responder text input. The app has multiple text-entry surfaces (search/find via focusSearch/requestFind, command palette ⌘K, new-playlist naming via beginNewPlaylist). When a track is loaded (currentTrack != nil so the command is enabled), pressing Space while typing in those fields can be intercepted as play/pause instead of inserting a space, or double-fire. This is a known SwiftUI footgun for the unmodified Space shortcut.
  - _Fix:_ Only enable the bare-Space command when no text field is focused (gate via a focus-state flag in AppModel), or remove the menu-level Space shortcut and handle play/pause via an AppKit local key monitor / .onKeyPress at a scope that excludes text editors.
- **L453** [bug] Window-tiling menu items gate .disabled on NSApp.keyWindow == nil, a non-observable AppKit value SwiftUI cannot react to, so the enabled/disabled state of "Tile Left/Right" is stale.
  - _Why:_ SwiftUI only re-evaluates a Commands body (and thus .disabled) when one of its tracked dependencies changes. NSApp.keyWindow is plain AppKit state with no Combine/Observation publisher, so there is no dependency to trigger re-evaluation when the key window appears or disappears. The disabled flag is captured once at body-build time and can be wrong (command enabled when there is no key window, or disabled when one exists), causing tileCurrentWindow to no-op via its guard or the shortcut to appear unavailable.
  - _Fix:_ Drop the .disabled(NSApp.keyWindow == nil) (tileCurrentWindow already guards on NSApp.keyWindow and safely returns), or drive disabled from an @Observable property that is actually updated on NSWindow.didBecomeKey/didResignKey notifications.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/LyrebirdErrorPresenter.swift`
- **L56** [bug] Error classification depends on `error.localizedDescription` which, for the UniFFI flat error, is `String(reflecting: self)` — Swift's reflection format, not a stable string. Substring matching against it is brittle and also subject to false positives from server-supplied response bodies.
  - _Why:_ Confirmed in generated bindings: `extension LyrebirdError: Foundation.LocalizedError { public var errorDescription: String? { String(reflecting: self) } }`. So `localizedDescription` = e.g. `LyrebirdCore.LyrebirdError.Server(message: "server returned an error: 500 <body>")`. (a) The matching only works by accident of reflection formatting; a future UniFFI/Swift change to that format silently breaks ALL classification, dumping every error to `error.other`. (b) The `Server` body text is embedded in the matched string, so a 5xx error page whose body contains `not logged in` or `401` would be misclassified as auth-expired and could trigger a spurious sign-out prompt; a body containing `forbidden`/`not found`/`rate limit` would mis-route inside the server block.
  - _Fix:_ Switch from substring matching on `localizedDescription` to a `switch` over the actual typed cases (`if let e = error as? LyrebirdError { switch e { case .forbidden: ... } }`). The generated `LyrebirdError` enum exposes exact cases (Forbidden/NotFound/RateLimit/Server/Auth/AuthExpired/Network/Decode/Storage/Credentials/Audio/InvalidInput/SelfSignedCertificate/...). Keep the string-matching path only as a fallback for non-LyrebirdError errors.
- **L95** [gap-stub] No branch for the `SelfSignedCertificate` error variant; self-signed/cert-verification failures collapse to the generic `error.other` (or context fallback) with no cert-specific guidance.
  - _Why:_ `core/src/error.rs` defines a dedicated `SelfSignedCertificate { host }` variant precisely so the UI can distinguish a cert problem from a generic network failure (the generated binding comment even says it lets the UI offer a 'Trust this server' action). The presenter ignores it: the message `"the server at '...' uses a certificate that could not be verified — it may be self-signed"` matches none of the branches (it does not contain `"network error"`), so it falls to `error.other`. There is also no Swift handling of `SelfSignedCertificate` anywhere in macos/Sources (verified via rg), so the user just sees 'Something went wrong'.
  - _Fix:_ Add `if description.contains("could not be verified") || description.contains("self-signed") { return "error.network" }` (or a new `error.certificate` key with actionable text), ideally via the typed-case refactor above so it maps `case .selfSignedCertificate`.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/NetworkMonitor.swift`
- **L14** [resource-leak] No `deinit`; the `NWPathMonitor` started via `monitor.start(queue:)` is never cancelled on teardown, leaking its dispatch source / network-path observer.
  - _Why:_ `NWPathMonitor` holds an active dispatch source while running; Apple's docs require `cancel()` to release it. `retry()` correctly cancels the old monitor before replacing it, proving the author knows cancel is needed — but object teardown has no such cleanup. In the shipping app NetworkMonitor is owned by AppModel for the process lifetime so the practical impact is one leaked monitor, but it is incorrect lifecycle hygiene and would leak per-instance if NetworkMonitor were ever created transiently (tests, previews, future multi-window).
  - _Fix:_ Add `deinit { monitor.cancel(); stableOnlineTask?.cancel() }`. Note `deinit` cannot be `@MainActor`-isolated cleanly for the Task cancel; cancelling the NWPathMonitor is safe from deinit, and the Task holds only a weak self so it self-cancels.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/AboutView.swift`
