- **L88** [consistency] App icon placeholder renders the glyph "J" (Jellify) while the app is branded "Lyrebird" (`AboutInfo.appName == "Lyrebird"`, window title `about-lyrebird`).
  - _Why:_ The About window's hero icon shows a 'J' monogram next to the 'Lyrebird' wordmark — a leftover from the Jellify->Lyrebird rename. It's the most visible branding surface (the About box) and directly contradicts the displayed product name. The sibling Preferences About surface (PreferencesAbout.swift:95) has the identical 'J' bug, confirming it's a systemic rename leftover, not a typo.
  - _Fix:_ Change the placeholder glyph to "L" (or drop in the real app icon asset). Fix both AboutView.swift:88 and PreferencesAbout.swift:95 together.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/AlbumDetailView.swift`
- **L67** [bug] Album-scoped @State (tracks/detail/moreByArtist/fetchedAlbum) is not reset when albumID changes, so the stat strip and liner notes flash the previous album's data during the reload window.
  - _Why:_ On album→album navigation the task re-runs but `tracks` and `detail` keep their previous values until each await completes. While `isLoading` gates only the trackList (line 371) to a spinner, the hero statStrip still calls formatSummary(tracks:) (line 178) on the OLD tracks and reads `detail.label` (line 177), and the inline linerNotes section (line 532) renders the old `detail`/`tracks` (Label/Format/Runtime/Tracks rows). The user sees the previous album's format/label/runtime under the new album's title until the new fetches land.
  - _Fix:_ At the top of the `.task` closure, reset `tracks = []`, `detail = AlbumDetail(label: nil, releaseDate: nil, people: [], overview: nil)`, and `moreByArtist = []` so stale per-album data does not paint during the load.
- **L176** [consistency] Hero "Minutes" stat uses album.runtimeTicks while the liner-notes Runtime row sums per-track ticks, so the two can disagree (and the hero shows "0" when the server reports no album runtime).
  - _Why:_ Jellyfin frequently returns RunTimeTicks=0 for album container items, while per-track ticks are populated. The hero stat (formatMinutes(album.runtimeTicks), line 762) then displays "0" Minutes, but the liner-notes Runtime row (runtimeSummary, lines 771-774) correctly sums the loaded tracks and shows the real duration. Same screen, two different durations.
  - _Fix:_ Have the hero "Minutes" stat reuse the same track-sum fallback as runtimeSummary (compute minutes from the summed track ticks when tracks are loaded, falling back to album.runtimeTicks only when empty).
- **L475** [gap-stub] The "Read more" button is rendered unconditionally regardless of whether the overview actually exceeds the 4-line clamp, so short descriptions get a no-op "Read more" that opens a popover identical to the visible text.
  - _Why:_ aboutBody clamps the overview to 4 lines (line 472) then always shows a "Read more" affordance (lines 475-481). For overviews that fit in ≤4 lines there is nothing further to reveal, yet the user is offered a button whose popover (aboutPopover) shows the same text. This is a misleading affordance and an accessibility annoyance (the action label promises a "complete description" that is identical).
  - _Fix:_ Only show "Read more" when the text is actually truncated — e.g. measure with a background GeometryReader / line-count heuristic, or compare the rendered height, and conditionally render the button.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/ArtistDetailView.swift`
- **L84** [performance] The `artist` computed property does an O(n) linear scan `model.artists.first { $0.id == artistID }` and is referenced by hero, transportBar, featuringPlaylistsSection, aboutSection, and footer. Each body invalidation therefore runs several full linear scans over the (potentially multi-thousand-entry) artists array, and body invalidates on every keystroke in the scoped filter (scopedQuery is @State on this view).
  - _Why:_ model.artists is a flat [Artist] holding a full page/accumulation of the library (~3839 artists on the reference server). Roughly 5 O(n) scans per render, repeated on every filter keystroke, is wasted main-thread work that scales with library size.
  - _Fix:_ Resolve the artist once per render: compute it into a local `let artist = self.artist` at the top of body and pass down, or cache it in @State keyed by artistID (you already store fetchedArtist), or have AppModel expose an O(1) dictionary lookup `artistsById[artistID]`.
- **L363** [consistency] The primary play button's accessibility label and help text claim 'Play all tracks', but in the common case (topTracks non-empty) it plays only the 5 top tracks, not the artist's full catalog. Only the fallback branch (topTracks empty) actually plays all tracks via playAll(artist:).
  - _Why:_ loadArtistTopTracks defaults to limit 5, so the button labelled 'Play all tracks' typically enqueues only 5 songs. The label misrepresents behavior to all users and especially VoiceOver users, who are told the entire catalog will play.
  - _Fix:_ Either make the button truly play all tracks (call playAll(artist:) unconditionally, or play the loaded discography), or relabel it to match reality (e.g. 'Play top songs' / 'Play' with help 'Play top songs'). Keep the accessibilityLabel consistent with the chosen behavior.
- **L398** [gap-stub] The artist transport bar's "Start instant mix" button is functionally identical to the adjacent "Start artist radio" button — both call model.startArtistRadio(artist:), which is just playInstantMix(seedId: artist.id). The instant-mix affordance does nothing distinct from artist radio.
  - _Why:_ A user sees two distinct buttons (different SF Symbols, different help/accessibility text: "Start artist radio" vs "Start instant mix") and reasonably expects two different behaviors. They produce identical playback. It's either a redundant button that should be removed, or a wired-to-the-wrong-method stub: there is no artist instant-mix primitive in AppModel, so the second button is a dead affordance dressed up as a feature.
  - _Fix:_ Either remove the duplicate "Start instant mix" button, or add a real artist instant-mix path (e.g. a core primitive distinct from instantMix-as-radio) and call it. If artist radio and instant mix are intended to be the same seed, collapse to one button to avoid misleading the user.
- **L565** [concurrency] The discography uses an eager HStack (not LazyHStack) inside a horizontal ScrollView, so every ArtistDiscographyTile for the group is instantiated immediately on first render. Each tile's body calls the synchronous, MainActor model.imageURL(...) which on cache-miss takes the Rust Inner mutex via `try? core.imageUrl(...)`. loadArtistAlbums fetches up to 200 albums, so a prolific artist can trigger up to ~200 serialized mutex-guarded FFI calls on the main thread in a single render pass.
  - _Why:_ This is exactly gap pattern #2 from CLAUDE.md (per-cell sync FFI on MainActor). The eager HStack (chosen to dodge the macOS 26.4 LazyHStack UAF) means the cost is paid up-front and unbounded by viewport, beach-balling the UI for large discographies until imageURLCache warms.
  - _Fix:_ Precompute the image URLs off the main thread once per load (e.g. resolve all tile URLs in the .task via Task.detached and pass URLs into the tiles), or batch-warm imageURLCache before rendering. If LazyHStack remains unsafe, at minimum cap eager rendering or hand tiles a pre-resolved URL instead of calling the sync FFI inside each tile body.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/FullQueueView.swift`
- **L119** [performance] All queue rows are rendered in non-lazy VStacks and every FullQueueTrackRow observes model.status, so the full list re-renders on each 1Hz status poll tick and large queues are materialized eagerly.
  - _Why:_ sessionPlayHistory is capped at 50 (AppModel.swift:507) but upNextUserAdded/upNextAutoQueue are unbounded. Because the stacks are plain VStack (not LazyVStack), every row is built up front; because each row reads the observed model.status, every status tick (1Hz while playing, per gap pattern #2) invalidates and re-renders the entire visible list. For a large user-added queue this is avoidable per-tick main-thread work plus a large eager view tree.
  - _Fix:_ Use LazyVStack for the history / up-next / auto-queue sections so off-screen rows aren't built, and/or derive isActive/isPlaying from a narrower equatable signal (e.g. pass the current track id + isPlaying bool down) so rows that aren't the active one don't re-render on every status tick.
- **L340** [bug] playFromHere resolves the start index via firstIndex(by track id), so when the same track id appears more than once in a queue (e.g. a song replayed in session history) it always jumps to the first occurrence rather than the row the user tapped.
  - _Why:_ sessionPlayHistory (and conceivably an up-next list) can legitimately contain duplicate track ids. firstIndex returns the earliest match, so tapping the second/third occurrence starts playback from the wrong position in the list. The row itself has no notion of its own index; the lookup discards the tapped instance.
  - _Fix:_ Thread the row's actual position into FullQueueTrackRow (e.g. pass an index alongside `queue`, as TrackListRow does) and call model.play(tracks: queue, startIndex: thatIndex) instead of recovering the index by id.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/GenreDetailView.swift`
- **L196** [performance] Inside `ForEach(tracks, id: \.id)` the row index is recomputed per row via `tracks.firstIndex(where: { $0.id == track.id }) ?? 0`, an O(n) scan for every row → O(n²) for the list. The `?? 0` fallback also silently maps a row to index 0 if the lookup ever fails, which would start playback from the wrong track.
  - _Why:_ The enumeration index is already available cheaply; the firstIndex scan is pure waste and, for duplicate ids, returns the first occurrence (wrong index for later duplicates). The `?? 0` masks any mismatch by pointing TrackListRow's play-from-here at track 0.
  - _Fix:_ Iterate with the index directly: `ForEach(Array(tracks.enumerated()), id: \.element.id) { index, track in TrackListRow(track: track, tracks: tracks, index: index) }`.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/HomeView.swift`
- **L32** [consistency] Two distinct Home sections both carry the heading 'Recently Played' and are both gated on the same `model.recentlyPlayed`, so they both render together: `recentlyPlayedSection` (line 385, title 'Recently Played', `RecentlyPlayedTile`) and `recentlyPlayedTracksSection` (line 537, title 'Recently Played', `RecentlyPlayedTrackRow`). The body mounts both (lines 32 and 36).
  - _Why:_ Whenever the user has recent plays, the Home screen shows the same 'Recently Played' header twice with two different layouts of the same underlying data — visually confusing and looks like a bug.
  - _Fix:_ Give one section a distinct title (e.g. keep the tile carousel as 'Recently Played' and rename the row variant, or 'Continue Listening'), or remove one of the two duplicate sections.
- **L347** [gap-stub] `handlePinAction()` is a bare `print(...)` stub for the already-CLOSED issue #253. It is the action behind both `PinnedStationsEmptyState` and `PinnedStationAddPill`, so the 'pin a station' affordance does nothing. It also violates the rc12 logging convention (CLAUDE.md gap pattern #1): stubs must use `Log.app.notice`, not `print`, or the message vanishes into Xcode's debug console instead of Console.app.
  - _Why:_ Tapping the add-pill / empty-state CTA gives no feedback and performs no action; users can't pin a station from Home at all. The `print` form also means even developers won't see the breadcrumb in Console.app where the rest of the app logs.
  - _Fix:_ Build the pin-picker UI, or at minimum replace `print(...)` with `Log.app.notice(...)` and gate/remove the dead affordance. Note the whole row is currently unmounted anyway (see line 217 finding), so this is only reachable once that is fixed.
- **L354** [gap-stub] `handleStationTap` only routes `.genre` stations; the `.artist`, `.playlist`, `.mood`, and `.mix` cases just log 'routing not yet wired' and do nothing. Tapping any non-genre pinned station is a silent no-op.
  - _Why:_ Four of the five station kinds are non-functional. Combined with the dead row, no pinned station is even reachable; but if the row is mounted (the obvious fix for the line-217 finding) without wiring these, tapping a pinned artist/playlist/mood/mix radio does nothing, which is a user-facing dead end.
  - _Fix:_ Wire the remaining kinds to their start-radio/navigation paths (artist radio via playInstantMix(seedId:), playlist via navigate(to:.playlist), etc.) before exposing the row, or constrain pinning to genres only.
- **L537** [consistency] Two distinct Home sections render the same `model.recentlyPlayed` array under the identical title "Recently Played". `recentlyPlayedTracksSection` (this range, line 537) duplicates `recentlyPlayedSection` (def line 385); both appear in `body` (lines 32 and 36) and both gate on `if !model.recentlyPlayed.isEmpty`, so the user sees the same header text and the same tracks twice on one screen.
  - _Why:_ Two carousels with the same header and same data look like a rendering bug to users and waste vertical space. Even if two presentations (compact tiles vs detailed rows with duration) are intentional, giving both the identical title "Recently Played" is a clear UX defect.
  - _Fix:_ Pick one presentation, or differentiate the second section's title/subtitle (e.g. "Recent Tracks" / "Jump back into a recent track") so the two carousels are not both labelled "Recently Played". If only one is intended, remove the other from `body`.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/LibraryView.swift`
- **L196** [consistency] sortOrder is not reset when switching to a tab that doesn't support the current sort, so the sort menu label misrepresents the actual ordering.
  - _Why:_ Set Albums sort to 'Year ↓', switch to Artists: the menu reads 'Year ↓' but artists are silently shown A–Z (artists have no year). Likewise 'Longest'/'Shortest' on Artists collapse to A–Z while the chip claims otherwise. The control lies about the state, which is a correctness/trust issue, not just polish.
  - _Fix:_ Either disable/hide sort options a tab can't honor (so the menu only offers valid orders per tab), or fall back to a sort the tab does support and update `selection` to match what is actually applied so the label stays truthful.
- **L234** [performance] The full collection is sorted (and filtered) multiple times per render pass via redundant computed-property chains.
  - _Why:_ On the documented ~20060-album library, every body re-evaluation runs 3+ full O(n log n) localized string sorts on the @MainActor (showAlphabetRail and alphabetPresentBuckets both evaluate even when the rail is off, because showAlphabetRail itself sorts to get .count). localizedCaseInsensitiveCompare on tens of thousands of elements on the main thread is a measurable hitch on every state change (hover id change, selection change, etc.).
  - _Fix:_ Compute the sorted+filtered array once per render (e.g. a single `let items = sortedAlbums` reused for the rail predicate, bucket set, and content), and/or cache the sorted result keyed on (sortOrder, filter, collection identity) so hover/selection re-renders don't re-sort.
- **L494** [gap-stub] No 'no results' state when an active filter excludes every loaded item; the user sees a blank content area.
  - _Why:_ A NoSearchResultsState component already exists in the codebase (Components/NoSearchResultsState.swift) for the search screen, but the library filter path renders nothing — no 'No matches for these filters' message, no 'clear filters' affordance. The user is left staring at empty space, unsure whether the app is broken or the filter is too narrow. EmptyLibraryState would also be wrong here (it prompts to add media to the server).
  - _Fix:_ When `filter.isActive && <filteredCollection>.isEmpty`, show a dedicated 'no matches' state with a button to clear the filter, distinct from EmptyLibraryState (which should remain gated on the raw count).
- **L552** [gap-stub] The 'Downloaded' tab is a permanently dead path: it always renders the generic empty state because downloads are capability-gated off.
  - _Why:_ Users see a 'Downloaded' tab that can never contain anything and lands on an 'add media to your server' empty state, which is nonsensical for a downloads view. This is the rot pattern called out in CLAUDE.md (downloads gated behind Capabilities, #70/#222) — visible here as a dead, misleading tab.
  - _Fix:_ Hide the Downloaded tab from LibraryTab.allCases (or filter the chip options) unless `model.supportsDownloads`, mirroring how the filter popover already gates its downloaded group via `showDownloaded: model.supportsDownloads`. When the FFI lands, show a downloads-specific empty state rather than EmptyLibraryState.
- **L659** [consistency] The header count subline ignores the active filter, so the displayed number contradicts the number of items actually shown.
  - _Why:_ With a filter narrowing the grid to e.g. 5 albums, the header still reads '100 OF 20060 ALBUMS'. The count is meant to describe the visible library state (it even has a matching accessibilityLabel at line 671) but is simply wrong whenever a filter is applied. countAccessibilityLabel (line 671) has the identical defect, so VoiceOver users get the same misleading number.
  - _Fix:_ When filter.isActive, report the filtered count (e.g. 'Showing N filtered of M'), or compute count/total from the filtered collections so the subline matches what is rendered.
- **L724** [gap-stub] None of the four `passesFilter` overloads honor `filter.onlyDownloaded`, even though that flag is counted by `LibraryFilter.activeGroupCount`/`isActive` and is surfaced as a real toggle in the filter popover. The filter will report itself active (dot badge shown) while filtering nothing for the downloaded criterion.
  - _Why:_ `onlyDownloaded` increments `activeGroupCount` and flips `isActive` true (LibraryFilterPopover.swift:88-96), which makes the filter button show its active dot (line 380) and announce N filters active (line 392), and makes `filteredAlbums`/etc. run the `passesFilter` path (line 784). But `passesFilter` never tests `onlyDownloaded`, so toggling Only-downloaded changes nothing in the results — a silently broken filter. Currently latent because the popover gates the toggle behind `showDownloaded: model.supportsDownloads` (line 400) and `supportsDownloads` is hard-coded false in Capabilities.swift, so the toggle is unreachable today; it becomes a live user-facing bug the moment downloads ship.
  - _Fix:_ Add a downloaded check to each relevant `passesFilter` overload, e.g. `if filter.onlyDownloaded, !model.isDownloaded(track: track) { return false }` (and album/artist/playlist equivalents once a download-state query exists), or — until downloads are implemented — drop `onlyDownloaded` from `activeGroupCount` so it cannot mark the filter active while doing nothing.
- **L871** [bug] `.random` sort re-shuffles on every access, producing unstable ordering and wasted work across the multiple evaluations of the sorted collection in one render.
  - _Why:_ Different evaluations within a single render see different orders, so the alphabet rail's index computation (when applicable) and the displayed content disagree; more generally the grid order jitters on every unrelated state change (hovering a card re-renders, re-shuffles, and the whole grid reorders under the cursor). It also throws away the prior shuffle each time. The rail is hidden for .random (showAlphabetRail requires .nameAscending), so the rail/content mismatch is masked there, but the per-render reshuffle of the visible grid is a real UX bug.
  - _Fix:_ Seed the shuffle deterministically (e.g. store a shuffled order or a seed in @State, regenerated only when sortOrder becomes .random or on an explicit reshuffle action) so the order is stable across re-renders.
- **L1227** [accessibility] AlbumCard's overlay Play button is hidden only via opacity (still in the a11y tree and hit-testable) and is nested inside the card's Button label.
  - _Why:_ An opacity-0 view remains focusable by VoiceOver and clickable by the mouse, so users can hit an invisible 'Play' control, and VoiceOver may announce a 'Play X' button that is not visually present. Additionally, a Button nested inside another Button's label is an ambiguous interactive structure on macOS — SwiftUI often flattens the outer Button's label into one accessibility element, which can make the inner Play button unreachable by VoiceOver entirely (its accessibilityLabel swallowed). Either outcome is an accessibility/interaction defect.
  - _Fix:_ Gate the Play button with `.accessibilityHidden(!isHovering)` (and ideally `.allowsHitTesting(isHovering)`), and restructure so the play affordance is not a Button inside a Button label (e.g. use a single tappable card with a separate overlay control that is not enclosed in the navigation Button's label, or expose play via the context menu / an accessibility action).

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/LoginView.swift`
- **L363** [bug] submit() mutates the shared model.errorMessage in place (auth.expired -> wrong_credentials) and gates the rewrite on `err != previousError`. Because errorMessage is a global AppModel property shared with every other screen and background task, this couples the login UI's display logic to mutation of shared state. If the post-await body runs after the user has navigated away (the Task is unstructured and not tied to view lifetime), it still rewrites global errorMessage, and the `err != previousError` guard can also skip the shake/rewrite in edge cases where errorMessage was already wrong_credentials from an unrelated source.
  - _Why:_ Rewriting shared global state to drive a view-local presentation is fragile; the display-time mapping approach (OnboardingView.visibleError) is the safer pattern and avoids the previousError-equality footgun. The unstructured Task also has no cancellation tie-in to onDisappear.
  - _Fix:_ Move the auth.expired->wrong_credentials translation entirely to display time (loginErrorMessage), keep only shakeAttempts in submit() driven by a returned/observed login result, and do not mutate model.errorMessage from the view.
- **L386** [consistency] The offline-mode user-facing strings are hardcoded English literals while every other label in this file uses LocalizedStringKey / String(localized:) keys. 'Last connected \(relative). Trying offline mode.' and 'Trying offline mode.' will never localize even once the String Catalog (#560) lands, and they also embed an interpolated value.
  - _Why:_ Mixed localization strategy within one screen: keys like "login.probe.checking" and "login.network_banner" are catalog-ready, but these two strings bypass the mechanism, producing partially-translated UI for non-English users.
  - _Fix:_ Replace with String(localized:) keys, e.g. "login.offline.last_connected" with a format argument for the relative time, and "login.offline.trying".
- **L390** [consistency] loginErrorMessage returns model.errorMessage raw, without the auth.expired -> wrong_credentials remap that the sibling OnboardingView applies at display time. The remap only happens inside submit(). Any code path that sets model.errorMessage to the raw 'error.auth.expired' string while LoginView is mounted (e.g. refreshLibrary()/poll hitting a 401 in the brief window after login() succeeds but before the screen is torn down, or a stale errorMessage carried over from a prior session) surfaces the cryptic 'authentication expired' copy on the login form instead of the intended 'wrong credentials' message.
  - _Why:_ OnboardingView.visibleError (lines 300-307) defensively maps auth.expired->wrong_credentials at render time, so it is robust to errorMessage being set from any source. LoginView relies solely on submit() having mutated model.errorMessage, so the two login surfaces present inconsistent copy for the same underlying error, and LoginView can leak the internal 'auth expired' wording to the end user during sign-in.
  - _Fix:_ Mirror OnboardingView: in loginErrorMessage, compare model.errorMessage against String(localized: "error.auth.expired") and return String(localized: "error.wrong_credentials") in that case, instead of (or in addition to) the in-place mutation in submit().

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/MainShell.swift`
- **L587** [bug] navigate(toBreadcrumbDepth:) ignores the segment that was actually clicked. It uses a hard-coded `idx < 3` cutoff and always calls `selectTab(model.screen)`, so intermediate breadcrumbs navigate to the wrong screen (or do nothing) whenever the breadcrumb list is longer than the simple library case.
  - _Why:_ breadcrumbSegments inserts an extra "Library" segment when `model.screen != .library` (lines 542/552/560/568). So for screen==.home, navPath==[.album(id)] the segments are ["Lyrebird","Home","Library","Albums","Name"]. Clicking "Library" (idx 2) calls selectTab(model.screen)==selectTab(.home) — it navigates to Home, not Library. Clicking "Albums" (idx 3) hits `idx < 3 == false` and does nothing even though it is not the leaf. The .genre case has the identical shape (["Lyrebird","Home","Library","Genres","Name"]) and the same two broken clicks. Breadcrumbs.swift passes the raw array index to onTap, so there is no offset that rescues this.
  - _Fix:_ Drive the navigation off the clicked segment, not a magic index. Map the breadcrumb index back to intent: index 0 -> clear navPath + stay on current tab; an inserted "Library"/tab-name segment -> selectTab(.library or the matching Screen) and clear navPath; the leaf -> no-op. At minimum, when the segment text equals "Library" call selectTab(.library) (not model.screen), and remove the `idx < 3` cap so non-leaf segments at any depth pop navPath to the tab root.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/NowPlayingView.swift`
- **L285** [performance] factTagline allocates two heavyweight date formatters per body re-evaluation while playing (~1 Hz).
  - _Why:_ factTagline is reached from body -> content -> heroPane on every observable change. While the Now Playing screen is open and playing, AppModel.status mutates ~once per second (per CLAUDE.md gap pattern #2), so body re-evaluates ~1 Hz. NowPlayingFacts.variants calls lastHeardQuip, which constructs a fresh ISO8601DateFormatter AND a fresh DateFormatter on each call (NowPlayingFacts.swift lines 64-75). For any played track (lastPlayedAt populated, the common case) that is two expensive formatter allocations + a string-format pass every second the screen is visible — pure churn since the result is identical until the track changes.
  - _Fix:_ Compute the facts array once per track instead of per render: cache it in @State keyed on track.id (e.g. set it inside the existing .task(id: currentTrack?.id)), or hoist the formatters in NowPlayingFacts to static lazily-initialized instances so variants() does no per-call allocation. DateFormatter/ISO8601DateFormatter are thread-confined but these calls are all on the MainActor, so a static cached formatter is safe here.
- **L449** [consistency] resolvedAlbum shows the previous album's track-count/genres next to the new track during the async album re-resolve when switching tracks.
  - _Why:_ The .task only nils out resolvedAlbum when the new track has NO albumId. When the user advances from track A (albumId X) to track B (albumId Y), the task id changes and re-runs, but resolvedAlbum keeps the stale Album X for the entire duration of the await model.resolveAlbum(id: Y) network/FFI round-trip. During that window the About tab renders track B's artist/title/runtime alongside album X's trackCount, name, and genres — a visible cross-track data smear, made more likely by resolveAlbum hitting the network on a cache miss.
  - _Fix:_ Reset resolvedAlbum = nil at the top of the .task before awaiting (unconditionally), or stamp resolvedAlbum with the resolved album's id and only render the album-derived sections when album.id == track.albumId.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/OnboardingView.swift`
- **L120** [consistency] All user-facing onboarding strings are hard-coded English literals instead of localized keys, even though sibling LoginView uses LocalizedStringKey and this same file already uses String(localized:) for error copy.
  - _Why:_ The first-run experience is entirely untranslatable while the rest of the auth flow is localized. With the i18n String Catalog work open (#560), onboarding will silently remain English-only and the inconsistency makes a future sweep error-prone.
  - _Fix:_ Move these literals into the String Catalog and reference LocalizedStringKey, mirroring LoginView.
- **L283** [bug] Re-onboarding while already authenticated leaves the user stuck on the Connect step: the auto-advance fires on a Bool change of `model.session != nil`, which does not change when an already-non-nil session is replaced by a fresh login.
  - _Why:_ When session is already non-nil, the observed expression `session != nil` is `true` before and after a successful login() (which reassigns to a new Session), so onChange never fires and onContinue() is never called. A user who resets onboarding while signed in and re-enters valid credentials gets no progression; the only escape that completes onboarding is 'Skip, explore offline'. This is the documented Preferences 'Reset Onboarding' flow.
  - _Fix:_ Observe the session identity/value rather than the nil-ness Bool (e.g. onChange(of: model.session?.user.id)), or check `model.session != nil` once in ConnectStep.onAppear and immediately advance if already signed in.
- **L335** [accessibility] The onboarding URL/username TextFields and the password SecureField have no accessibilityLabel, unlike the otherwise-identical LoginView fields which all carry explicit a11y labels.
  - _Why:_ VoiceOver announces these as unlabeled text/secure fields. A SecureField with no label is especially bad — a blind user cannot tell which field is the password during account setup, the most critical onboarding step.
  - _Fix:_ Add .accessibilityLabel for each field (pass the label string into labeledField/labeledSecureField and apply it), matching LoginView's pattern.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/PlaylistDetailView.swift`
- **L237** [gap-stub] Play Next / Add to Queue menu items are hard-disabled (.disabled(true)) even though the backing AppModel methods are fully implemented and used elsewhere, making working functionality unreachable.
  - _Why:_ AppModel.playNext(playlist:) (AppModel.swift:4590-4603) and addToQueue(playlist:) (4608-4621) are real implementations that load the playlist tracks and call core.playNext / core.addToQueue (the same primitives album/artist/track context menus use via playNext(tracks:)/addToQueue(tracks:)). Hard-coding .disabled(true) renders two advertised menu actions permanently dead. Either the queue primitives are considered unstable (CLAUDE.md #282) — in which case the menu items should be hidden, not shown-but-greyed — or the gate is stale and the actions should be enabled like every other surface.
  - _Fix:_ If the queue insert semantics are intentionally deferred, remove these two Buttons (and the trailing Divider) so they don't present as broken; otherwise drop the `.disabled(true)` and gate on `!tracks.isEmpty` like the export items.
- **L455** [error-handling] handleDrop swallows all decode/add failures silently inside loadDataRepresentation callbacks and always returns true.
  - _Why:_ The error argument from loadDataRepresentation is discarded (`{ data, _ in`), and both guards (`guard let data`, `guard !ids.isEmpty`) return from the closure with no user feedback. handleDrop unconditionally returns true, so SwiftUI treats every drop as accepted even when nothing was parsed or the provider failed. A user dropping an unsupported payload sees the drop 'succeed' with no tracks added and no error — indistinguishable from the silent-list-staleness bug above.
  - _Fix:_ Surface failures via model.errorMessage on the data==nil / empty-ids / provider-error branches, and return false (or compute acceptance from whether any provider yielded ids) so the OS drop animation reflects rejection.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/PlaylistView.swift`
- **L161** [consistency] Hero stat and footer display playlist.trackCount (server metadata) which can exceed the actually loaded/playable tracks; Play/Shuffle only operate on the loaded subset.
  - _Why:_ tracks is populated by AppModel.loadPlaylistTracks which caps the request at limit: 500 (AppModel.swift:3008). For playlists larger than 500 items the hero stat and footer report the true server trackCount (e.g. 800) while only the first 500 tracks are loaded into `tracks`. The Play and Shuffle buttons enqueue only `tracks` (the capped 500), so the UI promises 800 tracks but plays 500, and 'Shuffle' never reaches the tail of large playlists. This is a silent truncation with no indication to the user.
  - _Fix:_ Either page the full playlist before enabling Play/Shuffle, or derive the displayed count from the loaded set when it is known to be capped (e.g. show '500 of 800 loaded'), or raise/remove the 500 cap with proper pagination. At minimum surface a 'showing first 500 tracks' notice so the count and the playable set agree.
- **L241** [gap-stub] editableDescription is read-only despite its name; there is no UI affordance to edit a playlist description and the only writer never persists.
  - _Why:_ The function name and its sibling editableTitle (which has a full TextField/commit flow) imply this is an editable field, but the body only renders static Text with no tap gesture, TextField, or call to updatePlaylistDescription. When the description is empty, nothing renders at all, so there is no way to ever add one. The only writer, AppModel.updatePlaylistDescription (AppModel.swift:4788), is itself a local-only stub that logs 'not yet persisted — see #130' and only mutates an in-memory dictionary, and it has zero call sites (confirmed via rg). Net effect: playlist descriptions can be displayed but never created or edited from this screen, contradicting the function's name.
  - _Fix:_ Either rename to playlistDescription (read-only) to stop implying editability, or wire a real edit path: render an editable TextField (mirroring editableTitle) whose onSubmit/onBlur calls a persisting updatePlaylistDescription, and show an 'Add description' placeholder when empty. Gate behind a Capabilities flag until the core update_playlist FFI lands so the optimistic local edit isn't silently lost.
- **L386** [bug] Option+Up/Down keyboard reorder uses full unfiltered tracks indices while a scoped filter is active, so it swaps the focused row with an invisible filtered-out neighbor and drops keyboard focus.
  - _Why:_ idx (entry.index) is the index into the full unfiltered tracks array (filterTracks builds it via tracks.enumerated()). The ForEach iterates filteredTracks, and these handlers fire on the visible filtered rows, but moveTrackInPlaylist(from: idx, to: idx+2) and the bound check idx < tracks.count - 1 operate on the unfiltered list. When scopedQuery is non-empty, the 'next' unfiltered track at idx+1 is frequently a row that is filtered out and not on screen, so the move appears to do nothing visible or makes the row jump unexpectedly. Worse, keyboardFocusedIndex = idx+1 (or idx-1 for up) sets focus to an unfiltered index that may not exist in filteredTracks, so keyboard focus is lost and further arrow presses no-op. The up handler at line 379 has the same defect.
  - _Fix:_ Disable keyboard reorder when !scopedQuery.isEmpty (filteredTracks != full list), or remap: locate the previous/next entry within filteredTracks, translate those to unfiltered indices, call moveTrackInPlaylist with the real neighbor's slot, and set keyboardFocusedIndex to the moved track's new unfiltered index. Simplest correct fix is to guard both onKeyPress handlers with `guard scopedQuery.trimmingCharacters(in: .whitespacesAndNewlines).isEmpty else { return .ignored }`.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesAccount.swift`
- **L180** [bug] closePreferencesWindow closes whatever window happens to be key, not specifically the Preferences window.
  - _Why:_ Preferences is the standard SwiftUI Settings scene (LyrebirdApp.swift:76-77). NSApplication.shared.keyWindow is whichever window currently has key focus. After the destructive alert dismisses, the Settings window is normally key so this usually works, but it is fragile: in multi-window setups (mini player / about / shortcuts windows are all separate Scenes) or if focus shifts, performClose can target the wrong window, closing e.g. the main library window instead of Preferences. There is no assertion that the key window is actually the Settings window.
  - _Fix:_ Use the SwiftUI dismiss action for the Settings scene: add @Environment(\.dismiss) private var dismiss and call dismiss(), or identify the Preferences window explicitly before closing it rather than relying on keyWindow.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesAdvanced.swift`
- **L351** [error-handling] clearCaches swallows both filesystem errors with try? yet the UI unconditionally reports success ("Cleared"), so a failed or partial clear is invisible to the user.
  - _Why:_ Both FS operations are best-effort via try?. The caller (line 83-86) sets cachesClearedDone = true regardless of outcome, and the help text then shows "Cleared — artwork and temporary files have been removed." If removeItem succeeds but createDirectory throws (permissions, sandbox, race), the caches directory is gone and not recreated — subsequent DataCache writes silently fail. The user is told it worked either way. There is no rollback and no error surfaced.
  - _Fix:_ Capture and surface errors (do/catch -> set an errorMessage), and only set cachesClearedDone when the operation actually succeeded. At minimum, if removeItem succeeds, guarantee the directory is recreated and verify it.
- **L351** [performance] Recursive deletion + directory recreation of the caches root runs synchronously on the MainActor from the button action.
  - _Why:_ clearCaches() is invoked directly from the SwiftUI Button closure (main thread) and performs a recursive FileManager.removeItem over the entire caches directory, which can contain a 256 MB Nuke DataCache (Artwork.swift:65) plus downloaded music. A large recursive unlink blocks the main thread and beachballs the UI until it completes.
  - _Fix:_ Move the filesystem work to a background queue / Task.detached and marshal the completion flag back to MainActor, e.g. await the delete off-main then set cachesClearedDone.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesAppearance.swift`
- **L35** [gap-stub] The Sunset and Peanut themes have no backing ThemePreset case; ThemePreset(appearanceTheme:) silently maps them to .purple, so even once the theme engine lands these two swatches will render identically to Purple.
  - _Why:_ Two of the five offered themes are dead even on the happy path — selecting Sunset or Peanut will look exactly like Purple, while their swatch dots show orange/tan. This is a latent mismatch between the picker's catalog and the engine's catalog that will surface as a 'theme doesn't apply' bug the moment theming is wired.
  - _Fix:_ Either add ocean-style ThemePreset cases for sunset/peanut (with real primary/accent hex), or remove sunset/peanut from AppearanceTheme so the picker only offers themes the engine can actually render.
- **L245** [gap-stub] The Sidebar 'Auto-hide' option is a no-op alias for 'Visible' — it resolves to the same NavigationSplitViewVisibility and there is no auto-hide behavior.
  - _Why:_ Users selecting 'Auto-hide' get plain 'Visible' behavior; the sidebar never auto-hides. A settings option that does nothing distinct from another option is a hidden dead-end.
  - _Fix:_ Implement auto-hide (e.g. collapse the sidebar on focus/idle and reveal on hover) and map .autoHide to that behavior, or remove the .autoHide case until the sidebar-chrome work lands.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesAudio.swift`
- **L169** [gap-stub] The output-device list is enumerated once on appear and never refreshed; CoreAudio device hot-plug/unplug is not observed while the pane is open.
  - _Why:_ If the user plugs in headphones / connects an AirPlay or USB DAC while the Audio preferences are open, the new device never appears in the Picker, and a device they unplug stays listed. The savedDeviceMissing 'Saved device unavailable' hint also won't update live. Users expect device lists in audio settings to reflect the current hardware.
  - _Fix:_ Register a CoreAudio property listener for kAudioHardwarePropertyDevices (or observe AVAudioEngine/route-change equivalents) and call loadDevices() on change; remove the listener in onDisappear to avoid a leak.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesGeneral.swift`
- **L18** [gap-stub] The Language picker is a dead control: the selected value is persisted to @AppStorage("general.language") but never consumed to change the UI language. rg across the whole Swift tree shows the only readers of "general.language" / languageRaw / AppLanguage outside this file are DiagnosticBundle.swift (which just dumps the key for diagnostics). Nothing writes AppleLanguages, sets Bundle locale, or otherwise reacts to the choice, and AppLanguage only offers .system / .english — both no-ops today.
  - _Why:_ Changing the picker has zero observable effect. It presents a configurable setting that does nothing, which is a latent gap that will mislead users (and any future contributor) once a second language ships, because the wiring to actually apply the selection does not exist.
  - _Fix:_ Either remove the picker until localization is wired, or make it functional: on change, set UserDefaults ["AppleLanguages"] = [code] (with a relaunch prompt) or drive a runtime locale override the views read. At minimum, gate the control behind a capability flag so it isn't shown as a working setting while it is inert.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesLibrary.swift`
- **L277** [bug] Clear Cache may display a stale (non-zero) size and 'Cleared ✓' simultaneously due to a race with the asynchronous disk flush. Artwork.pipeline.cache.removeAll() clears both memory and disk, but DataCache.removeAll() returns instantly and removes files asynchronously (DataCache.swift:203-207: "The method returns instantly, the data is removed asynchronously"). refreshCacheSize() then reads totalSize from the actual on-disk directory after a fixed 0.6 s delay; if the background flush/file deletion has not completed, totalSize still reports the old bytes while the button shows 'Cleared ✓'.
  - _Why:_ The displayed cache size can lag the 'Cleared' confirmation, making the UI look inconsistent (size unchanged but says cleared). The 0.6 s magic number is not synchronized with the cache's flush queue.
  - _Fix:_ Call DataCache.flush() (synchronous wait for outstanding disk I/O) on a background queue after removeAll(), then refresh the size from that same background context and marshal the result to main — instead of guessing with a fixed 0.6 s delay.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesPlayback.swift`
- **L38** [consistency] Duplicate controls for the same backing keys across two Preferences panes. This screen (case .playback) and PreferencesAudio.swift (case .audio, both registered in PreferencesView.swift:84-85) each render a Streaming Quality and Download Quality picker bound to the identical @AppStorage keys playback.streamingQuality / playback.downloadQuality (PreferencesAudio.swift:27-28).
  - _Why:_ Two separate Preferences tabs expose the same setting with different UI affordances. It's confusing (which is authoritative?), and the two panes can momentarily disagree visually. Combined with the fact that neither actually drives playback (see other findings), it doubles the surface of the dead-control problem.
  - _Fix:_ Consolidate quality/codec into a single pane (likely Audio) and remove the duplicated Streaming/Downloads/Codec sections here, or vice versa, so each setting has exactly one editing surface.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesServer.swift`
- **L297** [gap-stub] The three account actions (signOut / changeUser / switchServer) only differ by which in-memory @Observable fields they null out; the persisted credentials state they all funnel through is identical, so the alert promises about cross-launch memory are not honored after a quit+relaunch.
  - _Why:_ LoginView pre-fills the form only from the in-memory model.serverURL / model.username (LoginView.swift lines 88-89, 94, 266), never from the persisted last_server_url / last_username. model.serverURL and model.username are plain in-memory vars (AppModel.swift lines 25-26, no didSet/persistence) that reset to "" on every launch and are only repopulated by a successful session restore. After Sign Out the token is gone so restore fails, leaving both fields empty. Result: after the user signs out, quits, and relaunches expecting to 'sign back in with just your password,' the login form is completely blank — the documented distinction between Sign Out (remember URL+user), Change User (remember URL), and Switch Server (forget all) only exists for the current run and silently collapses across launches.
  - _Fix:_ On a cold start where session restore fails, seed model.serverURL / model.username from the core's persisted last_server_url / last_username (add a small FFI such as core.rememberedServerURL()/rememberedUsername() and read them in LoginView.onAppear / attemptRestoreSession). Then have switchServer/changeUser clear the appropriate persisted keys via FFI so the next-launch pre-fill matches the in-session behavior. Until that exists, the alert copy overstates what is actually remembered.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/SearchView.swift`
- **L346** [bug] canLoadMore / load-more accounting can keep the 'Load more' button visible indefinitely because searchPageLoaded counts only artists+albums+tracks while searchPageTotal is the server's total_record_count, which may include other item types or be deduplicated, so `searchPageLoaded < searchPageTotal` can stay true after the server has actually returned everything it will.
  - _Why:_ If the server's total includes types Lyrebird doesn't bucket, or returns short final pages, the user sees a perpetual 'Load more' that, when tapped, fetches a page adding zero new visible items — an apparent hang. (Core-side accounting, but canLoadMore in SearchView is the consumer that renders the button.)
  - _Fix:_ Treat load-more as exhausted when a fetched page returns 0 new deduplicated items, or track loaded vs. total per the same set of types the server counts. At minimum, hide 'Load more' once a fetch adds nothing to the active scope's bucket.
- **L370** [bug] The per-section local reveal cap (perSectionLocalCap = 30) is completely bypassed whenever the server has more records. The `serverHasMore` branch unconditionally yields current+revealStep, which is always >= nextLocalCap, so revealed grows by 10 each click without ever being clamped to 30.
  - _Why:_ The intended 30-item soft cap per section (which would force the user toward narrowing the query) never applies on real libraries where the server almost always has more records. revealed can exceed both perSectionLocalCap and the loaded bucketSize, so the section quietly renders every locally-cached item with no cap, defeating the design intent of the constant.
  - _Fix:_ Decide the intended behavior. If the 30-cap should hold even when the server has more, set `next = min(current + revealStep, perSectionLocalCap)` for the local-reveal portion and trigger loadMoreFullSearch separately. If the cap was meant only as a floor, remove perSectionLocalCap entirely so it isn't dead. Currently it is silently no-op'd.
- **L371** [bug] perSectionLocalCap is bypassed entirely while serverHasMore is true, so the per-section reveal grows unboundedly (10 per tap) and the 'Load more' button is effectively perpetual for derived/secondary sections (e.g. genres, which are computed client-side from album/artist genres and never paged).
  - _Why:_ searchPageTotal is the server's global totalRecordCount and searchPageLoaded counts only artists+albums+tracks. For the genres section (bucket derived from album/artist genres, typically a handful), canLoadMore falls through to searchPageLoaded < searchPageTotal which stays true for a long time on a large library (~20k albums). Every tap advances revealed by 10 (40,50,60,...) past the 30 cap and fires loadMoreFullSearch() — a wasteful network page that adds nothing to the genres bucket — and the button never disappears.
  - _Fix:_ Clamp next to perSectionLocalCap in both branches: let next = min(serverHasMore ? current + revealStep : nextLocalCap, perSectionLocalCap, max(bucketSize, current + (serverHasMore ? revealStep : 0))). Better: track per-type 'has more' instead of a single global total so a section's button reflects that section's own remaining items.
- **L389** [performance] commitQuery cancels searchTask but does NOT cancel searchDebounce, so committing a query (Enter / tapping a recent search) leaves a stale 300ms debounce timer alive that fires a second, redundant identical search after the commit's search already ran.
  - _Why:_ Every Enter-press and every recent-search tap triggers two network round-trips for the same query/scope (the immediate commit, then the orphaned debounce ~300ms later cancels the just-finished task and re-runs it). Wasted server load and a visible second loading flash.
  - _Fix:_ Add `searchDebounce?.cancel()` at the top of commitQuery (and clearQuery already cancels both, so mirror that).
- **L389** [bug] commitQuery does not cancel the pending debounce task, and because runFullSearch mutates model.searchPageQuery, a duplicate search fires ~300ms after every commit (Enter key, recent-search tap, zero-results suggestion). The duplicate also cancels the commit's in-flight request mid-flight.
  - _Why:_ onSubmit→commitQuery runs an immediate search, but the debounce scheduled by the last keystroke (or by runFullSearch updating searchPageQuery, which re-triggers onChange) is still alive; after 300ms it cancels the commit's task (line 426) and re-runs the identical search. Result: a redundant network round-trip and a cancel/flicker on every commit path.
  - _Fix:_ In commitQuery, cancel the debounce first: searchDebounce?.cancel() before starting the committed search. Same guard should be applied wherever a search is committed synchronously.
- **L428** [bug] The debounced search writes the trimmed query back into the bound text field, so a user who pauses typing with a trailing/leading space has that space silently deleted from the search box mid-edit.
  - _Why:_ Typing 'the beatles ' (with a space, e.g. about to type another word) snaps the field to 'the beatles' after 300ms, moving the caret and dropping the space the user just typed. Disrupts in-progress editing.
  - _Fix:_ Don't write the trimmed value back into the user-facing binding. Either pass the raw query through and trim only for the network call, or keep a separate display string vs. query string so runFullSearch never mutates searchPageQuery while the field is focused.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/ServerReachability.swift`
- **L172** [bug] DiscoveredServer.id is set to the Bonjour service name, which is not guaranteed unique. apply() performs no de-duplication, so two NWBrowser results with the same service name (e.g. the same host advertised over IPv4 and IPv6, or in two domains) produce two DiscoveredServer values with identical id. Both LoginView and OnboardingView render these via ForEach over Identifiable.
  - _Why:_ ForEach over Identifiable with duplicate ids causes SwiftUI to log runtime warnings and drop/merge rows, so a discovered server can silently disappear from the picker or the list can misbehave on update.
  - _Fix:_ De-duplicate in apply() (e.g. keep a Set keyed by name or seedURL before appending), or make id incorporate the resolved endpoint/url so distinct endpoints get distinct ids.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/AboutInfo.swift`
- **L115** [bug] Same first-'@'-split flaw as DiagnosticBundle.redactServerHost in the host-extraction fallback. Here it only affects the host shown in the About window, so it is display-incorrect rather than a leak, but it can render a wrong/partial host string for scheme-less URLs with userinfo.
  - _Why:_ connectedServerHost is fed model.serverURL (raw user input). A scheme-less URL like "admin:p@ss@host/x" displays "ss@host" in About instead of "host". The two functions are near-duplicates and should share one correct implementation so a fix to one doesn't drift from the other.
  - _Fix:_ Extract a single shared host-redaction helper used by both AboutInfo and DiagnosticBundle, splitting on lastIndex(of: "@") and/or retrying URLComponents with a prepended scheme.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/AccessibilityAnnouncer.swift`
- **L25** [accessibility] Track-change VoiceOver announcements are silently dropped whenever there is no main window. The app ships a MenuBarExtra and a `general.showInMenuBar` mode, so music can play with the main window closed/minimized — exactly when an audible announcement matters most — yet `NSApp.mainWindow` is nil then and the announcement never posts.
  - _Why:_ announce(_:) is the only path for 'Now playing X by Y' VoiceOver feedback (AppModel.announceTrackChange -> AccessibilityAnnouncer.announce). With LyrebirdApp's MenuBarExtra, the main Window can be closed while playback continues; NSApp.mainWindow returns nil, so the guard fails and a blind user gets no track-change announcement.
  - _Fix:_ Fall back when mainWindow is nil, e.g. `NSApp.mainWindow ?? NSApp.keyWindow ?? NSApp.windows.first(where: { $0.isVisible })`. If no window exists at all, posting against NSApp itself is also an option for app-level announcements.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/DiagnosticBundle.swift`
- **L156** [validation] The manual host fallback returns garbage for malformed scheme-less input rather than "(not signed in)". Verified: redactServerHost("ht!tp://weird host/with space") returns "weird host" (a space-containing non-host) which is then written verbatim into manifest.json's serverHost field.
  - _Why:_ The prefix scan stops only on /, :, ?, so it happily accepts spaces, '!', etc. and emits a non-hostname string. Low blast radius (manifest cosmetics) but indicates the fallback does no real host validation, reinforcing that the URLComponents-retry-with-scheme approach is the correct fix.
  - _Fix:_ After retrying URLComponents with a prepended scheme, treat any result that fails a basic host-character check as "(not signed in)".

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/MenuBarController.swift`
- **L10** [concurrency] MenuBarController is a non-isolated singleton that mutates AppKit objects (NSStatusBar, NSStatusItem, button.toolTip/image) with no main-thread guarantee; correctness depends entirely on every caller happening to be on the main actor.
  - _Why:_ AppKit status-bar APIs are main-thread-only. Today all call sites (AppModel @MainActor, SwiftUI Preferences views) are on main, so it works by luck. Any future caller from a background Task/closure (a very plausible refactor) would mutate the status bar off-main, risking corruption/crashes that are hard to reproduce. The compiler currently provides no protection.
  - _Fix:_ Annotate the class (or at least setVisible/setVisibleWhilePlaying/setNowPlaying/applyVisibility) with @MainActor so the isolation is enforced by the compiler rather than assumed.
- **L65** [bug] setNowPlaying drops the now-playing title when the status item does not yet exist, and applyVisibility then hard-codes a generic "Lyrebird" tooltip on creation, so the first track played in show-only-while-playing mode never gets a now-playing tooltip.
  - _Why:_ In the "show in menu bar while playing" mode (NotificationPreference.showInMenuBarWhilePlaying), the status item first appears exactly when a track starts — which is precisely when the user wants the track title in the tooltip — yet it shows only "Lyrebird". The title only starts appearing on the *second* track change (once the item already exists). The captured now-playing title is silently lost.
  - _Fix:_ Cache the last now-playing title in MenuBarController (e.g. `private var nowPlayingTitle: String?` set by setNowPlaying regardless of item existence) and apply it when the button is created in applyVisibility instead of the hard-coded "Lyrebird".

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/MoveToApplications.swift`
- **L119** [bug] isTranslocatedOrEphemeral treats ANY path under /Volumes/ as ephemeral. A user who deliberately installs the app on a secondary internal/external volume mounted at /Volumes/<Disk>/Applications (a supported, persistent location) is incorrectly classified as ephemeral, so shouldPrompt returns false and they never get the move prompt — and other call sites relying on this predicate would mis-treat a permanent install as temporary.
  - _Why:_ /Volumes/ is the mount point for ALL non-boot volumes, not just DMGs. Persistent secondary-volume installs are common; flagging them as ephemeral suppresses the prompt for legitimate setups (and the inverse, a real DMG, is the case actually intended).
  - _Fix:_ Tighten the DMG/translocation detection: rely on /AppTranslocation/ and on checking whether the mounted volume is a disk image (e.g. via the mount's read-only / removable / disk-image flags from URLResourceValues / getmntinfo) rather than the blanket /Volumes/ prefix.
- **L120** [bug] The `.contains("/.dmg/")` check never matches a real mounted DMG path. Mounted disk images appear at /Volumes/<VolumeName>/... — the literal substring '/.dmg/' does not occur in those paths, so this clause is effectively dead and contributes nothing to DMG detection.
  - _Why:_ This branch looks like it was intended to catch app bundles still inside a mounted .dmg, but mounted images are not exposed with a '.dmg' path component, so the predicate is dead code that gives false confidence in DMG coverage (the only thing actually catching DMGs is the over-broad /Volumes/ prefix above).
  - _Fix:_ Remove the dead '/.dmg/' substring check and replace DMG detection with a proper mounted-disk-image test (URLResourceValues volumeIsRemovable/volumeIsInternal or matching the bundle's volume against getmntinfo entries flagged as disk images).

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/NotificationManager.swift`
- **L51** [bug] notifyTrackChange gates only on the trackChangeEnabled preference, not on authorization having been granted. If the user enabled the preference in a prior launch (persisted to UserDefaults) but later denied notifications in System Settings, every track change still builds and submits a UNNotificationRequest. The add(...) completion swallows the resulting authorization error into a single log line, so notifications silently never appear with no user-visible explanation.
  - _Why:_ shouldNotify only reflects the in-app toggle, not the OS authorization state. A persisted-true toggle plus OS-level denial yields per-track no-op requests and a confusing silent failure; the user has no signal that the OS is blocking them.
  - _Fix:_ Check UNUserNotificationCenter.current().getNotificationSettings().authorizationStatus before posting (or cache it after requestAuthorization), and surface a one-time hint in Preferences when the toggle is on but OS authorization is denied.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/ScrobbleGate.swift`
- **L74** [bug] When scrobbling is toggled OFF mid-track and then back ON for the same still-playing track, no fresh nowPlaying is emitted. The first noteTrack with enabled=false sets currentId but returns .none (no nowPlaying sent); a later noteTrack with enabled=true for the same id skips the id-changed branch and falls through to the threshold check, so the 'now playing' update for that track is never sent to the server even though scrobbling is now active.
  - _Why:_ The nowPlaying signal is only produced on the id-change transition, gated by the enabled flag at that single instant. Enabling scrobbling after the track started (or re-enabling it) leaves the server's now-playing state stale until the next track change, an observable scrobble gap.
  - _Fix:_ Track whether nowPlaying has been sent for the current id (separate from submittedListen) and emit .nowPlaying when enabled becomes true for a track whose nowPlaying was not yet sent, rather than only on id change.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Theme/Theme.swift`
- **L110** [accessibility] The Increase-Contrast variants of ink2/ink3/border/borderStrong are produced by an NSColor dynamic provider that reads `accessibilityDisplayShouldIncreaseContrast` (via `isIncreaseContrastEnabled`) at resolve time. That setting is NOT part of NSAppearance, so toggling "Increase Contrast" in System Settings at runtime does not by itself force AppKit/SwiftUI to re-resolve these already-rendered Color values; they only re-evaluate on a separate appearance/layout invalidation. The other contrast system (AccessibleTheme via @Environment(\.colorSchemeContrast)) IS reactive, so the two paths can disagree mid-session.
  - _Why:_ Theme.ink2/ink3/border/borderStrong are consumed directly at hundreds of view call sites (181 ink2, 104+ border). If a user enables Increase Contrast while the app is open, those surfaces may keep rendering the faint standard tokens until something else triggers a redraw, undermining the accessibility feature these tokens exist for. SwiftUI updates colorSchemeContrast-driven views on the same toggle, so the app shows mixed contrast.
  - _Fix:_ Drive the adaptive tokens off the SwiftUI environment (colorSchemeContrast / @Environment) like AccessibleTheme does, rather than a static NSColor provider keyed on an off-NSAppearance accessibility flag; or observe NSWorkspace.accessibilityDisplayOptionsDidChangeNotification and force a top-level view invalidation so the dynamic provider re-resolves. Confirm behaviour by toggling Increase Contrast live against a running build.
- **L175** [bug] Theme.font(_:weight:italic:) silently drops the `italic` flag for every weight except `.black` and the default/`.regular` branch. The `.heavy`, `.bold`, `.semibold`, `.medium`, and `.light/.thin/.ultraLight` cases ignore `italic` entirely and return the upright face.
  - _Why:_ A caller asking for italic at any of those weights gets an upright glyph with no error. This is a live bug, not hypothetical: macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/HomeView.swift:119 calls `Theme.font(14, weight: .semibold, italic: true)` and renders non-italic SemiBold. The italic request is dropped without any compile-time or runtime signal.
  - _Fix:_ Either honour `italic` for every weight by selecting an italic face / applying `.italic()` to the resulting Font, or constrain the API so unsupported italic+weight combinations are unrepresentable. Given only Regular/Black italic faces ship, the simplest correct fix is to apply SwiftUI's synthetic `.italic()` modifier when `italic == true` and no dedicated italic face exists for the chosen weight, so the request is never silently ignored.

### `macos/Sources/LyrebirdAudio/AudioEngine.swift`
- **L439** [bug] play() does not cancel a pending stall watchdog from the previous track. removePlayerObservers() (called at line 467) does not touch stallWorkItem, and play() never calls cancelStallWatchdog(), so a watchdog scheduled for the old player can fire during the new track's load.
  - _Why:_ A stale watchdog firing after a fresh play() can call handleStallTimeout against the new player/url, spuriously incrementing stallRetryCount or triggering recoverFromStall on a track that is loading normally, leading to false 'stalled' UI or an unwanted item replacement.
  - _Fix:_ Call cancelStallWatchdog() at the top of play() (and/or add `cancelStallWatchdog()` to removePlayerObservers).
- **L530** [concurrency] pause()/resume()/seek() each invoke reportProgressSnapshot, which is a synchronous network call (core.reportPlaybackProgress -> block_on) executed on the MainActor.
  - _Why:_ Tapping pause/play or scrubbing blocks the main thread for a server round-trip, producing micro-stutters or beachballs on poor connections. Progress is already reported by the 5s heartbeat task in core, so the immediate echo does not justify blocking the UI.
  - _Fix:_ Dispatch reportProgressSnapshot's core call via Task.detached, or rely on the existing heartbeat for progress and only fire an immediate report off-main.
- **L643** [concurrency] preloadNextTrack spawns a Task.detached that captures self strongly (no [weak self]) while doing network FFI, keeping AudioEngine alive for the duration of the detached work.
  - _Why:_ Unlike applyReplayGain (line 401, which uses `Task.detached { [weak self] ... }`), this detached task holds a strong reference to the @MainActor AudioEngine until playbackInfo/streamUrl/authHeader (network round-trips) complete. If the engine is torn down during preload it cannot deinit until the network call returns, and the work proceeds against a logically-dead engine (the generation guard mitigates the result application but not the lifetime extension / wasted network call).
  - _Fix:_ Use `Task.detached { [weak self] in ... guard let self else { return } ... }` to match applyReplayGain, and bail early after the await MainActor.run if self is gone.
- **L863** [error-handling] The item-failure path auto-skips to the next track on the very first transient error with no retry/backoff, unlike the stall-watchdog path which retries maxAutoRetries times. handleItemFailure immediately fires onTrackEnded on any transient error.
  - _Why:_ A single momentary network blip while loading an item skips the track outright; if the next track also blips it cascades through the queue rapidly, potentially blowing past many tracks during a brief outage. The watchdog path retries the same URL but the item-error path does not, an inconsistent resilience policy.
  - _Fix:_ Route transient item failures through the same retry/recover machinery (recoverFromStall with stallRetryCount budget) before falling back to onTrackEnded, so a brief blip retries the current track rather than skipping it.
- **L879** [consistency] A transient network item-failure immediately skips the track (onTrackEnded), while a transient stall on the same kind of network blip retries up to maxAutoRetries first — inconsistent recovery behavior for equivalent conditions.
  - _Why:_ If a track stalls mid-buffer the engine retries (good UX). If the same momentary connectivity loss instead surfaces as item.error/.failed, the engine skips the track entirely with no retry. A brief Wi-Fi hiccup can therefore silently drop a song from playback depending on which observer fires first, which is surprising and data-losing from the listener's perspective.
  - _Fix:_ For transient errors, attempt the same bounded recoverFromStall path (re-create the item from currentStreamURL/currentAuthHeader and retry up to maxAutoRetries) before falling back to skipping; only call onTrackEnded after retries are exhausted.
- **L1031** [security] AudioEngineError.invalidURL.errorDescription embeds the raw stream URL, which contains the Jellyfin access token as the `api_key` query parameter.
  - _Why:_ Any caller that logs or displays `error.localizedDescription` for this error will leak the user's access token. Today play()'s catch routes through LyrebirdErrorPresenter (a localized key), so it isn't surfaced raw — but the error type itself is a token-bearing string, a defense-in-depth hole that the next logging site (or a crash reporter capturing NSError userInfo) would exploit.
  - _Fix:_ Do not interpolate the full URL into a user/loggable description. Redact the query string (e.g. strip everything from `?` onward, or only include the path) before building the message: `URLComponents(string: s)?.path ?? "<redacted>"`.

### `macos/Sources/LyrebirdAudio/AudioOutputDevices.swift`
- **L95** [bug] Disabling exclusive (hog) mode unconditionally writes pid -1 to release the device, even when this process does not currently own the hog. This can release another app's exclusive lock, or report a confusing error.
  - _Why:_ kAudioDevicePropertyHogMode semantics: writing -1 releases hog ownership. The code never checks that getpid() currently holds the hog before releasing. In setOutputDevice() (AppModel.swift:5611) the previous device is always force-released on every device switch when exclusive is enabled, regardless of whether Lyrebird ever hogged it; and on toggle-off the release runs even if the hog was lost/stolen. Releasing a device this process doesn't own is at best a no-op and at worst stomps another client; the error path also rolls back the user's toggle on a failure that may be benign.
  - _Fix:_ Before releasing, read kAudioDevicePropertyHogMode; only write -1 if the returned pid == getpid(). Treat "not owned by us" as a successful no-op release rather than surfacing hogModeFailed.

### `macos/Sources/LyrebirdAudio/MediaSession.swift`
- **L160** [performance] Artwork cache and artwork fetch are keyed by track.id, but cover art is album-level. Every track on the same album triggers a fresh URLSession download and a separate cache entry, even though mediaSessionArtworkURL resolves to the album image (it uses track.albumId ?? track.id).
  - _Why:_ Playing through a 12-track album performs 12 identical image downloads and stores 12 duplicate MPMediaItemArtwork objects, churning the 100-entry NSCache (related open issue #883 about cache growth). It is redundant network and memory work on every track change.
  - _Fix:_ Key the artworkCache (and the dedup check) by a stable album-art identity such as "\(track.albumId ?? track.id)|\(track.imageTag ?? "")" instead of track.id, so all tracks sharing the same album cover hit the cache after the first fetch.
- **L408** [bug] skipForwardCommand does not clamp the seek target to the track duration. It computes positionSeconds + interval with no upper bound, then seeks there with zero tolerance.
  - _Why:_ skipBackward correctly clamps with max(0, ...), but skipForward can request a seek past the end of the track. With toleranceBefore/After: .zero in AudioEngine.seek, seeking beyond duration produces undefined/edge behavior (snap-to-end or a failed seek), and updateElapsedAndRate publishes an elapsed time greater than the reported PlaybackDuration, so the scrubber overshoots the end.
  - _Fix:_ Clamp the forward target to the track duration, e.g. let dur = delegate.currentStatus.durationSeconds; let target = min(delegate.currentStatus.positionSeconds + interval, max(0, dur)). PlayerStatus exposes durationSeconds for this.
- **L460** [consistency] refreshRemoteCommandEnablement is the only path that syncs Control Center's shuffle/repeat indicators and like state to the real player state, but the public MediaSession API exposes no method for callers to trigger it after an app-UI-driven shuffle/repeat/favorite change. It is only invoked from trackChanged, queueChanged, and the remote-command callbacks.
  - _Why:_ When the user toggles shuffle or repeat, or favorites the current track from the app's own UI (not via Control Center), AppModel calls core.setShuffle/setRepeatMode/setFavorite but has no MediaSession hook to push the change; Control Center's shuffle/repeat glyphs and the like button stay stale until the next track change or queue index change. The favorite case is partially patched in AppModel by poking MPRemoteCommandCenter.likeCommand.isActive directly, but shuffle/repeat have no such workaround, indicating the missing public refresh entry point.
  - _Fix:_ Expose a public method (e.g. statusChanged() / refreshTransportState()) that calls refreshRemoteCommandEnablement(), and have AppModel invoke it after setShuffle/setRepeatMode and after favorite mutations, so Control Center reflects app-initiated state changes.

### `macos/Sources/LyrebirdAudio/ReplayGain.swift`
- **L197** [bug] iTunNorm parser only reads the first 2 of the field's 10 hex values, ignoring the second (often more reliable) volume-base pair.
  - _Why:_ The canonical com.apple.iTunes iTunNorm string contains 10 space-separated hex values: indices 0/1 are L/R for one measurement base and 2/3 are L/R for a second base (the remaining are peak/duration data). Encoders disagree on which base is authoritative and several write the usable level into the 2/3 pair, leaving 0/1 as 0x00000000 — which this code already rejects via `left > 0, right > 0` (line 203) and then returns nil, silently dropping a valid tag. Only consulting fields[0]/[1] makes the parser miss real loudness data on a non-trivial subset of iTunes-encoded files.
  - _Fix:_ Read both pairs and combine, e.g. parse fields[0..3] when count >= 4, take the louder channel across the available pairs (or average the two bases), and only fall back to the 2-field path when count == 2. At minimum, if fields[0]/[1] are 0, try fields[2]/[3] before giving up.

### `macos/Sources/SmokeTest/main.swift`
- **L51** [resource-leak] Temp data dir is created per run and never cleaned up; every exit() path skips Swift deinit so LyrebirdCore is never shut down.
  - _Why:_ LyrebirdCore opens its DB/state inside tmpDir, but the program terminates exclusively via C `exit()`, which bypasses all Swift deinitializers — so the core's session/handles are torn down only by process death and the unique tmpDir (cache, sqlite, partial downloads) is left on disk. Run repeatedly in CI, NSTemporaryDirectory accumulates one `lyrebird-smoke-<uuid>` tree per invocation with no reaper. It also means the harness never exercises a clean core shutdown, so a shutdown-time crash/leak would never surface here.
  - _Fix:_ Wrap the body so cleanup runs before exit: compute the exit code into a variable and `defer { try? FileManager.default.removeItem(atPath: tmpDir) }` plus an explicit core logout/shutdown if the FFI exposes one, then exit once at the end. Or register an atexit handler that removes tmpDir.

## P3 (225)

### `core/src/client.rs`
- **L291** [error-handling] parse_retry_after only handles the integer-seconds form of Retry-After and silently returns None for the HTTP-date form, falling back to local backoff and ignoring a server-specified longer wait.
  - _Why:_ RFC 7231 allows Retry-After as an HTTP-date; some proxies/CDNs (and Cloudflare, which this app explicitly fronts via CF-Access) emit dates. When that happens the client ignores the directive and uses its own 200/400/800ms backoff, which is also capped at RETRY_AFTER_CAP=5s — so it may retry far sooner than the server asked and keep getting throttled.
  - _Fix:_ Parse the HTTP-date form too (httpdate crate or chrono) and compute the delay relative to now, still clamped to a sane cap; or at minimum log when a non-integer Retry-After is dropped.
- **L444** [consistency] Most read endpoints (latest_albums, album_tracks, tracks_by_artist, genres, playlists_items, instant_mix, similar_*, etc.) inline the http.get + build_headers builder closure instead of using the existing send_get helper, duplicating the headers wiring ~20 times.
  - _Why:_ Not a runtime bug, but the duplication means a future change to GET header construction (e.g. adding an Accept header) must be made in ~20 places, and any one missed produces an inconsistent request. send_get already exists for exactly this.
  - _Fix:_ Route the plain GET-with-headers call sites through self.send_get(url) and reserve the inline closure only where the request differs (POST/DELETE/raw).
- **L1105** [validation] add_to_playlist does not guard against an empty item_ids slice; it issues a POST with an empty Ids= query parameter.
  - _Why:_ An empty add (possible from a UI multiselect with nothing selected) fires a needless network POST with Ids= and, combined with the non-idempotent retry path (line 274), can be retried. At best wasted round-trips; behavior on the server for an empty Ids is undefined.
  - _Fix:_ Return Ok(()) early when item_ids.is_empty() (and/or validate in the FFI wrapper) to skip the request entirely.
- **L1118** [validation] add_to_playlist sends a request with an empty Ids parameter when item_ids is empty instead of short-circuiting.
  - _Why:_ item_ids.join(",") on an empty slice yields an empty string, so the client fires POST Playlists/{id}/Items?Ids=&UserId=... with no items. The FFI wrapper in lib.rs (add_to_playlist) passes Vec<String> straight through with no guard, so an accidental empty call produces a pointless network round-trip whose server behavior is undefined (no-op or 400 depending on version). Unlike artist_top_tracks/limit checks elsewhere in this file, there is no early return for the empty case.
  - _Fix:_ Add `if item_ids.is_empty() { return Ok(()); }` at the top of add_to_playlist (matching the `if limit == 0` guard in playlists_containing_artist).
- **L1353** [consistency] instant_mix maps every returned item to Track without filtering on kind, unlike suggestions and playlist_tracks which guard on kind == "Audio".
  - _Why:_ suggestions (line ~1386) and playlist_tracks (line ~1079) defensively filter `i.kind.as_deref() == Some("Audio")` before mapping to Track, but instant_mix does not. If the InstantMix endpoint ever returns a non-audio item (e.g. a folder/album seed echo), Track::from will produce a degenerate Track (empty media source / zero runtime) that the player cannot play. The inconsistency means the same defensive contract is applied unevenly across sibling endpoints.
  - _Fix:_ Apply the same `.filter(|i| i.kind.as_deref() == Some("Audio"))` before `.map(Track::from)` in instant_mix for consistency and robustness.
- **L1522** [consistency] Query parameter casing for the user id is inconsistent across endpoints (userId vs UserId), relying on Jellyfin's case-insensitive query binding.
  - _Why:_ ASP.NET Core model binding is case-insensitive so both currently work against Jellyfin, but the mixed casing is a latent fragility: any future strict/case-sensitive proxy, custom server, or query-signing layer could drop the lowercase variant, silently turning per-user projections (UserData/IsFavorite/PlayCount) into anonymous results. It also makes grepping/auditing the auth-scoped calls harder.
  - _Fix:_ Standardize on the canonical Jellyfin casing `UserId` everywhere (lines 1522, 1661, 1738) to match the majority of call sites in this file.
- **L2367** [performance] playlist_library_id (and the parallel music_library_id) does not cache the negative result, so when the server has no playlists library every call re-issues a full `GET /UserViews` network round-trip.
  - _Why:_ The cache is only populated on the success path. On a Jellyfin instance without a dedicated playlists view (common — playlists can live under the music library), every screen that needs the playlist library id triggers a fresh UserViews fetch instead of the intended one-time resolution, adding an avoidable per-call HTTP request.
  - _Fix:_ Cache the miss as well (e.g. store an Option<Option<String>> or a separate 'resolved' flag) so repeated lookups after a known-negative result short-circuit without hitting the network, matching the intent of the existing positive-cache fast path.
