- **L2536** [bug] stream_url silently substitutes an empty `UserId=` query parameter when `self.user_id` is None instead of returning an error.
  - _Why:_ An empty UserId on `Audio/{id}/universal` defeats user-specific transcode-profile / device-profile resolution and playback-state association on the Jellyfin side. In practice user_id is always Some after authentication so this branch is effectively unreachable, but as written it produces a malformed request URL rather than a clear NotAuthenticated error, masking the real cause if it ever fires (e.g. a streaming call issued before login completes).
  - _Fix:_ Return `Err(LyrebirdError::NotAuthenticated)` when `self.user_id` is None, consistent with fetch_item/user_views/rename_playlist which all guard on user_id, rather than emitting `UserId=`.

### `core/src/error.rs`
- **L246** [bug] `is_cert_error` detects self-signed/untrusted certs purely by substring-matching the error chain's Display strings ("invalid peer certificate", "certificate verify failed", "UnknownIssuer", etc.). These strings come from rustls/the TLS backend and are not a stable API; a backend upgrade or a non-English/locale-dependent message can change them, silently reclassifying a cert error as a generic Network error.
  - _Why:_ If the match misses, From<reqwest::Error> falls back to Network(...) and the user loses the (intended) self-signed-cert path entirely, getting a generic "check your connection" with no trust affordance. Substring matching on third-party error text is inherently fragile.
  - _Fix:_ Where possible, downcast the source error to the concrete rustls error type (e.g. rustls::Error::InvalidCertificate(...)) and match on the enum rather than its string. Keep the substring list as a fallback only. Add a regression test that exercises a real rustls cert error to catch backend message drift.

### `core/src/lib.rs`
- **L172** [validation] login validates only that username is non-empty, but the InvalidCredentials error it returns claims both username and password must be non-empty.
  - _Why:_ An empty password falls through to authenticate_by_name, which posts `Pw: ""` to the server (client.rs:500). Jellyfin allows passwordless accounts, so sending an empty password is arguably intentional — but then the InvalidCredentials message is misleading, and resume_session (lines 232-234) also only re-validates username. This is a message/behavior inconsistency, not a security hole.
  - _Fix:_ Either drop 'and password' from the InvalidCredentials message (if empty passwords are intentionally allowed) or, if they should be rejected, add `if password.is_empty()` to the guard to match the stated contract.
- **L315** [error-handling] Credential and setting deletions in logout/forget_token swallow errors with `let _ =`.
  - _Why:_ On logout, a failure to delete the keyring token or the last_server_id/last_user_id settings is security-relevant: a stale token left in the keychain plus stale last_* settings could let resume_session silently re-authenticate after the user explicitly logged out. clear_user_data failures are logged (line 312) but the token/setting deletes are not, so a partial logout passes silently.
  - _Fix:_ Log on failure (tracing::warn!) for each delete so a partial logout is observable, and consider that delete_token errors leaving a live token in the keychain is the more serious half — surface or at least record it.
- **L1247** [gap-stub] The heartbeat hardcodes is_muted: false. If the user mutes (volume 0 or system mute), the server's Now Playing never reflects the muted state.
  - _Why:_ PlayerStatus carries `volume` (player.rs:43) which the loop already has in `status`, so the real mute state (volume == 0.0) is available but ignored. Minor cosmetic divergence on remote-control surfaces.
  - _Fix:_ Set is_muted from status (e.g. `is_muted: status.volume <= 0.0`) and optionally populate volume_level from status.volume.
- **L1313** [error-handling] set_shuffle and set_repeat_mode silently swallow the persistence error and re-read the OTHER field from a fresh status() snapshot taken after mutating one field, which both drops persistence failures and opens a small TOCTOU window for an inconsistent (shuffle, repeat) pair to be written.
  - _Why:_ `let _ =` discards a Storage error, so shuffle/repeat preferences can silently fail to persist across launches with no signal. Reading status.repeat_mode after set_shuffle (two separate player-lock acquisitions) means another caller mutating repeat in between persists a torn pair. Low risk on a single-threaded UI but unnecessary.
  - _Fix:_ Read both fields from a single player snapshot taken after the mutation (or pass both intended values), and surface or at least log the save_shuffle_repeat error instead of discarding it.

### `core/src/models.rs`
- **L74** [consistency] Track carries favorite/play-count data twice: flat `is_favorite`/`play_count` fields AND nested `user_data: Option<UserItemData>` which holds the same values. Dual source of truth on the same struct.
  - _Why:_ Both are populated together from RawItem.user_data at construction (client.rs:2984-3001), so they agree at build time. But consumers disagree on which to trust: AppModel.isFavorite(track:) reads `track.userData?.isFavorite` then falls back to `track.isFavorite` (AppModel.swift:4128-4129), while TrackInfoSheet.swift:76 reads the flat `track.playCount` directly. Any future mutation that updates only one source (e.g. an optimistic favorite toggle that rewrites `userData` but not the flat field, or vice-versa) will make the two views of the same track disagree. Denormalized duplicate fields are a known staleness footgun.
  - _Fix:_ Pick one source of truth. Either drop the flat `is_favorite`/`play_count` from Track and have all Swift call sites read `user_data`, or make them computed accessors that delegate to `user_data` so they cannot drift. If kept for binding convenience, document the invariant that both must be rewritten atomically on any mutation.
- **L79** [consistency] Tick/bitrate fields use inconsistent signedness across the model structs, inviting deserialization fragility for any struct that ingests server JSON directly.
  - _Why:_ Jellyfin models RunTimeTicks and Bitrate as nullable signed longs. Structs that deserialize directly (MediaSourceInfo via resp.json in client.rs) use i64 and are safe; structs typed u64 (SearchHint.runtime_ticks) would hard-fail deserialization if the server ever emits a negative sentinel. SearchHint is built through a RawSearchHint intermediary whose field is also u64 (client.rs:2874), so a negative value would error the whole search-hint parse rather than degrade one field. Mixing u64 and i64 for the identical concept (ticks) across sibling structs is an avoidable inconsistency.
  - _Fix:_ Standardize all *_ticks fields to i64 (matching Jellyfin's wire type) and clamp/saturate to >=0 at the conversion boundary, or keep u64 only where the value is provably non-negative and document why. Same for bitrate.
- **L306** [dead-code] FavoriteState derives Serialize but is only ever used as a deserialize target for the favorite endpoints' responses; it is never serialized to the server.
  - _Why:_ Confirmed by grep: FavoriteState appears only as the Ok type of set_favorite/unset_favorite/toggle_favorite (client.rs:1771/1818/1859) and the corresponding lib.rs FFI returns (lib.rs:746/756/769), all read paths. The Serialize derive is dead. Harmless, but it also means the per-field PascalCase renames silently double as the (unused) serialization contract; if someone later starts serializing this struct they'd get PascalCase output, which may or may not be intended. Minor.
  - _Fix:_ Drop the Serialize derive unless round-tripping is intended. Not load-bearing.
- **L643** [validation] PlaybackStartInfo / PlaybackProgressInfo / PlaybackStopInfo derive Default with a required, non-optional `item_id: String`, so a defaulted instance serializes `ItemId: ""`.
  - _Why:_ These structs are serialized and POSTed to /Sessions/Playing* (the reporting endpoints). `Default` makes it trivially easy for a caller to construct one with an empty item_id, which the server will reject or silently drop, breaking PlayCount / resume-point reporting with no client-side signal. The Default derive exists presumably for the optional fields, but it masks the required-field invariant.
  - _Fix:_ Either drop the Default derive on these report structs and force callers through an explicit constructor that takes item_id, or add a debug_assert/validation at the serialization call sites in client.rs that item_id is non-empty before POSTing.

### `core/src/player.rs`
- **L108** [bug] queue_index and queue.len() are cast usize->u32 in snapshot() without bounds checking; a queue or index exceeding u32::MAX truncates silently.
  - _Why:_ PlayerStatus exposes queue_position/queue_length as u32 over the UniFFI boundary. On 64-bit hosts a queue larger than ~4.29 billion entries (queue_index/len > u32::MAX) would wrap and report a wrong, possibly tiny value to Swift, which uses these for queueChanged() diffing and queue UI. Not realistically hit by a music app's queue, hence p3, but it is an unchecked lossy cast on data crossing the FFI.
  - _Fix:_ Either widen these PlayerStatus fields to u64, or saturate the cast (e.g. u32::try_from(...).unwrap_or(u32::MAX)) so the value clamps rather than wraps. Low priority given realistic queue sizes.
- **L298** [bug] set_current (reached via mark_track_started) updates `current` and forces state=Playing but never updates queue_index, so it relies entirely on callers having already positioned the queue. Any future code path that plays a track directly (without setQueue/skipNext first) would desync current vs queue_index and make skip_next/peek_next navigate from the wrong position.
  - _Why:_ All current callers happen to pre-position the queue (AppModel.play -> core.setQueue sets queue_index; handleTrackEnded -> core.skipNext sets both before audio.play -> markTrackStarted), so today current always equals queue[queue_index]. But set_current takes a Track with no notion of its queue position; if any new feature plays a track that isn't queue[queue_index], skip_next()/peek_next() (player.rs:169/203) will return neighbors of the stale index, not of the actually-playing track. Latent footgun masked only by call ordering.
  - _Fix:_ Have set_current locate the track in the queue and update queue_index (or take an explicit index), or document/enforce that current must always be queue[queue_index] and assert it. At minimum, set_current should not unconditionally force state=Playing (it is called from load() before AVPlayer actually starts).
- **L434** [test-gap] set_queue boundary coverage is incomplete. `set_queue_rejects_out_of_bounds_start_index` tests index 5 / len 2 (far OOB) and `set_queue_rejects_empty_queue` tests len 0, but the exact off-by-one boundary `idx == len` (e.g. index 2 with a 2-element queue) — the precise threshold of the `idx >= tracks.len()` guard at line 138 — is never tested. There is also no test that re-calling set_queue on an already-populated player correctly replaces the queue and resets queue_index.
  - _Why:_ The most common off-by-one failure for a `>=` length guard is at exactly `idx == len`. If someone refactored the guard to `>` (allowing idx==len), the existing far-OOB test (idx 5) might still pass under a different bug shape, but the true boundary would slip. Re-setting the queue (second set_queue) is the normal runtime path (play a new album) and is untested for index/queue replacement.
  - _Fix:_ Add `set_queue(vec![track("a"),track("b")], 2)` and assert it returns Err(InvalidIndex{index:2,len:2}); add a test that calls set_queue twice with different vecs and asserts the second call's queue_length/queue_position/current reflect only the second queue.

### `core/src/query.rs`
- **L329** [performance] ItemsQuery never sends EnableTotalRecordCount; relies on the server defaulting it to true to populate total_count
  - _Why:_ total_count (query.rs:362) is read straight from TotalRecordCount, and RawItems deserializes it with #[serde(default)] so a missing field becomes 0 (client.rs:2716). I verified against the live server (music.skalthoff.com) that the current Jellyfin returns the correct TotalRecordCount=20060 even without the flag, because EnableTotalRecordCount defaults to true server-side — so this is NOT a live bug today. It is a latent robustness gap: any Jellyfin fork/version (or a future default flip) that requires the flag, or a deployment that sets it false globally, would silently report total_count=0 and break 'load more'/pagination math. The only test coverage (tests.rs:6895) passes solely because the mock hardcodes TotalRecordCount:1.
  - _Fix:_ Explicitly append `EnableTotalRecordCount=true` in apply() so total_count is deterministic regardless of server defaults (it's already the effective behavior, this just makes it contractual). If count-skipping is ever wanted for cheap existence checks, gate it behind a builder flag rather than depending on the implicit default.

### `core/src/scrobble.rs`
- **L70** [gap-stub] scrobble_threshold_reached cannot scrobble short tracks (<4 min) when runtime is unknown, even at 100% completion
  - _Why:_ When runtime_secs <= 0.0 (duration unavailable, which happens for some streamed/transcoded items where RunTimeTicks isn't projected), the half-runtime rule is skipped and only the absolute 4-minute rule remains. A 3-minute track played in full with unknown runtime returns false forever, so it is never scrobbled. The ListenBrainz/Last.fm convention is 'half the track OR 4 minutes', but the half-track arm is silently disabled whenever duration is missing.
  - _Fix:_ This matches the documented half-or-4min rule and is conservative (no false positives), so it's low severity. If completeness matters, have the caller pass the actual elapsed-vs-duration from the player (which always knows the real duration once playing) rather than relying on a possibly-zero runtime_secs, or treat 'position past a large fraction of observed max position' as a fallback when runtime is unknown.

### `core/src/storage.rs`
- **L39** [gap-stub] migrate() has no guard against opening a database whose stored schema_version is GREATER than SCHEMA_VERSION (a DB written by a newer build of the app, e.g. after a downgrade). It silently proceeds and operates on a future schema.
  - _Why:_ Running an older binary against a newer on-disk schema can read/write columns that no longer match expectations and corrupt user data or panic at query time. Harmless today (only version 1 exists) but the open path offers no safety net for the first time a v2 ships.
  - _Fix:_ After computing current, if current > SCHEMA_VERSION return Err(LyrebirdError::Storage(format!("database schema {current} is newer than supported {SCHEMA_VERSION}"))) so a downgraded app refuses to mangle a newer DB instead of operating blindly.
- **L62** [dead-code] The 'if current < SCHEMA_VERSION { }' block has an empty body (stripped of its placeholder comment). With SCHEMA_VERSION == 1 and the explicit 'if current < 1' migration immediately above it, this branch is structurally dead/no-op for every reachable value of current.
  - _Why:_ Dead conditional with no effect; a future maintainer adding migration N>1 may add it under the 'current < 1' style block above instead and never notice this generic hook, or assume this block already gates later migrations when it does nothing.
  - _Fix:_ Either remove the empty block, or convert the migration ladder to a single loop that bumps from current..SCHEMA_VERSION applying each step and writing the new version, so adding migration 2 is mechanical and this hook is actually used.
- **L220** [bug] CredentialStore builds the keyring account identifier as format!("{server_id}/{username}") with no escaping/separator-safety. A username (or server_id) containing '/' makes distinct (server_id, username) pairs map to the same keyring entry, e.g. ("a/b","c") and ("a","b/c") both produce "a/b/c".
  - _Why:_ Jellyfin usernames are user-controlled and may legitimately contain '/'. A collision means one account's token could be read or overwritten by another, or a delete on logout removes the wrong account's token — a credential-isolation defect, even if rare.
  - _Fix:_ Use an unambiguous encoding for the keyring account key, e.g. percent-encode server_id and username before joining, or store them as separate fields/use a delimiter that cannot appear in either after encoding. Apply consistently across save/load/delete so existing entries remain locatable.

### `core/src/tests.rs`
- **L39** [concurrency] Mock keyring is installed via a process-global Once but credential-using tests run in parallel against the shared store with only key-uniqueness as isolation
  - _Why:_ There is no serial_test dependency and no --test-threads=1 in core/Cargo.toml or any .cargo/config, so cargo runs these tests on multiple threads sharing one global mock keyring map. The whole isolation strategy is hand-picked unique server_id/username keys per test (srv-resume-full, srv-partial, srv-logout, srv-forget, srv-refresh-test, ...). Any future test that reuses an existing key, or a refactor that derives the key from a shared constant, will cross-contaminate in-flight with no compile-time guard. Additionally the Once only guards builder registration, not the first use, so a credential call scheduled before the first install_mock_keyring completes could momentarily hit the real OS keychain.
  - _Fix:_ Make the contract explicit and robust: gate credential-touching tests with serial_test::serial (add the dev-dep) or have install_mock_keyring clear the global STORE at the start of each test, so isolation no longer depends solely on every author remembering to choose a globally-unique key.
- **L1042** [test-gap] similar_items_builds_query_and_parses pins item kind/order but never asserts the parsed id or name fields of the returned ItemRefs.
  - _Why:_ similar_items maps via `ItemRef::from` (client.rs:1478). A break in id/name projection for ItemRef would pass since only kind is asserted; downstream navigation keys off id.
  - _Fix:_ Add `assert_eq!(items[0].id, "a2")` and `assert_eq!(items[1].id, "t2")` (and optionally names).
- **L1299** [test-gap] tracks_by_genre_builds_query asserts the SortBy triple but not the matching SortOrder triple that production emits, so a sort-direction regression on genre track listing is uncaught.
  - _Why:_ Jellyfin pairs SortBy and SortOrder positionally; a mismatch in count or direction (e.g. Descending) silently reorders the disc/track view. The test pins the key but not the direction it sorts.
  - _Fix:_ Add `assert!(q.contains("SortOrder=Ascending%2CAscending%2CAscending"), "query: {q}")`.
- **L1398** [test-gap] artist_detail_parses_overview_and_backdrops verifies overview, backdrops, external URLs, and image tag but not the genres field present in the fixture.
  - _Why:_ similar_artists_builds_query_and_parses does assert `artists[0].genres` (line 954), so the projection is known regression-prone; the artist detail mapping leaves it unchecked.
  - _Fix:_ Add `assert_eq!(detail.genres, vec!["Ambient".to_string(), "Electronic".to_string()])`.
- **L1528** [test-gap] lyrics_parses_plain_text does not verify the distinguishing behavior implied by its name: that embedded newlines in a single plain-text line are preserved.
  - _Why:_ The point of the plain-text path vs the synced path is preserving raw multi-line text; `LyricLine.text` is mapped straight through (client.rs:3145) with no transformation, so the test should assert the full string survives, otherwise truncation/normalization regressions pass.
  - _Fix:_ Assert the full value, e.g. `assert_eq!(lyrics.lines[0].text, "Just the words\nno timing")` (or at minimum `.contains("no timing")`).
- **L1845** [test-gap] latest_albums_applies_offset_client_side asserts page.total_count == 7 (the raw count of items the server returned for the inflated server_limit=offset+limit), even though only 3 items are returned to the caller. The test enshrines total_count == server-returned-array-length rather than a true library total, so it would block any future correction of latest_albums' total_count semantics.
  - _Why:_ /Items/Latest returns a bare array with no TotalRecordCount, so total_count here is inherently a heuristic. Asserting the exact value 7 couples the test to that implementation quirk; a reasonable refactor that set total_count to the sliced length (3) or to an Option would break this test even though it improved correctness.
  - _Fix:_ If 7 is the intended contract, add an assertion comment-free expectation that documents it via the test name (e.g. total_count_reflects_server_fetch_size); otherwise relax to assert_eq!(page.items.len(), 3) and drop the brittle total_count==7 expectation, or assert total_count >= items.len() to avoid pinning the heuristic.
- **L2150** [test-gap] playlist_tracks_uses_paging is materially weaker than its sibling playlist_tracks_preserves_order_and_builds_query: it omits the matchers for Fields, EnableUserData, IncludeItemTypes, and UserId on the /Items request, asserting only ParentId, Limit, and StartIndex. A regression that dropped EnableUserData=true or the PlaylistItemId/UserData fields on the paged path would not be caught here.
  - _Why:_ Paging and the field/user-data flags are produced by the same code path, but having two near-duplicate tests where one is a strict subset of the other adds maintenance cost without adding coverage; the weaker one gives a false impression that the paged path is independently validated for the favorite/playlist-item-id fields it actually needs.
  - _Fix:_ Either fold this into the stronger test (parameterize over paging values) or add the Fields/EnableUserData matchers here too so the paged request is held to the same contract as the offset-0 request.
- **L2377** [test-gap] search_hints_builds_expected_query_and_parses asserts includeItemTypes contains 'Playlist' (matcher at 2319-2322) but the mocked SearchHints array contains only MusicArtist / MusicAlbum / Audio — Playlist hint parsing is never exercised even though it is an advertised supported type.
  - _Why:_ The client deliberately requests Playlist hints (the matcher proves it), so Playlist is a live result kind users can receive. The SearchHint::from / kind-mapping path for Playlist is entirely uncovered, so a parsing regression for playlist search hints would ship undetected.
  - _Fix:_ Add a 4th SearchHint object with Type:"Playlist" (and e.g. ChildCount) and assert its kind/name parse, so the Playlist branch of SearchHint::from is covered.
- **L2535** [test-gap] search_hints_clamps_zero_limit_to_one verifies the clamp only indirectly via the mock's query_param("limit","1") matcher; the success-path assertions on an empty result are tautological and the actual outbound limit param is never inspected.
  - _Why:_ It does catch limit=0 (404 -> error -> test fails via send_with_retry/check), so the named behavior is minimally covered. But the assertions actually written (empty body, count 0) hold for ANY matched request and prove nothing about the clamp; the safety net is the implicit mock-mismatch behavior, which is brittle if the mock default changes. A direct query inspection would make the intent explicit and robust.
  - _Fix:_ After the call, pull server.received_requests(), find the GET to /Search/Hints, and assert its query contains limit=1 explicitly (mirroring the search_sends_enable_user_data_and_expanded_fields pattern at 2651-2668).
- **L2982** [test-gap] toggle_favorite_dispatches_to_set_when_true (2918) and _unset_when_false (2960) verify the HTTP verb dispatch but the true case asserts only is_favorite and omits play_count, so the PlayCount round-trip through toggle->set is unverified on that branch.
  - _Why:_ toggle_favorite delegates to set_favorite/unset_favorite (client.rs 1859-1865), each of which parses the FavoriteState body including play_count. The false branch confirms body fields propagate; the true branch leaves play_count parsing through the set path unchecked, an asymmetric coverage gap that would miss a regression dropping PlayCount on the set route.
  - _Fix:_ Add assert_eq!(state.play_count, Some(0)) (and last_played.is_none()) to the true case for parity, so toggle's body-parse path is fully covered on both branches.
- **L3525** [test-gap] The Fields-contains-PlaylistItemId check is performed via assert! inside the wiremock respond_with closure, which executes on the mock server's task rather than the test task. A failed assertion there panics the request handler thread, not the test; the client side typically observes a dropped/reset connection and fails later at the .unwrap() on line 3557 with a connection error instead of the intended message.
  - _Why:_ Assertions inside server-side responder closures do not propagate their failure message to the test runner; on failure the developer sees an opaque connection error from the client unwrap rather than the descriptive "Fields must contain PlaylistItemId" message, making the failure harder to diagnose. It also means the assertion is only reached if the request actually arrives.
  - _Fix:_ Prefer matching the requirement with a wiremock matcher (e.g. add a custom matcher / query_param check on Fields so a non-matching request 404s deterministically), or capture the request via server.received_requests() after the call and assert on the Fields query param on the test thread, so the descriptive assertion message surfaces correctly.
- **L3974** [test-gap] playback_info_posts_device_profile_and_parses_response asserts only a subset of the parsed MediaSource fields. The mock returns SupportsDirectStream, SupportsTranscoding, TranscodingSubProtocol, TranscodingContainer, Size, RunTimeTicks and Path, none of which are asserted.
  - _Why:_ Field-rename or wrong serde alias regressions on the unasserted MediaSource fields (e.g. TranscodingContainer -> transcoding_container) would not be caught despite this being the one test that parses a full PlaybackInfo response.
  - _Fix:_ Extend the assertions to cover the remaining deserialized fields (supports_direct_stream, supports_transcoding, transcoding_container, size, run_time_ticks, path) so each serde mapping is exercised.
- **L4100** [test-gap] music_library_id_returns_404_when_no_music_view asserts the NotFound variant but does not pin the negative-caching behavior. The impl does not cache a miss (client.rs:2331-2345 only sets cache on success), so a second call re-hits /UserViews; the test never calls it twice, leaving that behavior unspecified.
  - _Why:_ If a future change started caching the negative result (returning a stale NotFound after the user adds a music library), this test would still pass. The 404-cache contract is exactly the kind of subtle behavior worth pinning.
  - _Fix:_ Add a second music_library_id() call after the server is re-mounted to return a music view, and assert it now resolves (and/or assert /UserViews was hit twice) to lock in that misses are not cached.
- **L4292** [test-gap] remove_from_playlist_is_noop_on_empty_entry_ids authenticates before calling with an empty slice, so it cannot detect a reorder of the empty-short-circuit ahead of the auth check. The impl currently checks require_token() (client.rs:2410) before the empty short-circuit (2411), and that ordering is unpinned.
  - _Why:_ If someone moves the `if entry_ids.is_empty() { return Ok(()) }` above require_token(), an unauthenticated empty call would silently succeed instead of returning NotAuthenticated. Neither this test nor the requires_authenticated_session test (which passes a non-empty slice) covers that combination.
  - _Fix:_ Add an assertion that an UNauthenticated remove_from_playlist with an empty slice still returns NotAuthenticated, pinning that the auth check precedes the empty short-circuit.
- **L4343** [test-gap] remove_from_playlist_propagates_server_errors asserts only the error variant (Forbidden) and ignores the server-provided body. The mock returns the body string "forbidden" (line 4331) but the test never checks the message is surfaced.
  - _Why:_ Error messages are user-facing in this app (errorMessage surfacing per CLAUDE.md). A regression that drops the body and produces an empty Forbidden("") would pass, hiding the server's reason from the UI.
  - _Fix:_ Assert the Forbidden payload contains/equals the server body (e.g. `if let Forbidden(msg) = err { assert!(msg.contains("forbidden")) }`) to lock in that the server reason propagates.
- **L4386** [test-gap] default_macos_profile_serializes_to_pascal_case enforces no-underscore only on top-level keys; nested objects (DirectPlayProfiles / TranscodingProfiles entries) are not checked for PascalCase despite the test name implying full PascalCase serialization.
  - _Why:_ A nested field that serialized as snake_case (e.g. `audio_codec` instead of `AudioCodec`) would silently fail to bind on the Jellyfin server but pass this test, since only top-level keys are scanned.
  - _Fix:_ Recurse the no-underscore key check into DirectPlayProfiles and TranscodingProfiles entry objects, or add explicit per-entry key assertions for nested PascalCase fields.
- **L4519** [test-gap] No stream_url test exercises the unauthenticated branch: every stream_url test calls set_session first, so the impl branch that omits api_key when no token (client.rs:2549) and emits UserId="" via unwrap_or("") (client.rs:2536) is never covered.
  - _Why:_ A regression that always appends `api_key=` (empty) or panics on a missing token/user_id would go undetected. The conditional token append and the `unwrap_or("")` fallback for user_id are real branches that ship in playback URL construction.
  - _Fix:_ Add a test that builds stream_url on a fresh mock_client (no set_session) and asserts the URL contains neither `api_key=` nor a non-empty UserId, confirming the no-session path is safe.
- **L4742** [consistency] resume_session_returns_session_when_all_settings_present saves a keyring token but never deletes it, unlike its sibling resume tests
  - _Why:_ The mock keyring STORE is a process-global OnceLock<Arc<Mutex<HashMap>>> (install_mock_keyring, tests.rs:48-53) shared by all tests in the run. resume_session_returns_none_when_token_missing (4732) and resume_session_noop_when_only_partial_settings (4817) both delete their token at the end to keep the global store clean; this test leaves srv-resume-full/resume-full-user populated for the rest of the process. It is harmless today only because the key is unique, but it breaks the cleanup convention the other tests establish and would silently mask a regression if another test ever reused that key.
  - _Fix:_ Append CredentialStore::delete_token(server_id, username).unwrap(); at the end of the test to mirror the cleanup the sibling resume tests perform.
- **L4974** [test-gap] forget_token_preserves_server_url_and_username does not assert the in-memory client teardown that forget_token performs
  - _Why:_ forget_token (core/src/lib.rs:341) sets inner.client = None and also calls stop_heartbeat()/player.clear(). The resume tests elsewhere consistently assert core.inner.lock().client state, but this test verifies only persistence side effects, leaving the client/heartbeat teardown uncovered. A regression that forgot to drop the live client (leaking an authenticated session after the user chose 'forget') would not be caught here.
  - _Fix:_ Add assert!(core.inner.lock().client.is_none(), "forget_token must drop the live client"); after the forget_token call, mirroring the client assertions in the resume tests.
- **L6355** [test-gap] heartbeat_fires_at_expected_cadence couples tokio::time::pause() with real wiremock HTTP round-trips inside the spawned task. Whether report_playback_progress completes before the next tokio::time::advance depends on a fixed 8-yield budget, making the request count nondeterministic; only the lenient '>= 2' threshold hides the flakiness.
  - _Why:_ Real network I/O is not virtual-time-controlled, so under CI load the heartbeat task may not finish its POST within 8 yields before the next advance, and the actual count drifts. The assertion is so loose (>=2 of an expected 3) that it would also pass if the cadence were wrong, e.g. fired every 7s instead of 5s.
  - _Fix:_ Either assert an exact count against deterministic virtual time (stub report so it doesn't block on real I/O), or assert the spacing of captured request timestamps rather than just the count, so a wrong cadence actually fails.
- **L6698** [test-gap] playlist_tracks_rejects_non_audio_items asserts items.len()==1 after filtering, but never asserts page.total_count. Production sets total_count = raw.total_record_count (3 here) even though only 1 item survives the client-side Audio filter (client.rs:1079,1088), so total_count disagrees with the returned items.
  - _Why:_ This is a real pagination-correctness ambiguity (total_count=3 vs 1 visible row) that the test leaves unpinned. If the intended behavior is to keep the server count, the test should document it; if not, this masks a paging bug where the UI shows '3 tracks' but only 1 loads.
  - _Fix:_ Add assert_eq!(page.total_count, ...) documenting the intended value. If total should reflect filtered count, this also flags a production fix in playlist_tracks.
- **L6839** [test-gap] with_client_releases_inner_lock_before_http relies on wall-clock thresholds (b_elapsed < 200ms while a 400ms mock runs, plus a fixed 50ms thread::sleep to order the threads). On a loaded CI box the lock-free image_url path can exceed 200ms purely from scheduler latency, producing a false failure unrelated to lock contention.
  - _Why:_ Timing-based concurrency assertions with absolute millisecond bounds are inherently flaky under CI contention. The 50ms sleep also doesn't guarantee thread A has actually entered its HTTP await before B runs; if A is slow to start, the test no longer proves the lock was released.
  - _Fix:_ Use a synchronization primitive (e.g. a Barrier or a channel signalled from inside list_albums via a test hook) to deterministically order the threads, and assert relative timing (b_elapsed << a_elapsed) rather than an absolute 200ms bound.
- **L6862** [test-gap] items_query_builder_round_trips_through_server asserts the outgoing query contains each param but never asserts the Fields parameter carries the requested fields(vec![Genres, ProductionYear]). The builder's .fields() serialization is therefore unverified by this round-trip test.
  - _Why:_ A regression where .fields() is dropped or mis-serialized (e.g. wrong casing, missing Fields= param) would pass this test, yet would cause Jellyfin to omit genre/year data and break album shelves. The test name implies a full round-trip but a key builder output is unchecked.
  - _Fix:_ Add assert!(q.contains("Fields=")) and assert the CSV contains Genres and ProductionYear.
- **L7091** [test-gap] structured_error_server_5xx_is_retryable sleeps in real wall-clock time. 503 is classified retriable, so client.albums() exhausts MAX_ATTEMPTS=3 with real backoff sleeps (backoff_for: ~200ms then ~400ms with jitter, ~0.6s total) before returning the Server{status:503} error.
  - _Why:_ Smaller cost than the 429 test but the same avoidable pattern; accumulates across the many retry-exercising tests and is inconsistent with the pause()/advance() pattern already used in this file.
  - _Fix:_ Wrap with tokio::time::pause() + advance() (see tests.rs:6341-6360) or #[tokio::test(start_paused = true)] so the 3 backoff waits are virtualized; the Server{status:503} / is_retryable() assertions remain unchanged.
- **L7404** [test-gap] mark_played_falls_back_to_legacy_route_on_404 does not assert request ordering — it only asserts that both the preferred POST and the legacy POST were each issued at least once (.any), not that the preferred route was attempted BEFORE the legacy one. The test name and comment-stripped intent ('preferred route tried first') are not actually verified.
  - _Why:_ If a future refactor inverted the order (legacy first, preferred as fallback) the test would still pass, defeating its purpose of pinning the preferred-then-fallback contract. The play_count==1 assertion proves the legacy body was consumed but not the call order.
  - _Fix:_ Capture the positions of the two matching requests in `requests` and assert the preferred index < legacy index (e.g. requests.iter().position(|r| ... preferred ...) < requests.iter().position(|r| ... legacy ...)). Apply the same ordering assertion to mark_unplayed_falls_back_to_legacy_route_on_405 (tests.rs:7488-7501).
- **L8098** [test-gap] single_listen_payload / track_metadata empty-string album branch is untested. The scrobble payload builder in core/src/scrobble.rs:107 uses `track.album_name.as_ref().filter(|a| !a.is_empty())`, so it has two distinct suppression paths for release_name: album is None, and album is Some(""). The tests only cover the None case.
  - _Why:_ The `!a.is_empty()` half of the filter predicate in scrobble.rs is dead from the test suite's perspective. If a future refactor changed `filter(|a| !a.is_empty())` to plain `track.album_name.as_ref()`, an empty-string album would start emitting `"release_name": ""` to ListenBrainz (a malformed metadata submission) and no test would fail. This is exactly the kind of guarded edge the tests otherwise pay close attention to.
  - _Fix:_ Add a test that builds a Track with `album_name: Some("".into())` (e.g. via a `Some("")` argument to scrobble_track, after widening its album param), calls single_listen_payload, and asserts `md.get("release_name").is_none()` — locking in the empty-string suppression behavior alongside the existing None case.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/AppDelegate.swift`
- **L125** [consistency] Dock play/pause menu item is gated on hasTrack (currentTrack != nil), but refreshDockTile uses a separate code path that shows a '▶' badge when state == .playing with NO currentTrack — the two notions of 'playing' disagree.
  - _Why:_ If status reports state==.playing while currentTrack==nil (a transient/loading state the codebase explicitly handles elsewhere — see togglePlayPause's `.loading` case and many `status.currentTrack == nil` checks in AppModel), the dock tile shows a play badge but the dock menu's Play/Pause/Next/Previous are all disabled (isEnabled = hasTrack on lines 125/134/143). The user sees 'it's playing' on the icon but cannot pause from the dock menu. Minor and edge-case, but it is an internally inconsistent definition of the playing state across the same file.
  - _Fix:_ Gate playPauseItem.isEnabled on `hasTrack || isPlaying` (or on `status.state != .idle`) so the menu control is usable whenever the badge claims playback; align the two playing-state predicates.
- **L264** [concurrency] handleSleep spawns an unstructured, untracked Task to pause audio; it is never cancelled and is not stored.
  - _Why:_ Unlike wakeProbeTask (stored + cancelled), this fire-and-forget Task is detached from any lifecycle. The work (audio.pause) is trivial so the practical risk is low, but it is the same unstructured-Task pattern the codebase otherwise tracks. If the app terminates between willSleep and the Task running, the pause may not happen; more importantly there is no way to cancel/observe it. The dock* @objc actions (lines 283-309) share this fire-and-forget shape.
  - _Fix:_ If pause must be synchronous on sleep, call `appModel?.audio.pause()` directly only if you can guarantee main-thread (willSleep is delivered on `.main` per the observer queue, line 78), avoiding the Task hop entirely; otherwise this is acceptable as-is but worth noting the inconsistency with wakeProbeTask's tracked lifecycle.
- **L301** [bug] dockPlayRecentAlbum re-resolves the clicked album from the live jumpBackIn cache; if jumpBackIn changed between menu build and click, the action silently does nothing.
  - _Why:_ The menu stores album.id in representedObject (line 164) from jumpBackIn at build time, then on click looks the id back up in the *current* jumpBackIn. jumpBackIn is refreshed asynchronously (refreshJumpBackIn, AppModel.swift:1918) including by reconnectIfNeeded after wake. If a refresh reorders/drops the album between the user opening the dock menu and clicking, `first(where:)` returns nil and the click is a no-op with no feedback. Per CLAUDE.md gap pattern #3, cache-only resolution should fall back to a core FFI (resolveAlbum) on miss.
  - _Fix:_ Store the whole Album in representedObject instead of just the id, or on cache miss fall back to AppModel.resolveAlbum(id) (the documented reference resolver) so a stale menu entry still plays.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/AppModel.swift`
- **L370** [consistency] Two near-identical search page-size constants with confusingly similar names coexist: `searchPagePageSize` (line 370, = 100) and `searchPageSize` (line 445, = 50). Both are live but feed different pagination paths.
  - _Why:_ The doubled 'Page' token in one name plus the tiny lexical delta makes it easy to grab the wrong constant when editing pagination math, yielding inconsistent page sizes (e.g. an off-by-2x offset/limit mismatch) that compiles cleanly and only manifests as missing or duplicated search rows.
  - _Fix:_ Rename to self-describing, clearly-distinct identifiers, e.g. `instantSearchPageSize` (50) and `fullSearchPageSize` (100), and update the four call sites accordingly.
- **L731** [gap-stub] `openInMainWindowFromMiniPlayer(_:)` activates the main window and pushes a route but neither dismisses the mini player nor switches the active tab, and because `navigate(to:)` appends unconditionally with no dedup, repeated taps from the mini player stack duplicate routes onto `navPath`.
  - _Why:_ Tapping the album art (or artist) twice in the mini player pushes `.album(id)` (or `.artist(id)`) onto navPath twice, so the back stack contains the same screen consecutively and the user must press Back multiple times to leave it. The mini player also stays on top of the freshly activated main window, so the navigation target may be obscured. Confidence is low on whether keeping the mini player visible is intentional (a large stripped comment precedes the function), hence p3.
  - _Fix:_ Either guard `navigate` against pushing a route equal to `navPath.last`, or in `openInMainWindowFromMiniPlayer` route through the tab/selectTab logic and only append when the target differs from the current top. If the mini player should close on navigation, also set `isMiniPlayerVisible = false` here as `returnToFullWindow()` does.
- **L822** [gap-stub] When there is no current track, the palette "Play" action is a no-op, and "Play Next"/"Add to Queue" are still appended to the roster but also no-op. These show as live commands that silently do nothing.
  - _Why:_ togglePlayPause() (line 5713) only acts when status.currentTrack != nil in the .ended/.stopped/.idle/.loading branch (line 5720), so the no-track "Play" action does nothing. "Play Next"/"Add to Queue" guard on currentTrack and return early when nil. With an empty queue (no current track) the command palette presents three playback commands that all silently fail, which reads as a broken feature.
  - _Fix:_ Only append playNext/addToQueue (and the no-track "Play") when hasTrack is true, or give the no-track "Play" a real action (e.g. start a default/last context); don't list commands that can't run in the current state.
- **L1143** [concurrency] retryNetwork()/retryServer() fire unstructured `Task { await refreshLibrary() }`, and refreshLibrary() has no reentrancy guard, so rapid retries (or a retry overlapping the initial load) run multiple concurrent full library refreshes.
  - _Why:_ Unlike loadMoreAlbums()/loadMoreArtists() which guard `!isLoadingMore*`, refreshLibrary() (line 1424) has no `guard !isLoadingLibrary` gate. Two overlapping invocations both issue albums/artists/tracks/playlists + all the downstream refresh* calls, doubling network/FFI work; the first to finish runs its `defer { isLoadingLibrary = false }` while the second is still loading, so the loading indicator flickers off prematurely. Mutations are MainActor-serialized so no data corruption, but it is wasted work and an inconsistent loading state.
  - _Fix:_ Add `guard !isLoadingLibrary else { return }` at the top of refreshLibrary(), or hold the retry Task in a stored property and cancel any in-flight refresh before starting a new one.
- **L1466** [error-handling] refreshLibrary() funnels every section's failure into the single shared errorMessage, so when more than one section fails only the last writer's message survives and earlier failures are masked.
  - _Why:_ All three catch blocks assign the same context (.libraryLoad) to the same errorMessage. If albums and artists both fail, the albums error is immediately overwritten by the artists error; the user sees only one of potentially several distinct failures, which is misleading when the failures differ.
  - _Fix:_ Accumulate per-section failures (or only set errorMessage if it is still nil), and prefer a single consolidated "some library sections failed to load" message rather than letting later blocks clobber earlier ones.
- **L1722** [error-handling] refreshRecentlyPlayed swallows all non-auth errors with no reachability accounting and no success note, diverging from every sibling refresher (refreshTracks/loadMore*) which call serverReachability.noteSuccess/noteFailure.
  - _Why:_ ServerReachability drives the app's online/offline UI. Because this path neither notes success on the happy path nor failure on the error path, a transient recently-played failure leaves reachability state unchanged in either direction, making the offline indicator inconsistent relative to other library fetches that do report.
  - _Fix:_ Mirror the sibling pattern: noteSuccess() after assigning the page, and in catch gate noteFailure() behind ServerReachability.shouldCount(error:) after handleAuthError.
- **L2052** [error-handling] refreshSuggestions and refreshRecentlyDiscoveredArtists swallow every FFI error via `try?` inside a detached task, including auth-expiry errors, so handleAuthError/markAuthExpired is never consulted from these paths and failures are completely silent (no log, no surfaced error).
  - _Why:_ If the token has expired, these calls throw an auth error that is dropped to []; the shelf silently empties and the session is not marked expired from here. It works only because some concurrently-running refresher (refreshLibrary) will independently trip markAuthExpired. There is also no log line, so a genuine server fault here is invisible during diagnosis.
  - _Fix:_ Replace `try?` with do/catch that routes through handleAuthError(error) and at least Log.net.error on other failures, consistent with the other refreshers in this file.
- **L2111** [error-handling] The Items-query fetch helpers only special-case HTTP 401; any other non-2xx (403/404/500/503) is fed straight into the JSON parser, which returns an empty collection, so server faults are indistinguishable from 'no results' and never surfaced or logged.
  - _Why:_ A 500 returning an error JSON body has no 'Items' key, so parse* returns [] and the shelf shows empty with no Log.net.error and no errorMessage. For supplementary home shelves silent degradation is defensible, but a persistent server-side 5xx is then invisible, and an auth problem returned as 403 (rather than 401) would also be missed by markAuthExpired.
  - _Fix:_ Add an else branch that, for non-2xx responses, at minimum logs the status code (Log.net.error) and treats 401/403 uniformly through markAuthExpired before attempting to parse.
- **L2160** [concurrency] buildItemsQuery and fetchLatestAlbumsWithDates call the synchronous Rust FFI core.authHeader() on the @MainActor, taking the core Inner mutex on the main thread.
  - _Why:_ Per the repo's own concurrency contract (CLAUDE.md gap pattern #2: 'every try core.X(...) on a @MainActor function takes the Rust Inner mutex on the main thread'), this acquires the FFI mutex on main. It is once-per-shelf-refresh rather than per-cell, so contention is bounded, but it is still a synchronous lock acquisition on the UI thread under the same mutex every other FFI call serializes through.
  - _Fix:_ Hoist the authHeader() call into the Task.detached block that already runs the network/parse off-main (or cache the header), so no FFI mutex is taken on the main actor in the query-build path.
- **L2321** [concurrency] buildItemsQuery calls the synchronous core FFI core.authHeader() directly on the @MainActor (not inside Task.detached), taking the Rust Inner mutex (and the client token mutex) on the main thread.
  - _Why:_ Every load/refresh that builds an items query (favorites, jump-back-in, quick-picks, rediscover, genre/year/tag filters) hits authHeader() on the MainActor. core.authHeader() -> with_client locks inner (lib.rs:1379) and auth_header locks the token mutex (client.rs:196) — two locks on the main thread per query. It is brief and not per-cell, so impact is small, but it is the documented 'sync FFI on the MainActor' anti-pattern.
  - _Fix:_ authHeader is cheap and stable for a session; cache the formatted header string on the model (invalidate on login/token refresh) so buildItemsQuery doesn't take the core mutex on the main thread on every query build.
- **L2399** [performance] parseLatestAlbumsWithDates allocates one ISO8601DateFormatter and toggles its formatOptions inside the parse loop on every fractional-seconds miss.
  - _Why:_ Mutating formatOptions per element forces the formatter to rebuild its internal state repeatedly. For the 20-item Latest call it is negligible, but the pattern is a minor inefficiency and slightly fragile (two assignments per non-fractional date). DateCreated from Jellyfin is consistently formatted, so the fallback rarely helps.
  - _Fix:_ Use two pre-configured static formatters (one with fractional seconds, one without) and try them in sequence, instead of mutating one formatter's options inside the loop.
- **L2775** [consistency] parseAlbum(from:) accepts ProductionYear == 0 as a real year, whereas albumFromDTO treats year <= 0 as nil.
  - _Why:_ Both functions produce Album objects from Jellyfin JSON but disagree on the sentinel: parseAlbum (used by resolveAlbum's FFI fallback) yields year = 0 for items missing a year, while albumFromDTO yields nil. UI that formats `year` will show '0' for an album resolved via the fallback path but blank for the same album from the items-query path.
  - _Fix:_ Mirror albumFromDTO's guard in parseAlbum: `let year: Int32? = (root["ProductionYear"] as? NSNumber).map { Int32(truncating: $0) }.flatMap { $0 > 0 ? $0 : nil }`.
- **L3409** [consistency] startInstantMix and regenerateInstantMix call playInstantMix directly without setting instantMixSeedLabel, so the InstantMixSheet's 'last mix' label (which only generateInstantMix updates) goes stale and can name a different seed than what is actually playing.
  - _Why:_ After starting a mix via the toolbar/keyboard (startInstantMix) or regenerate, opening the picker shows 'last mix: <previous seed>' which no longer matches the running radio, a small but real UI inconsistency.
  - _Fix:_ Set instantMixSeedLabel to the resolved seed's display name in startInstantMix and regenerateInstantMix (or clear it to nil when the seed name is unknown), so the picker label always reflects the active mix.
- **L3493** [error-handling] searchSeeds swallows all search errors with `try?`, returning nil indistinguishably from an empty result set; auth/reachability failures are never surfaced or counted.
  - _Why:_ Every other search/load path in this file routes errors through handleAuthError + ServerReachability + errorMessage (see search() at 3554-3567, loadMoreSearchResults at 3611-3617). searchSeeds drops them entirely, so a token expiry or server outage during a seed lookup looks identical to 'no matches', and the auth-recovery path (handleAuthError) is never triggered.
  - _Fix:_ Do/catch the FFI: on success return results; on failure call handleAuthError / ServerReachability.shouldCount / set errorMessage (or at least feed serverReachability) before returning nil, consistent with the other search functions.
- **L3600** [bug] loadMoreSearchResults dedups incoming page items against already-seen ids; if a returned page is entirely (or mostly) duplicates, the combined `loaded` count does not advance, so the next call recomputes the same offset and re-fetches the same page, stalling pagination at that boundary instead of progressing.
  - _Why:_ core.search paginates a single combined (artist+album+track) result set by offset (core/src/client.rs:2065-2104), and the client splits by kind. If the server ever returns overlapping items at a page boundary, the dedup silently drops them and the offset never moves past them, so 'load more' keeps returning the same already-shown items and never reaches the tail of the result set. It is gated by isLoadingMoreSearch + scroll so it is not a hard infinite loop, but pagination effectively dead-ends.
  - _Fix:_ Track the raw server offset separately (advance it by the page's returned item count, not by the deduped accumulated count) so progress is guaranteed even when dedup removes items, and stop when a page returns zero items.
- **L3676** [concurrency] runInstantSearch checks Task.isCancelled at line 3673 but not again inside the MainActor.run hop, so a stale in-flight task can overwrite instantSearchResults with older results if a newer keystroke cancels-and-replaces searchTask in the window between the check and the main-thread write.
  - _Why:_ searchTask?.cancel() (line 3639) cancels the previous task, but a task that already passed its line-3673 isCancelled check will still execute MainActor.run and clobber instantSearchResults set by a newer task. The 250ms debounce makes this rare, but last-writer-wins is not guaranteed, so a fast typist can briefly see results for a stale query.
  - _Fix:_ Re-check Task.isCancelled inside the MainActor.run closure before assigning, or carry a monotonically increasing request token (like scopedSearchFocusToken) and only commit if the token still matches the latest.
- **L3846** [gap-stub] Full-search Genres scope is a page-local best-effort derivation, not a real genre search; it is user-visible because supportsGenreActions is true.
  - _Why:_ The 'Genres' tab in full search shows only the genres that happen to appear on albums/artists already paged in for the text query — not a search of the server's 254 genres. Results are partial and grow non-deterministically as more pages load, which reads as incomplete to the user.
  - _Fix:_ Back the Genres scope with a real genre query (filter the server's genre list by the search term) instead of deriving from incidental album/artist genre tags, or scope the Genres tab's expectations in the UI.
- **L3990** [bug] play(tracks:startIndex:) sets the core queue before validating startIndex is in bounds, so an out-of-range startIndex leaves the core queue set but no audio playing.
  - _Why:_ Latent inconsistency: a bad index produces a populated core queue with the AudioEngine idle and no error surfaced. Currently unreachable because every caller in this file passes startIndex: 0 (or a known-valid index), so it's a robustness gap rather than an active bug.
  - _Fix:_ Validate startIndex (and non-negativity) before calling core.setQueue: `guard tracks.indices.contains(startIndex), let first = tracks[safe: startIndex] else { errorMessage = ...; return }`, then set the queue.
- **L4039** [concurrency] self.status = core.status() is a synchronous core FFI taken on the @MainActor after detached queue mutations (also at 4058 addToQueue, 4496 playNextArtist).
  - _Why:_ Per the repo's gap pattern #2, every sync core call on the MainActor serializes through the Inner mutex on the main thread. These are one-shot user actions so beachball risk is low, but it is inconsistent with the codebase's own convention of marshalling FFI results back from Task.detached and could contend with a concurrent detached call still holding the mutex.
  - _Fix:_ Marshal the status read off-main like the other call sites: `let s = await Task.detached { [core] in core.status() }.value; self.status = s` — or fold the status read into the same detached block that performs the insert.
- **L4216** [gap-stub] enqueueDownload(album:) is a no-op stub that only logs; same shape at enqueueDownload(playlist:) (line ~4637).
  - _Why:_ It matches the repo's documented 'Log.app.notice ... not yet wired' stub anti-pattern. It is, however, currently unreachable: all call sites are gated behind `if model.supportsDownloads` (AlbumContextMenu.swift:73, AlbumDetailView.swift:267) and Capabilities.swift:20 hard-codes `supportsDownloads { false }`. Offline downloads is tracked as OPEN feature #819 (kind:feat, effort:XL).
  - _Fix:_ Intentional gated deferral — acceptable as-is. When #819 lands, wire the body and flip supportsDownloads. No action needed now beyond awareness that flipping the capability flag would expose a no-op.
- **L4598** [dead-code] The `try?` wrapping core.playNext/core.addToQueue is redundant: both bindings are non-throwing (generated as `func playNext(tracks:) -> UInt32`, no throws). The detached closure performs no throwing work, so the `try?` swallows nothing and the compiler would normally warn 'no calls to throwing functions occur within try'.
  - _Why:_ Confirmed in lyrebird_core.swift: `func playNext(tracks: [Track]) -> UInt32` and `func addToQueue(tracks: [Track]) -> UInt32` are not throwing. The `try?` is dead syntax (also at lines 4616, 5101, 5118, and the album variants at 4036/4055). Harmless but misleading — implies error handling that doesn't exist, and the UInt32 return (count) is discarded.
  - _Fix:_ Drop the `try?` (just `_ = await Task.detached { ... }.value`). If the returned UInt32 count is meaningful, use it; otherwise the closure could simply not be wrapped in a Task at all since the call is cheap and non-blocking-ish (still a sync FFI, so detaching is fine).
- **L4652** [dead-code] requestDelete(playlist:) is a pure pass-through to confirmDelete(playlist:), which only assigns playlistPendingDelete. Two public entry points (requestDelete, confirmDelete) for the same one-line assignment add indirection with no behavioral difference.
  - _Why:_ Redundant indirection increases the API surface and the chance of callers diverging on which to use. Not a bug, just maintenance noise.
  - _Fix:_ Collapse to a single function (keep confirmDelete, drop requestDelete or vice-versa) unless one is a documented external contract.
- **L5259** [other] copyShareLink gives no user feedback, and webURL does not percent-encode the track id
  - _Why:_ copyShareLink silently writes to the pasteboard with no confirmation toast/HUD, so the user cannot tell whether the copy succeeded (and on the guard-fail path of an empty serverURL it does nothing at all, also silently). Separately, track.id is interpolated raw into the URL string with no addingPercentEncoding; Jellyfin ids are GUID-shaped today so it works, but any id containing a reserved character would corrupt the link or make URL(string:) return nil.
  - _Fix:_ Surface a brief confirmation (or set errorMessage on the empty-serverURL path), and build the URL via URLComponents/percent-encoding rather than raw string interpolation of track.id.
- **L5295** [concurrency] resolvedGenreId can fire the genre fetch twice when two genre actions run concurrently
  - _Why:_ browseGenre/startGenreRadio/shuffleGenre each wrap their call in `Task { @MainActor in await resolvedGenreId(...) }`. Although MainActor-isolated, the `await` on the detached fetch suspends BEFORE _genresLoaded is set, so two near-simultaneous genre actions (tap + context-menu, or two pinned-station taps) both observe !_genresLoaded and both launch the core.genres FFI + network round-trip. It self-corrects (the second just overwrites the dictionary) but wastes a redundant FFI/network call.
  - _Fix:_ Guard with an in-flight Task handle: store the loader Task and await the same instance if a load is already running (single-flight), or set a loading flag before the first await.
- **L5407** [performance] probeAvailableMoods' task-group parallelism is defeated and serializes 5 sync core.authHeader() FFI calls on the MainActor
  - _Why:_ moodHasTracks and buildItemsQuery are MainActor-isolated (members of the @MainActor class, not nonisolated), so each child task immediately hops to the MainActor to run them. The five probes therefore cannot run their synchronous portions in parallel, and each buildItemsQuery takes the Rust Inner mutex via core.authHeader() on the main thread (CLAUDE.md gap #2). Only the URLSession await actually overlaps. Net effect: five serial main-thread FFI mutex acquisitions on startup probe.
  - _Fix:_ Make buildItemsQuery (or at least the authHeader fetch) nonisolated / hoist authHeader out once before the loop, and ensure the probe bodies run off the MainActor so the task group genuinely parallelizes.
- **L5419** [gap-stub] probeAvailableMoods never shrinks availableMoods — a genuinely-empty probe result leaves stale mood chips visible
  - _Why:_ If every moodHasTracks probe returns false (library no longer has any tagged tracks, or all five probes hit transient failures that map to false in moodHasTracks' catch), `present` is empty and the function returns without touching availableMoods, so previously-shown mood radio entries persist even though tapping them now yields the empty-state error. The early return conflates 'all transient failures' with 'legitimately none', and there is no path that ever clears availableMoods back to [].
  - _Fix:_ Distinguish failure from emptiness (e.g. only early-return if probes errored, otherwise assign the filtered result even when empty), or always assign `availableMoods = Mood.all.filter { present.contains($0) }` and accept brief flicker on transient failure.
- **L5717** [bug] togglePlayPause restarts playback while a track is already .loading, risking a double load/glitch
  - _Why:_ When state is .loading the track is already being loaded by AudioEngine; a play/pause keypress in that window calls playCurrent again, which kicks off a second `audio.play(track:)` for the same item. Depending on AudioEngine this can cancel/restart the in-flight load or cause an audible glitch. .loading does not belong in the same branch as .ended/.stopped/.idle.
  - _Fix:_ Drop .loading from this case (treat an in-flight load as a no-op for toggle), or map .loading to pause()/cancel rather than a fresh playCurrent.
- **L5855** [error-handling] scrobbleNowPlaying error is swallowed with try?
  - _Why:_ Lower impact than submitListen (a missed 'now playing' update is cosmetic on the scrobble service), but it is still a swallowed FFI error: repeated failures here are the canary for a revoked/expired scrobble token, yet nothing is logged or surfaced, so scrobbleConnected stays true while updates silently no-op.
  - _Fix:_ Replace try? with a do/catch that logs via Log.net.error; optionally feed auth failures into the same re-check used for submitListen.
- **L6082** [concurrency] Per track-change, two fire-and-forget unstructured Tasks are spawned for details/lyrics without cancelling prior in-flight fetches
  - _Why:_ On rapid track changes (e.g. fast skipping), multiple overlapping fetchCurrentTrackDetails/fetchCurrentTrackLyrics tasks run concurrently. They are individually safe (each re-checks status.currentTrack?.id == id after the await before assigning), so this is not a correctness bug, but stale tasks still issue redundant core.fetchItem/core.lyrics network calls that are then discarded. A stored, cancellable task handle (like trackAnnounceTask) would avoid the wasted requests.
  - _Fix:_ Store the two Tasks in cancellable properties and cancel the prior task before launching a new one on track change, or debounce the fetch.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/AirPlayRoutePicker.swift`
- **L38** [performance] updateNSView unconditionally re-applies the full color plan (4 setRoutePickerButtonColor calls + a bordered toggle) on every SwiftUI update even when the ButtonColorPlan is unchanged.
  - _Why:_ AVRoutePickerView lives in the now-playing/transport chrome that re-renders on frequent state changes (playback status, hover). Each update rebuilds 4 NSColors and pushes them into AppKit even when restingTint/activeTint didn't change. Cheap individually but needless churn on a hot view; the Equatable conformance signals the intent to diff was there.
  - _Fix:_ Cache the last-applied ButtonColorPlan in the Coordinator (or via context.coordinator) and early-return when `colorPlan == previous`, only re-applying on actual change.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/AlbumContextMenu.swift`
- **L74** [gap-stub] The "Download" menu item is wired to a not-yet-implemented stub; it only stays hidden because the capability flag is hard-coded false.
  - _Why:_ Not currently user-facing (gate is false), but the moment supportsDownloads is flipped to true the menu offers a Download action that silently does nothing but log. Flagging per CLAUDE.md gap #1 (Log.app.notice 'not yet wired' = live bug, not a TODO) and the deferred-work note for #819-class download stubs.
  - _Fix:_ Keep the flag false until enqueueDownload(album:) actually enqueues a download; do not enable supportsDownloads without implementing the FFI. Tracked under #819 / downloads #70/#222.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/ArtistCard.swift`
- **L111** [accessibility] The card combines all children into one accessibility element while still containing a separate interactive "Play all" Button, which can hide the inner button's action from VoiceOver.
  - _Why:_ `children: .combine` merges descendants into the parent element, so the inner play button's distinct action/label is folded into the card and may not be independently activatable by VoiceOver; combined with opacity-0 (still hit-testable) the play affordance is effectively inaccessible. The card itself is fine, but the secondary play action is lost for assistive tech.
  - _Fix:_ Either expose the play action on the parent via `.accessibilityAction(named: "Play all") { model.playAll(artist: artist) }`, or don't combine and let the inner button remain its own element. Hide the inner button from a11y when opacity is 0 if it's meant to be hover-only.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/Artwork.swift`
- **L93** [dead-code] The `state.error != nil` branch and the trailing `else` branch are identical, making the explicit error branch dead.
  - _Why:_ Both the error case and the loading/default case render `placeholder`, so the `else if state.error != nil` test does nothing — it neither distinguishes a failed load (e.g. to show a distinct broken/retry affordance) nor changes output. It is dead branching that reads as if error handling exists when it does not.
  - _Fix:_ Either collapse to a single `else { placeholder }`, or make the error branch render a distinct state (e.g. a retry/broken-image affordance) so the branch earns its existence.
- **L111** [accessibility] `overlayLabel` text drawn on the placeholder is hidden from VoiceOver whenever `decorative` is true (the default).
  - _Why:_ When a caller supplies `overlayLabel` (meaningful text rendered over the artwork placeholder) but leaves `decorative` at its default `true`, the whole `Artwork` — including that text — is `accessibilityHidden`. The label becomes invisible to VoiceOver even though it conveys real information. The two flags are independent, so it is easy to set `overlayLabel` without remembering to also set `decorative: false`.
  - _Fix:_ When `overlayLabel != nil`, do not unconditionally hide the view: either force `decorative` effectively false in that case, or expose the overlay text via `.accessibilityLabel(overlayLabel)` on a non-hidden element so the information reaches assistive tech.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/Breadcrumbs.swift`
- **L20** [consistency] `ForEach` keys breadcrumb rows by array index (`id: \.self` over `segments.indices`).
  - _Why:_ Indexing as identity means SwiftUI cannot diff rows by content when the path changes (e.g. navigating sibling-to-sibling keeps the same indices), so view identity/animations track position rather than the actual segment. Breadcrumbs are short and mostly static so this is low-impact, but it is the documented index-as-id anti-pattern and can produce mismatched transitions if breadcrumb segments ever animate on change.
  - _Fix:_ Key by a stable per-segment identifier. If segments can repeat, build a small identifiable model (`(index, name)` wrapped in an Identifiable struct) rather than relying on `\.self` over indices.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/CommandPalette.swift`
- **L238** [consistency] ForEach is keyed by \.offset (array index) even though Row conforms to Hashable, so SwiftUI diffs rows by position rather than identity when the result set changes.
  - _Why:_ Position-keyed identity means when search results change, a row at a given index is treated as the "same" view as the previously different content at that index. This can cause incorrect cell reuse/animation and momentary mismatch of onHover/selection binding to stale content during the swap. The Hashable conformance exists specifically to enable stable identity but is unused here.
  - _Fix:_ This is a deliberate tradeoff because proxy.scrollTo needs an Int id matching the ForEach id. If keeping index ids, it is acceptable; otherwise key the ForEach by \.element (Row) and maintain a separate index<->Row map for scrollTo, or scroll to the Row identity directly.
- **L326** [performance] visibleRows is a computed property accessed from ~10 call sites (body, onChange(of: visibleRows.count), resultsScroll, moveSelection, activate, commitSelection); each evaluation calls model.paletteActions, which reallocates ~13 PaletteAction structs and closures every time.
  - _Why:_ Every render pass and every onChange recomputes visibleRows, and each recompute rebuilds the entire actions roster (closures included) and (for the empty-query path) constructs two Sets in orderedActionRows(). The row counts are small (≤13 actions + ≤18 library rows), so this is not a beachball, but it is wasteful churn on the MainActor on every keystroke and arrow press, and executePaletteAction(id:) (AppModel.swift line 972) rebuilds the whole roster again just to look up one action by id.
  - _Fix:_ Memoize the rows into @State updated only when its inputs (libraryResults, category, query, pinned/recent ids) change, or cache model.paletteActions. At minimum compute visibleRows once per body and pass it down rather than re-reading the computed property at multiple sites.
- **L426** [bug] selectedIndex is not reset to the top when a query is refined; it is only reset on an empty query (line 123). After new results arrive it is merely clamped to the last valid index, which can leave the highlight on an unexpected row.
  - _Why:_ If the user has arrow-navigated to e.g. index 5, then types another character and the new result set has 3 rows, the selection clamps to index 2 (the last row) rather than the most-relevant top match. Pressing Enter would then activate an arbitrary trailing row instead of the best match the user expects after refining the search.
  - _Fix:_ Reset selectedIndex = 0 whenever the effective query changes (e.g. in the query onChange before launching the debounce, and after libraryResults is assigned), so a refined search always pre-selects the top result.
- **L462** [dead-code] For the .action case, commitSelection calls executePaletteAction(id:) (which already sets isCommandPaletteOpen = false) and then immediately calls close() again, a redundant second dismiss.
  - _Why:_ Harmless (setting a Bool false twice), but it duplicates the dismiss responsibility across two layers and is a latent foot-gun: if executePaletteAction's run() closure ever decides to keep the palette open (or open a different surface), the unconditional close() here would override that intent. The other branches (.artist/.album/.track) own the close() themselves, so the responsibility is inconsistent.
  - _Fix:_ Pick one owner of the dismiss. Either let executePaletteAction own it and drop the close() in this branch, or have executePaletteAction not dismiss and let commitSelection own all four branches uniformly.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/DecadeBrowseRow.swift`
- **L65** [gap-stub] The decade browser hard-codes its range to 1960-2020 (seven fixed tiles). Albums released before 1960 or in the current/2020s+ decade are not reachable through this UI, and the row never reflects the actual year span of the user's library.
  - _Why:_ music.skalthoff.com holds ~20060 albums; classical/jazz/reissues commonly carry pre-1960 dates and new releases land in the 2020s. Those years cannot be browsed via the decade shelf, and as time passes the top of the range becomes increasingly stale (no 2030s tile). It is a quiet feature gap rather than a crash.
  - _Fix:_ Derive the decade list from the library's min/max release year (or extend the stride to the current decade, e.g. through the decade containing the current year, and add an open-ended pre-1960 "Earlier" bucket).

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/HomeAlbumTile.swift`
- **L48** [consistency] Single-click play is delayed by double-tap detection because count:1 and count:2 tap gestures share the same view
  - _Why:_ When both a count:1 and a count:2 tap gesture are attached to the same view, SwiftUI must wait out the system double-click interval before it can commit the single tap, so every play-on-click incurs that latency. TrackRow.swift (line 157) deliberately uses only a single count:1 gesture for exactly this reason. This is a known interaction wart rather than a correctness bug (the documented hint matches the behavior), but it makes the primary action feel sluggish compared to other tappable rows in the app.
  - _Fix:_ Accept the latency tradeoff as a product decision, or replace the dual tap gestures with a single primary gesture plus a separate affordance for the secondary action (e.g. the existing context menu / a dedicated open button), mirroring TrackRow which avoids the double-tap penalty.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/HomeQuickTile.swift`
- **L52** [bug] The nested Play button is hidden with `opacity(isHovering ? 1 : 0)` but never has hit-testing disabled. `opacity(0)` keeps a view hittable, so an invisible 36x36 button occupies the trailing area of every non-hovered tile and intercepts clicks that the user expects to fall through to the tile's `action`. For pointer input hover precedes the click (so the button is usually visible by click time), but trackpad taps / rapid clicks before the 0.2s hover animation, or focus-driven activation, can land on the hidden button and fire `onPlay` instead of `action`.
  - _Why:_ Clicking the right edge of a tile can navigate-vs-play unpredictably. Same omission exists in ArtistCard.swift:65 and ArtistRadioTile.swift:43, so it is a codebase-wide convention, but it remains technically incorrect hit-testing.
  - _Fix:_ Gate interactivity with visibility: add `.allowsHitTesting(isHovering)` to the nested Play button so it cannot receive clicks while hidden.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/InstantMixSheet.swift`
- **L451** [consistency] A seed row cannot be deselected by tapping it again; select() only assigns, never toggles.
  - _Why:_ Standard single-select pickers usually let you tap the highlighted row to deselect. Here the only way to get back to a no-seed state is to empty the search field (which resets selectedSeed via queryChanged's empty branch). Minor friction, not a correctness bug.
  - _Fix:_ Make select() a toggle: `selectedSeed = (selectedSeed?.id == item.id) ? nil : item`.
- **L479** [consistency] isSearching is set true for the full debounce window before any search actually runs, so the spinner appears even when no network/FFI work is in flight yet.
  - _Why:_ Cosmetic: on every keystroke the spinner flickers on immediately even though the actual search is still 250ms away and may be cancelled by the next keystroke. Not harmful, just slightly misleading feedback. Acceptable but worth noting.
  - _Fix:_ Set `isSearching = true` after the debounce sleep (just before `await self.search(trimmed)`), or leave as-is if the immediate-feedback flicker is desired.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/LibraryListRow.swift`
- **L49** [accessibility] The hover-only inline Play button has no accessibility label and is collapsed by the parent's accessibilityElement(children: .combine), so there is no VoiceOver-reachable per-row Play action (only Open detail).
  - _Why:_ The play affordance appears only on pointer hover and carries no accessibilityLabel; .combine flattens it into the row element, which exposes only the open-detail action and hint. Assistive-technology and keyboard users get no direct 'Play' on the row. (Play is still reachable via the context menu, which mitigates severity.)
  - _Fix:_ Either expose a row-level play action via .accessibilityAction(named: "Play") { playPrimary() } on the combined element, or give the inline button .accessibilityLabel("Play") and an .accessibilityActions block so VoiceOver users can trigger playback without hover.
- **L226** [bug] formattedDuration rounds any sub-minute non-zero playlist runtime up to '1 min', overstating very short playlists.
  - _Why:_ A playlist whose total runtime is, e.g., 20 seconds (runtimeTicks=200_000_000) computes minutes=0 and renders '1 min'. It is a minor display inaccuracy; harmless but slightly misleading for tiny playlists.
  - _Fix:_ For sub-minute totals show seconds (e.g. '< 1 min' or 'Ns') instead of forcing 1, e.g. if totalSeconds < 60 return "< 1 min".

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/LyricsView.swift`
- **L126** [validation] parseTimestamp rejects an entire timestamp when the fractional part is present but empty or non-numeric (e.g. '[00:12.]'), silently demoting a timed line to untimed.
  - _Why:_ '[00:12.]' splits into seconds='12', frac='' ; Int('') is nil so the whole stamp is rejected, extractTimestamps returns ([], line), and the line is shown as untimed text (losing sync) rather than parsed as 12.0s. Malformed-but-recoverable timestamps from real-world LRC files therefore drop out of the synced view. Low frequency, but it degrades silently.
  - _Fix:_ Treat an empty/zero-length fractional as 0 (only fail on a non-numeric, non-empty fraction): if frac.isEmpty { fractional = 0 } else { guard let num = Int(frac) else { return nil }; ... }.
- **L176** [bug] activeId @State is not reset when the lines array changes on track change, leaving a stale highlighted/scrolled line for up to one poll interval.
  - _Why:_ When the surrounding panel swaps in a new track's lyrics (model.currentLyrics changes), LyricsView keeps the same identity, so activeId retains the previous track's line id. .onAppear does not re-run on a value change, so the highlight/auto-scroll points at a stale line until the 0.2s timer's next tick recomputes it. With the timer at 5Hz the window is small (~200ms), but if the timer cadence is lowered per the fix above, the stale window grows proportionally and becomes noticeable.
