  - _Fix:_ Add .onChange(of: lines) { _, _ in updateActiveLine() } (or key the view with .id(trackId) from the caller so state resets), so the active line is recomputed immediately when the lyrics change rather than waiting for the next poll.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/MiniPlayerView.swift`
- **L88** [performance] onContinuousHover .active spawns and cancels a Task on every mouse-move sample while the cursor is inside the mini player.
  - _Why:_ Continuous-hover delivers many .active events per second during pointer movement; allocating/cancelling a Task per event is needless churn on the MainActor. It's not catastrophic but is avoidable per-event work in a hover-hot path (gap pattern #2 spirit).
  - _Fix:_ Debounce: only re-arm the idle timer when it isn't already pending, or reset an existing DispatchSourceTimer/deadline instead of tearing down and recreating a Task on every .active sample. Alternatively store a target deadline and have one long-lived task poll it.
- **L521** [accessibility] Volume accessibilityValue is a hard-coded English string ('… percent') in an otherwise-localized view.
  - _Why:_ VoiceOver users in non-English locales hear an untranslated 'percent'. It is consistent with PlayerBar.swift:357 (same raw string), so this is a codebase-wide gap rather than a one-off, but it is still an unlocalized a11y string.
  - _Fix:_ Use a localized/format-style value, e.g. `Text(Double(volume), format: .percent.precision(.fractionLength(0)))` or a localized format key, and apply the same fix at PlayerBar.swift:357 for consistency.
- **L678** [bug] window.performDrag(with:) is invoked with a .leftMouseDragged event rather than the originating mouseDown event.
  - _Why:_ NSWindow.performDrag(with:) is documented to be called with the mouse-down event so it can compute the grab offset from the initial click. Passing a drag event captured after the pointer has already moved past the 4pt threshold can make the window snap by that initial offset at drag start. Minor visual jump on the first drag frame.
  - _Fix:_ Capture the initial mouseDown event and pass it: `window.performDrag(with: event)` (the original), not `next`, when the threshold is exceeded.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/NoSearchResultsState.swift`
- **L19** [accessibility] User-facing strings are hard-coded English (not localized), so the body text and accessibility label are untranslated.
  - _Why:_ In a localized build these render English only. (Lower priority because the view is dead code — see the dead-code finding — but if it is revived instead of deleted, the strings need localizing.)
  - _Fix:_ If the view is kept/revived, route the copy through LocalizedStringKey / String Catalog like the mini player keys; otherwise delete the file.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/NowPlayingBackdrop.swift`
- **L33** [dead-code] `seed` property is declared and passed by the caller but never read in the view body.
  - _Why:_ NowPlayingView.swift:77 passes `seed: model.status.currentTrack?.name ?? ""`, but `body` (lines 59-99) renders only `url`-driven artwork and a `Color.clear` placeholder (line 84). The placeholder no longer derives any gradient/hash from `seed`, so the stored value is computed and threaded through for nothing. Misleading API surface: a future maintainer may assume the backdrop falls back to a seeded placeholder when artwork is missing, but it just goes clear.
  - _Fix:_ Remove the `seed` property (and the corresponding argument at NowPlayingView.swift:77), or actually use it to drive a deterministic placeholder gradient in the `else { Color.clear }` branch on line 84 if a seeded fallback was the intent.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/NowPlayingCredits.swift`
- **L155** [dead-code] `Person.id` is declared and populated but never consumed by the credits-rendering path.
  - _Why:_ `AppModel.parsePeople` (AppModel.swift:5967) and the album-detail parser (AppModel.swift:4320) both populate `id`, and `Credit.rows` is the only consumer in this file, yet it never reads `id`. The field is dead for the credits feature. If the intent was tappable credit names (navigate to the person/artist), that path is unbuilt — `CreditRow` (lines 56-86) renders plain `Text`, no link/button.
  - _Fix:_ Either drop `id` from `Person` if no consumer needs it, or wire `CreditRow` to make credited names tappable (navigate by `Person.id`) so the populated id is actually used. Low priority since `Person` is a shared model and removing the field touches two parsers.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/PinnedStationTile.swift`
- **L259** [validation] `PinnedStationsStore.save`/`load` do not enforce the 6-item cap that the only writer applies, leaving the invariant the caller's responsibility.
  - _Why:_ The HomeView UI and AppModel.pinGenreToHome (AppModel.swift:5558 — `if stations.count > 6 { stations = Array(stations.prefix(6)) }`) assume at most 6 pinned stations, but the store persists/loads whatever it's handed. Today the single caller caps before saving, so it's not an active bug; it is a latent fragility — any future caller of `save` (or stale on-disk data from a prior build) can exceed the cap and the horizontal pinned row will render more tiles than the design budgets for.
  - _Fix:_ Centralize the cap in the store, e.g. `save(Array(stations.prefix(6)))` and `return Array(decoded.prefix(6))` in `load()`, so the 6-item invariant holds regardless of caller. Then the ad-hoc cap in pinGenreToHome becomes redundant rather than load-bearing.
- **L260** [error-handling] `save` silently no-ops if JSON encoding fails, giving no signal that a pin was dropped.
  - _Why:_ `PinnedStation` is a simple Codable of String/enum, so encoding realistically won't fail — but if it ever did (e.g. a future non-encodable field added), the user's pin action would appear to succeed (HomeView re-reads @AppStorage and shows the old list) while nothing was persisted, with zero diagnostics. Mirrors the swallowed-error gap pattern (#5 in CLAUDE.md) at low stakes.
  - _Fix:_ Log the encode failure (`Log.app.error(...)`) instead of swallowing it, so a regression surfaces in Console rather than silently losing pins.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/PlayerBar.swift`
- **L142** [consistency] Subtitle renders a dangling ' · ' separator when albumName is nil/empty.
  - _Why:_ When a track has no album (albumName == nil) the bar shows e.g. "Some Artist · " with a trailing middot and space, which looks broken. The accessibility label on line 152 only reads name + artist, so visual and a11y output also diverge for these tracks.
  - _Fix:_ Build the string conditionally: artistName + (albumName.flatMap { $0.isEmpty ? nil : " · \($0)" } ?? "").
- **L420** [bug] format(_:) does not guard against NaN/infinite input the way its sibling voiceOverTime(_:) does; Int(NaN) / Int(.infinity) traps at runtime.
  - _Why:_ format is called with model.status.durationSeconds (line 286) and displayPosition (line 242). Converting a non-finite Double to Int via Int(seconds) is a runtime trap in Swift. The duration value flows from server metadata / AVPlayer; the audio engine guards position with isFinite (AudioEngine.swift:281,712) so today's path is safe, but durationSeconds has no equivalent guard and an unusual/live duration would crash the player bar. The asymmetry with the already-defensive voiceOverTime is the tell.
  - _Fix:_ Mirror voiceOverTime's guard: let safe = seconds.isFinite ? max(0, seconds) : 0; let total = Int(safe.rounded()) before dividing.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/PlaylistCard.swift`
- **L34** [error-handling] Tapping Play on a playlist whose track load yields nothing gives no user feedback.
  - _Why:_ model.play(playlist:) loads tracks then `guard !tracks.isEmpty else { return }`. For a genuinely empty playlist the Play button does nothing with no indication. (Network failures are partially covered because loadPlaylistTracks sets errorMessage, but the empty-playlist case is silent.)
  - _Fix:_ In AppModel.play(playlist:)/shuffle(playlist:), surface an errorMessage (e.g. "This playlist has no tracks.") when tracks.isEmpty, matching exportPlaylist's empty-guard messaging.
- **L44** [bug] The Play overlay button is hidden with opacity 0 (not allowsHitTesting(false)), so while not hovering it still occupies its 40x40 hit region inside the outer navigation Button, creating ambiguous nested-button hit-testing.
  - _Why:_ opacity(0) does not disable hit testing in SwiftUI; an invisible button can still intercept taps in its frame. A click in the bottom-trailing corner of a non-hovered card could be routed to the hidden Play button (start playback) instead of the outer Open button. Nesting a Button inside another Button's label is also discouraged by Apple. The same shape exists in ArtistCard/HomeAlbumTile, so it is the house pattern, but it remains a latent hit-routing ambiguity.
  - _Fix:_ Gate the overlay with .allowsHitTesting(isHovering) so it cannot capture taps while hidden, or restructure to a single Button with a separate hover-revealed play affordance using a tap gesture rather than a nested Button.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/PlaylistReorderHandle.swift`
- **L112** [dead-code] The custom drag UTI org.lyrebird.playlist-track is never declared or produced, so the onDrop type list and the public constant are dead.
  - _Why:_ There is no UTExportedTypeDeclarations entry anywhere in the repo for org.lyrebird.playlist-track, so UTType("org.lyrebird.playlist-track") returns nil and the `?? .plainText` collapses the list to [.plainText, .plainText] (a redundant duplicate). The onDrag at line 107 produces an NSString (public.text), and both validateDrop (line 135) and performDrop (line 152) only ever look for .plainText. The custom UTI is referenced nowhere else and never registered, so the constant and the second element of the type list are dead and misleading.
  - _Fix:_ Either remove lyrebirdPlaylistTrackDragUTI and the second UTType entry entirely (the flow only uses plain text), or properly register the exported UTI in Info.plist and have onDrag register a data representation for it so reorder drags are distinguishable from arbitrary text drops.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/QueueInspector.swift`
- **L64** [resource-leak] The pending `jumpToastDismissWork` `DispatchWorkItem` is not cancelled in `onDisappear`. `onDisappear` (line 146) only removes the drag monitors; if the user triggers the jump toast (3s auto-dismiss timer armed in `showJumpToastMessage`) and then closes the inspector, the scheduled work item still fires ~3s later and mutates `@State showJumpToast` on a torn-down view.
  - _Why:_ It's a dangling one-shot timer holding a closure capture past view lifetime. Benign today (SwiftUI tolerates state writes on disappeared views and the item self-cancels after firing), but `onDisappear` conspicuously cleans up the other timer-like resources (the event monitors) and omitting this one is an inconsistency that could bite if the closure grows side effects.
  - _Fix:_ In `onDisappear`, also call `jumpToastDismissWork?.cancel(); jumpToastDismissWork = nil` (or fold both teardown steps into one cleanup helper) so no scheduled work outlives the view.
- **L146** [resource-leak] onDisappear removes the drag monitors but does not cancel the pending jump-toast dismiss DispatchWorkItem, so a scheduled dismissJumpToast() can fire after the view is gone.
  - _Why:_ If the inspector is dismissed within 3s of a double-tap, the queued work item still runs and mutates @State after disappearance. It is harmless for value-type State today, but it is an avoidable dangling scheduled closure and inconsistent with the explicit cancel done in showJumpToastMessage/dismissJumpToast.
  - _Fix:_ Add `jumpToastDismissWork?.cancel(); jumpToastDismissWork = nil` to the onDisappear handler alongside removeDragCancelMonitors().
- **L406** [accessibility] The now-playing progress bar (named 'scrubber') exposes no accessibility value and is non-interactive; VoiceOver users get only two bare time strings with no 'position of duration' context, and the name implies a seek control that doesn't exist.
  - _Why:_ The element looks like a scrubber but cannot seek, and assistive tech reads the start/end times as disconnected static text rather than a progress indicator, giving no sense of how far through the track playback is.
  - _Fix:_ Either make it an actual ProgressView/Slider with .accessibilityValue (e.g. percentage or 'm:ss of m:ss'), or at minimum combine the bar+labels into one accessibility element with a descriptive value; rename to reflect read-only if seeking isn't intended.
- **L766** [bug] The drop delegate's above/below split point is a hardcoded 22pt midline, implicitly coupled to the 44pt row-height assumption in boundedListHeight; if row metrics change the insert position will land on the wrong side.
  - _Why:_ The magic 22 must stay exactly half of the (also magic) 44; a future tweak to row padding/artwork size silently desyncs the drop indicator and the chosen insertion index, causing items to drop one slot off from where the indicator shows.
  - _Fix:_ Derive the midline from the actual drop region height (e.g. via the DropInfo/GeometryReader bounds) or from a single shared rowHeight constant rather than a duplicated literal.
- **L766** [bug] `QueueRowDropDelegate.dropUpdated` hardcodes the above/below split point as `midline: CGFloat = 22`, assuming each row is exactly 44pt tall. Actual row height is driven by content (Artwork 32pt + `.padding(.vertical, 6)`), not the 44pt constant used only by `boundedListHeight`. If the row's intrinsic height drifts (font scaling, Dynamic Type, layout changes) the drop indicator and insertion point land on the wrong half of the row.
  - _Why:_ A magic constant decoupled from the real row geometry makes the reorder drop target subtly wrong under any height change, producing off-by-one inserts that are hard to diagnose.
  - _Fix:_ Derive the midline from the actual row bounds rather than a literal — e.g. pass the measured row height (GeometryReader / PreferenceKey) into the delegate, or compute the split from `info`'s available rect, so the above/below decision tracks the real cell height.
- **L822** [consistency] The Save sheet's 'Creates a new playlist with N tracks' count can overstate the real result because it sums raw counts while the save routine dedupes track IDs.
  - _Why:_ When the now-playing track also appears in Up Next, or the same track is queued twice, the dialog promises more tracks than are actually saved, a small but real expectation mismatch.
  - _Fix:_ Compute the displayed count using the same dedupe-by-id logic the save routine uses (or expose a shared helper) so the sheet's number matches what gets created.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/RadioStationRows.swift`
- **L224** [consistency] `RadioStationTile`'s `hue` / `seedColor` / `gradient` (FNV-1a hash → HSB color + the exact same two-stop gradient) are copy-pasted verbatim from at least four other components: GenresToExploreSection.swift (line 100-119), DecadeBrowseRow.swift (line 121-130), and BrowseByGenreSection.swift (line 106-126). All use identical magic constants (2_166_136_261 / 16_777_619) and identical saturation/brightness values.
  - _Why:_ Five divergent copies of the same seed-to-color algorithm means any palette tweak (e.g. the colour-blind-safe theme work in commit 78d2793) must be hand-applied in five places, and they will inevitably drift, producing inconsistent tile colours across the app.
  - _Fix:_ Extract a single shared helper (e.g. `SeedColor.hue(_:)` / `SeedColor.gradient(for:)` in Theme or a small util) and have RadioStationTile, GenresToExploreSection, DecadeBrowseRow, and BrowseByGenreSection all call it.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/ScopedSearchBar.swift`
- **L30** [accessibility] The filter TextField has no accessibilityLabel; it relies solely on the placeholder. When the field already contains text, VoiceOver has no stable label for the control.
  - _Why:_ On macOS, a plain TextField's placeholder is not a reliable accessibility label once the user has typed; VoiceOver users may hear only the typed value with no indication of the field's purpose (filter). The adjacent magnifyingglass image is decorative and unlabeled, so there is no other cue.
  - _Fix:_ Add `.accessibilityLabel(placeholder)` (or a dedicated label string) to the TextField so the control's purpose is announced regardless of content.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/Sidebar.swift`
- **L143** [consistency] Footer server name placeholder and the "albums" suffix are hard-coded literals, not localized.
  - _Why:_ Consistent with the broader localization gap: "—" as a fallback is fine, but the " albums" suffix and "Connected" word will not translate while sibling rows (`sidebar.stats.albums`, etc.) use LocalizedStringKey. Minor, but it is mixed-language output in the always-visible footer.
  - _Fix:_ Localize the footer status line (count + unit + connection word) via String(localized:) with a pluralized albums string; keep the em-dash fallback.
- **L343** [bug] Hover-exit logic for playlist rows is convoluted and can leave a stale hovered id when moving directly between rows.
  - _Why:_ On exit (`hovering == false`) it only clears `hoveredPlaylistId` if it currently equals this row's id; otherwise it leaves it untouched. If two rows' hover callbacks fire out of order (enter B before exit A — common with fast pointer movement), A's exit sees `hoveredPlaylistId == B.id` and preserves B, which is correct, but the inverse ordering (exit A after enter B already wrote B, then a spurious exit B) can briefly clear the wrong row's highlight. The expression is harder to reason about than necessary and the highlight can flicker or stick.
  - _Fix:_ Use the simpler standard pattern: `if hovering { hoveredPlaylistId = playlist.id } else if hoveredPlaylistId == playlist.id { hoveredPlaylistId = nil }` — functionally the same but clearer; or drive hover via a single `.onContinuousHover`/per-row state to avoid cross-row interference.
- **L565** [concurrency] Focus is forced via an unstructured `DispatchQueue.main.async` from `onAppear`, with no guard against the view having disappeared.
  - _Why:_ Setting `isFocused = true` one runloop later can land after the edit row has already been torn down (e.g. user cancels immediately), making the field grab focus from whatever replaced it. It is also a fire-and-forget hop on an already-MainActor view where the idiomatic approach is a structured await. Low impact but a latent focus-stealing edge case.
  - _Fix:_ Prefer `Task { @MainActor in isFocused = true }` (cancellable with the view) or `defer`/`focusable`-driven focus; at minimum guard on `model.sidebarEditingPlaylistId` still matching before forcing focus.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/TrackListRow.swift`
- **L147** [consistency] User-facing accessibility strings and labels in this file are hardcoded English while the sibling TrackInfoSheet.swift uses LocalizedStringKey / String(localized:), leaving these strings untranslatable.
  - _Why:_ These are presented to the user (VoiceOver, tooltip) but bypass the String Catalog (tracked open i18n work #560), so they will not localize and the plural form is English-only.
  - _Fix:_ Route these through String(localized:) / LocalizedStringKey and use a proper plural rule for the play-count, consistent with TrackInfoSheet's approach.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/TrackRow.swift`
- **L113** [accessibility] The favorite Button only renders when `isFav || isHovering`, and the play-count text only when hovering, so hovering inserts/removes interactive width inside the row — a layout shift and a hover-gated control that is unreachable by keyboard-only users.
  - _Why:_ The favorite toggle for a non-favorited track is reachable only via mouse hover; a keyboard/VoiceOver user who focuses the row (the row sets `.accessibilityElement(children: .ignore)` at line 162, hiding child controls anyway) has no way to favorite. The appearing/disappearing button also shifts the duration label horizontally on hover. The duration/play-count are fine, but the favorite action being hover-only is a genuine a11y gap.
  - _Fix:_ Expose favorite as an accessibility custom action on the row (it already collapses children with `.ignore`), and/or reserve fixed width for the favorite button (render it always with opacity 0 when not hovered/favorited) to avoid the layout shift.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Components/TrackSelectionBanner.swift`
- **L91** [consistency] Escape is double-bound: the banner's xmark Button has `.keyboardShortcut(.escape)` and the host LibraryView (LibraryView.swift:168) also binds `.onKeyPress(.escape)` to clearSelection. Two handlers race for the same key.
  - _Why:_ Both ultimately clear the selection, so the user-visible result is the same, but two competing Escape handlers for the same logical action is fragile — if either path later diverges (e.g. banner gains a different Escape meaning, or LibraryView wants Escape to also close a sheet) behavior becomes order-dependent and hard to reason about.
  - _Fix:_ Own Escape in one place. Drop `.keyboardShortcut(.escape)` from the banner button (keep it as a plain Clear button) and let the host screen's `.onKeyPress(.escape)` be the single source of truth, or vice-versa.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/LyrebirdApp.swift`
- **L402** [consistency] Volume Up / Volume Down menu commands are not disabled when there is no session or no current track, unlike every other transport command in the same menu.
  - _Why:_ Every adjacent command (play/pause, next, previous, seek, stop) carries .disabled(model.status.currentTrack == nil), but the two volume commands do not. The result is minor UI inconsistency: ⌘Up/⌘Down adjust volume (and are enabled) even when nothing is playing and the rest of the menu is greyed out. Volume is arguably global, so this may be intentional, but the asymmetry is unexplained and inconsistent with the menu's own conventions.
  - _Fix:_ Either intentionally keep volume always-enabled (fine), or add .disabled to match the rest of the transport commands for consistency; decide and apply uniformly.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/NetworkMonitor.swift`
- **L59** [bug] `retry()` tears down and recreates the monitor but does not reset `isOnline`, leaving the UI on the stale value until the new monitor's first path callback arrives.
  - _Why:_ Between `retry()` returning and the fresh `NWPathMonitor` delivering its initial `pathUpdateHandler` callback, `isOnline` retains its previous value. If the user taps a Retry affordance while the banner shows offline, the offline banner can linger briefly even though monitoring restarted. Self-corrects on first callback, so impact is a transient stale state, not a persistent bug.
  - _Fix:_ Either leave as-is (acceptable, NWPathMonitor delivers an initial update promptly) or optimistically not change state and rely on the callback. If a snappier reset is desired, the first callback already handles it; no functional fix strictly required — document/lower severity accordingly.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/AboutView.swift`
- **L98** [accessibility] User-facing About strings are hardcoded English literals (not localized) despite the app shipping a `Localizable.xcstrings` catalog.
  - _Why:_ The window title (`about.window.title`) and all error keys ARE in Localizable.xcstrings, but the About body labels and their accessibility labels are raw literals. For a localized build these strings (and the VoiceOver labels) stay English regardless of locale. Low severity because much of the app's view layer is similarly un-localized (sibling PreferencesAbout.swift has the same pattern), so it's consistent debt rather than a regression.
  - _Fix:_ Wrap the literals in `String(localized:)` / use `LocalizedStringKey` and add entries to Localizable.xcstrings, consistent with the error-key and window-title localization already present.
- **L170** [bug] `#Preview` instantiates `AboutView()` without injecting an `AppModel`; the view's `@Environment(AppModel.self)` is force-resolved and will crash the SwiftUI preview.
  - _Why:_ `@Environment(AppModel.self) private var model` with no default traps when read if no AppModel is in the environment. The computed `serverHost` reads `model.serverURL`, which `body` evaluates, so the preview crashes on render. Preview-only (the real Window scene injects `.environment(model)` at LyrebirdApp.swift:122), so no shipping impact — but the preview is non-functional for the developer.
  - _Fix:_ Inject a stub in the preview: `AboutView().environment(AppModel.preview)` (or whatever the project's preview/mock AppModel factory is), matching how other previews in the codebase provide the model.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/AlbumDetailView.swift`
- **L541** [dead-code] Liner-notes content is rendered twice: an always-visible inline `linerNotes` section and a slide-out drawer triggered by the "Liner Notes" CTA both call linerNotesContent(album:) with identical output.
  - _Why:_ The inline `linerNotes` section (lines 531-547) unconditionally shows Released/Label/Format/Runtime/Tracks + Credits whenever album != nil. The "Liner Notes" CTA (lines 280-288) opens linerNotesDrawer → linerNotesPanel → the SAME linerNotesContent (line 695). So the drawer presents content that is already fully visible by scrolling the page — redundant UI and duplicated layout/measurement work each render.
  - _Fix:_ Pick one presentation: either drop the always-inline section in favor of the on-demand drawer, or remove the drawer CTA, to avoid showing the same credits/details twice.
- **L607** [consistency] creditRowView uses array offset as the ForEach identity for credit people (`id: \.offset`).
  - _Why:_ Offset-as-identity is the standard SwiftUI anti-pattern: if the underlying people list ever reorders or mutates, SwiftUI animates/reuses views by position rather than content, causing stale state on CreditChip (e.g. its @State isHovering). The list is currently static and deduplicated by name|id in ExtendedCredit.rows, so it is harmless today, but Person carries a stable `id`/`name` that would make a better key.
  - _Fix:_ Key on a stable composite: `ForEach(row.people, id: \.self)` after making Person Hashable, or `ForEach(Array(row.people.enumerated()), id: \.element.id)` (falling back to name when id is nil).
- **L794** [performance] releasedSummary allocates a fresh DateFormatter on every invocation. It is called once per liner-notes-content render pass.
  - _Why:_ DateFormatter construction is relatively expensive (locale/calendar setup, historically ~ms). It is invoked inside a SwiftUI view-builder helper (linerRow("Released", releasedSummary(album:))), so it re-runs on each body re-evaluation of the liner-notes section. Not per-cell, so impact is low, but it is needless churn on a hot-ish render path.
  - _Fix:_ Hoist to a `static let releasedFormatter: DateFormatter = { ... }()` and reuse it, or use `date.formatted(date: .abbreviated, time: .omitted)` which avoids the allocation.
- **L834** [consistency] formatSummary displays the FIRST track's bitrate as the album-wide kbps figure, but the local variable is named `avg`, implying an average. The displayed kbps is `Int(avg)/1000` where `avg = bitrates.first`, not a mean.
  - _Why:_ The tolerance check (all within 32kbps of the first track) gates whether a single number is shown, but the number shown is whichever track happens to be first in the array, not a representative average. If the first track is an outlier still inside the +/-32kbps window, the badge under-/over-reports the album's typical bitrate. Misleading name invites future maintainers to assume averaging that isn't happening.
  - _Fix:_ Compute an actual average for display: `let kbps = Int(bitrates.reduce(0,+)/UInt32(bitrates.count))/1000`, or rename `avg` to `first` to make the behavior explicit. Either way decouple the displayed value from array ordering.
- **L837** [consistency] formatSummary emits a bare bitrate number with no "kbps" unit, and the local variable named `avg` is actually just the first bitrate, not an average.
  - _Why:_ `avg` (line 834) is `bitrates.first`, not a mean — only the dispersion check uses it. The returned string "\(ordered[0]) \(kbps)" (line 837) yields e.g. "FLAC 1411" with no unit, which reads ambiguously in the Format stat/liner row (could be misread as anything). Cosmetic, but the Format field is user-facing.
  - _Fix:_ Append the unit (e.g. `return "\(ordered[0]) \(kbps) kbps"`) and rename the variable to `firstBitrate` for clarity.
- **L1026** [resource-leak] AddToPlaylistPopover starts an unstructured Task per playlist tap that is not cancelled when the popover is dismissed, and `isAdding` is a single shared flag for all rows.
  - _Why:_ If the popover is dismissed externally (the parent toggles `showAddToPlaylist`, e.g. clicking away) while an add is in flight, the detached `Task` keeps running and may call `onDismiss()` / mutate `isAdding` after the view is gone. It also writes `errorMessage` indirectly via model on failure even though the user already closed the sheet. Low impact (the network call completes harmlessly), but it is an unmanaged task with no cancellation tie to the view lifecycle.
  - _Fix:_ Use `.task`/a cancellable task bound to the view, or check for cancellation/`Task.isCancelled` before calling onDismiss; at minimum guard the post-await UI mutations.
- **L1028** [error-handling] In AddToPlaylistPopover, when addToPlaylist returns false (server failure OR empty trackIds), the popover does not dismiss and shows no in-view feedback; the user sees the row tap do nothing. Error only surfaces via the global model.errorMessage banner elsewhere.
  - _Why:_ On `ok == false` the popover stays open with the spinner gone and no row-level error state, so a failed add looks identical to no action. For the empty-trackIds path (addToPlaylist guards `!trackIds.isEmpty` and returns false), tapping a playlist before tracks finish loading silently no-ops. Discoverability of the failure depends entirely on the user noticing the separate global error banner.
  - _Fix:_ Surface a local failure state in the popover (e.g. set an @State errorText shown beneath the list on `!ok`), and/or disable/empty-state the playlist list when `trackIds.isEmpty` so the action isn't a dead tap.
- **L1089** [other] FlowLayout.sizeThatFits over-reports each row's width by one trailing `spacing` because the cursor (which already includes a trailing spacing) is folded into the row max after the increment.
  - _Why:_ Each completed row's recorded width includes the inter-item spacing that follows its last chip, so the layout's intrinsic width is up to one `spacing` (6pt) wider than the actual content. It is clamped by `min(totalWidth, maxWidth)`, so it cannot push past the proposal, but it can cause a marginally-too-wide intrinsic size when the container sizes to fit (e.g. credits flow inside a fixed 360pt drawer is fine, but a self-sizing context would inherit the slop).
  - _Fix:_ Record the row extent before adding the trailing spacing, e.g. `rows[rowIdx] = max(rows[rowIdx], cursor + size.width)` then `cursor += size.width + spacing`, mirroring the bounds check at line 1082.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/ArtistDetailView.swift`
- **L121** [consistency] The top-tracks loading spinner stays visible longer than necessary: isLoadingTopTracks is only set false after both loadArtistAlbums and loadArtistTopTracks complete, because the awaits run serially with albums first. The spinner in topSongsSection is blocked on an unrelated albums fetch.
  - _Why:_ The Top Songs section shows a spinner while the (separate, possibly slower) album list loads first, making top songs feel slower than they are. Minor UX latency, not a correctness bug.
  - _Fix:_ Load top tracks before albums, or load them concurrently with independent do/catch tasks and flip isLoadingTopTracks as soon as the top-tracks fetch returns, independent of the albums fetch.
- **L190** [accessibility] Hero decorative artwork (backdrop and portrait AsyncImages) is not hidden from accessibility, so VoiceOver announces unlabeled image elements.
  - _Why:_ These images carry no information beyond the already-announced artist name; without .accessibilityHidden(true) VoiceOver users hear extra noise ("image") with no label or trait. The artist name, genres, and stats are already exposed as text, so the artwork is redundant decoration.
  - _Fix:_ Add .accessibilityHidden(true) to the backdrop ZStack and the hero portrait image, since their semantic content is fully covered by the adjacent text.
- **L757** [consistency] The "Read more" biography button is shown unconditionally whenever a bio exists, even when the overview fits within the 4-line limit, so it opens a popover containing the identical, already-fully-visible text.
  - _Why:_ For short bios (<= 4 lines) nothing is truncated, so "Read more" is a no-op affordance that opens a popover repeating what the user already sees — minor polish/UX inconsistency.
  - _Fix:_ Only render the "Read more" button when the overview actually exceeds the line limit (e.g. measure truncation via a ViewThatFits / line-count heuristic, or gate on overview length), otherwise omit it.
- **L850** [bug] decodingHTMLEntities replaces named entities by iterating an unordered Dictionary, and decodes `&amp;` to `&` in the same pass as other named entities. Input containing an escaped entity reference such as `&amp;lt;` can be double-decoded into `<` instead of the literal `&lt;`, depending on iteration order.
  - _Why:_ Standard HTML-entity-decoding pitfall: `&amp;` must be decoded last (or in a single pass) so that already-encoded ampersands don't get re-interpreted as the start of another entity. With dictionary order undefined, the output is non-deterministic for inputs like `&amp;lt;`.
  - _Fix:_ Decode `&amp;` last, or do a single-pass scan over `&...;` tokens resolving each token exactly once, rather than sequential global replaces. The numeric-entity pass below it already uses the correct single-pass-reversed approach; mirror that for named entities.
- **L850** [bug] HTML named-entity decoding iterates a Swift Dictionary, whose order is nondeterministic, so double-encoded entities can decode inconsistently run-to-run.
  - _Why:_ Dictionary iteration order is not stable in Swift. For an input like "&amp;lt;", correct output depends on processing "&amp;" before the resulting "&lt;". Because order is random, the same bio string can decode to "&lt;" on one launch and "<" on another. This is an edge case (double-encoded entities are uncommon) but it is a real nondeterminism bug in the displayed biography text.
  - _Fix:_ Process &amp; last (or use an ordered array of (entity, replacement) pairs with &amp; placed after the others), so already-decoded ampersands aren't re-interpreted. Alternatively decode &amp; only after all other named/numeric entities are resolved.
- **L939** [concurrency] Discography / similar-artist / featuring tiles call the synchronous model.imageURL(...) FFI during body evaluation inside EAGER HStacks, so the first cache-cold render of a prolific artist fires N main-thread Rust-mutex acquisitions in one render pass.
  - _Why:_ Each call is only string formatting under the FFI mutex, but the count is unbounded by album count and they all resolve at once because the HStack is eager. For an artist with dozens of releases across 4 discography groups + 12 similar + 6 featuring, that's 60+ sequential mutex round-trips on the main thread during the first render, a measurable hitch under contention with the playback poll. This is the exact MainActor-sync-FFI pattern CLAUDE.md gap #2 warns about; memoization only helps after the first pass.
  - _Fix:_ Resolve artwork URLs off-main (Task.detached) and store on the tile model, or prewarm the imageURLCache in the .task that loads artistAlbums/similar/featuring so body hits are pure cache reads. At minimum confirm via Activity Monitor that the eager-HStack burst doesn't beachball on large discographies.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/DiscoverView.swift`
- **L33** [consistency] DiscoverView's .task self-loads genresToExplore when empty but never triggers refreshForYou(); the For You section silently hides and never recovers if forYou is empty on direct navigation.
  - _Why:_ refreshForYou is a cheap, network-free derivation from recentlyPlayed. If a user lands on Discover (e.g. restored tab / deep link) before the post-login refresh at AppModel.swift:1497 has populated forYou, the For You shelf is absent and never repopulates without leaving and returning. The asymmetry with genresToExplore (which does self-heal) is the concrete inconsistency.
  - _Fix:_ In the same .task, also call await model.refreshForYou() (it is idempotent and local), or guard it on model.forYou.isEmpty like the genres branch.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/FavoritesView.swift`
- **L193** [accessibility] The decorative heart SF Symbol in the empty state is not hidden from accessibility, so VoiceOver announces a meaningless image next to the 'No favorites yet' heading.
  - _Why:_ The icon is purely decorative; the adjacent text already conveys the state. Without .accessibilityHidden(true) (or combining the HStack into one element) VoiceOver reads it as an unlabeled/decorative image, adding noise to the empty-state announcement.
  - _Fix:_ Add .accessibilityHidden(true) to the Image, or wrap the HStack with .accessibilityElement(children: .combine) so the icon is folded into the text.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/HomeView.swift`
- **L361** [consistency] `handleStationTap` reconstructs `Genre(name: station.title)` from the title, discarding the real server id stored on the pinned station. `pinGenreToHome` (AppModel:5557) saves `PinnedStation(type:.genre, id: genre.id, title: genre.name)` with the resolved server id, but tap uses the name-only initializer (which sets `id = name`) and forces `browseGenre` to re-resolve the id by name.
  - _Why:_ Wastes the persisted real id and adds a network round-trip / cache lookup that was already done at pin time. If two genres share a display name, name-based re-resolution can also resolve to the wrong genre.
  - _Fix:_ Pass the stored id: `model.navigate(to: .genre(Genre(id: station.id, name: station.title)))` (or add a browseGenre overload taking an id) instead of round-tripping through the name.
- **L815** [accessibility] The decorative `heart.fill` glyph inside `favoritesEmptyState` is not hidden from assistive tech. Unlike `HomeQuickTilePlaceholder` (which correctly sets `.accessibilityHidden(true)` at line 948), this purely-decorative icon will be announced by VoiceOver as a separate element before the explanatory text.
  - _Why:_ An unlabeled decorative SF Symbol read aloud adds noise to the VoiceOver experience of the empty state and offers no information beyond the visible text.
  - _Fix:_ Add `.accessibilityHidden(true)` to the decorative `Image(systemName: "heart.fill")` (and ideally to the section-header icons rendered by `carouselSection`/`favoritesSectionHeader`), since the accompanying text already conveys meaning.
- **L922** [dead-code] `HomeQuickTilePlaceholder` is dead code. Its only call site is `quickTilesRow` (HomeView.swift:240), and `quickTilesRow` itself is never referenced anywhere in `HomeView.body` or elsewhere in the file — confirmed by grep (`quickTilesRow` appears only at its own definition, line 217). So this private view is unreachable.
  - _Why:_ Dead view code adds maintenance surface and compile time and misleads readers into thinking a placeholder/skeleton state ships when it never renders.
  - _Fix:_ Remove `HomeQuickTilePlaceholder` together with the unused `quickTilesRow`/`tileAlbums`/`placeholderCount` (and `pinnedStationsRow` if also confirmed unused), or wire `quickTilesRow` into `body` if it was meant to ship.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/KeyboardShortcutsView.swift`
- **L172** [dead-code] `KeyChord`'s `.accessibilityLabel(Text(glyphs))` can never surface. The only call site (line 127) is inside `shortcutRow`, whose container sets `.accessibilityElement(children: .ignore)` (line 132) and supplies its own `.accessibilityLabel`/`.accessibilityValue` (lines 133-134). With children ignored, the child KeyChord's accessibility modifiers are dropped.
  - _Why:_ The label is inert today; it gives a false impression that KeyChord is independently accessible and could mask a regression if KeyChord is later reused outside an `children: .ignore` context.
  - _Fix:_ Drop the redundant `.accessibilityLabel` on `KeyChord` (the parent row already exposes the glyphs via `accessibilityValue`), or keep it only if KeyChord is intended for reuse in a non-ignored context.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/LibraryView.swift`
- **L165** [consistency] The selection-banner animation is keyed on `selectedTrackIds.isEmpty` while the banner's presence is driven by `selectedTracks.isEmpty`; the two can diverge under an active filter.
  - _Why:_ selectedTracks = sortedTracks.filter { selectedTrackIds.contains } can be empty while selectedTrackIds is non-empty (e.g. a filter excludes the selected rows). In that case the banner's appearance/disappearance is driven by a value the animation isn't observing, so the move/opacity transition can be skipped or mistimed. Cosmetic, but the animation trigger and the visibility condition should reference the same quantity.
  - _Fix:_ Animate on `selectedTracks.isEmpty` (matching the banner condition), or compute both from the same source of truth.
- **L211** [bug] Applying a filter does not clear the track selection, leaving a ghost selection that reappears when the filter is removed.
  - _Why:_ selectedTrackIds can retain ids for tracks that the new filter excludes. selectedTracks recomputes so the banner correctly hides them, but the underlying selection persists; removing the filter resurfaces a stale selection the user thought was gone, and any future 'act on selection' operation would target rows no longer visible.
  - _Fix:_ Call clearSelection() (or prune selectedTrackIds to the new filtered set) inside onChange(of: filter).
- **L724** [gap-stub] The `onlyDownloaded` filter dimension is counted toward filter.isActive/activeGroupCount but is never evaluated by any passesFilter implementation (latent no-op filter).
  - _Why:_ Currently masked because the popover only exposes the 'Only downloaded' toggle when showDownloaded (== model.supportsDownloads == false), so it can't be set today. But if a persisted/legacy filter has onlyDownloaded == true, filter.isActive becomes true and triggers the slow client-side filtering path while filtering on nothing — every item passes, yet the active-filter badge shows and the (already buggy) count/pagination behavior engages. It is a dormant inconsistency waiting on the downloads feature.
  - _Fix:_ When supportsDownloads is false, ignore/strip onlyDownloaded from the effective filter (don't count it in activeGroupCount); when downloads land, implement the predicate in each passesFilter.
- **L872** [gap-stub] `.recentlyAdded` sort is an identity pass that returns the unsorted filtered list, so the option does nothing once any client-side filter reorders/subsets the data.
  - _Why:_ This relies entirely on the server already returning items in recently-added order, but the loaders fetch with plain offset/limit and the view applies client-side filtering. After filtering (which preserves source order) the result is whatever order the pages happened to load in, not a guaranteed recency order — and there is no client fallback if the server order isn't recency-sorted. Selecting 'Recently Added' can therefore be a no-op relative to the default, with no visible effect.
  - _Fix:_ Either request a recently-added-sorted page from the core for this option (server-side sort) or, if the model carries a dateAdded/createdAt field, sort on it client-side as the other recency-based cases do (recentlyPlayed sorts on userData.lastPlayedAt).
- **L1256** [consistency] AlbumCard shows a year of 0 in the visible subline while the accessibility label correctly suppresses year 0, producing an inconsistent '· 0'.
  - _Why:_ Albums with a missing/zero year (year == 0 rather than nil) display a meaningless '· 0' next to the artist, while VoiceOver users hear no year. The two code paths apply different validity rules to the same field.
  - _Fix:_ Apply the same `year > 0` guard in the visible subline: `if let year = album.year, year > 0 { Text("· \(String(year))") }`.
- **L1256** [consistency] AlbumCard shows the year unconditionally when `album.year != nil`, but the accessibility label only includes the year when `year > 0`. A sentinel year of 0 would render '· 0' visually while VoiceOver omits it.
  - _Why:_ The visual (1256) and the a11y label (1291) use different predicates for showing the year: `year != nil` vs `year > 0`. If the backend ever projects an unknown ProductionYear as 0 rather than null, the card displays the meaningless '· 0' while VoiceOver correctly hides it — an inconsistency between sighted and VoiceOver users. Low confidence the trigger occurs in practice (Jellyfin typically maps a missing year to null/None, which would be nil here), but the guards should match.
  - _Fix:_ Make both predicates identical, e.g. gate the visual on `if let year = album.year, year > 0` to match `albumAccessibilityLabel`, so a 0 sentinel is hidden in both places.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/LoginView.swift`
- **L46** [dead-code] hasSeenRepeatedUnreachable is set to true (line 108) but is never reset to false for the lifetime of the view. The flag is effectively write-once; the real gating in loginErrorMessage is the live `!model.serverReachability.isServerReachable` term, making hasSeenRepeatedUnreachable redundant once it has flipped true.
  - _Why:_ A sticky flag that is never cleared either should be removed (if the live reachability check suffices) or actually reset on recovery; as written it carries no additional signal after the first unreachable event and is confusing latent state.
  - _Fix:_ Either drop hasSeenRepeatedUnreachable and gate solely on serverReachability.isServerReachable, or reset it to false in the onChange when reachable becomes true.
- **L169** [dead-code] Tapping a discovered server sets `url` AND immediately calls probe.schedule(url:) (line 171). But mutating `url` also fires the .onChange(of: url) handler (line 100-106), which calls probe.schedule(newValue) again. The probe is thus scheduled twice for one tap.
  - _Why:_ Redundant work. It is harmless because ServerProbe.schedule cancels the prior task first, but the explicit probe.schedule call here is dead/duplicate given the onChange already handles it.
  - _Fix:_ Remove the explicit probe.schedule(url: url) inside the discovered-server button; rely on onChange(of: url).
- **L189** [accessibility] The discovered-server button's accessibilityLabel is a hardcoded English literal 'Use discovered server \(server.name)', whereas the other accessibility labels in this file use localization keys (e.g. login.a11y.server_url, login.a11y.username, login.a11y.password). VoiceOver users on non-English locales get an untranslated label here, and it is interpolated so it can never be a catalog key.
  - _Why:_ Inconsistent a11y localization within a single view; this label will not localize alongside the catalog-keyed labels nearby.
  - _Fix:_ Use a String(localized:) format string, e.g. String(localized: "login.a11y.use_discovered_server \(server.name)") or an AttributedString-free format with an argument.
- **L266** [consistency] The username field binds directly to global model.username via a custom Binding, so every keystroke in the login username field mutates shared AppModel state before any login attempt. The URL and password fields, by contrast, use view-local @State (url, password). This asymmetry means a half-typed username persists in the model across navigation, while url/password do not.
  - _Why:_ Inconsistent ownership of the three credential fields; binding username to global state means an abandoned login attempt leaves a partial username in AppModel.username that other code (canSubmit, restore logic) reads.
  - _Fix:_ Use a view-local @State for username during entry (mirroring password) and assign model.username only on successful login, or document/justify why username alone is global.
- **L355** [concurrency] submit() launches an unstructured Task that is not bound to the view's lifecycle and is not cancelled in onDisappear. If the user dismisses the login screen (or it is replaced) mid-login, the Task still runs to completion and writes to shared model state (model.errorMessage). Writing shakeAttempts after teardown is benign since the @State is gone, but the model.errorMessage write persists globally and can show a stale error on the next screen.
  - _Why:_ Unstructured Task leaks: the continuation can mutate global AppModel.errorMessage after the view is gone, producing a stale error on whatever screen shows next.
  - _Fix:_ Track the task in a @State Task handle and cancel it in onDisappear, or move the post-login presentation logic into AppModel.login itself so the view does not own the continuation.
- **L384** [bug] When the server is currently unreachable and hasSeenRepeatedUnreachable is true, loginErrorMessage returns the 'Trying offline mode' string and thereby suppresses any real login error in model.errorMessage. A user who typed wrong credentials and then experiences a transient server reachability blip will see 'Trying offline mode' instead of the actual credential error, masking the real failure.
  - _Why:_ The reachability banner takes precedence over the credential error, so the actionable error (fix your password) is hidden behind a transient connectivity message.
  - _Fix:_ Only show the offline-mode message when there is no concrete model.errorMessage to display, or surface both (reachability hint plus the credential error).

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/MainShell.swift`
- **L191** [accessibility] The PlayerBar region is never given the intended named Switch Control group. SwitchControlGroup defines a `.playerBar` ("Player Bar") case and the sidebar/content regions apply their cases as accessibilityLabels, but the player bar gets only an accessibilitySortPriority and no matching `.accessibilityElement(children: .contain)` + `.accessibilityLabel(SwitchControlGroup.playerBar.rawValue)`.
  - _Why:_ The three SwitchControlGroup cases exist to give VoiceOver/Switch Control three labelled navigation containers (Sidebar / Content / Player Bar). Two of the three are wired; the third is not, so `SwitchControlGroup.playerBar` is effectively dead and the player-controls region has no group label for assistive navigation. PlayerBar.swift's internal `.accessibilityElement(children: .contain)` carries no label, so the region is unnamed.
  - _Fix:_ Add `.accessibilityElement(children: .contain)` and `.accessibilityLabel(SwitchControlGroup.playerBar.rawValue)` to the PlayerBar() call site (matching the sidebar/content pattern), so the third Switch Control group is actually exposed and the enum case is used.
- **L412** [dead-code] routeDestination handles seven tab-screen Route cases (.home/.discover/.radio/.library/.favorites/.search/.settings) that are never pushed onto navPath, so these navigationDestination branches are unreachable.
  - _Why:_ A repo-wide search for navPath.append shows only .album/.artist/.playlist/.genre/.nowPlaying/.fullQueue are ever pushed; tab switching goes through selectTab (which sets `navPath = []`). The seven tab cases therefore can never be reached via `.navigationDestination(for: AppModel.Route.self)`. They are harmless but dead, and `.settings -> EmptyView()` in particular would render a blank detail if it ever were reached.
  - _Fix:_ Either remove these cases from the Route enum / routeDestination, or replace the unreachable group with a single `default` that asserts in debug, to keep the destination switch honest and prevent a silent blank screen if a future call site pushes one of them.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/NowPlayingView.swift`
- **L84** [performance] Track-detail and lyrics fetches are awaited sequentially in one .task, so the Lyrics tab stays on its spinner until the (unrelated) People fetch completes.
  - _Why:_ fetchCurrentTrackDetails (People/Credits) and fetchCurrentTrackLyrics are independent core FFI round-trips, but the second await cannot start until the first finishes. If the People fetch is slow, the lyricsPanel keeps rendering its 'Loading lyrics…' ProgressView (lyricsPanel shows the spinner whenever currentLyrics == nil) longer than necessary, even though lyrics could have loaded in parallel.
  - _Fix:_ Run the two fetches concurrently, e.g. async let a = model.fetchCurrentTrackDetails(); async let b = model.fetchCurrentTrackLyrics(); _ = await (a, b) — or kick each off in its own child task — so neither endpoint's latency gates the other.
- **L493** [dead-code] formatRuntime duplicates the existing Track.durationFormatted extension verbatim.
  - _Why:_ AppModel.swift defines extension Track { var durationFormatted: String } with byte-identical m:%02d formatting (lines 6409-6414). The view already has the Track in hand at the only call site (aboutPanel: formatRuntime(track.durationSeconds)). Maintaining two copies of the same minutes:seconds formatter invites drift (e.g. one gets hour support and the other doesn't) and is unnecessary code.
  - _Fix:_ Delete formatRuntime and call track.durationFormatted at line 432-433. (Both renderings share the same limitation of not emitting an hours component for >60min items, which is consistent app-wide, so changing only this copy is not warranted — collapse to the shared one.)
- **L560** [dead-code] The previousScreen fallback branch in dismiss() is unreachable while the view is on screen.
  - _Why:_ NowPlayingView is presented by appending AppModel.Route.nowPlaying to navPath (LyrebirdApp.toggleNowPlaying), and isShowingNowPlaying is defined as navPath.last == .nowPlaying. Therefore navPath always contains at least the .nowPlaying entry whenever this view (and its close button / .cancelAction shortcut) is active, so the !navPath.isEmpty branch always wins and the else-if previousScreen path can never execute from here. It is harmless but dead.
  - _Fix:_ Either drop the else-if (the removeLast() path fully covers dismissal), or, if previousScreen-based dismissal is genuinely intended for some entry path, document/guard it explicitly — as written it is misleading defensive code that never runs.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/OnboardingView.swift`
- **L68** [gap-stub] WelcomeStep's 'I already have an account' action is functionally identical to 'Get started' — both just set step = .connect — making the secondary CTA pointless.
  - _Why:_ Two visually distinct buttons that do exactly the same thing is a dead/confusing UI affordance; users expecting the 'existing account' path to behave differently (e.g. jump straight to credentials) get the same generic connect screen.
  - _Fix:_ Either differentiate the existing-account path (e.g. focus the username field, pre-fill model.serverURL) or remove the redundant button.
- **L94** [consistency] The 'Skip, explore offline' path completes onboarding without configuring an offline/guest session, so the subsequent app state depends entirely on global gating with no signal that the user opted into offline mode.
  - _Why:_ The button promises 'explore offline' but, with no session, the app gate sends the user to LoginView, contradicting the affordance. At minimum it is a confusing dead-end; users who tap it expecting to browse cached content are bounced to a sign-in screen.
  - _Fix:_ Confirm the intended offline path; if offline browsing requires a cached/guest session, establish it here, otherwise relabel the button to reflect that it ends setup and shows the sign-in screen.
- **L200** [accessibility] Discovered-server chip buttons in onboarding lack an accessibilityLabel, while the identical chips in LoginView label them ('Use discovered server <name>').
  - _Why:_ VoiceOver will read the server name but the 'wifi' SF Symbol may also be announced and the action ('use this server') is not conveyed, an inconsistency with the login screen for the same control.
  - _Fix:_ Add .accessibilityLabel("Use discovered server \(server.name)") to match LoginView; optionally .accessibilityHidden(true) on the decorative wifi image.
- **L524** [performance] counterLabel allocates a fresh NumberFormatter on every body evaluation; this computed property is read inside the body that re-renders on each animatedProgress tick (~15 steps/phase x 4 phases) and each library-count change.
  - _Why:_ NumberFormatter construction is comparatively expensive and this is on a per-animation-frame hot path during the sync screen. It is wasteful churn for a label that changes only when counts change.
  - _Fix:_ Use a cached/static NumberFormatter, or IntegerFormatStyle (e.g. tracks.formatted(.number)), instead of allocating per render.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/PlaylistDetailView.swift`
- **L86** [bug] showUndoToast can remain true with a nil pendingPlaylistRemoval after a failed remove, leaving stale state and a scheduled dismiss that fires uselessly.
  - _Why:_ performRemove sets showUndoToast = true synchronously (line 376) and schedules a 10s dismiss. If the server remove fails, AppModel rolls back and sets pendingPlaylistRemoval = nil (AppModel.swift:3147). The toast body then renders nothing (the `let pending = ...` guard fails — so no crash), but showUndoToast stays true for up to 10s and the DispatchWorkItem still runs to set it false. It's cosmetically harmless but leaves the view's @State out of sync with the model, and the .animation(value: showUndoToast) tracks a value that no longer corresponds to any visible UI.
  - _Fix:_ Tie toast visibility to the model rather than a separate Bool — e.g. derive `showUndoToast` from `model.pendingPlaylistRemoval != nil` — or clear showUndoToast when pendingPlaylistRemoval becomes nil (onChange) so the flag and the model can't diverge.
- **L222** [consistency] Shuffle plays a one-time client-side tracks.shuffled() snapshot rather than enabling shuffle mode, so it diverges from how shuffle behaves elsewhere and won't re-shuffle on queue exhaustion.
  - _Why:_ This builds a single shuffled order and plays it as a fixed queue. There is no shuffle flag set on the player, so any global shuffle state and the queue UI won't reflect 'shuffle on', and when the queue ends there's no re-shuffle. AppModel has dedicated shuffle helpers (e.g. shuffle(album:)) used for other entities; using play(tracks: tracks.shuffled()) here is an inconsistent ad-hoc path.
  - _Fix:_ Route shuffle through the same shuffle API used by album/artist surfaces (or set the player's shuffle mode) so behavior and UI state are consistent across screens.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/PlaylistView.swift`
- **L96** [bug] On playlistID change, isLoadingTracks is set true only after the resolvePlaylist await, so the previously-viewed playlist's tracks flash before the spinner and new data appear.
  - _Why:_ When navigating from playlist A to playlist B (uncached), the task re-runs but `tracks` and `isLoadingTracks` retain A's values during the `await model.resolvePlaylist` call. Because isLoadingTracks is flipped to true only on line 106 (after the resolve await), the trackList branch at line 323 (`!isLoadingTracks && !tracks.isEmpty`) keeps rendering playlist A's rows until resolvePlaylist returns, producing a stale-content flash and a momentarily incorrect ScopedSearchBar/header.
  - _Fix:_ Reset state at the top of the task before any await: set `tracks = []`, `isLoadingTracks = true`, `scopedQuery = ""` immediately, then resolve and load. This guarantees the spinner shows for the new playlist instead of the previous one's rows.
- **L212** [accessibility] The tappable title Text that triggers rename has an accessibility label and hint but no button trait, so assistive tech doesn't announce it as actionable.
  - _Why:_ The Text carries a tap gesture (enter rename mode) and an accessibilityHint of 'Tap to rename', but a plain Text is exposed to VoiceOver as static text, not a button. Without .accessibilityAddTraits(.isButton) VoiceOver users get the hint but the element isn't announced as a control and isn't reliably activatable, making rename unreachable via assistive tech.
  - _Fix:_ Add `.accessibilityAddTraits(.isButton)` (and ideally `.accessibilityAction { titleDraft = playlist.name; DispatchQueue.main.async { titleFocused = true } }`) so the rename affordance is announced and activatable.
- **L229** [validation] commitTitle passes the raw untrimmed draft; whitespace-only or unchanged names are silently dropped server-side with no user feedback, and the field reverts.
  - _Why:_ draft is forwarded verbatim. AppModel.renamePlaylist(id:) (AppModel.swift:4876) trims and rejects empty (`guard !trimmed.isEmpty`) and no-op when unchanged, so a whitespace-only or unchanged entry results in no rename, yet titleDraft is set to nil regardless, snapping the field back to the old name with no indication that the edit was ignored. A user who clears the name and presses Enter sees it silently revert. Functionally non-destructive but confusing.
  - _Fix:_ Trim in commitTitle and short-circuit when empty (keep the field in edit mode or show a brief 'Name can't be empty' message), e.g. `let trimmed = draft.trimmingCharacters(in: .whitespacesAndNewlines); guard !trimmed.isEmpty else { titleFocused = true; return }`. This gives the user feedback instead of a silent revert.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesAccount.swift`
- **L138** [gap-stub] Quick Connect button is permanently disabled with an empty action — a visible dead control.
  - _Why:_ The button has an empty closure and is hard-disabled. It ships a non-functional control in the Account pane. The help/accessibility text does explain it is unavailable, so this is low severity, but it is dead UI that occupies the actions row and can confuse users. (Consistent with CLAUDE.md's catalogue of feature-flagged stubs.)
  - _Fix:_ Hide the control behind a capability flag (as the repo does for other unimplemented features via Capabilities.swift) rather than rendering a permanently disabled empty-action button, or remove it until Quick Connect FFI lands.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesAdvanced.swift`
- **L292** [concurrency] Two unstructured asyncAfter timers reset transient flags with no cancellation; rapid re-taps stack overlapping timers that can fight over the flag.
  - _Why:_ Each tap schedules a new asyncAfter that flips the flag back to false. If the user taps the button again before the timer fires, multiple timers are queued; an earlier-scheduled timer can reset the flag while the latest tap expected it to stay true, producing flicker (e.g. the "Copied" / "Paste in search bar" label reverting early). Minor cosmetic-only, but it is uncancelled fire-and-forget work tied to view state.
  - _Fix:_ Track and cancel the prior DispatchWorkItem (or use a Task you store and cancel) before scheduling a new one, so only the most recent reset is in flight.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesAppearance.swift`
- **L234** [consistency] The Density section's hint claims row heights are not yet wired ('hook in once #162 lands — selection persists now'), but density is already fully consumed.
  - _Why:_ This is user-facing copy (rendered in the pane), not a code comment, so it survives the comment-stripping and actively misinforms the user that a working feature is non-functional. It will read as a stale/abandoned feature.
  - _Fix:_ Update the hint to describe the live behavior (e.g. 'Compact tightens track rows and shrinks artwork in lists.') and drop the #162 reference.
- **L401** [bug] Stale persisted state (mode=light + non-purple theme) renders the Light segment as both selected and enabled, despite Light being invalid for non-purple themes; no normalization runs on load.
  - _Why:_ A user who had Purple+Light, switched to a non-default theme in a build where that combo was permitted, or whose persisted defaults predate this constraint, will see Light shown as the active mode under e.g. Ocean — a state the binding's setter explicitly forbids. The displayed mode contradicts the actual enforced rule.
  - _Fix:_ Normalize on read: in the mode getter, if the resolved theme != .purple and the stored mode == .light, return .dark (and/or correct modeRaw in an onAppear). That makes the invalid combo self-heal instead of presenting an enabled-but-illegal selection.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesLibrary.swift`
- **L274** [bug] Rapid double-clicks of the Clear Cache button schedule overlapping asyncAfter timers with no guard. Unlike rescan() (which guards with `guard !isRescanning`), clearCache() has no in-flight guard, so each click re-sets justCleared = true and schedules another nested pair of asyncAfter closures. Two clicks ~1s apart cause the 'Cleared ✓' label to flicker back to 'Clear Cache' early when the first click's 1.4 s reset fires while the second click is still in its window.
  - _Why:_ Minor visual glitch (confirmation label flickering) under repeated taps. Not data-affecting, but inconsistent with the rescan guard pattern in the same file.
  - _Fix:_ Add a `guard !justCleared else { return }` at the top, or track the work with a cancellable Task and cancel the prior one before scheduling a new reset.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/Preferences/PreferencesServer.swift`
- **L318** [consistency] switchServer() clears the server URL only in memory; the persisted server URL and username are left on disk after every sign-out/switch.
  - _Why:_ After 'Switch Server' (whose alert promises to connect to a different server) or 'Sign Out', the previous server URL and username remain persisted in the app's local settings DB indefinitely. It is not user-visible because nothing reads those persisted values back into the UI, but it is stale credential-adjacent metadata that survives an explicit 'switch/forget' action and contradicts the stated intent of clearing the connection.
  - _Fix:_ Either expose an FFI that deletes last_server_url/last_username and call it from switchServer (and last_username from changeUser), or accept the leftover and surface it intentionally by reading it back for pre-fill (see the related p2 finding). Pick one so persisted state and the alert copy agree.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Screens/SearchView.swift`
- **L27** [resource-leak] searchDebounce and searchTask are never cancelled on view disappearance; there is no .onDisappear. An in-flight debounce or search outlives navigation away from the Search tab.
  - _Why:_ Leaving the Search tab mid-search keeps a Task running a network call whose result is discarded; the debounce can also fire after the view is gone. Minor because the tasks are short-lived and SearchView is typically a persistent top-level tab, but it's an unstructured-task lifecycle gap.
  - _Fix:_ Add `.onDisappear { searchDebounce?.cancel(); searchTask?.cancel() }` to body.
- **L316** [consistency] A single shared model.isLoadingFullSearch flag is passed as isLoading to every SectionView, so loading more in one section replaces the 'Load more' button with a spinner in ALL sections simultaneously.
  - _Why:_ When the user taps 'Load more' on, say, Albums, the Artists/Tracks/Playlists/Genres sections also flip to spinners even though nothing is loading for them, which looks like the whole page is reloading.
  - _Fix:_ Track loading per section/scope, or only show the spinner on the section whose onLoadMore was invoked (e.g. a @State loadingScope set in handleLoadMore).
- **L359** [bug] Clicking 'Load more' within one section (e.g. Tracks) can fetch a global page that adds items only to a different scope (e.g. Albums), inflating the tapped section's revealed count past its bucket size while showing the user nothing new in that section.
  - _Why:_ User taps 'Load more' under Tracks, sees a spinner, and the next page only contains albums — the Tracks list is unchanged, making the button feel broken. revealed quietly grows past the available item count.
  - _Fix:_ Only bump revealed for a scope by the number of NEW items actually added to that scope's bucket after the fetch, or disable per-section 'Load more' once that scope's bucket is fully revealed and gate further loads on whether the global fetch actually grew this bucket.
- **L412** [consistency] The empty-query branch in scheduleDebouncedSearch launches a runFullSearch(query: "") network/FFI-wrapped call to clear state, which is redundant work since runFullSearch short-circuits empty queries to local resets anyway, and it overlaps with clearQuery doing the same thing.
  - _Why:_ Not a correctness bug (runFullSearch handles empty safely), but it spins up a Task to do a pure local reset that could be done synchronously on the MainActor, and duplicates clearQuery's logic. Minor churn / inconsistency.
  - _Fix:_ For the empty case, reset model state directly (or call a dedicated synchronous reset) instead of dispatching an async runFullSearch(""); consolidate with clearQuery.
- **L509** [dead-code] The `.all` case inside SectionView.content is unreachable dead code. SectionView is only ever instantiated with concrete scopes; when activeSearchScope == .all, sectionedResults expands it into allScopes, so a SectionView with scope == .all is never created.
  - _Why:_ Dead branch; also if it were ever reached it would render unstyled plain-text titles with no actionable rows, inconsistent with every other scope. Maintenance hazard.
  - _Fix:_ Remove the `case .all` branch (or `assertionFailure`/return EmptyView) since the type system can't be made exhaustive here but the path is provably unreachable.
- **L509** [dead-code] The `case .all` branch in SectionView.content renders raw item titles, but SectionView is never instantiated with scope == .all — sectionedResults expands .all into the concrete scopes ([.artists,.albums,.tracks,.playlists,(.genres)]) which never contains .all.
  - _Why:_ Dead branch; if ever reached it would render an unstyled, non-interactive list of titles with no navigation, inconsistent with every other scope. It is misleading code that masks the fact .all is handled by expansion upstream.
  - _Fix:_ Remove the .all case from content (or replace with an assertionFailure), since SectionView only ever receives concrete scopes.
- **L601** [accessibility] The 'Load more' inline ProgressView (and the top-level loadingIndicator ProgressView) have no accessibility label and are not hidden, surfacing to VoiceOver as an unlabeled progress element.
  - _Why:_ VoiceOver users hear an unlabeled 'in progress' control with no context about what is loading.
  - _Fix:_ Add .accessibilityLabel("Loading more \(scope.label.lowercased())") to the inline spinner and a label (or .accessibilityHidden(true) plus an announcement) to loadingIndicator.
- **L675** [accessibility] RecentSearchRow combines its children into one accessibility element (.combine) while also containing an interactive 'Remove' Button, which makes the per-row clear action hard or impossible to invoke independently via VoiceOver.
  - _Why:_ VoiceOver users get a single 'search for term' element and lose easy access to the 'Remove from recent searches' action that sighted users get via the X button. There's still a global 'Clear history' button, but per-item removal is part of issue #87's acceptance criteria.
  - _Fix:_ Use `.accessibilityElement(children: .contain)` (so the nested button stays focusable) or add an `.accessibilityAction(named:)` on the combined element for removal, instead of .combine.
- **L675** [accessibility] RecentSearchRow combines all children for accessibility (.combine) while also containing a separate 'Remove' Button; combining can swallow the inner button so VoiceOver users may be unable to invoke the per-row clear action independently of the row tap.
  - _Why:_ With children combined into one element exposing only the search hint, the clear (xmark) button's action and label may not be reachable, leaving no accessible way to remove a single recent search.
  - _Fix:_ Use .accessibilityElement(children: .contain) and add an .accessibilityAction(named:) for removal, or expose the clear button as a separate accessible element with its existing label.
- **L716** [gap-stub] GenreResultRow renders an empty view (no else) when model.supportsGenreActions is false; combined with genreRows still iterating the bucket, this would create invisible zero-content rows and a section count that doesn't match visible items. Mitigated today only because supportsGenreActions is hard-coded true and sectionedResults already filters out .genres when unsupported.
  - _Why:_ This is a latent gap: if supportsGenreActions ever becomes false at runtime while a genres bucket is non-empty (race between filtering and capability flip), the genres section header would show a count of N but render N invisible rows.
  - _Fix:_ Either render a non-interactive labelled row in the else branch, or gate genreRows itself on supportsGenreActions so no rows are produced when actions are unavailable.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/ServerReachability.swift`
- **L59** [performance] ServerReachability.noteSuccess() writes a Date to UserDefaults on every successful network call via LastConnectedStore.noteSuccess(); with ~15 success call sites in AppModel (including paged loads), this performs a synchronous UserDefaults write on the MainActor on essentially every successful FFI.
  - _Why:_ During heavy paging/scrolling many successes fire per second, each issuing a UserDefaults write on the main thread. It is individually cheap but unbounded in frequency and unnecessary — only the last-success timestamp matters, not every success.
  - _Fix:_ Throttle the persisted timestamp (e.g. only write if more than N seconds since last write), or move the write off the timestamp-on-every-success path (write on app background / periodically).
- **L216** [bug] hostString for IPv6/IPv4 NWEndpoint.Host interpolates the raw address, and extract() then wraps it as "\(name).local" and builds an unbracketed URL; an IPv6 address would produce an invalid host/URL (e.g. fe80::1%en0.local) for the .hostPort branch.
  - _Why:_ For the (rare) .hostPort Bonjour result with an IP host, the synthesized seedURL is malformed and probeServer would fail. Most Jellyfin Bonjour results are .service so this is uncommon, but the address handling is incorrect when it occurs.
  - _Fix:_ Only append '.local' for service-name hosts; for IP hosts use the address directly and bracket IPv6 ([addr]) and strip the zone before forming the URL.
- **L284** [error-handling] ServerProbe reports a misleading 'Couldn't reach server' message when core is nil (not yet configured) — a configuration/programmer error is surfaced to the user as a reachability failure, and state briefly flashes .checking before .failed.
  - _Why:_ If schedule() runs before configure(core:), the user sees 'Couldn't reach server' for what is actually an unconfigured probe, which is confusing during onboarding edge cases.
  - _Fix:_ Guard for core before setting .checking, and either return to .idle or surface a distinct internal-state message when core is nil rather than a network-style failure.
- **L300** [bug] If the probe task is cancelled after state is set to .checking but during/after the detached probeServer call, the function returns without resetting state, so the UI can be left showing a spinner (.checking) until a superseding schedule completes; if none does, it stays stuck.
  - _Why:_ View teardown or a cancel without a follow-up schedule leaves the probe pill in an indefinite 'checking' state. In the normal type-and-supersede flow this is transient, but a final cancel (e.g. field loses focus / view disappears) can leave it stuck.
  - _Fix:_ On cancellation reset to a defined terminal state (e.g. .idle) instead of returning with .checking left in place, or only set .checking after confirming the task is still the active one.
- **L354** [performance] relativeLastConnected() allocates a new RelativeDateTimeFormatter on every call; it is invoked from LoginView's loginErrorMessage computed property which is read during view body evaluation.
  - _Why:_ DateFormatter-family objects are comparatively expensive to allocate; constructing one per body re-evaluation on the login error path is wasteful, though bounded to the unreachable-state path.
  - _Fix:_ Cache a static RelativeDateTimeFormatter (it is reusable) instead of allocating per call.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/DiagnosticBundle.swift`
- **L182** [dead-code] Redundant guard `where out[key] == nil`. settingsAllowlist is a static array with no duplicate keys and `out` starts empty, so `out[key]` is always nil on each iteration; the clause never filters anything.
  - _Why:_ Harmless but dead: it implies a dedup intent that the data structure already guarantees, and could mislead a future editor into thinking duplicate keys are handled. Purely cosmetic.
  - _Fix:_ Drop the `where out[key] == nil` clause, or add a debug assertion that settingsAllowlist has no duplicates if dedup is genuinely desired.
- **L244** [error-handling] manifest.json is added to the bundle via a swallowed `try?`; if JSON encoding ever fails the bundle is produced WITHOUT a manifest and no error is surfaced to the user or the maintainer who receives the bundle.
  - _Why:_ Manifest is all String/[String:String] so encoding is practically infallible today, but the silent-drop pattern means a future field change that breaks encoding would ship a manifest-less bundle that looks complete. assemble() returns [String:Data] with no signal that a promised file is missing.
  - _Fix:_ Either make encode non-optional (it cannot throw for this shape — use try! is also undesirable) and assert, or capture the error and inject a placeholder file (e.g. manifest.json = "(manifest encoding failed: ...)") so the omission is visible.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/DockTileController.swift`
- **L58** [validation] progressFraction does not guard against a NaN position; a NaN propagates through min/max and yields NaN progress, which feeds SwiftUI's Circle.trim(to:).
  - _Why:_ If the core ever reports a NaN positionSeconds (e.g. an unseekable/streaming source mid-load), the ring's trim end becomes NaN, which SwiftUI handles inconsistently (no arc, or a console warning about invalid geometry). It is a cheap defensive gap.
  - _Fix:_ Add `guard position.isFinite, duration.isFinite, duration > 0 else { return 0 }` before dividing, so a non-finite input collapses to 0 progress.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/LaunchAtLogin.swift`
- **L25** [bug] disable() only unregisters when status == .enabled, so it no-ops when the registration is in the .requiresApproval state, leaving a pending login item the user asked to remove.
  - _Why:_ If the app previously called register() and macOS put it in .requiresApproval, the app is still listed as a (pending) login item. A user toggling the preference off would expect it gone, but disable() returns early and never calls unregister(), so the pending item lingers.
