  - _Fix:_ Relax the guard to also unregister when status is .requiresApproval (e.g. `guard status == .enabled || status == .requiresApproval else { return }`), or just attempt unregister() and ignore the not-registered error.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/NotificationManager.swift`
- **L21** [concurrency] NotificationManager is a non-Sendable final class shared singleton whose mutable state didRequestAuthorization is read/written with no synchronization and no actor isolation. It is currently called only from MainActor SwiftUI contexts (LyrebirdApp .task and Preferences toggle), so it works today, but nothing enforces that; a future off-main caller would introduce a data race on this flag (and a possible double authorization request).
  - _Why:_ Unsynchronized mutable shared state on a class with no isolation guarantee is a latent data race; the read-modify-write of the guard flag is not atomic, so concurrent callers could both pass the guard and issue duplicate authorization prompts.
  - _Fix:_ Annotate the class (or at least requestAuthorizationIfNeeded and the flag) with @MainActor, or make NotificationManager an actor, to make the single-fire contract enforced rather than incidental.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/ScrobbleGate.swift`
- **L33** [bug] submitListen carries listenedAt=startedAtUnix, the wall-clock time the track FIRST became current, not the time the listen threshold was actually reached. For long tracks this can report a listen timestamp many minutes earlier than the moment the scrobble criterion was met, and startedAtUnix can be stale if the track was paused/seeked.
  - _Why:_ Scrobble services typically expect the listen timestamp to reflect when playback started, but using the first-seen instant can be inaccurate under pause/resume or when the gate is constructed before playback truly begins, skewing listening history ordering.
  - _Fix:_ Confirm the server's expected semantics for listenedAt; if it should be the playback-start instant this is acceptable, but consider recording the timestamp at actual playback start and document the intent. At minimum ensure startedAtUnix is reset appropriately so a paused-then-resumed track does not report a misleading time.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/System/WindowStateStore.swift`
- **L142** [consistency] restoredInspectorVisible parses the persisted inspector flag as a bare 'true'/not-true string while every other persisted enum in this file uses a typed persistedRawValue/init?(persistedRawValue:) round-trip. The asymmetry means any value other than the exact literal 'true' (including a legacy or differently-cased value) silently resolves to false with no fallback distinction between 'never saved' and 'saved false'.
  - _Why:_ Inconsistent serialization style across the same store is a maintenance hazard and brittle: the writer (MainShell line 239) emits 'true'/'false', so a string-equality check works today, but it is fragile to any change in the writer and unlike the validated round-trips used for screen/sidebar.
  - _Fix:_ Use a typed round-trip (or Bool(persistedRaw ?? "")) consistent with the other keys, and keep the writer and reader encodings co-located so they cannot drift.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Theme/Theme.swift`
- **L110** [concurrency] `isIncreaseContrastEnabled` is a process-global mutable closure annotated `nonisolated(unsafe)`, read from inside the NSColor dynamic-provider block which AppKit may invoke on a non-main thread during drawing. It is mutated (in tests) without synchronization.
  - _Why:_ The `unsafe` opt-out disables Swift's data-race checking precisely here. In production it is only mutated never (set once at definition) and the read inside a drawing-time provider is benign, but the seam is overridden at runtime by AccessibleThemeTests (`Theme.isIncreaseContrastEnabled = { increaseContrast }`); if any concurrent draw races a test mutation the read is unsynchronized. It is a latent footgun rather than a live production bug.
  - _Fix:_ Restrict the override seam to test builds (e.g. behind #if DEBUG or an injected protocol) or guard the storage so the provider read and any mutation are serialized; avoid mutating a globally shared drawing-time predicate from arbitrary threads.
- **L188** [consistency] font() selects a weight-specific named face and then also chains `.weight(weight)` on the resulting Font. For weights whose named face does not match the nominal weight value this double-application is inconsistent: `.heavy` maps to the "Figtree-ExtraBold" face but then `.weight(.heavy)` is applied on top.
  - _Why:_ Applying `.weight()` to an already weight-named custom font is redundant and, for the .heavy→ExtraBold mismatch, asks the renderer to re-weight a face that is already a specific named instance, which can produce subtly different (synthetically bolded) glyphs depending on the platform's handling of weight on named custom fonts.
  - _Fix:_ Drop the trailing `.weight(weight)` since the face name already encodes the weight, or stop mapping by name and rely solely on a single base family + `.weight()`. Pick one mechanism rather than both.
- **L211** [concurrency] FontRegistration.registered is a plain non-isolated mutable static read/written in register() with no synchronization and no actor isolation.
  - _Why:_ register() is in practice only invoked once from LyrebirdApp.init() on the main thread (macos/Sources/Lyrebird/LyrebirdApp.swift:27), so today it is safe, but the guard-then-set is a non-atomic check-and-set on shared mutable state. Under Swift 6 strict concurrency this is a data-race diagnostic, and any future off-main caller would race the flag and potentially double-register.
  - _Fix:_ Mark register()/registered @MainActor (matching its sole call site) or wrap the registration in a dispatch_once-style lazy let so the once-only guarantee is enforced regardless of caller thread.
- **L230** [error-handling] Font registration ignores both the BOOL return value and the error out-pointer of CTFontManagerRegisterFontsForURL (passed `nil`), so a failed registration is completely silent.
  - _Why:_ If a bundled .otf fails to register (corrupt file, name collision, sandbox issue), there is no log or signal; the app then silently substitutes a system fallback inside Font.custom, making a font regression hard to diagnose. Severity is low because Font.custom degrades gracefully and this runs once at launch, but the failure is invisible.
  - _Fix:_ Pass a CFError out-pointer and check the BOOL return; on failure emit Log.app.notice/error with the font name and CFError so registration failures are observable in Console.app.

### `macos/Sources/Lyrebird/Updater.swift`
- **L74** [error-handling] checkForUpdates() optional-chains through a nil controller and silently no-ops when Sparkle is not configured, giving no feedback if it is ever invoked while the controller is absent.
  - _Why:_ Today this is mostly defended because CheckForUpdatesView disables the button via `!updater.canCheckForUpdates` (which is false when controller is nil), so the user can't reach the no-op through that view. It is fragile if checkForUpdates() is ever called from another path (menu command, shortcut) that does not check canCheckForUpdates first — the action would silently do nothing.
  - _Fix:_ Either keep the no-op but document/guarantee all callers gate on canCheckForUpdates, or surface a user-visible message/log when invoked with no configured updater so a misconfigured build (placeholder SUPublicEDKey) is diagnosable.

### `macos/Sources/LyrebirdAudio/AudioEngine.swift`
- **L211** [resource-leak] deinit removes only timeObserver and endObserver and does not stop the core heartbeat or send a final stop report; if the engine is torn down mid-playback the core heartbeat task keeps reporting progress to the server.
  - _Why:_ On engine deallocation without an explicit stop(), the server continues to believe playback is in progress (Now Playing on other clients stays active) and the heartbeat task lingers. Low impact because the engine is app-lifetime-owned, but the cleanup is incomplete.
  - _Fix:_ In deinit, call core.stopHeartbeat() and a final reportStopped() (or ensure stop() is always invoked before teardown).
- **L312** [error-handling] reportStarted records reportingItemId/MediaSourceId/PlaySessionId even when the server start report fails: the try? swallows the error but the subsequent assignments run unconditionally.
  - _Why:_ If the start report failed (e.g. network), the later reportStopped()/reportProgressSnapshot will send stop/progress for a play session the server never registered, producing orphaned or rejected session reports.
  - _Fix:_ Only set the reporting identifiers when the start report succeeds (use do/try with the error path leaving reportingItemId nil), or accept the inconsistency explicitly — but as written it silently desyncs client/server session state.
- **L585** [bug] seek() completion reads self.player?.rate to decide isPaused, but a seek with toleranceBefore/After .zero plus the seekGeneration guard can race the rate observer; using rate at completion time may report paused immediately after a programmatic seek that the user expects to keep playing.
  - _Why:_ During a precise seek AVPlayer can momentarily drop rate to 0 while it re-buffers at the new position; reading rate in the completion handler can therefore report isPaused:true to the server even though playback was active and will resume. This produces a spurious paused progress report (and a paused Now-Playing state on other clients) right after scrubbing. Minor, but it sends a misleading server state.
  - _Fix:_ Track the intended playback state explicitly (e.g. a wasPlayingBeforeSeek captured before player.seek) and report that, rather than sampling player.rate at an arbitrary point in the re-buffer cycle.
- **L593** [consistency] setVolume clamps the value applied to the AVPlayer to [0,1] but passes the raw unclamped value to core.setVolume, so persisted/core volume state can diverge from actual output.
  - _Why:_ If a caller passes v outside [0,1], the core's stored volume (used for Now Playing volumeLevel / persistence) no longer matches the real output level.
  - _Fix:_ Compute `let clamped = max(0, min(1, v))` once and pass `clamped` to both player.volume and core.setVolume.
- **L615** [bug] preloadNextTrack sets the DEBUG test hook lastPreloadedTrackIdForTesting before any validation, so it records a 'preloaded' id even when the URL is invalid or resolution later fails and nothing is actually queued.
  - _Why:_ Tests asserting on lastPreloadedTrackIdForTesting will pass even when the preload silently failed, masking regressions in the preload resolution path (a test-gap / false-positive signal).
  - _Fix:_ Set lastPreloadedTrackIdForTesting only after the AVPlayerItem is successfully inserted into the queue (inside the MainActor.run block after player.insert).
- **L645** [error-handling] preloadNextTrack swallows playbackInfo failures with `try?`, so a failed PlaybackInfo silently proceeds with nil mediaSourceId/playSessionId instead of being logged like the rest of the preload path.
  - _Why:_ A server error on PlaybackInfo (e.g. transcode negotiation) is dropped entirely. The subsequent streamUrl is built without a mediaSourceId/playSessionId, which can yield a different (possibly wrong-bitrate or un-resumable) preloaded stream than the eventual real play() of that track, with no diagnostic. This mirrors gap pattern #1 (silently-rotting try?).
  - _Fix:_ Capture and log the playbackInfo error (do/catch or `if case .failure`) so a degraded preload is at least visible in Console; consider aborting the preload when PlaybackInfo fails rather than fabricating a source-less URL.
- **L711** [concurrency] The 1Hz periodic time observer calls synchronous FFI core.markPosition on the main thread, taking the Rust Inner mutex on .main once per second during playback.
  - _Why:_ Per CLAUDE.md gap pattern #2, sync FFI on the MainActor contends the Inner mutex. This one is the documented-acceptable cadence (1Hz, skipped when paused), so it is not a regression — but it is still a main-thread mutex acquisition every second that competes with any other FFI call (status poll, heartbeat) and could contribute to brief hitches if Inner is held by a slow operation. Flagged for awareness, not as a defect to fix blindly.
  - _Fix:_ Acceptable as-is given the 1Hz + skip-when-paused contract. If contention is observed, marshal markPosition through a serial background actor/queue and avoid holding the position write on the main thread; do not increase the cadence (per the documented constraint).

### `macos/Sources/LyrebirdAudio/AudioOutputDevices.swift`
- **L84** [error-handling] setExclusiveMode silently no-ops (returns successfully) when uid is empty, so the AppModel.setExclusiveMode toggle reports success even though exclusive mode was never applied.
  - _Why:_ Enabling Exclusive Mode while on "System Default" (empty uid) leaves the UI toggle ON but applies nothing, with no feedback. The Preferences UI does .disabled(outputDeviceUID.isEmpty) (PreferencesAudio.swift:111) which mitigates the toggle path, but setOutputDevice's later re-application and any programmatic caller would still silently succeed-but-do-nothing.
  - _Fix:_ When enabled == true and uid.isEmpty, throw AudioOutputDeviceError.deviceUnavailable (or a dedicated case) so callers can keep the toggle off and inform the user that a specific device must be selected first.

### `macos/Sources/LyrebirdAudio/MediaSession.swift`
- **L287** [consistency] nextTrackCommand and previousTrackCommand handlers omit the currentTrack/queue guard that every other transport command performs, so they invoke the skip delegate even when there is nothing actionable.
  - _Why:_ These commands rely solely on isEnabled (set in refreshRemoteCommandEnablement) for gating. If a remote control sends next/previous in a window where the cached status is stale (e.g. queue just emptied), the handler still calls mediaSessionSkipNext/Previous and reports .success instead of .noActionableNowPlayingItem, diverging from the guarded behavior of the other commands and the pattern established by issue #684.
  - _Fix:_ Add the same guard used by the other transport commands: if delegate.currentStatus.currentTrack == nil { return .noActionableNowPlayingItem } (and/or a queue-bounds check) before calling the skip delegate.
- **L522** [security] The full Authorization header (containing the Jellyfin access token) is attached to the artwork image request. This is correct/necessary, but note the token is sent on a plain image GET; if the resolved artwork URL is ever non-HTTPS the token leaks in cleartext. There is no scheme check before attaching the credential.
  - _Why:_ mediaSessionArtworkURL is built from core.imageUrl with whatever base URL the server advertises. If a server (or a misconfigured one) returns an http:// image base, the access token is transmitted unencrypted with every cover-art fetch. The token is the same credential used for the whole session.
  - _Fix:_ Only attach the Authorization header when url.scheme == "https" (or when the host matches the trusted server origin), and otherwise skip the credential or refuse the request.

### `macos/Sources/LyrebirdAudio/ReplayGain.swift`
- **L166** [validation] parseGainDb truncates European-decimal and sign-with-space forms instead of rejecting/parsing them.
  - _Why:_ A tag like `12,5 dB` parses to 12.0 (comma stops the walk, fractional part dropped) and `- 7.5 dB` (space after sign) parses to nil because index 0 is '-' but the next char is a space. ReplayGain tags are conventionally written `%+.2f dB`, so this is an edge case, and the downstream ±15 dB clamp in linearVolume bounds any garbage value — hence low severity — but the comma case yields a wrong-magnitude gain rather than a rejection.
  - _Fix:_ Trim a trailing unit suffix and let Double()/a NumberFormatter do the parse, or at least normalize ',' to '.' and skip an optional space after the sign so locale-formatted tags are either parsed correctly or cleanly rejected.

### `macos/Sources/SmokeTest/main.swift`
- **L126** [dead-code] Guard after waitFor(positionAdvanceFrom:byAtLeast:) re-checks a condition the helper already enforces, duplicating the threshold in two places.
  - _Why:_ waitFor returns early precisely when `latest > start + delta` (line 233) and otherwise returns the last sample on timeout, so the literal `0.5` lives both in the call argument and the guard. The guard is correct for the timeout case but the magic number is now stated twice; if one is edited (e.g. delta bumped to 1.0) and the other isn't, the assertion silently weakens. Same pattern at line 161 for resume.
  - _Fix:_ Have waitFor return an optional/Bool that already encodes success (nil/false on timeout) and branch on that, or thread `delta` through so the guard reuses the same constant instead of re-hardcoding 0.5.

### `macos/Tests/LyrebirdTests/MenuBarNowPlayingTests.swift`
- **L15** [test-gap] Tests cover only the three pure static helpers (showsNowPlaying, transportIcon, MenuBarNowPlayingLabel.icon); the interactive transport actions (skipPrevious/skipNext/togglePlayPause wiring) and the rendering branches (nowPlaying vs idle vs openButton) in MenuBarNowPlaying.swift have no coverage.
  - _Why:_ A future refactor that, e.g., swaps backward.fill and forward.fill action closures (lines 71-85) or mis-wires the centre button to the wrong model method would compile and pass CI silently. The transport panel is the menu-bar feature's whole point.
  - _Fix:_ This is partly self-imposed (the test header notes headless runs have no window server). Extract the button->action mapping into a small testable indirection, or add a lightweight model spy asserting that tapping prev/next/play-pause routes to the expected AppModel call. Acceptable to leave given the documented constraint; flagging for completeness only.
